# Bootstrap

> The Bootstrap (leaf-boot) area is the SpringApplication.run() analogue: a 10-feature set (spring-application-run orchestrator + app-type-deduction, application-arguments, context-initializers, run-listeners-events, runners, failure-analysis, banner, exit-code-shutdown, bootstrap-context as sub-features) sitting ATOP the Phase-1 container/refresh layer (refresh-lifecycle, context-close, runtime-lifecycle, lifecycle-events in 05-events-lifecycle.md). The layering is fundamentally COHERENT: the run pipeline correctly drives refresh-lifecycle (delegates refresh wholly, all-or-nothing), context-close (triggers, never tears down beans itself), and runtime-lifecycle (does not auto-start Lifecycle beans — leaves that to finish_refresh, fires Started after) without duplicating them, and the cancel-vs-close failure fork matches exactly what refresh-lifecycle and context-close model. Bootstrap correctly defers the availability STATE model to lifecycle-events, the discovery substrate + anti-DCE manifest to the cross-crate keystone, the error/diagnostics model to the §3 keystone, and the early-multicaster handoff to the events meta-design. TWO genuine ownership GAPS surfaced: (1) process keep-alive (spring.main.keep-alive) — its value is stored in extra-11 but NO design owns the await-until-signal behavior that keeps a server-less app from exiting after run() returns; (2) the ApplicationStartup recorder wiring at boot (context.setApplicationStartup) + establishing the boot-level root step as parent of the refresh root — startup-instrumentation roots at leaf.context.refresh and never owns installing the boot recorder or the boot->refresh parent linkage. The sharpest COHERENCE issues are: availability publication sits on an unreconciled reactive-state substrate (re-proposed 4x across lifecycle-events/runtime-lifecycle/context-close/exit-code-shutdown); application-arguments is designed TWICE (Bootstrap + config-environment extra-6) and must collapse to one owner; the early-event-buffering and non-uniform milestone-error-isolation questions are consumers of unresolved lifecycle-area keystones; and FailureAnalysis must share its anti-DCE/report-rendering machinery with condition-report. JVM-shaped scaffolding the designs already correctly question for Phase-3 design-out (banner-as-bean, two-multicaster split, bootstrap-context prototype scope, StackWalker main-deduction, configureHeadlessProperty) need not be ported. Confidence: high on the layering coherence (verified against the actual lifecycle doc); the two missing features are concrete unowned seams, not speculative.

_10 feature designs (the leaf-boot entry-point layer). Implementation-agnostic — candidate realizations for Phase 2/3, not decisions._

## Application Entry Point & Run Pipeline (SpringApplication.run equivalent)  `[spring-application-run]`

leaf's single opinionated bootstrap entry point — the SpringApplication.run analogue — that replaces hand-wiring a container. Its intent (per spring-boot-4-di-design.md §"The SpringApplication bootstrap pipeline", lines 238-321): deduce the application type, prepare the Environment, create+configure the context, run ApplicationContextInitializers, refresh, invoke runners, then signal ready — firing a FIXED, NAMED event sequence at every phase (Starting → EnvironmentPrepared → ContextInitialized → Prepared → [Refreshed+ServerInitialized during refresh] → Started → AvailabilityChange(Liveness CORRECT) → Ready → AvailabilityChange(Readiness ACCEPTING_TRAFFIC) | Failed-on-throw). It owns the run ORCHESTRATION above refresh-lifecycle: the ordered run() sequence (timer, shutdown-hook arm, bootstrap-context create, run-listeners.starting, parse args, prepareEnvironment (which fires environment-prepared → where config-data/EnvironmentPostProcessors run), banner, createContext (app-type-driven factory), prepareContext (apply initializers, register arg/banner singletons, contextLoaded → Prepared), refreshContext (delegates to refresh-lifecycle), afterRefresh, started+Availability-Liveness, callRunners (window AFTER refresh+started, BEFORE ready — the K8s readiness-gate window), then if running: ready+Availability-ACCEPTING_TRAFFIC). It owns: the transient pre-container BootstrapContext/BootstrapRegistry (shared singletons before the real container exists, promoted at close); the RunListener event taxonomy + standalone early-multicaster (first events fire before the context/multicaster exist — early listeners CANNOT be beans, must be registered on the application or via the registry); ApplicationContextInitializer hook (applied after setEnvironment/postProcessContext, before definitions load, before refresh); the Runner family (single ordered @Order stream interleaving ApplicationRunner/CommandLineRunner, throw aborts startup); bindToApplication (spring.main.* config bound back onto the live application instance so externalized config overrides programmatic setters); the banner; AvailabilityState publication as CORE (not actuator); the run HOOK (withHook / thread-local single-run listener for test-slicing + AbandonedRunException short-circuit); and — the marquee charter §1.7/§2.9 surface — FailureAnalysis: a startup failure should TEACH (port-in-use, missing bean, bad binding are predictable), via FailureAnalyzer SPI → first non-null FailureAnalysis(description, action, cause) rendered into a clean diagnostic, with AbandonedRunException short-circuiting analysis+close. App-type deduction follows "the classpath is the configuration" intent (dependency choice expresses servlet/reactive/none) with explicit escape hatches. Must replicate the INTENT WITHOUT JVM lineage: no spring.factories runtime SPI loading, no classpath scanning, no StackWalker main-class deduction, no GC-mopped failed run, sync-around-main assumption, or ListenableFuture; in async Rust the whole pipeline is an awaited async fn on the bootstrap task with explicit execution context, the event sequence carries parent linkage explicitly (no ambient thread-local current-phase across the eager-singleton/background fan-out), teardown is the explicit container-driven async pass (no async Drop), and cross-crate "what participates" is SCOPED (static link-time registry + optional dynamic source), never implicitly global.

### Candidate realizations

#### R1 — Literal ordered async run() driver: one concrete async pipeline function over a typed RunPhase state machine, with run-participants (initializers/listeners/runners/analyzers) collected as origin-agnostic descriptors and the fixed named event sequence fired explicitly at each phase boundary
Mirror SpringApplication.run() as ONE concrete async function `async fn run(app: &Application, args: Args) -> Result<RunningContext, RunFailure>` that executes the named steps in literal fixed order, each an explicit `.await` point, advancing a typed `RunPhase` enum (Created → Starting → EnvironmentPrepared → ContextCreated → ContextInitialized → ContextPrepared(Loaded) → Refreshing → Refreshed → Started → RunnersInvoked → Ready | Failed) so each step asserts its predecessor phase and the event sequence is fired EXPLICITLY at each transition. The pipeline: (1) start a startup timer (delegates to startup-instrumentation; the run is the root span/step); (2) arm the shutdown hook (an opt-in ctrl-c/SIGTERM task that will call context-close once — armed early, fires only after a RunningContext exists); (3) create the transient `BootstrapContext` (a tiny typed pre-container registry — promote-on-close) and run `BootstrapRegistryInitializer` descriptors; (4) build the run-listener set (the standalone early multicaster + the thread-local withHook injection) and fire `Starting`; (5) parse `Args` into a typed ApplicationArguments; (6) `prepare_environment(args)` — get-or-create the Environment (environment), add the command-line property source + activate profiles (profiles), then fire `EnvironmentPrepared` — THE hook where config-data's EnvironmentPostProcessor-analogues run (config-import/ConfigData loading), then `bind_to_application(spring.main.*)` rebinding banner-mode/app-type/lazy-init/etc onto the live `app` so externalized config overrides programmatic setters; (7) print the banner (banner-mode from bound config); (8) `create_context()` — pick the context type via an origin-agnostic `ContextFactory` chain keyed by the deduced AppType (none/servlet/reactive — 'the classpath is the configuration' via a Deducer descriptor chain + explicit `set_app_type` escape hatch); (9) `prepare_context()` — set the environment, post-process (name-generator/conversion-service), `apply_initializers()` (ordered ApplicationContextInitializer descriptors — register BFPP-analogues, set profiles; BEFORE definitions load, BEFORE refresh), fire `ContextInitialized`, close the bootstrap context (promoting its registered singletons into the real context), register the args+banner singletons, load definition sources, fire `ContextPrepared/Loaded` (→ Prepared); (10) `refresh_context()` — delegate WHOLLY to refresh-lifecycle's refresh() (its ContextRefreshed + any ServerInitialized fire DURING this); (11) `after_refresh()` no-op hook; (12) end the startup timer, fire `Started` + publish AvailabilityState Liveness=CORRECT (core, via lifecycle-events) — the runtime-lifecycle auto-start already happened inside finish_refresh; (13) `call_runners()` — collect all Runner beans (ApplicationRunner + CommandLineRunner) as ONE @Order-sorted stream, await each in order; a runner throw wraps into a RunFailure and aborts (after refresh+started, BEFORE ready — the K8s readiness-gate window is an execution-context boundary, not just a comment); (14) if the context is running, fire `Ready` + publish Readiness=ACCEPTING_TRAFFIC. ANY throw routes to `handle_run_failure()`: check for an Abandoned short-circuit (rethrow, no analysis/close — the test-slice/withHook abort path), else fire `Failed`, run the FailureAnalyzer descriptor chain (first non-null FailureAnalysis(description, action, cause) wins), render it via a FailureAnalysisReporter, then drive context-close's cancel/close path and return a rich RunFailure carrying the failing phase + the FailureAnalysis + the underlying cause-chain. Run-participants (BootstrapRegistryInitializers, RunListeners, ContextInitializers, Runners, FailureAnalyzers, AppType Deducers, ContextFactories) are all collected as thin origin-agnostic `const` descriptors from the SAME catalog substrate the rest of leaf uses (Phase-2-undecided: linkme/codegen/explicit), addressed by role — never a runtime spring.factories scan. `#[leaf::main]` is a THIN macro that emits a hand-writable `Application::new(PrimaryConfig).run(Args::from_env()).await` plus the force-link `use leaf_x as _;` references (Architecture B/D), nothing hidden.

**Pros:** Highest INTENT fidelity and maximal teachability: the ordered run() steps, the fixed named event sequence at each transition, the bootstrap-context-then-promote, the initializers-before-refresh, the runners-after-started-before-ready window, and the failure-analysis-then-close route all map 1:1 to SpringApplication.run() — a stepped trace / cargo expand reads exactly like the Spring sequence (DX #1, §2.10 legibility, intent-not-mechanism parity).; The typed RunPhase enum makes the boot state machine's invariants checkable: each step asserts its predecessor phase, the event sequence is provably fired in order (a phase transition IS the event), and 'fire Ready only if running' / 'Failed on any throw' become enforced transitions rather than conventions — directly serving the fixed-named-sequence intent and §2.9 legible failure.; Async-first by construction (§2.3): the whole pipeline is one awaited fn on the bootstrap task; config-data loading at EnvironmentPrepared, an async context factory, async runners, and an async shutdown hook all await without blocking — Spring's sync-around-main assumption dissolves, and the runners-window (after-refresh-before-ready) is an explicit execution-context boundary that integrates cleanly with K8s readiness gating (await the runners, THEN flip ACCEPTING_TRAFFIC).; Cleanly DELEGATES rather than reinvents: refresh_context() is a single call into refresh-lifecycle; close on failure/exit is context-close's job; auto-start/Availability are runtime-lifecycle+lifecycle-events; prepare_environment is environment+config-data+profiles. This feature stays a THIN orchestrator over already-designed neighbours (§2.11 unification), so its surface is the run sequence and the run-listener taxonomy, not container internals.; The FailureAnalyzer chain is the natural home for charter §1.7/§2.9 'fail with rich, complete, actionable context': predictable boot failures (port-in-use, missing bean, bad binding) become a description+action+cause rendered diagnostic, and because the run owns the failing-phase context, the RunFailure carries the full causal chain (what phase, what was being assembled, what it needed, candidates considered) — the bootstrap layer where complete diagnostics shine.; BootstrapContext as a tiny typed pre-container registry honours the real need (an expensive client an EnvironmentPostProcessor uses BEFORE the container exists) with a deliberately minimal surface that promotes into the context at close — and the standalone early-multicaster + thread-local withHook fall out as honest rust-native ports (early listeners are registered on the Application or via descriptors, not beans, exactly as Spring requires).

**Cons:** A single concrete run() with ~14 fixed steps is the most rigid shape: it commits early to 'these steps, this order', foreclosing R2's pluggable-stage pipeline and making a genuinely new phase (an integration that needs a step Spring never had) a core-function edit rather than a contributed stage — and it risks carrying JVM-shaped steps (banner, headless-property analogue, bootstrap-context-promotion) that a rust-native design may not need.; The event sequence is fired by hand at each transition, so 'the named sequence is complete and correctly ordered' is a hand-maintained property of this one function — a missed or mis-ordered fire is a correctness bug with no structural guard beyond the RunPhase assertions, and the early-vs-context multicaster split (first events on a standalone multicaster, later ones on the context's) is a subtle two-multicaster handoff that must stay coherent with events/event-multicaster's eventual design.; handle_run_failure must coordinate TWO downstream teardown semantics it doesn't own — context-close's clean-close vs refresh-lifecycle's cancelRefresh (cancel, not close) — plus the Abandoned short-circuit (rethrow WITHOUT analysis or close); getting 'which teardown path on which failure' right is a real correctness burden inherited from Spring's own handleRunFailure/cancelRefresh/AbandonedRunException tangle.; bind_to_application (rebinding spring.main.* onto the live Application mid-run, so config overrides programmatic setters set before run()) is an inherently mutate-the-driver-from-its-own-input pattern that fights Rust ownership: the run() fn must hold the Application in a form it can re-bind a handful of typed fields on between phases — modeling 'externalized config overrides the programmatic builder' cleanly (vs a confusing two-source-of-truth) is non-trivial and couples to environment's read/mutate seam.; Run-participant collection inherits every cross-crate DCE hazard (Layer 0/A/B): a FailureAnalyzer, ContextInitializer, AppType Deducer, or RunListener in a crate the binary never force-links is SILENTLY absent — and unlike a missing bean (loud at resolution) a missing analyzer just yields a worse diagnostic, a missing deducer silently picks the wrong app type, a missing initializer silently skips a tweak. Mandates the anti-DCE self-check, and the failure modes are quieter than the container's.; Several steps (banner, AppType deduction, ContextFactory selection) presuppose ecosystem concerns (servlet/reactive) the charter scopes OUT of core — so the run() must keep these as descriptor-driven extension slots that resolve to NONE/no-op in a coreonly app, or it bakes web-shaped assumptions into the core entry point against §1 scope.

**Mechanisms considered:** one concrete `async fn run(&Application, Args) -> Result<RunningContext, RunFailure>` running ~14 named steps in literal fixed order, each an `.await` point; typed `RunPhase` enum advanced by the driver; each step asserts its predecessor phase; the fixed named event sequence fired EXPLICITLY as phase-transition side effects (Starting/EnvironmentPrepared/ContextInitialized/Prepared/Started/Ready, Failed-on-throw); transient typed `BootstrapContext`/`BootstrapRegistry` (promote-registered-singletons-into-the-context at close) + `BootstrapRegistryInitializer` descriptors; standalone early-multicaster for the first events (before the context/its multicaster exist) + a thread-local `withHook` single-run RunListener injection + `AbandonedRunException`-analogue short-circuit; prepare_environment: get-or-create Environment → add command-line source + activate profiles → fire EnvironmentPrepared (config-data/EnvironmentPostProcessor-analogues run here) → bind_to_application(spring.main.*) rebinding typed knobs onto the live Application; origin-agnostic `ContextFactory` chain keyed by a deduced `AppType` (Deducer descriptor chain — 'the classpath is the configuration' — with explicit set_app_type escape hatch); resolves to NONE in a core-only app; apply_initializers() (ordered ApplicationContextInitializer descriptors, before definitions load, before refresh) then refresh_context() delegating wholly to refresh-lifecycle; call_runners(): collect ApplicationRunner+CommandLineRunner as ONE @Order-sorted stream awaited in order, in the after-refresh+started / before-ready window; Availability publication (Liveness=CORRECT with Started, Readiness=ACCEPTING_TRAFFIC with Ready) as CORE via lifecycle-events, not an add-on; handle_run_failure(): Abandoned short-circuit (rethrow, no analysis/close) else fire Failed → FailureAnalyzer descriptor chain (first non-null FailureAnalysis(description,action,cause)) → FailureAnalysisReporter render → drive context-close → return rich RunFailure carrying failing phase + analysis + cause-chain; thin `#[leaf::main]` macro emitting hand-writable Application::new(Cfg).run(Args::from_env()).await + force-link `use leaf_x as _;` (Architecture B/D); opt-in shutdown hook = a ctrl-c/SIGTERM task calling context-close once (registerShutdownHook analogue), armed once a RunningContext exists

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** leaf-core/leaf-boot defines run()'s steps, the RunPhase enum, the run-listener event taxonomy + stable names, the RunFailure/FailureAnalysis types, and the descriptor traits (RunListener, ContextInitializer, BootstrapRegistryInitializer, Runner, FailureAnalyzer, AppTypeDeducer, ContextFactory). Per charter §6 topology the bootstrap layer is leaf-boot (the SpringApplication-equivalent on top of leaf-framework). Each run-participant TYPE is collected as a thin `const` descriptor from the SAME catalog substrate refresh-lifecycle/auto-configuration use (Phase-2-undecided: linkme distributed-slice / build.rs codegen / explicit with(); cross-crate doc Arch A-D) — never a runtime spring.factories scan and never a StackWalker main-class probe. This is the entry-point feature, so it INHERITS the full DCE story acutely: the run-participant registries are additional cross-crate discovery surfaces, and a FailureAnalyzer/RunListener/Initializer/Deducer in a crate the binary never force-links is SILENTLY absent (Layer 0), or DCE'd (Layer A pre-1.62 / Layer B under LLD pre-1.89). Failure modes are QUIETER than the container's (a missing analyzer = a worse diagnostic, not a crash; a missing deducer = silently-wrong AppType) so this feature MANDATES the anti-DCE self-check (expected-vs-found per source crate, warn on enabled-feature-zero-contributions) and is the natural HOST for 'leaf doctor'/startup-report consuming it. The Cargo-feature-as-starter mapping bites here ('adding the starter expresses intent' = 'the classpath is the configuration'): a feature must BOTH gate compilation AND cause the generated app-root (`#[leaf::main]`/scan!) to emit a force-link `use leaf_x as _;` — cfg gates compilation, not linkage. The run owns the Layer-0 solution surface (the generated force-link prelude). AppType deduction is the rust-native answer to WebApplicationType.deduce()'s SPI: a Deducer descriptor chain over enabled capabilities (cfg/feature-keyed) rather than a classpath probe — origin-agnostic (a WASM-module-contributed deducer/factory/initializer/runner participates identically), and it resolves to NONE in a core-only binary so no web knowledge leaks into core (§1 scope). Generics can't carry a 'static descriptor → macros hard-error with a register_runner!/register_initializer!(Concrete) shim. Stable cross-crate surface: the run-listener event-name taxonomy (an ABI-ish const vocabulary, like startup-instrumentation's) + the descriptor traits in leaf-core, emitted with absolute paths by the thin macros. The thread-local withHook is process-local (a single run), not cross-crate.

**T2 — execution context:** Entirely a COLD-PATH orchestration on the bootstrap task — but it threads through code that becomes async-concurrent inside refresh, so execution context matters (§2.3). The whole run() is one awaited async fn; each step is an explicit `.await` point. prepare_environment awaits config-data file/network IO (fenced off as config-data's own async-IO concern, joined back into the synchronous stack before the context is built). create_context/apply_initializers are cold sequential; refresh_context awaits refresh-lifecycle (which fans out the eager-singleton/background-bootstrap waves — the run() simply awaits the whole refresh as one all-or-nothing unit). call_runners awaits each Runner in @Order; a blocking runner must spawn_blocking (documented execution-context discipline). NO GLOBAL LOCK (§2.5): the only serialization is the single-container bring-up guard (concurrent run/close on the same container), never a global monitor. The fixed named events fire on the bootstrap task; the early-vs-context multicaster handoff means the first events dispatch synchronously on the standalone early-multicaster (before the container's exists) and later ones on the context's — both ordered, neither busy-waiting (§2.4 reactive). PARENT LINKAGE for the startup trace is carried EXPLICITLY into the refresh fan-out (the run is the root span; refresh phases nest under it — never read off an ambient thread-local current-phase, the §2.3 fix shared with startup-instrumentation). CANCELLATION: cancelling the bootstrap task mid-run routes to handle_run_failure — drive refresh-lifecycle's cancelRefresh (partial teardown of what was built, NO ContextClosedEvent) OR context-close (if past Refreshed) and produce a rich RunFailure recording the failing phase; an Abandoned short-circuit (test-slice/withHook abort) rethrows WITHOUT analysis or close. There is no async Drop, so failure teardown is the explicit awaited container-driven pass (context-close), never a Drop. ERRORS propagate as RunFailure carrying the failing RunPhase + the FailureAnalysis + the full cause-chain (§2.9). The shutdown hook is a SEPARATE cold task awaiting ctrl-c/SIGTERM that calls context-close once (close-once is a CAS / state transition, not a lock). The ready signal (Readiness=ACCEPTING_TRAFFIC) is the precise execution-context boundary after which the app accepts traffic — runners complete (data load/migrations) on the bootstrap task BEFORE that flip, integrating with readiness probes.

#### R2 — Pluggable named-stage run pipeline: run() is an ordered sequence of named, dependency-declaring RunStages the driver sequences, with the standard SpringApplication steps shipped as default stages and the fixed event sequence emitted by event-emitting stages between them
Question whether the run order must be a hard-coded function. Instead model run() as a PIPELINE of named `RunStage { id: StageId, after: &[StageId], before: &[StageId], order: Order, run: async fn(&mut RunCtx) -> Result<(), RunFailure> }` contributions the driver topologically sequences (with cycle/constraint detection as an early rich diagnostic) and runs in resolved order over a shared `RunCtx` capability object. The standard SpringApplication steps become DEFAULT stages leaf-boot ships — CreateBootstrapContext, FireStarting, ParseArgs, PrepareEnvironment, FireEnvironmentPrepared, BindToApplication, PrintBanner, CreateContext, PrepareContext (ApplyInitializers), FireContextInitialized, LoadSources, FireContextPrepared, RefreshContext, AfterRefresh, FireStarted+Liveness, CallRunners, FireReady+Readiness — with their ordering encoded as before/after EDGES (data, not a hard sequence). The FIXED NAMED EVENT SEQUENCE is preserved as HARD edges: each Fire<Event> stage declares 'after <the work it observes>, before <the next work>', so EnvironmentPrepared is structurally pinned after PrepareEnvironment and before CreateContext, Ready is pinned after CallRunners — and a contributed stage that tried to violate the canonical order (e.g. fire-Ready-before-CallRunners) produces a constraint/cycle error at sort time (the earliest, richest diagnostic, §2.9). RunCtx is a STAGE-PHASE-TYPED capability object: it exposes the mutable bootstrap-registry only to pre-CreateContext stages, the mutable context/initializer handle only between CreateContext and RefreshContext, the running context only after — so 'what a stage may do' is gated by where it sits, and the bootstrap-context-promotion + the early-vs-context multicaster handoff are RunCtx capability transitions rather than hand-coded branches. An integration crate inserts a NEW stage (not just a callback) by contributing a RunStage with edges (e.g. a CreateWebServer-context-factory stage after CreateContext before PrepareContext, or a custom AwaitMigrations stage after RefreshContext before FireReady) — strictly more expressive than R1's fixed steps, and the K8s-readiness window becomes a named, contributable region (any stage declaring after-CallRunners before-FireReady runs in the gate window). The standard run-listeners, initializers, runners, and failure-analyzers are still collected as descriptors and consumed BY the relevant default stages (FireStarting iterates RunListeners; CallRunners iterates Runners; the failure path iterates FailureAnalyzers); R2 changes only that the run SEQUENCE is data, not a fixed fn. handle_run_failure is itself a defined terminal transition: any stage erroring aborts, runs the FailureAnalyzer chain, and unwinds via the executed-stages ledger (drive close/cancel for exactly the stages that ran their setup). `#[leaf::main]` emits the default stage set + force-link references; the escape hatch is editing the contributed stage list / declaring stages programmatically.

**Pros:** Maximal unification + extensibility (§2.11): the run pipeline is ONE primitive (a RunStage DAG) and integration crates extend bootstrap by contributing STAGES with declared edges — the exact 'extend by hooking a layer' intent, generalized so a new bootstrap step (web-server context factory, await-migrations-before-ready, a custom availability gate) is data, not an entry-point edit (R1's limitation), and it reuses the SAME topo-sort-over-edges-as-data primitive refresh-lifecycle R2, auto-config-ordering, and the cross-crate doc §170 all mandate.; The fixed named event sequence is ENFORCED as hard edges, so 'the canonical order holds' is a sort-time structural property, not a hand-maintained one: a contributed stage that mis-orders an event fire fails with a full constraint/cycle path BEFORE any stage runs (the earliest possible diagnostic, §2.9) — strictly better than R1's hand-fired sequence for guaranteeing the named-sequence invariant the feature exists to provide.; The stage-typed RunCtx capability object enforces 'what you may do here' by position (bootstrap-registry only pre-CreateContext, context handle only pre-refresh, running context only after) — the bootstrap-context-promotion boundary and the early-vs-context multicaster handoff become properties of the ctx handed in, holding for contributed stages too, and dissolving R1's hand-coded two-multicaster branch.; The K8s readiness-gate window (after-refresh+started, before-ready) becomes a NAMED, contributable region: data-loading/migration stages slot in by declaring after-CallRunners before-FireReady, so the precise 'container ready but not yet accepting traffic' window is a first-class extension point rather than a comment — directly serving the intent that runners complete before readiness probes pass.; Most AOT-friendly + symmetric with refresh-lifecycle R2/R3: a topo-sorted stage schedule is exactly what a build-time pass could emit as a const ordering, and the run pipeline mirrors the refresh phase-DAG, so the whole bring-up (run stages → refresh phases) shares one ordering/scheduling shape — the cleanest compile-vs-runtime keystone fit (still a CANDIDATE).; Cancellation/teardown is driven by the executed-stages ledger (unwind exactly the stages that ran), so the failure path is mechanically derived rather than R1's hand-coded which-teardown-on-which-failure tangle — less chance of cancel-vs-close coherence drift.

**Cons:** Directly contradicts the deliberate Spring design that the order is FIXED and NOT a configurable pipeline (refresh-lifecycle's intent doc is explicit that fixing the order turns bring-up into a predictable state machine) — a re-orderable run-stage DAG, even resolving to the same order by default, weakens the 'you cannot accidentally reorder bootstrap' guarantee and the teachable linear run() mental model, cutting against intent fidelity for the ENTRY POINT specifically (the place users most need a predictable story).; Reasoning about 'what order will my app actually boot in' now requires reading the resolved DAG, not a fixed list — a real DX cost (#1) at exactly the feature whose value is a single predictable opinionated sequence; a contributed stage with wrong/missing edges can land in a surprising position or create a cycle (louder than Spring's, but the SPACE of orderings is now open).; More machinery for the common case where nobody adds a stage: every run pays topo-sort + cycle-detection over ~17 default stages that always resolve to the same order — cold-path-tolerable but real, and it pre-judges that run-stage re-orderability is even wanted (a Phase-2 bias against the fixed-pipeline keystone).; The stage-typed RunCtx capability enum means every RunStage matches on the ctx variant it expects and must handle wrong-position arms — ergonomics friction and a class of must-handle-but-unreachable arms a fixed-signature run() avoids (the recurring uniformity-vs-type-safety tradeoff).; The hard event-order edges must be authored correctly and COMPLETELY on the default stages, and every contributed stage must declare enough edges to be safely placed relative to the event fires — an under-constrained contributed stage (merely under-specified, not cyclic) can slip between an event and the work it should observe, a footgun the topo-sort can't catch.; Pushing the run order to runtime-resolved data partly pre-decides the metadata/codegen and compile-vs-runtime keystones (§3) — presenting the run pipeline as a DAG risks biasing those Phase-2 calls; it must stay strictly a CANDIDATE, and the event-fire-as-a-stage model couples tightly to the (undecided) events/event-multicaster substrate.

**Mechanisms considered:** run() as an ordered set of named `RunStage { id, after, before, order, run }` contributions topologically sorted by the driver (cycle/constraint detection as an early startup diagnostic); the ~17 standard SpringApplication steps shipped as DEFAULT stages in leaf-boot with ordering encoded as before/after edges (data, not a hard sequence); the fixed named event sequence preserved as HARD edges: each Fire<Event> stage pinned after-the-work-it-observes / before-the-next-work, so EnvironmentPrepared-after-PrepareEnvironment, Ready-after-CallRunners etc. are sort-time-enforced; a mis-ordering contribution fails at sort time; stage-phase-typed `RunCtx` capability object gating what each stage may do (bootstrap-registry pre-CreateContext; context/initializer handle pre-refresh; running context post-refresh) — bootstrap-context-promotion + early-vs-context multicaster handoff as capability transitions; integration crates contribute NEW stages (CreateWebServer context factory, AwaitMigrations, custom availability gate) by declaring edges — extension by data, not an entry-point edit; the K8s readiness-gate window as a NAMED contributable region (stages declaring after-CallRunners before-FireReady run in the gate window); standard run-listeners/initializers/runners/failure-analyzers still collected as descriptors and consumed BY the relevant default stages (FireStarting iterates listeners; CallRunners iterates runners; the failure terminal stage iterates analyzers); handle_run_failure as a defined terminal transition unwinding via the executed-stages ledger (drive close/cancel for exactly the stages that ran); topo-sort = the SAME ordering primitive refresh-lifecycle R2, auto-config-ordering, and cross-crate doc §170 mandate (one shared scheduling engine over edges-as-data); `#[leaf::main]` emits the default stage set + force-link references; escape hatch = edit the stage list / declare stages programmatically

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** Strongest fit for the cross-crate doc's ordering-as-data guidance (§170: do all ordering at runtime via topo-sort over descriptor edges, NEVER link/section/constructor order) and the extension story: leaf-boot defines RunStage/StageId/the RunCtx capability object and ships the standard stages as default contributions; integration crates depend only on leaf-core/leaf-boot and contribute additional RunStages via the Phase-2 catalog substrate (linkme/codegen/explicit). The topo-sort over stage edges is the SAME primitive refresh-lifecycle R2 and auto-config-ordering want, so the cross-crate ordering machinery is shared across the whole bring-up (the unification dividend). The sort step is the natural place to run BOTH the anti-DCE self-check AND constraint validation: a silently-DCE'd contributing crate shows up as a MISSING expected stage (or a missing expected run-listener/initializer count) → a loud sort-time RunFailure with per-source provenance, strictly richer than a count-only check because it names which stage/source is absent and which ordering constraint is unsatisfiable. The fixed event-order edges turn 'the canonical event sequence' into a verifiable cross-crate contract (a contributed stage cannot legally sit between an event fire and the work it must observe). Generics still can't register a stage (no 'static symbol until concrete) → macro hard-errors with a register_stage!(Concrete) shim. The two-source duality: the static link-time stage set is the default; a dynamic directory-scanned WASM-module source contributing a stage must register BEFORE the sort runs (a timing constraint = a phase2Question, flagged not resolved). AppType deduction + the context-factory selection become contributed stages keyed by enabled capabilities (cfg/feature) rather than a classpath probe — origin-agnostic, resolving to a NONE context in a core-only binary. Because the order is data, an AOT/build-time pass could emit the resolved stage schedule as a const (Architecture C) the runtime consumes — the cleanest AOT fit, but it WIDENS the stable surface (the stage-edge vocabulary + StageId namespace become ABI). The run-listener event-name taxonomy remains a stable const vocabulary (ABI-ish). CANDIDATES, not a decision.

**T2 — execution context:** Topo-sort + cycle/constraint detection is SYNCHRONOUS cold-path work (single-threaded, around startup, before any stage runs) — pure analysis over stage descriptors producing a resolved schedule + the earliest diagnostics. Stage EXECUTION runs on the bootstrap task in resolved order, each stage's run() an `.await` point under the same discipline as R1: PrepareEnvironment awaits config-data IO; RefreshContext awaits the whole refresh fan-out as one all-or-nothing unit; CallRunners awaits each Runner (blocking → spawn_blocking, §2.3). The stage-typed RunCtx gives each stage only the capabilities valid at its position — the mutable context/initializer handle (pre-refresh stages) is held only on the single-threaded cold path, sidestepping &mut-across-await aliasing by execution context, not a lock (§2.5). NO GLOBAL LOCK — only the per-container bring-up guard (concurrent run/close on the same container). The fixed events fire from the Fire<Event> stages on the bootstrap task; the early-vs-context multicaster handoff is a RunCtx capability transition (the first Fire stages get the standalone early-multicaster, later ones the context's), both ordered/reactive (§2.4). CANCELLATION uses the executed-stages ledger: cancelling the bootstrap task unwinds exactly the stages that ran their setup, in reverse, driving refresh-lifecycle cancelRefresh / context-close as appropriate (no async Drop; explicit awaited teardown). A sort-time failure (cycle / unsatisfiable event-order constraint / missing-expected-stage) aborts BEFORE any stage runs (earliest, richest); a run-time stage failure aborts all-or-nothing, runs the FailureAnalyzer chain, and returns a rich RunFailure carrying the failing StageId + the FailureAnalysis + the cause-chain + the resolved-schedule context (§2.9). The K8s readiness window is the execution-context region between CallRunners and FireReady — any after-CallRunners-before-FireReady stage runs on the bootstrap task before ACCEPTING_TRAFFIC flips. The shutdown hook is a separate cold task; ready/availability publication is reactive via lifecycle-events.

#### R3 — Build-time-frozen run PLAN + thin async run executor: the bootstrap pipeline's STRUCTURE (app type, resolved environment+profiles, stage/event schedule, initializer/runner/analyzer order, deduced context factory) is computed once and frozen into an inspectable RunPlan; run() is a thin executor that does only the genuinely-runtime work (IO, instance construction, signalling)
Push the AOT lineage (the doc's 'definitions are knowable at build time; instances are not', Spring 7's refreshForAotProcessing, and the doc's own 'AOT path forks the pipeline' note where createDefaultApplicationContext returns a plain context, sources are NOT loaded at runtime, and a generated <Main>__ApplicationContextInitializer is injected first) hardest — for the WHOLE run, not just refresh. Separate the run pipeline's STRUCTURE from its EXECUTION. A PLAN phase (build-time codegen via leaf-codegen reading cargo metadata + the resolved feature set, OR a runtime startup-validation pass when not AOT) resolves everything statically knowable: the deduced AppType (from the enabled capability/feature set — 'the classpath is the configuration' becomes 'the resolved Cargo feature graph is the configuration'), the selected ContextFactory, the ORDERED initializer/run-listener/runner/failure-analyzer sets (collected, deduped, @Order-sorted at plan time), the event-emission schedule (the fixed named sequence resolved to a concrete ordered list of emission points), the bind_to_application targets, and — fused with refresh-lifecycle R3's RefreshPlan — the frozen definition set + eager-singleton waves. It emits a `RunPlan { app_type, context_factory, initializer_order, run_listener_order, runner_order, analyzer_order, event_schedule, refresh_plan, env_skeleton }` as a checked-in/const artifact (sqlx model, Architecture C). The RUNTIME run() is then a THIN async executor that consumes the frozen RunPlan and does ONLY what genuinely needs runtime values/instances/IO: create the bootstrap context + run registry-initializers (in the frozen order); fire Starting (from the frozen event schedule); parse the actual Args; resolve env-dependent VALUES into the env_skeleton (config-data file/network IO happens here — the only place loading is runtime; structure/precedence was resolved at plan time) and fire EnvironmentPrepared; bind the actual spring.main.* runtime values onto the live Application; print the banner; instantiate the frozen ContextFactory; apply initializers in frozen order; fire ContextInitialized/Prepared; run refresh-lifecycle's thin plan-executor (wave-parallel eager instantiation per the frozen RefreshPlan); fire Started+Liveness; await the frozen-order Runner set; if running, fire Ready+Readiness. Validation moves EARLIEST: the plan VALIDATES the whole bootstrap (every initializer/runner/analyzer resolvable, the app type unambiguous, the context factory present, the refresh graph valid, all expected infrastructure linked) at plan/build time BEFORE the binary even runs — so a misconfigured app fails the BUILD (or a runtime startup-validation pass) with a complete diagnostic and ZERO side effects. The runtime failure path (a runner throws, config IO fails) still runs the frozen-order FailureAnalyzer chain and drives context-close. The same executor serves AOT-emitted and runtime-computed plans (no bimodality). When NOT building AOT, the plan is computed at runtime in a dedicated validation pass (same code, same artifact, not checked in).

**Pros:** Best fit for the AOT lineage + §3 compile-vs-runtime keystone, applied to the WHOLE entry point: the run STRUCTURE (app type, factory, initializer/listener/runner/analyzer order, event schedule, refresh waves) is exactly what Spring 7's AOT fork freezes, so the most expensive bootstrap analysis (collection, dedup, @Order sort, app-type deduction, graph validation) moves to build time — dramatically faster/leaner startup and a thin, readable runtime run() executor.; Earliest + richest fail-fast (§2.9, charter §1.7) taken to its limit: the plan validates the whole bootstrap (initializer/runner/analyzer resolvability, app-type unambiguity, context-factory presence, refresh-graph validity, expected-infrastructure-linked) at BUILD time — so the predictable boot failures (missing bean, ambiguous app type, an enabled-starter-that-contributed-nothing) surface as a BUILD error with complete context and ZERO runtime side effects, the purest 'a context that started is a context that works'. The FailureAnalysis vocabulary applies at plan time too.; Directly addresses the cross-crate doc's strongest recommendation (Architecture C / sqlx model is the deterministic, fully platform-independent path including wasm): a build-time cargo-metadata-driven plan SIDESTEPS all three DCE layers AND non-deterministic DCE entirely — the anti-DCE self-check becomes a build-time manifest cross-check (expected-vs-found per declared integration crate) rather than a fragile runtime count, turning the entry point's worst silent-failure trap into a --check-able CI gate.; The frozen RunPlan is INSPECTABLE data (a generated file / dumped artifact): 'what app type, which initializers in what order, what is the event schedule, which beans are eager, what are the waves' is a readable artifact, not emergent runtime behaviour — excellent debuggability/reproducibility (sqlx --check lineage) and a thin-macro story (§2.10: the plan is hand-inspectable code, nothing hidden).; Identical async executor across AOT-emitted and runtime-computed plans means ONE entry-point code path serves both the native-image/optimized build and the dev/JIT build — no bimodality, the substrate swappable per target (the cross-crate doc's identical-runtime-API goal), and wasm/embedded (where link-time discovery fails) get a first-class path.; 'The classpath is the configuration' is realized HONESTLY for Rust: app-type deduction over the resolved Cargo feature graph at plan time is the rust-native analogue of WebApplicationType.deduce() over a classpath — deterministic given the final feature set, with the explicit set_app_type escape hatch as a plan override.

**Cons:** Diverges MOST from Spring's runtime-dynamism mental model and pre-judges the §3 compile-vs-runtime AND metadata/codegen keystones the hardest — presenting a frozen-plan entry point as THE realization risks strongly biasing Phase-2's signal; it must be held strictly as a CANDIDATE, and its value is only as large as the fraction of the bootstrap that can be planned statically (app-type, order, event-schedule yes; runtime env values, IO results, dynamic conditions no).; Requires app-type/initializer-set/condition outcomes to be knowable at plan time, but several are inherently runtime: bind_to_application can FLIP the app type from externalized config (spring.main.web-application-type), config-data can activate profiles that change which initializers/runners apply, and runtime conditions gate participants — so the plan needs a conservative over-approximation plus a runtime re-resolution/fallback, partially reintroducing the dynamism it sought to eliminate, and the bindToApplication-overrides-the-plan case is a direct contradiction to freeze-early.; The dynamic WASM-module 'classpath' source has NO build-time presence, so it can only contribute initializers/runners/listeners through a runtime path — a direct tension with the plan-at-build-time shape (it forces a runtime re-plan or a separate runtime-only lane for dynamically-sourced participants), flagged as a phase2Question, not resolved.; Two computation modes (build-time codegen plan + runtime-computed plan) that must produce IDENTICAL plans, plus the runtime fallback for dynamic participants, is essentially R1/R2's driver anyway — so the plan's payoff is bounded and keeping the two modes coherent (same app type, same order, same event schedule, same waves) is a real coherence burden.; Heaviest cold-path/build-time machinery and the largest conceptual surface (a whole RunPlan IR: app type + factory + four ordered participant sets + event schedule + fused RefreshPlan + env skeleton) — overkill for a small CLI app, and the RunPlan artifact becomes a stable ABI/format commitment that must version cleanly across leaf releases.; The interactive/late knobs of SpringApplication (programmatic setters before run(), withHook test-slicing, AbandonedRunException single-run aborts) are awkward to express against a frozen plan — withHook injects a one-shot listener that the plan didn't anticipate, and a test slice runs a CURATED subset that differs from the planned full set, so the plan needs an explicit 'runtime overlay/override' lane that erodes the frozen-plan simplicity for exactly the test/tooling cases.

**Mechanisms considered:** separate PLAN phase (build-time codegen via leaf-codegen reading cargo metadata + resolved feature set, OR a runtime startup-validation pass) resolving everything statically knowable WITHOUT running side effects (the run-pipeline analogue of refreshForAotProcessing + the AOT pipeline fork); a frozen `RunPlan` artifact: app_type + context_factory + initializer_order + run_listener_order + runner_order + analyzer_order + event_schedule (the fixed named sequence resolved to concrete emission points) + fused refresh_plan + env_skeleton; app-type deduction over the resolved Cargo FEATURE GRAPH at plan time ('the resolved feature graph is the configuration' = the rust-native WebApplicationType.deduce), with an explicit set_app_type plan override; thin async run executor consuming the plan: bootstrap context + registry-initializers (frozen order) → fire Starting → parse Args → resolve env-dependent VALUES + config-data IO + fire EnvironmentPrepared → bind runtime spring.main.* → banner → instantiate frozen ContextFactory → apply initializers (frozen order) → fire ContextInitialized/Prepared → refresh-lifecycle thin plan-executor (wave-parallel) → fire Started+Liveness → await frozen-order Runners → fire Ready+Readiness; whole-bootstrap validation at plan/build time (participant resolvability, app-type unambiguity, factory presence, refresh-graph validity, expected-infrastructure-linked) — fail-fast as a BUILD error, zero runtime side effects; FailureAnalysis vocabulary applied at plan time; conservative over-approximation + runtime re-resolution fallback for bindToApplication-app-type-flip, profile-activated participants, and runtime-conditioned participants the plan can't fully fix; identical executor across AOT-emitted and runtime-computed plans (sqlx --check lineage); plan checked-in + --check-able as the build-time anti-DCE manifest cross-check; explicit runtime overlay/override lane for withHook single-run listeners, AbandonedRunException aborts, and curated test-slice subsets the frozen plan didn't anticipate; Architecture C (build-time codegen) as the substrate — fully platform-independent incl. wasm/embedded, sidestepping all DCE layers

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** This is the realization that confronts 'the classpath is the configuration' WITHOUT a classpath most directly, via the cross-crate doc's most-reliable path (Architecture C, sqlx model). A build.rs / `cargo leaf prepare` in the binary crate reads the resolved dependency graph (cargo metadata) + a manifest convention and emits the RunPlan into OUT_DIR (or a checked-in --check-able artifact), include!'d into the binary — sidestepping Layer 0 (the plan ENUMERATES declared integration crates and emits the force-link references), Layer A (rustc reachability), and Layer B (--gc-sections) ENTIRELY, and being fully platform-independent including wasm/embedded where linkme fails. The anti-DCE self-check becomes a BUILD-TIME manifest cross-check (expected-vs-found per declared crate, --check fails CI on a silently-lost contribution) — strictly more reliable than R1/R2's runtime count, turning the entry point's worst silent-failure trap into a deterministic build gate. App-type deduction is plan-time over the resolved feature graph (the rust-native deduce()), and the four participant orders (initializers/listeners/runners/analyzers) are resolved at plan time so registration/link order is irrelevant (honouring §170: never rely on link order). BUT it cannot scan crates the build doesn't know about: it enumerates DECLARED integration crates via metadata, not a true classpath, and a dynamic WASM-module source has NO build-time presence — it must contribute through a runtime overlay lane (a phase2Question). Origin-agnostic: a declared native crate and a build-known integration crate are planned identically; a runtime-overlay (WASM-module / withHook test injection) participant joins via the same executor but bypasses the plan. The RunPlan format + the run-listener event-name taxonomy + the participant descriptor traits in leaf-core/leaf-boot become a stable ABI/format commitment (must version cleanly). leaf-codegen (proc-macro/build crates isolated from runtime, charter §6) owns the plan emission; leaf-boot owns the executor. CANDIDATES, not a decision throughout — the plan's scope is exactly the fraction of bootstrap that is statically knowable.

**T2 — execution context:** The PLAN phase is SYNCHRONOUS cold-path/build-time work (single-threaded, no IO into the running app, before the binary runs or in a dedicated runtime validation pass) — pure analysis producing the RunPlan + the earliest (build-time) diagnostics. The runtime EXECUTOR is async on the bootstrap task and does only the genuinely-runtime work: config-data file/network IO at the resolve-env-values step (the only runtime loading; structure was planned), instance construction (the refresh-lifecycle thin plan-executor fans out wave-parallel per the frozen RefreshPlan with NO creation guard on the planned path — the strongest §2.5 answer), and Runner await (blocking → spawn_blocking, §2.3). The fixed events fire at the frozen event_schedule's concrete emission points on the bootstrap task — ordered by construction, reactive (§2.4). NO GLOBAL LOCK — only the per-container bring-up guard. PARENT LINKAGE for the startup trace is carried explicitly (the run is the root; planned refresh waves nest under it). CANCELLATION: because the plan validated the graph before any side effect, the runtime abort surface is smaller (only IO/instance/runner failures remain) — a runtime failure runs the frozen-order FailureAnalyzer chain and drives context-close (explicit awaited teardown of what was constructed in reverse wave order; no async Drop). The bindToApplication-app-type-flip and profile-activated-participant cases need a runtime RE-RESOLUTION step on the bootstrap task (cold, sync analysis over the plan + the now-loaded environment) before construction proceeds — an execution-context boundary where the plan is reconciled with runtime reality. The runtime overlay lane (withHook single-run listener, test-slice curated subset, WASM-module participants) runs on the same bootstrap task, joined into the executor's ordered emission. ERRORS: build-time plan validation failures are compile/prepare errors with complete context; runtime failures are a rich RunFailure carrying the failing step + FailureAnalysis + cause-chain. The shutdown hook + ready/availability publication are identical to R1 (a separate cold ctrl-c/SIGTERM task; reactive availability via lifecycle-events).

### Rust clashes
- No spring.factories runtime SPI loading + no runtime classpath. Spring drives the ENTIRE run pipeline by loading RunListeners, Initializers, BootstrapRegistryInitializers, FailureAnalyzers, ContextFactories, and AppType Deducers from spring.factories via SpringFactoriesLoader at runtime — a classpath scan Rust cannot do (no global classpath, no runtime reflection). Every run-participant must instead be collected as a thin origin-agnostic 'static const descriptor from a SCOPED catalog (static link-time registry + optional dynamic source; Phase-2-undecided linkme/codegen/explicit), addressed by ROLE, never a runtime type-scan. This is THE central cross-crate divergence for the entry point, and it inherits the silent-DCE failure mode acutely (a missing participant is silently absent, not a load error).
- No StackWalker main-class deduction. Spring uses StackWalker(RETAIN_CLASS_REFERENCE) to find the main frame for banner/version/AOT-initializer naming. Rust has no runtime stack-class reflection; the primary config + app identity must be passed explicitly (the #[leaf::main] macro / Application::new(PrimaryConfig)) — the deduction is replaced by an explicit, hand-writable handoff (thin macro, §2.10), not an ambient probe.
- 'The classpath is the configuration' has no classpath. Spring deduces servlet/reactive/none by which web jars are on the classpath. Rust's analogue is the resolved CARGO FEATURE GRAPH (an enabled capability/feature expresses intent), but a Cargo feature gates COMPILATION, not LINKAGE — so 'enabled the web starter' can compile the deducer/factory and still leave it unlinked unless the generated app-root force-links the crate. App-type deduction must be a capability-keyed descriptor chain over the resolved feature set + a force-link discipline + the explicit set_app_type escape hatch — and it must resolve to NONE in a core-only binary so no web knowledge leaks into core (charter §1 scope).
- No GC-mopped failed run; no async Drop. Spring's handleRunFailure can rely on GC to clean up a half-built context, and Spring runs synchronously around main. In Rust there is no GC AND no async Drop (nightly doc: AsyncDrop is experimental-incomplete with tokio-shutdown crashes — avoid), so a failed/cancelled run's teardown MUST be the explicit, awaited, container-driven async pass (delegate to refresh-lifecycle's cancelRefresh for a pre-Refreshed failure or context-close for post-Refreshed), with per-bean timeouts + error aggregation — never a Drop, never a forget.
- The standalone early-multicaster + early-listeners-cannot-be-beans. Spring's first four events (Starting/EnvironmentPrepared/ContextInitialized/Prepared) fire BEFORE the context's multicaster/most beans exist, via a standalone SimpleApplicationEventMulticaster, and contextLoaded then hands the application's listeners to the live context's multicaster. This two-multicaster handoff is real and must be ported: early run-listeners are registered on the Application (or via descriptors), NOT discovered as @Beans — leaf must own this early-vs-context dispatch seam (and reconcile it with events/event-multicaster's eventual design, incl. the early-event-buffering concern).
- bind_to_application mutates the driver from its own input. Spring binds spring.main.* (banner-mode, web-application-type, lazy-init, allow-override, keep-alive, register-shutdown-hook) back onto the live SpringApplication instance mid-run, so externalized config overrides programmatic setters called before run(). This 'config rebinds the builder' pattern fights Rust ownership/single-source-of-truth — the run driver must hold the Application in a form it can re-bind a fixed set of typed knobs on between phases, coupling to environment's read/mutate seam and risking a confusing two-source-of-truth if modeled naively.
- Availability is CORE, not actuator, and must be reactive. Spring publishes LivenessState.CORRECT (with Started) and ReadinessState.ACCEPTING_TRAFFIC (with Ready) from the core run listener. In leaf this availability state is consumed by readiness/liveness probes that MUST observe it reactively (a watch/notify on a state transition, §2.4), never busy-poll a flag — and the runners-complete-before-ACCEPTING_TRAFFIC ordering is an execution-context boundary (K8s readiness gating) the async pipeline must honour explicitly.
- The withHook thread-local + AbandonedRunException. Spring's getRunListeners consults a thread-local SpringApplicationHook to inject a single-run RunListener (the mechanism behind test-context bootstrapping / SpringApplication.withHook), and AbandonedRunException short-circuits handleRunFailure (rethrow WITHOUT analysis or close). A thread-local across .await is hazardous in async Rust (the §2.3 ThreadLocal-across-await concern); leaf must carry the single-run hook + the abandon signal as EXPLICIT values threaded through the run (or a task-local with documented semantics), not an ambient thread-local read at an arbitrary await point.
- The run-listener event-name taxonomy + RunPlan/descriptor formats become a cross-crate ABI with no classpath to anchor them. The fixed named event sequence's names, the participant descriptor traits, and (R3) the RunPlan format are agreed by convention within one JVM in Spring; in leaf, downstream/integration crates depend on them, so leaf must PUBLISH them as a versioned public surface (an ABI-ish commitment) — like startup-instrumentation's stable name taxonomy, but for events and participants.
- FailureAnalyzer realizes charter §1.7/§2.9 but cannot use Spring's typed-cause-matching reflection naively. Spring's AbstractFailureAnalyzer<T> matches a specific cause TYPE via generics + reflection. leaf's FailureAnalyzer chain must match on a rust-native error model (downcast over a typed error enum / Any, or pattern-matched cause-chain) — and since the unified error/diagnostics model is a deferred §3 keystone, the analyzer-matching mechanism must stay a candidate, not bake in a specific error representation. The FailureAnalysis(description, action, cause) shape is exactly where the bootstrap layer's complete-context-failure intent lands.

### Interactions
- **refresh-lifecycle** — PRIMARY DOWNSTREAM / the thing run() invokes. The run pipeline's refresh_context() step delegates WHOLLY to refresh-lifecycle's refresh() — the run owns the OUTER orchestration (bootstrap context, environment prep, initializers, the run-listener event sequence, runners, ready signalling) and refresh-lifecycle owns the INNER container bring-up (the fixed phase sequence, no-bean-before-all-processors, freeze boundary, eager fail-fast, ContextRefreshed). The run awaits refresh as one all-or-nothing unit; a refresh failure routes into the run's handle_run_failure (FailureAnalyzer + teardown). The run's ContextInitialized/Prepared events fire BEFORE refresh; ContextRefreshed (+ any ServerInitialized) fire DURING refresh; Started/Ready fire AFTER. The two share the bootstrap-task execution context and the single-container bring-up guard.
- **context-close** — TEARDOWN COLLABORATOR on the failure + shutdown paths. The run arms the shutdown hook (a ctrl-c/SIGTERM task that calls context-close once a RunningContext exists — the registerShutdownHook analogue), and handle_run_failure drives context-close (clean close) for a post-Refreshed failure OR refresh-lifecycle's cancelRefresh (partial teardown, no ContextClosedEvent) for a pre-Refreshed failure. The cancel-vs-close fork that context-close models is exactly the fork the run must choose between on a boot failure. The run never tears down beans itself — it triggers context-close's idempotent (CAS) ordered teardown.
- **runtime-lifecycle** — DOWNSTREAM auto-start + availability. The run does NOT start Lifecycle/SmartLifecycle beans — refresh-lifecycle's finish_refresh auto-starts them by ascending phase. The run fires Started AFTER auto-start completes and publishes Liveness=CORRECT; the runners window then runs; Ready + Readiness=ACCEPTING_TRAFFIC flips last. runtime-lifecycle owns the running-state machine; the run owns the Started/Ready milestones and the availability publication layered on top of it.
- **environment** — DRIVEN in prepare_environment. The run gets-or-creates the one owned Environment, adds the command-line property source, and fires EnvironmentPrepared — the hook where config-data runs. It uses environment's read/mutate seam (ConfigurableEnvironment to mutate during prep, the read view handed to beans after) and is where bind_to_application reads spring.main.* back onto the live Application. The run owns WHEN the environment is prepared/sealed; environment owns the abstraction.
- **config-data** — RUNS AT the EnvironmentPrepared hook (the EnvironmentPostProcessor moment). config-data's deterministic single-pass file/import loading + multi-document activation + precedence assembly executes when the run fires EnvironmentPrepared, populating the property-source stack before the context is created. config-data's early-control-keys (config.name/location/additional-location consumed before files are located) are consumed in this run step. The async file/network IO config-data fences off is awaited here on the bootstrap task.
- **profiles** — ACTIVATED during prepare_environment. The run's configure_environment step activates profiles (the active/include/group/default levers) so the active-profile set is decided UP FRONT — before config-data filters documents (config-data's on-profile document activation) and before the container filters profile-gated beans (the @Profile condition preset). Activation is itself a property (spring.profiles.active), read through the same stack a CLI arg overrides — the environment unification the run sets up.
- **auto-configuration** — ENABLED by the run's primary-config + kill-switch. The run's primary application config is where @EnableAutoConfiguration-analogue wiring attaches; auto-configuration's deferred-batch engine runs INSIDE refresh-lifecycle (after user defs) but the run owns the kill-switch surface (leaf.enable-autoconfiguration via the Environment it prepared) and the starter-as-Cargo-feature mental model + the force-link discipline that makes 'adding a starter' (the classpath-is-configuration intent) actually link the auto-config crate. App-type deduction and auto-config both key off the resolved capability/feature set.
- **events / event-multicaster** — PUBLISHES the fixed named run event sequence — POTENTIAL UNIFICATION TENSION. The run fires Starting/EnvironmentPrepared/ContextInitialized/Prepared (on a STANDALONE early multicaster, before the context's exists) then Started/Ready (on the context's multicaster) — exactly the early-vs-context handoff + early-event-buffering concern refresh-lifecycle and startup-instrumentation also face. Whether the run reuses events/event-multicaster's substrate or uses a distinct lightweight early channel (since early events fire before the bus/most beans exist) is a phase2Question shared with those features.
- **startup-instrumentation** — INSTRUMENTED + provides the root. The whole run is the ROOT startup step/span (leaf.application.run), under which refresh-lifecycle's phases and bean-instantiation nest; the run's named phases (prepare-environment, create-context, refresh, call-runners) are child steps. The run carries parent linkage explicitly into the refresh fan-out (the §2.3 fix). On a boot failure the run tags the in-flight step with the outcome so the recorded trace is a boot-failure forensic — sharing the diagnostics spirit with FailureAnalysis.
- **container-core** — CREATES the context via the engine-vs-facade split. The run's create_context step picks the context type (an origin-agnostic ContextFactory keyed by AppType) — container-core's facade is what the run instantiates and configures (vs the bare engine). The run is the opinionated bootstrap facade SpringApplication is; container-core is the container it wires. prepare_context (set environment, post-process, apply initializers, register arg/banner singletons) operates on container-core's context before refresh.
- **post-processor-spi** — FED by ApplicationContextInitializers. The run's apply_initializers step is where ApplicationContextInitializer-analogues register BFPP-analogues (post-processor-spi's definition-tier processors) and set profiles — AFTER setEnvironment/postProcessContext but BEFORE definitions load and BEFORE refresh runs the processors. The initializer hook is the run's pre-refresh programmatic-tweak slot; post-processor-spi owns the processor contracts those initializers register into.
- **task-execution** — EXECUTION-CONTEXT SOURCE. The run executes on the bootstrap task; the shutdown hook, async runners, and config-data IO use task-execution's executor, and the refresh fan-out (eager-singleton/background-bootstrap waves) runs on the bootstrapExecutor task-execution provides. A blocking runner / context factory must spawn_blocking — explicit execution-context discipline the run documents and threads through (§2.3).

### Open questions for Phase 2
- Is leaf's run pipeline a FIXED async function (R1, predictable single opinionated sequence, intent-faithful, but a new bootstrap step is a core edit) or a re-orderable named-stage DAG (R2, extensible-by-data + shared topo-sort primitive + sort-time event-order enforcement, but weakens the 'cannot accidentally reorder bootstrap' guarantee Spring deliberately chose) or a build-time-frozen RunPlan + thin executor (R3, AOT/sqlx determinism + earliest fail-fast + platform-independent, but pre-judges the compile-vs-runtime keystone hardest and struggles with bindToApplication-app-type-flip + dynamic/test-overlay participants)? This is the run-orchestration shape, downstream of the §3 compile-vs-runtime + metadata/codegen keystones — must stay a candidate.
- Which cross-crate substrate collects the run-participant registries (RunListeners, ContextInitializers, BootstrapRegistryInitializers, Runners, FailureAnalyzers, AppTypeDeducers, ContextFactories)? linkme (zero-cost, DCE-sensitive, no wasm), inventory (DCE-robust, wasm, life-before-main — but registering live run-listeners pre-main is hostile to async), build-time codegen (Architecture C, deterministic, the entry point's natural fit for the force-link + anti-DCE manifest), or explicit with() (Architecture D, the universal escape hatch)? The entry point is the natural HOME for the force-link discipline + the mandated anti-DCE self-check, so this is acute here. Cross-cuts auto-configuration, refresh-lifecycle, and every discovery feature.
- Does the run's fixed named event sequence REUSE leaf's general events/event-multicaster/lifecycle-events substrate, or is it a DISTINCT lightweight channel? The first run events fire BEFORE the context/its multicaster/most beans exist (the standalone early-multicaster + early-event-buffering concern, shared with refresh-lifecycle and startup-instrumentation), and early run-listeners structurally cannot be beans. If unified, the early-emission semantics (buffer vs lose events fired before any listener attaches) and the early-vs-context multicaster handoff must be defined. Belongs to the events meta-design, not this feature.
- What is the unified error/diagnostics model that FailureAnalysis/FailureAnalyzer realizes (the charter §1.7/§2.9 keystone)? The FailureAnalysis(description, action, cause) shape + the analyzer-chain-matches-on-cause-type mechanism are where the bootstrap layer's complete-context-failure intent lands, but the analyzer-matching mechanism (downcast over a typed error enum vs Any vs pattern-matched cause-chain) depends on the deferred unified error model. Cross-cuts condition-report, startup-instrumentation, and every feature that fails with context.
- How is 'the classpath is the configuration' (app-type deduction + starter-as-feature) resolved given Cargo features gate compilation not linkage, and is dependency-based auto-configuration (the deferred §3 keystone) the mechanism? App-type deduction over the resolved feature graph, the force-link discipline, and the kill-switch all hinge on whether 'a starter's presence' maps onto Cargo features + force-link or something richer. Cross-cuts auto-configuration and the cross-crate composition keystone.
- How is bindToApplication (externalized spring.main.* config overriding programmatic builder setters mid-run) modeled without a confusing two-source-of-truth, against Rust ownership? This 'config rebinds the live builder' pattern needs a clean realization (a typed knob set re-bound between phases vs a precedence-resolved single source) and couples to environment's read/mutate seam — the resolution affects the run driver's shape.
- How are the thread-local withHook single-run listener + AbandonedRunException carried across .await without an ambient thread-local read at an arbitrary suspension point (the §2.3 ThreadLocal-across-await hazard)? Test-context bootstrapping + test slicing depend on this; the answer (explicit threaded value vs documented task-local) is downstream of the deferred async-context-propagation model. Cross-cuts the testing story and task-execution.
- Does a dynamic (WASM-module / runtime) participant source contribute run-participants (initializers, listeners, runners, analyzers, deducers) and at what timing relative to the run sequence — especially under R3 where dynamically-sourced participants have no build-time presence and need a runtime overlay lane that erodes the frozen plan? The two-source duality (static link-time + optional dynamic) applies to the entry point's participants exactly as it does to definitions; the timing/overlay semantics are unresolved. Cross-cuts refresh-lifecycle and auto-configuration's same duality.
- How much of the SpringApplication surface is even rust-native intent vs JVM-shaped scaffolding to be designed OUT? Candidates to question: the banner (a print-a-figlet step), the headless-property analogue, the bootstrap-context-promotion-into-context mechanic, and the two-multicaster split — each must be judged against intent-parity (does leaf NEED it, or does a rust-native design make it unnecessary, per charter §2.2). Belongs to the per-feature Phase-3 re-unify, but flagged so it isn't ported blindly.

### Notes
Scope boundary honoured: this feature is the OUTER run orchestration (the SpringApplication.run analogue, charter §6 leaf-boot), strictly above and delegating to refresh-lifecycle (container bring-up), context-close (teardown/shutdown-hook), runtime-lifecycle (auto-start/availability), environment+config-data+profiles (prepare-environment), auto-configuration (deferred batch inside refresh), and events (the fixed named sequence). It owns ONLY: the ordered run() sequence + the run-listener event taxonomy + the standalone early multicaster, the transient BootstrapContext/registry + promotion, ApplicationContextInitializers, the Runner family + the after-refresh-before-ready window, bind_to_application, the banner, AvailabilityState publication as CORE, the withHook/Abandoned single-run + test-slice hooks, app-type deduction + ContextFactory selection, and FailureAnalysis/FailureAnalyzer (the marquee charter §1.7/§2.9 surface). All three realizations stay implementation-agnostic and hold the deferred §3 keystones (metadata/codegen boundary, compile-vs-runtime split, dependency-based auto-config, unified error/diagnostics model, cross-crate composition substrate, async-context-propagation) as CANDIDATES — R1 leans intent-faithful/fixed, R2 leans unify-via-DAG, R3 leans AOT/build-time-frozen, deliberately spanning the compile-vs-runtime axis so Phase 2's signal stays unbiased. Provider/registry abstractions kept ORIGIN-AGNOSTIC throughout (a native, WASM-module, or test-double run-participant participates identically). Grounding fully cross-checked: spring-boot-4-di-design.md §238-321 (the run sequence, app-type deduce() SPI v4.0.1, ContextFactory, prepareEnvironment order + bindToApplication, the run-listener event sequence + standalone early multicaster + availability-as-core, ApplicationContextInitializer, prepareContext, bootstrap context v4 package move, banner, Runner single-ordered-stream, FailureAnalyzer + AbandonedRunException + withHook + StackWalker + the AOT pipeline fork); the four Phase-1 upstream docs (refresh-lifecycle R1/R2/R3, context-close R1/R2/R3, runtime-lifecycle, startup-instrumentation R1/R2/R3, environment, config-data, profiles, auto-configuration R1); the nightly envelope (AsyncDrop avoid → explicit awaited teardown; AFIT/RPITIT not dyn-safe → boxed futures at the dyn edge; inventory/linkme tradeoffs; no async-context primitives); and the cross-crate doc (the three DCE layers, the force-link/anti-DCE-self-check mandate, Architectures A-D, §170 ordering-as-data, the charter §6 leaf-core/leaf-boot/leaf-macros/leaf-codegen topology). Notable tension to flag for Phase 3: the early-event multicaster handoff + the bindToApplication rebind + the withHook thread-local are the three JVM-shaped mechanics most at risk of being ported blindly — each must be re-judged for rust-native necessity. The FailureAnalysis surface is the single highest-leverage place for charter §1.7's complete-context-failure promise and deserves first-class attention in the unified diagnostics meta-design.

## Application Type Deduction  `[application-type-deduction]`

leaf's rust-native realization of Spring Boot's WebApplicationType.deduce() (spring-boot-4-di-design.md §246-254, "Classpath-driven application type deduction") — the bootstrap step that decides WHAT KIND of application this binary is (Spring's SERVLET / REACTIVE / NONE) so the rest of the pipeline can wire the matching context, environment seeding, and conditionally-gated beans. Spring's load-bearing principle is "the classpath is the configuration": adding spring-boot-starter-web makes it servlet, adding webflux makes it reactive, neither makes it plain — dependency choice EXPRESSES intent, with setWebApplicationType()/setApplicationContextFactory() as explicit escape hatches. Spring v4/v7 modularized this: deduce() loads WebApplicationType.Deducer SPI impls via SpringFactoriesLoader (WebMvcWebApplicationTypeDeducer in spring-boot-webmvc, WebFluxWebApplicationTypeDeducer in spring-boot-webflux), each checking for specific classes (jakarta.servlet.Servlet+DispatcherServlet → SERVLET; reactor Mono+DispatcherHandler → REACTIVE), first match wins, core enum fallback else NONE — so core spring-boot no longer hard-codes WebFlux/WebMvc knowledge. The deduced type then drives ApplicationContextFactory selection (§254, also supplies the matching Environment type) and is read by @ConditionalOnWebApplication(SERVLET/REACTIVE)/OnNotWebApplication to gate auto-config. The intent leaf must replicate WITHOUT a JVM lineage: there is no runtime classpath, no SpringFactoriesLoader SPI scan, no class-presence probe, no global reflection. The rust-native analogue of "the classpath is the configuration" is "the resolved Cargo capability/feature graph is the configuration" — an enabled integration crate / cargo feature expresses servlet/reactive/none-equivalent intent. This feature is a NARROW sub-step of the run-pipeline's create_context() (spring-application-run R1 step 8): it produces the AppType/Flavor value that (a) the EnvironmentConverter feature [02-configuration-environment.md extra-15] consumes to pick which FlavorSeeder seeds the environment, (b) the ContextFactory chain consumes to pick the context type, and (c) condition-family's OnWebApplication consumes to gate beans. It owns ONLY: the AppType/Flavor vocabulary (open, NOT a closed servlet/reactive enum — core knows NONE/Plain, integrations contribute the rest so no web knowledge leaks into core per charter §1 scope), the origin-agnostic Deducer descriptor chain over enabled capabilities, the first-match-wins resolution with a NONE fallback, the explicit set_app_type escape hatch (setWebApplicationType analogue), and the bind-back hook letting leaf.main.app-type / leaf.main.web-application-type override the deduction from externalized config (the bindToApplication edge, §260). It must honor the silent-DCE hazard acutely: unlike Spring's classpath probe which always sees a present class, a leaf deducer in a crate the binary never force-links is SILENTLY ABSENT (Layer 0), so a missing deducer silently picks the wrong app type — mandating the anti-DCE self-check and a rich "deduced X but no provider for X registered — did you add AND force-link leaf-web?" diagnostic (charter §1.7/§2.9). It must NOT decide leaf's meta-architecture (Phase 2's job): the compile-vs-runtime split for the deduction, the cross-crate substrate (linkme/codegen/explicit), and whether this unifies with the condition/capability substrate stay CANDIDATES.

### Candidate realizations

#### R1 — Runtime origin-agnostic Deducer descriptor chain: first-match-wins over enabled-capability descriptors, NONE fallback, explicit set_app_type + config bind-back overrides
The most literal rust-native port of WebApplicationType.deduce()'s v4 SPI shape. AppType is an OPEN value (not a closed enum): the core kernel knows exactly one variant — AppType::None (the Plain analogue) — and every other variant (Servlet-analogue, Reactive-analogue, a WASM-host flavor, custom deployment flavors) is contributed by an integration crate as data, so NO web/servlet/reactive knowledge lives in core (charter §1 scope). Concretely AppType is a small stable identity (an interned capability-key / &'static str or u64 hash) plus optional metadata, NOT a Rust enum the core must enumerate — this is exactly the open Flavor descriptor the EnvironmentConverter feature [extra-15] already posits. Deduction is a chain of origin-agnostic `Deducer` descriptors: `struct DeducerDescriptor { app_type: AppTypeKey, order: Order, applies: fn(&CapabilitySet) -> bool }` (or a thin `trait Deducer { fn deduce(&self, caps: &CapabilitySet) -> Option<AppTypeKey> }` at the dyn edge). Each integration crate that wants to claim a flavor registers ONE deducer descriptor through the SAME origin-agnostic catalog substrate the rest of leaf uses (Phase-2-undecided: linkme distributed-slice / build.rs codegen / explicit with()), addressed by ROLE (deducer), never a runtime type-scan.
