The run-pipeline's create_context step (before prepareEnvironment finalizes, or as the very first sub-step of prepare_environment so the provisional Flavor is known — see extra-15's deduce-flavor-first R3) calls `deduce(&capabilities)`: it sorts the registered deducer descriptors by Order, calls each in turn against a CapabilitySet (the resolved set of compiled-in capabilities — see T1), and the FIRST that returns Some(AppTypeKey) wins; if none match, the result is AppType::None — a literal mirror of Spring's 'first Deducer match wins, else NONE'. The CapabilitySet is the rust-native answer to 'the classpath': it is the set of capability markers contributed by force-linked integration crates (a servlet-analogue crate contributes a 'web.servlet' capability marker AND a deducer that claims Servlet when that marker is present). Two explicit override edges preserve Spring's escape hatches: (1) `app.set_app_type(AppType::Reactive)` — the programmatic setWebApplicationType analogue, set on the Application before run(); (2) the config bind-back — after config-data loads (the bindToApplication moment, §260), leaf.main.app-type / leaf.main.web-application-type is read and OVERRIDES both the deduction and the programmatic setter (config wins as the last write, per extra-15's two-phase deduce-then-rebind). The deduced AppType flows to exactly three consumers: the FlavorSeeder/EnvironmentFactory selection (extra-15), the ContextFactory chain (run-pipeline create_context), and condition-family's OnWebApplication. A self-check runs immediately after deduction: if the deduced/overridden AppType has NO registered FlavorSeeder/ContextFactory provider, fail fast with a rich diagnostic naming the type, the capability that triggered it, and the likely cause (a flavor crate added but not force-linked). The thin macro story: the integration crate ships `register_deducer!(ServletDeducer)` / a capability-marker macro emitting one const descriptor; nothing hidden, hand-writable as an explicit `with_deducer(...)` on the Application builder.

**Pros:** Highest intent fidelity to Spring v4's modular deduce(): a first-match-wins ordered Deducer chain over capabilities maps 1:1 onto WebApplicationType.deduce()'s 'load Deducer SPIs, first non-null wins, else NONE', and core stays free of web/servlet/reactive knowledge exactly as Spring's v4 modularization intended (the whole point of the §250 change) — so `cargo expand` / a startup trace reads like Spring's deduction, serving DX #1 and intent-not-mechanism parity (§2.2).; AppType-as-open-key (not a closed core enum) is the clean charter §1-scope answer: core knows only None, every flavor is a contributed descriptor, so a third-party or WASM-host deployment flavor participates IDENTICALLY to a native servlet/reactive one (origin-agnostic), and no ecosystem concern leaks into the kernel — directly matching the EnvironmentConverter feature's already-posited open Flavor value (charter §1, §11 unification).; Minimal new machinery and maximal reuse: a Deducer is the SAME thin origin-agnostic const-descriptor shape every other run-participant uses (run-listeners, initializers, context-factories), addressed by role — so this feature adds only an AppTypeKey vocabulary + a Deducer descriptor trait + a first-match resolution, riding the one catalog substrate (charter §11).; Entirely a cold-path synchronous query (T2): deduction is a pure in-memory fold over const descriptors with no IO, no .await, no allocation beyond the result — it runs once in the bootstrap window before the environment is shared, so it imposes zero hot-path or concurrency cost (charter §2.3, overhead #2).; The two override edges (set_app_type + config bind-back) land Spring's setWebApplicationType + bindToApplication(spring.main.web-application-type) escape hatches cleanly and make config-overrides-deduction a single last-write rule, integrating with extra-15's deduce-then-rebind two-phase flow without re-running deduction.; The self-check is the natural §1.7/§2.9 home for the silent-DCE trap: 'deduced Servlet (triggered by capability web.servlet from leaf-servlet) but no FlavorSeeder/ContextFactory for Servlet is registered — leaf-servlet may be in Cargo.toml but not force-linked' is a complete, actionable diagnostic at exactly the point a missing deducer would otherwise silently mis-deduce.

**Cons:** Inherits the silent-DCE hazard acutely and QUIETLY: a deducer in a crate the binary never path-references is silently absent (Layer 0), so the binary silently deduces a WRONG (usually None/Plain) app type with no error UNTIL the self-check fires — and the self-check can only catch the case where the deduced type lacks a downstream provider, NOT the case where the RIGHT deducer never ran and a lower-precedence (or fallback NONE) deducer won instead. A 'why did my web app boot as Plain' failure is among the quietest in the whole framework (cross-crate doc Layer 0; charter §1.7).; 'First-match-wins by Order' reintroduces an ordering-sensitivity the cross-crate doc warns against (§154: registration/link order is unspecified, never rely on it). The Order MUST be explicit data on each descriptor and resolved by sort, never by link/section order — but two deducers claiming incompatible types at the SAME order is an ambiguity this realization must detect and fail on (Spring sidesteps this because its two deducers check disjoint classes), adding an ambiguity-resolution rule Spring never needed.; The CapabilitySet abstraction ('what is compiled in') is itself underspecified here and pushes the hard question downstream: is a capability a cargo feature (cfg-gated, but cfg gates compilation not linkage — cross-crate doc §201), a force-linked marker descriptor, or a runtime-registered flag? R1 says 'capability markers from force-linked crates' but that just relocates the Layer-0 problem into the CapabilitySet's own population (a capability marker in an unlinked crate is equally absent).; Two override edges + a deduction = three sources of truth for 'what app type is this' (deducer chain, programmatic setter, config bind-back), with a precedence rule (config > setter > deduction) the run driver must apply at the right phase; mis-sequencing it (e.g. reading config-bound app-type before config-data has loaded) silently uses a stale value — the same mutate-the-driver-from-its-own-input tension bindToApplication has (rustClash).; The dyn-edge Deducer (`fn(&CapabilitySet) -> Option<AppTypeKey>`) or boxed trait is fine, but a deducer that wants to inspect RICH capability facts (e.g. 'reactive present AND servlet present → ambiguous, prefer reactive') needs a richer CapabilitySet API than a flat presence set — and defining that API risks baking servlet/reactive-shaped assumptions into the CapabilitySet contract the core owns, against §1 scope.; Provides no build-time validation: a misconfigured app (ambiguous deduction, deduced type with no provider) fails at the runtime startup self-check, not at build — weaker than R3's build-time fail-fast for the charter §1.7 'as early as the richest diagnostic allows' goal (though still a clean startup diagnostic, not a runtime crash).

**Mechanisms considered:** open AppTypeKey value (interned &'static str / u64 hash + metadata) with ONLY AppType::None known to core; all other flavors contributed as descriptors — the open Flavor value extra-15 already posits; origin-agnostic Deducer descriptor: `struct DeducerDescriptor { app_type: AppTypeKey, order: Order, applies: fn(&CapabilitySet)->bool }` or a thin boxed `trait Deducer` at the dyn edge, collected from the one catalog substrate (linkme/codegen/explicit — Phase-2-undecided); CapabilitySet = the resolved set of compiled-in capability markers from force-linked integration crates (the rust-native 'classpath'); a servlet-analogue crate contributes both a 'web.servlet' marker and a deducer claiming Servlet when present; first-match-wins resolution: sort deducers by explicit Order, call each against the CapabilitySet, first Some(AppTypeKey) wins, else AppType::None — literal mirror of WebApplicationType.deduce(); explicit set_app_type(AppType) programmatic escape hatch (setWebApplicationType analogue) on the Application builder; config bind-back override: leaf.main.app-type / leaf.main.web-application-type read after config-data loads (bindToApplication moment §260) overrides both deduction and programmatic setter (config = last write wins); post-deduction self-check: deduced/overridden type with no registered FlavorSeeder/ContextFactory/EnvironmentFactory provider → rich fail-fast diagnostic naming type + triggering capability + likely force-link cause; thin register_deducer!(Concrete) / capability-marker macro emitting one const descriptor; hand-writable with_deducer(...) on the builder as the explicit escape hatch; ambiguity rule: two deducers claiming incompatible types at the same Order → detect + fail (an ambiguity Spring's disjoint-class deducers never hit)

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** This is THE feature where 'the classpath is the configuration' confronts Rust's no-classpath reality head-on. The Deducer descriptors are cross-crate contributions: leaf-core/leaf-boot defines the AppTypeKey vocabulary, the Deducer descriptor trait, and the CapabilitySet contract; integration crates (leaf-servlet-analogue, leaf-reactive-analogue, a WASM-host crate) depend only on leaf-core/leaf-boot and each register ONE deducer + ONE capability marker via the Phase-2-undecided catalog substrate (linkme distributed-slice = the static link-time 'classpath' default; optional dynamic dir-scanned WASM source = the loadable 'classpath' from the wasm-modules exploration; or build.rs codegen; or explicit with() — Architectures A-D). This INHERITS the full DCE story acutely and QUIETLY (cross-crate doc Layer 0/A/B): a deducer or capability marker in a crate the binary never force-links is silently absent, so the binary silently deduces the wrong app type — a missing deducer is QUIETER than a missing bean (no resolution crash, just a silently-wrong Flavor), so this feature MANDATES the anti-DCE self-check (expected-vs-found per declared integration crate; warn on an enabled-feature-zero-contributions) and is a natural input to 'leaf doctor'/the startup report. The Cargo-feature-as-starter mapping bites exactly here: a cargo feature gates COMPILATION not LINKAGE (cross-crate doc §201), so 'enabled the web feature' compiles the deducer+marker and still leaves them unlinked unless the generated app-root (#[leaf::main]/scan!) emits `use leaf_servlet as _;` — cfg gates compilation, the force-link prelude gates linkage. CRUCIAL T1 subtlety from the cross-crate doc §50: `cfg!(feature=...)`/`#[cfg]` reflect the HOST config, while CARGO_CFG_*/CARGO_FEATURE_* (readable in build.rs) reflect the TARGET — so a runtime `cfg!`-based deduction is a cross-compilation footgun; the capability set must be populated by force-linked markers (link-time truth) or by build.rs reading CARGO_FEATURE_*, not by host-`cfg!`. The AppTypeKey vocabulary + the Deducer descriptor trait + the CapabilitySet contract become a STABLE cross-crate ABI (ABI-ish, like the run-listener event-name taxonomy) that downstream crates hard-code paths to, so leaf must publish them as a versioned minimal surface emitted with absolute paths by the thin macros. Generics can't carry a 'static descriptor → the macro hard-errors with register_deducer!(Concrete). Deduction is documented to differ between `cargo build -p` and `--workspace` (the resolved feature set differs) — the same -p-vs-workspace caveat extra-15 flags. Origin-agnostic throughout: a native, build-known, or WASM-module-contributed deducer participates identically.

**T2 — execution context:** Entirely a COLD-PATH synchronous query on the bootstrap task, run ONCE in the bootstrap window — before the environment is Arc-shared, before any eager singleton, before refresh. deduce(&caps) is a pure in-memory fold over const descriptors: no IO, no .await, no blocking, minimal allocation (only the AppTypeKey result). It runs at the head of (or just before) prepare_environment so the provisional Flavor is known when the environment is seeded (extra-15's Phase A deduce-first), and the config bind-back override runs at the TAIL of prepare_environment after config-data's async IO has joined back (extra-15's Phase B) — both synchronous, both pre-context, neither on a hot path. A Deducer's applies() fn MUST NOT block or do IO (it only inspects the in-memory CapabilitySet); any IO-backed capability detection (e.g. a WASM-host directory scan contributing a flavor) must already be a resolved fact in the CapabilitySet by deduction time, so the single async/sync boundary (the WASM scan) is crossed exactly once, explicitly, BEFORE deduction — never inside applies(). NO global lock (charter §2.5): the deduction reads an immutable descriptor set and writes the result into the bootstrap-owned (not yet shared) Application state. Cancellation is trivial (aborting the bootstrap drops everything; nothing constructed yet). Errors (ambiguous deduction, deduced type with no provider) propagate as a rich bootstrap-failure diagnostic, fail-fast (charter §1.7). The deduced AppType is then read by three downstream consumers on the same bootstrap task (FlavorSeeder selection, ContextFactory selection, OnWebApplication condition evaluation during refresh) — it must be FINAL before condition evaluation begins (extra-15 interaction: flavor must be queryable before any OnWebApplication condition runs).

#### R2 — App-type as a precedence-ranked capability projection unified with the condition/capability substrate: deduction is a pure query over the SAME CapabilitySet that OnWebApplication/OnFeature read, resolved by a ranked rule table
Question whether deduction needs its own bespoke Deducer-chain mechanism at all. condition-family already posits that OnWebApplication 'probes a capability set' and OnFeature/OnClass-analogue reads 'a capability set for OnFeature' (03-conditions-auto-configuration.md line 316); auto-configuration keys off 'the resolved capability/feature set'. So UNIFY: there is ONE authoritative CapabilitySet for the binary (the rust-native 'classpath' — the resolved set of compiled-in, force-linked capability markers), and app-type deduction becomes a PURE PROJECTION of that set, not a separate SPI. The deduction is expressed as ranked DATA: a set of `AppTypeRule { app_type: AppTypeKey, requires: &[CapabilityKey], rank: i32 }` contributions the engine evaluates by (1) filtering to rules whose required capabilities are ALL present in the CapabilitySet, (2) picking the highest-rank survivor, (3) AppType::None if none survive. This is strictly more declarative than R1's imperative Deducer fns: a rule is pure data (no fn pointer), so it is inspectable, AOT-friendly, and the ambiguity case (two rules at the same rank both satisfied) is a sort-time/eval-time DETECTABLE conflict with a rich diagnostic naming both rules and the shared capabilities — rather than R1's opaque first-match-wins where the winner depends on registration Order. Because deduction and OnWebApplication now read the SAME CapabilitySet and the SAME AppType result, there is ONE source of truth: OnWebApplication(Servlet) is literally 'deduced AppType == Servlet' (or 'capability web.servlet present', depending on the Phase-2 condition-strategy blend), eliminating the risk that the condition and the deduction disagree about what kind of app this is. Integration crates contribute (a) capability markers into the CapabilitySet and (b) AppTypeRules claiming a flavor — both as data, through the one catalog substrate. The escape hatches are modeled as the highest-rank rules: set_app_type(Reactive) injects a rank=MAX rule with no requirements (always wins); the config bind-back (leaf.main.app-type) injects an even-higher-rank rule after config loads. So the override precedence (config > programmatic > deduced) is encoded as RANK, not as imperative override branches — uniform with the rule evaluation. The CapabilitySet contract is shared with condition-family/auto-configuration (a single capability-facet design Phase 2 owns), so app-type deduction adds only the AppTypeKey vocabulary + the AppTypeRule shape + the ranked-projection evaluator, riding the shared capability substrate maximally (charter §11).

**Pros:** Maximal unification (charter §11): app-type deduction, OnWebApplication, OnFeature/OnClass-analogue, and auto-configuration's starter-keying ALL read ONE authoritative CapabilitySet, and the deduced AppType is a pure projection of it — so the condition and the deduction CANNOT disagree about 'what kind of app this is' (R1's two-source-of-truth risk is structurally eliminated), and Phase 2 designs the capability substrate ONCE for the whole bootstrap (the unification dividend the charter exists to capture).; Deduction-as-data (ranked AppTypeRules, no fn pointers) is inspectable and AOT-friendly: 'which rules, what capabilities, what ranks, which survived' is readable data, not emergent fn-pointer behaviour — excellent for a startup report / leaf doctor, and it makes the ambiguity case a DETECTABLE eval-time conflict (two satisfied rules at the same rank → rich 'both Servlet-rule and Reactive-rule satisfied at rank 0, sharing no disambiguator' diagnostic) rather than R1's link-order-dependent silent first-match (charter §1.7, §2.10).; Override precedence as RANK is uniform and free of imperative branches: set_app_type = a rank-MAX rule, config bind-back = a rank-MAX+1 rule, deduced rules = rank 0 — so config > programmatic > deduced falls out of the same evaluator with no special-cased override sequencing (cleaner than R1's three-source precedence applied by hand), and the winning rule's provenance ('app type Reactive set by leaf.main.app-type in application.yaml:7') is a precise diagnostic.; Pure-data rules with no fn pointers carry naturally across the cross-crate boundary and are the cleanest fit for build-time freezing (composes with R3): a rule is a const struct of keys + an int, so it can be linkme-collected, codegen-emitted, or explicit — and it can migrate to a future compile-time global-registration without an fn-pointer ABI commitment (cross-crate doc §163).; Cold-path pure query (T2) like R1, but even cheaper and lock-free: a filter+max over const rule data, no fn calls, no dyn dispatch — trivially correct, trivially cancellable, zero hot-path cost (charter §2.3, §2.5, overhead #2).; Keeps core §1-scope-clean identically to R1: core knows only AppType::None and the CapabilityKey vocabulary; servlet/reactive rules + their capability markers are entirely contributed, so no web knowledge in the kernel.

**Cons:** Pre-judges/leans-on the condition-strategy AND capability-substrate keystones (charter §3): unifying deduction with OnWebApplication on a shared CapabilitySet presumes that capability substrate exists and is shaped a certain way (a flat presence set vs a richer facet model) — but condition-family explicitly defers HOW OnWebApplication is reframed (cfg/feature vs runtime flag, line 385) and whether the conditional strategy is cfg vs codegen vs runtime (charter §3). Presenting deduction as a projection of that set risks biasing those calls; it must stay strictly a CANDIDATE.; A flat 'all required capabilities present, highest rank wins' rule model may be too weak for real disambiguation: Spring's deducers check DISJOINT class sets (servlet needs DispatcherServlet, reactive needs DispatcherHandler) so they never both match — but if a binary force-links BOTH a servlet and reactive analogue (plausible in Rust where features union, cross-crate doc §194), both rules are satisfied and rank alone must break the tie, requiring authors to assign correct global ranks across independently-developed crates (a cross-crate ranking coordination problem Spring's disjoint checks avoid).; Ranks as the override mechanism collapse two different concepts (deduction precedence among flavors vs override authority of config/programmatic setters) onto ONE integer axis — workable, but it means a third-party flavor crate could accidentally choose a rank colliding with or exceeding the reserved override ranks, silently beating set_app_type; the rank namespace must be partitioned/reserved (a contract authors must respect), a footgun R1's explicit override branches avoid.; Loses R1's literal 1:1 mapping to Spring's deduce() SPI: Spring authors write a Deducer with imperative class-presence logic; an AppTypeRule is a more abstract 'these capabilities → this type at this rank', so the mental-model parity is slightly lower for someone porting a Spring deducer (intent parity preserved, mechanism parity reduced — acceptable per §2.2 but a teachability cost).; The shared CapabilitySet becomes a wide, heavily-depended-on cross-crate contract (deduction + every condition + auto-config all read it), so its ABI stability and capability-key namespace governance are higher-stakes than R1's deducer-only surface — a change to the capability model ripples across more features.; If the Phase-2 conditional strategy turns out to be cfg/compile-time for OnWebApplication (line 311/385 hint this is likely for the OnClass-analogue), then 'OnWebApplication == deduced AppType == projection of a RUNTIME CapabilitySet' may be a layer mismatch — the condition wants a compile-time fact while deduction-with-config-override is inherently runtime, so the unification may not hold cleanly across the compile/runtime seam (a tension this realization must flag, not resolve).

**Mechanisms considered:** ONE authoritative CapabilitySet for the binary (the rust-native 'classpath') shared by deduction, OnWebApplication, OnFeature, and auto-configuration's starter-keying (unify with condition-family line 316's 'capability set for OnFeature'); app-type deduction as a PURE PROJECTION of the CapabilitySet, not a separate SPI: AppTypeRule { app_type: AppTypeKey, requires: &[CapabilityKey], rank: i32 } evaluated by filter-all-present then highest-rank, else None; deduction-as-data (no fn pointers) for inspectability + AOT-friendliness + ambiguity detection (two satisfied rules at same rank → rich conflict diagnostic naming both); escape hatches as ranked rules: set_app_type = rank-MAX no-requirement rule; config bind-back (leaf.main.app-type) = rank-MAX+1 rule — config > programmatic > deduced encoded as rank, not imperative branches; OnWebApplication(Servlet) reframed as 'deduced AppType == Servlet' (or 'capability web.servlet present') — ONE source of truth shared with condition-family, eliminating condition/deduction disagreement; shared CapabilitySet contract owned by Phase 2 (the capability-facet/conditional-strategy keystone); this feature adds only AppTypeKey vocabulary + AppTypeRule shape + ranked-projection evaluator; reserved/partitioned rank namespace so contributed flavor rules cannot collide with the override ranks; rules collected as const data via the one catalog substrate (linkme/codegen/explicit), migratable to future compile-time global-registration without an fn-pointer ABI

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** Shares R1's force-link/anti-DCE story but UNIFIES the discovery surface: instead of a deducer-only registry, there is ONE CapabilitySet populated by force-linked capability markers (the rust-native classpath) that deduction, OnWebApplication, OnFeature, and auto-configuration all read — so the cross-crate composition substrate (Phase-2-undecided: linkme/codegen/explicit) is exercised once for the whole bootstrap, and the anti-DCE self-check is shared (a crate whose capability marker silently didn't link is invisible to deduction AND to every condition that reads it — so the self-check that catches it serves all consumers). AppTypeRules are pure const data (keys + an int, NO fn pointers), which is the cleanest cross-crate shape: linkme-collectable, codegen-emittable, explicitly-registerable, and migratable to a future compiler-native #[global_registration] without an fn-pointer ABI commitment (cross-crate doc §163). The same cfg-gates-compilation-not-linkage trap (§201) and the host-`cfg!`-vs-target-CARGO_CFG hazard (§50) apply identically: a capability marker compiled-but-unlinked is absent, so the force-link prelude (#[leaf::main] emitting `use leaf_servlet as _;`) and the build.rs/CARGO_FEATURE_* path (not host `cfg!`) are mandatory. The shared CapabilitySet + AppTypeKey + CapabilityKey vocabulary + AppTypeRule shape become a STABLE, WIDE cross-crate ABI depended on by more features than R1's deducer trait, so its versioning/namespace governance is higher-stakes (a §3 capability-substrate keystone Phase 2 owns). -p-vs-workspace deduction caveat (resolved feature set differs) applies. Origin-agnostic: native, build-known, or WASM-module capability markers/rules participate identically; a WASM-host dynamic 'classpath' scan contributes capability markers into the same set (timing wrinkle = a phase2Question shared with extra-15).

**T2 — execution context:** Identical cold-path discipline to R1, even cheaper and fully lock-free: deduction is a pure filter+max over const rule data against the immutable CapabilitySet — no fn calls, no dyn dispatch, no IO, no .await, no allocation beyond the result — run ONCE in the bootstrap window before the environment is shared. The CapabilitySet itself must be FULLY POPULATED before deduction (all force-linked markers present at link time; any dynamic WASM-host markers joined in via a clearly-fenced cold startup scan that crosses the async/sync boundary exactly once, before deduction) — this populate-then-query ordering is the key T2 constraint, shared with every condition that reads the set. Provisional deduction runs at the head of prepare_environment (extra-15 Phase A); the config bind-back rule is injected and re-evaluated at the tail after config-data IO joins back (Phase B) — both synchronous, both pre-context. NO global lock (§2.5): immutable read of rules + capabilities, write the result into bootstrap-owned (unshared) state. The deduced AppType must be FINAL before refresh, because OnWebApplication conditions read it (or read the same CapabilitySet) during refresh on the same bootstrap task — so the evaluator runs strictly before condition evaluation begins. Cancellation trivial (nothing constructed). Errors (same-rank ambiguity, deduced type with no provider) fail fast with a rich diagnostic (charter §1.7). Because rules are pure data, the whole evaluation could equally run at build time (composes with R3) — the runtime execution context is just the not-yet-AOT path.

#### R3 — Build-time-frozen AppType resolved from the resolved Cargo feature/dependency graph: a build.rs / cargo-metadata pass computes the AppType once and freezes it (+ the force-link prelude + an anti-DCE manifest), runtime just reads the const
Push the AOT lineage and the cross-crate doc's most-reliable path (Architecture C / sqlx model) hardest, applied to deduction specifically. The realization that confronts 'the classpath is the configuration' WITHOUT a classpath most directly: since the deduction is a pure function of WHAT IS COMPILED IN, and what-is-compiled-in is knowable at BUILD TIME from the resolved Cargo dependency/feature graph, compute the AppType ONCE at build time and freeze it as a const. A build.rs (or a `cargo leaf prepare` step) in the binary crate reads the resolved dependency graph (cargo metadata) + the resolved feature set (CARGO_FEATURE_* / CARGO_CFG_* — the TARGET config, NOT host `cfg!`, per cross-crate doc §50) and a manifest convention declaring which integration crates claim which flavor. It resolves the AppType deterministically (servlet-analogue crate present → Servlet; reactive-analogue present → Reactive; both → an explicit declared tiebreak or a build ERROR; neither → None) and emits, into OUT_DIR (include!'d into the binary): (1) `const DEDUCED_APP_TYPE: AppType = ...` — the frozen result; (2) the force-link prelude `use leaf_servlet as _;` for every flavor crate it found (sidestepping Layer 0 ENTIRELY — the deduction and the force-link are computed from the SAME graph walk, so they cannot disagree); (3) an anti-DCE manifest (expected capability markers per declared crate) for a --check-able CI gate. The runtime 'deduction' is then a trivial read of DEDUCED_APP_TYPE — no descriptors, no chain, no CapabilitySet query, no runtime cost. Validation moves EARLIEST: an ambiguous app type (two flavor crates, no declared tiebreak), a declared-but-not-resolvable flavor, or an enabled-feature-zero-contributions situation fails the BUILD (or a `--check` gate) with a complete diagnostic and ZERO runtime side effects — the purest charter §1.7 'fail as early as the richest diagnostic allows'. The escape hatches still work but at the right layer: set_app_type(Reactive) is a programmatic RUNTIME override of the frozen const (the const is the deduced default, the setter overrides it); leaf.main.app-type config bind-back is a runtime override after config loads (same precedence: config > programmatic > frozen-deduced). The genuinely-runtime case — a DYNAMIC WASM-host module contributing a flavor with NO build-time presence — cannot be frozen, so it needs a runtime re-resolution overlay lane: the frozen const is the static-graph answer, and a dynamically-discovered flavor (post-startup-scan) can override it through the same setter precedence, flagged as the overlay path. When NOT building via the prepare step (pure dev / no codegen), the SAME deduction logic runs at runtime as a startup pass (R1/R2's evaluator) producing the identical AppType — so there is no bimodality of RESULT, only of WHEN it is computed.

**Pros:** Best fit for the §3 compile-vs-runtime keystone applied to deduction, and the cross-crate doc's strongest recommendation (Architecture C / sqlx model is the deterministic, fully platform-independent path incl. wasm): 'the resolved Cargo feature graph IS the configuration' is the HONEST rust-native realization of 'the classpath is the configuration' — a deterministic build-time graph walk, not a fragile runtime registry, sidestepping ALL THREE DCE layers AND non-deterministic DCE entirely (cross-crate doc §305-315, §345-346).; Eliminates the silent-DCE trap at the SOURCE rather than catching it after the fact: because the deduction AND the force-link prelude are emitted from the SAME cargo-metadata graph walk, a flavor crate that is in the graph is BOTH deduced AND force-linked — they cannot disagree, so 'deduced Servlet but leaf-servlet not linked' becomes structurally impossible (vs R1/R2 where a marker can silently fail to link). The anti-DCE self-check becomes a build-time --check-able manifest cross-check, turning the entry point's worst silent-failure trap into a deterministic CI gate (cross-crate doc §269, §345).; Earliest + richest fail-fast (charter §1.7 taken to its limit): an ambiguous app type, a declared-but-unresolvable flavor, or an enabled-feature-zero-contributions case fails the BUILD with complete context and ZERO runtime side effects — the purest 'a binary that builds has an unambiguous, providable app type', strictly earlier than R1/R2's runtime startup self-check.; Zero runtime cost: 'deduction' is a const read (DEDUCED_APP_TYPE), no descriptor chain, no CapabilitySet fold, no dyn dispatch — strictly cheaper than R1/R2's (already cheap) cold-path query, and the frozen const is inspectable data in a generated file (a readable artifact, not emergent behaviour — charter §2.10, overhead #2).; Fully platform-independent incl. wasm/embedded/staticlib where linkme/inventory are fragile (cross-crate doc §356) — the build-time path is the FIRST-CLASS answer for exactly the targets the other substrates fail on, and it is the cleanest force-link-prelude generator (the run-pipeline's owned Layer-0 solution surface).; No bimodality of RESULT: the SAME deduction logic runs either at build time (frozen) or at runtime (startup pass) producing the IDENTICAL AppType — so the dev (no-codegen) and release (AOT) builds agree, and the substrate is swappable per target (the cross-crate doc's identical-runtime-API goal).

**Cons:** Diverges MOST from Spring's runtime-deduce() mental model and pre-judges the §3 compile-vs-runtime AND metadata/codegen keystones the HARDEST — presenting a build-time-frozen AppType as THE realization risks strongly biasing Phase 2's signal; it must be held strictly as a CANDIDATE (and the charter §3 explicitly defers the compile-vs-runtime split and the metadata/codegen boundary).; The config bind-back (leaf.main.app-type can OVERRIDE the deduced type from externalized config, §260) is inherently RUNTIME and directly contradicts freeze-early: the frozen const is only the DEFAULT, and config can flip it after config-data loads — so the build-time freeze covers only the deduction, not the final app type, partially reintroducing the runtime dynamism it sought to eliminate (the same bindToApplication-flips-the-deduction tension R1/R2 have, but sharper because the freeze advertised earliness).; The dynamic WASM-host 'classpath' has NO build-time presence (cross-crate doc + extra-15 + wasm-modules exploration): a WASM-contributed flavor can only join through a runtime overlay lane that overrides the frozen const, a direct tension with the build-time shape — it forces a runtime re-resolution path that erodes the frozen-deduction simplicity for exactly the dynamic case, flagged as a phase2Question.; Requires a build.rs / cargo-metadata prepare step + a manifest convention declaring which crate claims which flavor — heavier tooling than R1/R2's runtime registry, and a build.rs can only see its OWN crate's dependency declarations (cross-crate doc §30), so the metadata walk must be anchored at the BINARY crate (the only place with whole-graph awareness, §77) and the manifest convention must be authored correctly per flavor crate (an integration-author burden Spring's automatic classpath scan avoids).; Two computation modes (build-time-frozen + runtime startup-pass) that must produce IDENTICAL results, plus the runtime overlay for dynamic/config-override cases, is essentially R1/R2's runtime evaluator ANYWAY — so the build-time payoff is bounded to the static-graph deduction, and keeping the two modes coherent (same AppType from the same inputs) is a real coherence burden.; The DEDUCED_APP_TYPE const + the manifest format + the AppType vocabulary become a build-artifact/ABI commitment that must version cleanly across leaf releases (like R3 of the run-pipeline's RunPlan), and the manifest-convention-per-flavor-crate is a new public surface; for a small CLI app (always None) the whole prepare-step machinery is overkill (the runtime path should be the default there).

**Mechanisms considered:** build.rs / `cargo leaf prepare` in the BINARY crate reads cargo metadata (resolved dependency graph) + CARGO_FEATURE_*/CARGO_CFG_* (TARGET config, NOT host cfg!) + a manifest convention (which crate claims which flavor) — Architecture C / sqlx model; emit into OUT_DIR (include!'d): (1) const DEDUCED_APP_TYPE: AppType; (2) force-link prelude `use leaf_servlet as _;` per found flavor crate; (3) anti-DCE manifest (expected markers per declared crate) for a --check gate; deduction + force-link computed from the SAME graph walk so they cannot disagree — 'deduced X but X not linked' becomes structurally impossible; build-time validation: ambiguous app type (two flavor crates, no declared tiebreak), declared-but-unresolvable flavor, enabled-feature-zero-contributions → BUILD error / --check gate with complete context, zero runtime side effects; runtime 'deduction' = trivial const read of DEDUCED_APP_TYPE — no chain, no CapabilitySet query, no runtime cost; escape hatches as runtime overrides of the frozen const: set_app_type (programmatic) and leaf.main.app-type config bind-back (config > programmatic > frozen-deduced); runtime re-resolution overlay lane for dynamic WASM-host flavors (no build-time presence) — override the frozen const post-startup-scan via the setter precedence; identical deduction logic runnable at build time (frozen) OR runtime (startup pass, = R1/R2's evaluator) producing the IDENTICAL AppType — no result bimodality; leaf-codegen (proc-macro/build crates isolated from runtime per charter §6) owns the prepare step; leaf-boot owns the const consumer + runtime fallback

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** This is the realization built FOR the cross-crate/tooling concern: a build.rs / `cargo leaf prepare` at the BINARY crate reads the resolved dependency graph (cargo metadata) + the resolved feature set (CARGO_FEATURE_*/CARGO_CFG_* — TARGET, never host `cfg!`, §50) and emits the deduced AppType const + the force-link prelude + an anti-DCE manifest into OUT_DIR (Architecture C, the sqlx model, cross-crate doc §305-315). It sidesteps Layer 0 (the prepare step ENUMERATES the flavor crates from the graph and emits their force-link refs), Layer A (rustc reachability), and Layer B (--gc-sections) ENTIRELY, and is fully platform-independent incl. wasm/embedded/staticlib where linkme fails (§356) — the FIRST-CLASS path for those targets. CRITICAL constraint (§30, §77): a build.rs sees only its OWN crate's deps, so the metadata walk MUST be anchored at the binary crate (the only whole-graph-aware point), never in the kernel — leaf-codegen owns this, charter §6. The deduction and the force-link emitted from the SAME walk is the key reliability win: they cannot disagree, so the silent-DCE mis-deduction (R1/R2's quiet failure mode) is structurally impossible, and the anti-DCE self-check becomes a build-time --check manifest cross-check (deterministic CI gate, §269, §345) rather than a runtime count. BUT it cannot see crates the build doesn't know about: it enumerates DECLARED integration crates via metadata + the manifest convention, NOT a true classpath, and a dynamic WASM-host flavor has NO build-time presence — it joins only through a runtime overlay lane (a phase2Question). The DEDUCED_APP_TYPE const + the manifest format + the AppType vocabulary become a stable build-artifact/ABI commitment (must version cleanly). The manifest-convention-per-flavor-crate is a new authored public surface. -p-vs-workspace caveat applies (the resolved graph differs). Origin-agnostic: a declared native crate and a build-known integration crate are deduced identically; a runtime-overlay (WASM-module) flavor joins via the same setter-precedence override but bypasses the freeze. CANDIDATE throughout — the freeze's scope is exactly the statically-knowable fraction of the deduction.

**T2 — execution context:** The DEDUCTION PHASE is SYNCHRONOUS build-time work (single-threaded, in the build.rs/prepare step, before the binary runs) OR a synchronous cold-path startup pass in the no-codegen dev build — pure analysis over the dependency graph / capability set producing the AppType + the earliest (build-time) diagnostics. The RUNTIME read of DEDUCED_APP_TYPE is a const access — zero cost, no IO, no .await, no lock, no allocation. The escape-hatch overrides run on the bootstrap task: set_app_type is a synchronous pre-run setter; the config bind-back override runs at the tail of prepare_environment after config-data's async IO has joined back (extra-15 Phase B) — a synchronous reconciliation of the frozen const with the now-loaded config on the bootstrap task, the execution-context boundary where the static deduction meets runtime reality. The dynamic WASM-host overlay (if a flavor is contributed by a startup directory scan) crosses the async/sync boundary exactly once in a clearly-fenced cold startup step (wasm-modules exploration: one configured location, no recursion, no network) BEFORE the overlay override is applied — never on a hot path. NO global lock (§2.5): const read + bootstrap-owned (unshared) override write. The final AppType must be settled before refresh (OnWebApplication reads it). Build-time validation failures are compile/prepare errors with complete context (charter §1.7); runtime failures (config-override to an unprovidable type, dynamic-overlay flavor with no provider) are rich bootstrap-failure diagnostics. Cancellation: build-time = the build fails; runtime = aborting the bootstrap drops everything (nothing constructed). No async Drop concern (deduction constructs nothing).

### Rust clashes
- No runtime classpath, no SpringFactoriesLoader SPI scan, no class-presence probe. Spring's WebApplicationType.deduce() loads WebApplicationType.Deducer SPI impls via SpringFactoriesLoader at runtime and each probes for specific CLASSES on the classpath (jakarta.servlet.Servlet+DispatcherServlet, reactor Mono+DispatcherHandler). Rust has no global classpath, no runtime class-presence query, no reflection. The rust-native analogue is 'the resolved Cargo capability/feature graph is the configuration' — an enabled/force-linked integration crate expresses the flavor — collected as thin origin-agnostic descriptors (Deducers/AppTypeRules/capability markers) from a SCOPED catalog (static link-time registry + optional dynamic source; Phase-2-undecided linkme/codegen/explicit), addressed by ROLE, never a runtime type-scan. This is the central cross-crate divergence for deduction.
- cfg(feature) gates COMPILATION, not LINKAGE — and host `cfg!` lies about the TARGET. Spring deduces from classpath PRESENCE, which is unambiguous at runtime. In Rust, a cargo feature that 'enables the web starter' compiles the deducer/capability-marker but does NOT force the crate onto the link graph, so deduction can silently see an EMPTY registry and pick None/Plain (cross-crate doc §201). Worse, runtime `cfg!(feature=...)`/`#[cfg]` reflect the HOST config, while CARGO_CFG_*/CARGO_FEATURE_* (build.rs-readable) reflect the TARGET (§50) — so a runtime cfg-based deduction is a cross-compilation footgun. Deduction must rest on force-linked markers (link-time truth) or a build.rs/cargo-metadata graph walk, plus a force-link prelude (#[leaf::main] emitting `use leaf_servlet as _;`) — a feature alone is necessary but not sufficient.
- The silent-DCE mis-deduction is QUIETER than a missing bean. Spring's classpath query ALWAYS sees a present class; a leaf deducer/capability-marker in a crate the binary never path-references is silently absent (Layer 0; cross-crate doc §149), so the binary silently deduces the WRONG app type (usually None) with NO error — unlike a missing bean (loud at resolution). This mandates the anti-DCE self-check (expected-vs-found per declared crate) and a rich 'deduced X but no provider/marker for X — did you add AND force-link leaf-web?' diagnostic (charter §1.7); it cannot be left to surface as a confusing downstream 'no FlavorSeeder' or 'OnWebApplication didn't match' failure.
- SERVLET vs REACTIVE is a JVM-ecosystem artifact; leaf is async-first with no servlet model. Spring's deducer set encodes servlet-vs-reactive web-stack knowledge (DispatcherServlet vs DispatcherHandler). leaf is async-first with no servlet/WAR model (03-conditions-auto-configuration.md line 361/385), so the AppType vocabulary must NOT be a closed servlet/reactive enum in core — core knows only None/Plain, and every other flavor (a web-integration flavor, a WASM-host flavor) is a CONTRIBUTED open AppTypeKey, so no web/servlet/reactive knowledge leaks into the kernel (charter §1 scope). The deduction reframes onto 'which web-integration capability is compiled in', not a 1:1 port of servlet/reactive.
- The app type is mutate-the-driver-from-its-own-input (bindToApplication). Spring binds spring.main.web-application-type back onto the live SpringApplication mid-run so externalized config OVERRIDES the deduced type and the programmatic setWebApplicationType (§260). This 'config rebinds the deduction' pattern fights Rust ownership/single-source-of-truth: the run driver must hold the AppType in a form re-bindable between phases (deduce provisionally pre-environment, re-bind from config post-config-data — extra-15's two-phase flow), with a clean precedence (config > programmatic > deduced) rather than a confusing three-source-of-truth.
- The deduced type must be FINAL before condition evaluation, and there is no subtype reinterpretation for the matching environment. Spring's ApplicationContextFactory also supplies the matching Environment TYPE (§254), and EnvironmentConverter re-types the environment if it mismatches the deduced type — but Rust has no subtype reflection (02-configuration-environment.md extra-15 rustClashes), so 're-typing' is either re-seeding one environment's source stack (Flavor-as-data) or an explicit total transplant. Deduction must therefore PRODUCE the AppType/Flavor LOSSLESSLY and EARLY enough (before the environment is Arc-shared, before any OnWebApplication condition runs) that the environment can be seeded/transplanted for the right flavor without re-running config loading.
- The AppType vocabulary + Deducer/AppTypeRule descriptor + CapabilityKey set become a cross-crate ABI with no classpath to anchor them. Spring's WebApplicationType enum + Deducer interface are agreed within one JVM; in leaf, integration crates depend on and hard-code paths to the AppTypeKey vocabulary, the Deducer/AppTypeRule shape, and (R2) the shared CapabilitySet contract, so leaf must PUBLISH them as a versioned, minimal, ultra-stable public surface emitted with absolute paths by thin macros (like the run-listener event-name taxonomy) — a deliberate ABI-ish commitment.
- No StackWalker, no automatic main-class identity. Spring's deduceMainApplicationClass uses StackWalker to find the main frame (§319). Rust has no runtime stack-class reflection; the primary config + app identity that the deduction context attaches to must be passed EXPLICITLY (the #[leaf::main] macro / Application::new(PrimaryConfig)), a thin hand-writable handoff, not an ambient probe (charter §2.10).
- The dynamic-classpath (WASM-host) flavor has no build-time presence and complicates the deduce-before-environment ordering. A WASM-host module can contribute a flavor (extra-15, wasm-modules exploration), but it is discovered by a startup directory scan (IO-bearing, async-boundary-crossing) AFTER the link-time registry is fixed — so a WASM-contributed flavor isn't known until after the scan, pulling an async/IO step into the otherwise-synchronous pre-environment deduction window (or forcing a runtime overlay over a build-time-frozen result in R3). Spring's classpath is fixed at JVM start; leaf's 'second classpath' is dynamic, so the deduction timing/overlay semantics are genuinely new.

### Interactions
- **spring-application-run** — OWNED-BY / SUB-STEP. App-type deduction is a narrow sub-step of the run-pipeline (the create_context step 8, and the head of prepare_environment): the run driver calls deduce(&capabilities) to produce the AppType, which then keys the run-pipeline's origin-agnostic ContextFactory chain (which context type to instantiate) and is overridden by the run's bind_to_application (leaf.main.app-type, §260). The run owns the WHEN (deduce provisionally pre-environment, re-bind from config post-config-data); this feature owns the HOW (the deducer chain / capability projection + first-match/ranked resolution + NONE fallback + set_app_type escape hatch). It resolves to AppType::None in a core-only binary so no web knowledge leaks into the run's core path (charter §1).
- **environment** — PRODUCER for EnvironmentConverter [02-configuration-environment.md extra-15]. The deduced AppType IS the Flavor that EnvironmentConverter consumes to pick which FlavorSeeder/EnvironmentFactory seeds the environment's default property sources (Spring's ApplicationContextFactory also supplying the matching Environment type, §254). This feature decides the Flavor; extra-15 acts on it (re-seed the stack or transplant). The escape hatches align exactly: this feature's set_app_type == extra-15's set_flavor; the open AppTypeKey == extra-15's open Flavor value. The two MUST share one Flavor/AppType vocabulary or they will assume incompatible flavor identities — a coherence requirement to flag.
- **config-data** — OVERRIDE SOURCE + ordering dependency. The config bind-back (leaf.main.app-type / leaf.main.web-application-type overriding the deduced type) reads through the property-source stack config-data populates, so deduction's final pinning happens AFTER config-data's deterministic single-pass load completes (extra-15 Phase B / the bindToApplication moment §260). The hard inherited constraint: the Flavor must NOT change how config-data LOADS (only which default sources sit at the bottom afterward), so provisional deduction must be safe enough that config loads against a correct source set — leaf must prove flavor affects only post-load default-source precedence, not config loading itself.
- **profiles** — ADJACENT in prepare_environment, no direct coupling. Profile activation and app-type deduction both happen in the prepare_environment window and both can be driven by config (spring.profiles.active and leaf.main.app-type), but they are orthogonal axes: the deduced AppType selects flavor seeding; the active profiles gate profile-conditioned beans. They must both be FINAL before refresh/condition evaluation, sharing the same property-source stack and the same first-source-wins precedence so a CLI arg can override either.
- **auto-configuration** — PRODUCER of the keying signal + shares the starter-as-feature/force-link discipline. auto-configuration keys off 'the resolved capability/feature set' (03-conditions-auto-configuration.md line 499) and its OnWebApplication-gated auto-configs read the deduced AppType; the 'adding a starter expresses intent' == 'the classpath is the configuration' mental model and the force-link discipline are SHARED — a flavor crate that contributes a deducer is the same kind of starter crate that contributes auto-configs, both needing the same cfg-gates-compilation-plus-force-link-gates-linkage treatment and the same anti-DCE self-check. Deduction must produce a FINAL AppType before the deferred auto-config batch runs inside refresh.
- **conditions** — PRIMARY DOWNSTREAM CONSUMER via condition-family's OnWebApplication. condition-family (03-conditions-auto-configuration.md lines 316, 361, 385) explicitly posits OnWebApplication(SERVLET/REACTIVE)/OnNotWebApplication 'probes the sealed Environment for OnWebApplication' or 'a capability set for OnFeature' — that probe reads the deduced AppType (or the shared CapabilitySet, R2). The deduced type MUST be final and queryable before any OnWebApplication condition evaluates during refresh. R2 proposes UNIFYING them (OnWebApplication == 'deduced AppType == X') so the condition and the deduction cannot disagree — a unification tension condition-family flags as a Phase-2 reframing question (which JVM-ecosystem condition members survive/reframe/drop).
- **container-core** — DRIVES ContextFactory selection (indirect). The deduced AppType keys the run-pipeline's origin-agnostic ContextFactory chain that picks which container-core context facade to instantiate (Spring's createApplicationContext via ApplicationContextFactory.DEFAULT, §254). This feature produces the type; the run-pipeline's create_context + container-core's engine-vs-facade split act on it. In a core-only (None) binary the default plain context is selected, so no web context knowledge is required in core.
- **events-lifecycle** — INDIRECT / no direct event. App-type deduction itself fires no event (it is a pre-context computation), but the AppType it produces influences what the run-pipeline's fixed named event sequence carries downstream (e.g. whether a WebServerInitialized-analogue fires during refresh for a web flavor). Deduction is upstream of and orthogonal to the event sequence; it feeds the ContextFactory/FlavorSeeder selection that determines whether server-init-style lifecycle steps exist at all.

### Open questions for Phase 2
- Is app-type deduction its own bespoke Deducer-chain SPI (R1, literal Spring-deduce() parity, first-match-wins over fn-pointer descriptors) or a PURE PROJECTION of a shared CapabilitySet unified with condition-family's OnWebApplication/OnFeature and auto-configuration's starter-keying (R2, one source of truth, deduction-as-data, ambiguity-detecting) or a BUILD-TIME-FROZEN const computed from the resolved Cargo feature/dependency graph (R3, AOT/sqlx determinism, force-link-and-deduce-from-the-same-walk, earliest fail-fast)? This is downstream of the §3 compile-vs-runtime split, the metadata/codegen boundary, AND the conditional strategy — must stay a candidate.
- How is 'the classpath is the configuration' (app-type deduction + starter-as-feature) actually resolved given a Cargo feature gates COMPILATION not LINKAGE, and is dependency-based auto-configuration (the deferred §3 keystone) the mechanism? Whether 'a flavor crate's presence' maps onto a cargo feature + force-link, a build-time cargo-metadata walk, or something richer determines the whole shape of deduction and the force-link discipline. Cross-cuts auto-configuration and the cross-crate composition keystone identically.
- Which cross-crate substrate collects the deduction contributions (Deducers / AppTypeRules / capability markers): linkme distributed-slice (zero-cost, DCE-sensitive, no wasm), build-time codegen (Architecture C, deterministic, the natural force-link+anti-DCE-manifest fit), inventory (DCE-robust, wasm, but life-before-main hostile to async), or explicit with() (Architecture D escape hatch)? Deduction is a natural host for the force-link discipline + the mandated anti-DCE self-check (a missing deducer is quietly mis-deducing). Shared with every discovery feature.
- Is there ONE authoritative CapabilitySet for the binary shared by app-type deduction, condition-family's OnWebApplication/OnFeature, and auto-configuration's starter-keying — and what is its shape (a flat capability-presence set vs a richer facet model)? If unified (R2), the condition and the deduction cannot disagree, but it pre-judges the capability-substrate and conditional-strategy keystones; if not, deduction has its own deducer registry. Belongs to the capability-substrate meta-design, not this feature.
- Does leaf carry an OPEN AppType/Flavor vocabulary (core knows only None; servlet/reactive/WASM/custom are contributed descriptors) and is it the SAME vocabulary as EnvironmentConverter's Flavor [extra-15] and condition-family's OnWebApplication target? The three features (deduction, environment-flavor-seeding, OnWebApplication) must share one Flavor/AppType identity or assume incompatible flavors — a coherence requirement spanning Bootstrap + Configuration + Conditions areas.
- How is the config bind-back (leaf.main.app-type overriding the deduced type from externalized config, the bindToApplication edge §260) modeled without a confusing three-source-of-truth (deduced / programmatic setter / config), against Rust ownership? The precedence (config > programmatic > deduced) and the re-bind timing (deduce provisionally pre-environment, re-bind post-config-data) couple to environment's read/mutate seam and the run driver's shape — and under R3 it directly erodes the build-time freeze (config can flip the frozen const at runtime).
- How is OnWebApplication(SERVLET/REACTIVE)/OnNotWebApplication reframed for an async-first, no-servlet leaf — onto a web-integration capability fact, a runtime web-context flag, or dropped — and does that reframing match the AppType vocabulary deduction produces? condition-family explicitly defers this (line 385); deduction's AppType vocabulary and OnWebApplication's target must be co-designed. Needs a web/integration co-review.
- Does a dynamic (WASM-host / runtime) source contribute deduction flavors, and at what timing relative to the otherwise-synchronous pre-environment deduction window — especially under R3 where a dynamically-contributed flavor has no build-time presence and needs a runtime overlay over the frozen const? The static+dynamic discovery duality applies to deduction exactly as to definitions/environment-seeders [extra-15]; the timing (does the IO-bearing WASM scan complete before deduction, or only at the post-config re-evaluation?) and the overlay semantics are unresolved. Cross-cuts environment-flavor-seeding and auto-configuration's same duality.
- How much of WebApplicationType/ApplicationContextFactory deduction is even rust-native intent vs JVM-shaped scaffolding to design OUT? Candidates to question per charter §2.2 intent-parity: the servlet/reactive enum itself (vs an open capability flavor), the ApplicationContextFactory-supplies-the-matching-Environment-type coupling (vs leaf's single environment + Flavor-seeding), and whether deduction even needs to be a runtime step at all (R3 says no). Belongs to the per-feature Phase-3 re-unify, flagged so it isn't ported blindly.

### Notes
SCOPE BOUNDARY: this feature is the NARROW deduction step (the WebApplicationType.deduce() analogue, spring-boot-4-di-design.md §246-254), a sub-step of the run-pipeline's create_context/prepare_environment, NOT the whole run pipeline (that is spring-application-run) and NOT the environment re-seeding/transplant (that is 02-configuration-environment.md extra-15 EnvironmentConverter). It OWNS ONLY: the open AppType/Flavor vocabulary (core knows only None; everything else contributed — charter §1 scope), the origin-agnostic deduction over enabled capabilities (Deducer chain R1 / capability projection R2 / build-time freeze R3), first-match-or-ranked resolution with a NONE fallback, the set_app_type escape hatch (setWebApplicationType analogue), and the config bind-back override (leaf.main.app-type, the bindToApplication edge §260). It PRODUCES one value (the AppType/Flavor) consumed by exactly three neighbours: EnvironmentConverter/FlavorSeeder selection [extra-15], the run-pipeline ContextFactory chain [spring-application-run], and condition-family's OnWebApplication [03-conditions-auto-configuration.md]. CRITICAL COHERENCE FINDING: 02-configuration-environment.md extra-15 ALREADY designed the open Flavor value (Plain/Servlet/Reactive/WASM-host/custom), the FlavorSeeder/EnvironmentFactory registries, the set_flavor escape hatch, AND explicitly states 'Flavor DEDUCTION itself (which flavor does the binary want) is a runtime query over the resolved feature set' — so THIS feature is the producer of extra-15's Flavor, and the two MUST share ONE Flavor/AppType vocabulary and ONE provider-registry substrate or they will assume incompatible flavor identities. Likewise condition-family (line 316) posits OnWebApplication 'probes the sealed Environment / a capability set' — R2's unification (OnWebApplication == deduced AppType) is the natural convergence point and is flagged as a Phase-2 question, not resolved. The three realizations deliberately SPAN the compile-vs-runtime axis to keep Phase 2's signal unbiased: R1 leans literal-runtime-SPI-parity (most Spring-faithful, but inherits the quietest silent-DCE mis-deduction), R2 leans unify-via-shared-capability-set (most charter-§11-unifying, but pre-judges the capability/conditional keystones), R3 leans build-time-frozen-from-the-Cargo-graph (most deterministic + earliest fail-fast + platform-independent + structurally DCE-proof since deduce-and-force-link come from one walk, but pre-judges the compile-vs-runtime + metadata/codegen keystones hardest and struggles with the config-override + dynamic-WASM cases). All three hold the deferred §3 keystones as CANDIDATES and keep provider/registry abstractions ORIGIN-AGNOSTIC (a native, build-known, or WASM-module deducer/rule/marker participates identically). The marquee charter-§1.7 surface here is the silent-DCE mis-deduction diagnostic: unlike Spring's always-present classpath, a missing deducer silently picks the wrong app type, so the anti-DCE self-check + a rich 'deduced X but X has no provider / X's crate not force-linked' diagnostic is mandatory and is a natural input to leaf doctor / the startup report. Grounding fully cross-checked: spring-boot-4-di-design.md §246-254 (the classpath-is-configuration principle, WebApplicationType.deduce() v4.0.1 SPI + the WebMvc/WebFlux deducers + NONE fallback + the v4 modularization intent, ApplicationContextFactory selection also supplying the Environment type, §260 bindToApplication, §319 StackWalker, §321 AOT fork); 02-configuration-environment.md extra-15 (the open Flavor value, FlavorSeeder/EnvironmentFactory, set_flavor, two-phase deduce-then-rebind, the no-subtype-reinterpretation + silent-DCE + flavor-must-not-affect-config-loading clashes); 03-conditions-auto-configuration.md (OnWebApplication probes a capability set / sealed Environment line 316, the servlet/reactive-is-a-JVM-artifact reframing lines 361/385, the starter-as-feature/force-link discipline line 499); the cross-crate doc (the three DCE layers + Layer-0 unreferenced-crate silent vanish §149, cfg-gates-compilation-not-linkage §201, host-cfg!-vs-target-CARGO_CFG §50, Architectures A-D, build.rs-sees-only-own-crate §30 + anchor-at-binary §77, the anti-DCE self-check / leaf doctor mandate §269/§345); the nightly envelope (stable const-eval enough for const descriptor tables + key hashing; no adt_const_params needed for an interned AppTypeKey on stable; boxed futures at any dyn edge). The single highest-leverage Phase-3 convergence is making the AppType/Flavor vocabulary + its provider registry IDENTICAL across this feature, extra-15, and OnWebApplication.

## Application Arguments  `[application-arguments]`

leaf's realization of Spring Boot's `DefaultApplicationArguments` + `CommandLinePropertySource` (spring-boot-4-di-design.md §run() line 244 "build DefaultApplicationArguments"; §prepareEnvironment line 258 "configureEnvironment() adds a CommandLinePropertySource"; §prepareContext line 293 "register the springApplicationArguments singleton"; §Runners line 307 "CommandLineRunner.run(String[]) receives raw args; ApplicationRunner.run(ApplicationArguments) receives parsed options/non-option args"; §PropertySource line 1296 lists CommandLinePropertySource; §externalized precedence line 1429 puts command-line args at rung 11, the highest OPERATIONAL source, just above SPRING_APPLICATION_JSON). INTENT (two faces of one parse): (1) raw `argv` is parsed ONCE into a typed `ApplicationArguments` value object exposing the THREE Spring questions — `getSourceArgs()` (the raw ordered list), `getOptionNames()`/`getOptionValues(name)` (`--key` / `--key=value` option args, MULTI-VALUED: `--foo=a --foo=b` yields `[a,b]`, and a bare `--flag` yields an empty-list option that is PRESENT), and `getNonOptionArgs()` (everything not matching the `--key[=value]` option grammar, including positional args and a literal `--` terminator's tail). (2) The SAME parse is exposed as a NAMED, ENUMERABLE, HIGHEST-PRECEDENCE-operational command-line `PropertySource` (`commandLineArgs`) over leaf's `[property-sources]` stack: a `--server.port=8080` arg resolves through the same first-source-wins walk as a file or env var, overriding everything operational below it, so a CLI switch can flip `leaf.profiles.active`, `leaf.main.*` knobs, etc. The value object is also exposed as an INJECTABLE singleton bean (Spring's `springApplicationArguments`) so any bean can `@Autowired ApplicationArguments`, and is the argument passed to the `ApplicationRunner`-analogue. SCOPE: this feature owns ONLY the argv→typed parse (the option/non-option grammar, the multi-valued + flag-present semantics), the `ApplicationArguments` value-object shape, its adaptation INTO a `[property-sources]` `PropertySource` (the key mapping `--a.b.c=v` → property `a.b.c`, the multi-valued→indexed/CSV adaptation, enumerability for relaxed-binding), and the WHERE/WHEN of its placement in the run pipeline + its registration as a bean. It does NOT own the property-source stack mechanics ([property-sources]), the read/mutate seam ([environment]), the precedence ORDER policy ([config-data]), profile activation ([profiles]), relaxed-binding canonicalization ([relaxed-binding]), or the runner family / run sequence (spring-application-run) — it plugs into all of them. This is a Phase-1 gap explicitly flagged by 02-configuration-environment.md (its top-level summary names "command-line args" as a concrete SOURCE TYPE "not a generic Map" with "its own grammar/behavior" that has no owner inside that area). It honors charter §1.7 (a malformed `--` or an unparseable option fails with the offending token + position, not a panic), §2.3 (parsing is pure cold-path sync; argv acquisition via std::env is the only OS touch), and §2.10 (a thin macro at most; `Args::from_env()` is hand-writable).

### Candidate realizations

#### R1 — Eager parse-once value object adapted to a PropertySource facet: argv parsed into one owned typed ApplicationArguments, which both IS the injectable singleton and is wrapped by a thin CommandLineArgsPropertySource adapter placed at the highest operational rung
The most literal transcription of DefaultApplicationArguments + CommandLinePropertySource. A single eager, pure, synchronous parse: `fn parse(argv: Vec<OsString>) -> Result<ApplicationArguments, ArgParseError>` runs ONCE at the run-pipeline's parse-args step (mirroring Spring's `build DefaultApplicationArguments`). The owned value object:
```rust
pub struct ApplicationArguments {
    source: Arc<[String]>,                              // getSourceArgs — raw ordered argv (after lossy/strict OsString decode)
    options: IndexMap<String, Vec<String>>,             // getOptionNames/getOptionValues — order-preserving, multi-valued
    non_options: Vec<String>,                           // getNonOptionArgs — positional + post-`--` tail
}
impl ApplicationArguments {
    pub fn source_args(&self) -> &[String];
    pub fn option_names(&self) -> impl Iterator<Item=&str>;
    pub fn option_values(&self, name: &str) -> Option<&[String]>;  // Some(&[]) == flag PRESENT but valueless; None == ABSENT
    pub fn contains_option(&self, name: &str) -> bool;
    pub fn non_option_args(&self) -> &[String];
}
```
Grammar (Spring's SimpleCommandLineArgsParser): a token is an OPTION iff it starts with `--`; `--name=value` splits on the first `=`; `--name` with no `=` is a present, empty-valued option; repeated `--name` accumulate into the Vec (multi-valued); a bare `--` terminates option parsing and everything after is non-option; anything not starting with `--` is a non-option. Malformed `--=value` (empty name) is the one hard error → `ArgParseError{ token, position, reason }` (charter §1.7). The SAME instance is exposed three ways without re-parsing: (a) registered as the injectable `applicationArguments` singleton (Spring's `springApplicationArguments`) — wrapped in whatever the [container-core] singleton handle is (Arc-shared, since the property source also references it); (b) handed to the ApplicationRunner-analogue (spring-application-run's call_runners passes `&ApplicationArguments`, while a CommandLineRunner-analogue gets `source_args()`); (c) wrapped by a thin `CommandLineArgsPropertySource(Arc<ApplicationArguments>)` adapter that impls [property-sources]'s `PropertySource` + `EnumerablePropertySource`. The adapter's `get(key)` looks up `key` in `options`: a single-value option returns `Some(PropertyValue{ raw: value, origin: Origin::CommandLine{ token_index } })`; a multi-valued option `--foo=a --foo=b` adapts to CSV `a,b` (Spring's CommandLinePropertySource default) AND the binder's indexed forms `foo[0]`/`foo[1]` are synthesized as enumerable keys for [relaxed-binding] list binding; a valueless flag `--debug` returns `Some("")` (present-empty, which under first-source-wins WINS and does not fall through — the null-never-overrides contract). `option_names()` is exposed as the `EnumerablePropertySource::keys()` so [relaxed-binding] can canonicalize. Non-option args are NOT property-source keys (Spring exposes them under a synthetic `nonOptionArgs` key as CSV — leaf replicates that one synthetic enumerable key). The run pipeline (spring-application-run) places this source via [property-sources]'s ordering vocabulary with a position-hint that resolves to the highest OPERATIONAL rung (above env/system-properties/SPRING_APPLICATION_JSON-analogue, below test overrides) — the source carries its precedence as DATA, never link order. A thin `#[leaf::main]`-emitted or hand-written `ApplicationArguments::from_env()` calls `std::env::args_os().collect()` then `parse(..)`; argv acquisition is the ONLY OS touch and is isolated so a test/embedded caller passes an explicit `Vec<String>`.

**Pros:** Highest intent fidelity + maximal DX legibility (charter §1, §2 intent-parity): `option_values`/`option_names`/`non_option_args`/`source_args` map 1:1 to Spring's `getOptionValues`/`getOptionNames`/`getNonOptionArgs`/`getSourceArgs`; a Spring dev recognizes it instantly, and the value object IS the bean IS the runner argument IS the backing of the property source — one parse, one owned truth, no duplication.; ONE parse, ONE owned value (charter §5 memory discipline): the raw decode happens once into an owned struct; the property-source adapter, the singleton bean, and the runner argument all share the SAME `Arc<ApplicationArguments>` rather than re-parsing or copying — the property source is a near-zero-cost facet over the already-parsed options map.; Cleanly plugs into the existing [property-sources] design without reinventing it: `CommandLineArgsPropertySource` is just another origin-agnostic `Box/Arc<dyn PropertySource>` + `EnumerablePropertySource` impl, placed by the SAME add_first/position-hint vocabulary, honoring first-source-wins, never-blend (a present option value entirely replaces a lower source), and null-never-overrides (a valueless flag = present-empty, ABSENT option = `None` fall-through) as TYPE-level guarantees via `Option`.; The flag-present-vs-absent distinction is sharper than Spring's: `option_values(name)` returns `Some(&[])` for a present valueless flag vs `None` for an absent option — encoding Spring's 'present option with empty list' as a type-level fact, and feeding the property source's present-empty-wins-first-source semantics correctly.; Pure synchronous cold-path parse (charter §2.3): no async, no IO except the isolated `args_os()` acquisition; trivially testable by passing an explicit `Vec<String>` (no global argv dependency), serving the test-slice/withHook story spring-application-run flagged.; Origin tracking is first-class and free (interaction with [origin-tracking]): every value the source returns carries `Origin::CommandLine{ token_index }`, so diagnostics can say 'server.port came from command-line arg #3 (--server.port=8080)' — the single-traceable-origin guarantee the bootstrap layer's §1.7 diagnostics want.

**Cons:** Bakes ONE option grammar (Spring's `--key[=value]`) into core — but real CLI apps want richer parsing (short flags `-v`, subcommands, `clap`-style derive, count flags, `=`-less `--key value`). R1's single struct gives no seam to swap the parser, so a clap-integration must either bypass this feature entirely (two sources of truth for argv) or this feature must expose the raw `source_args()` for clap to re-parse (double parse). The grammar-extensibility seam is absent (R2's whole point).; The multi-valued→property-source adaptation is a lossy/opinionated mapping with NO single right answer: Spring picks CSV (`--foo=a --foo=b` → `foo=a,b`), but the binder also wants indexed `foo[0]`/`foo[1]`; synthesizing BOTH into the enumerable key set risks ambiguity (does `foo` mean the CSV or is it a map prefix?) and couples this feature to [relaxed-binding]'s list/index conventions — a contract that must be pinned and is easy to get subtly wrong.; OsString decoding is a forced early policy decision baked into the eager parse: lossy (`to_string_lossy`, silently mangles non-UTF8 args) vs strict (error on non-UTF8) is decided once at parse time for ALL args, but a binary path or a file argument might legitimately be non-UTF8 while option keys must be UTF8 — a one-size decode is either too lenient or too strict, and R1 has no per-token policy.; Eager full parse means even an app that never reads an option pays the parse + the IndexMap build at startup — negligible for small argv but a (tiny) always-on cost vs a lazy R3 that parses on first query; more importantly it commits to materializing the options map before anyone has declared what options exist (no validation against a declared schema).; The synthetic `nonOptionArgs` property-source key (Spring's mechanism to expose positional args as a CSV property) is a JVM-shaped convention that may not be rust-native intent — porting it blindly risks a confusing 'why is there a nonOptionArgs property' surprise; R1 ports it for fidelity but it deserves the intent-vs-mechanism question.

**Mechanisms considered:** one eager `fn parse(Vec<OsString>) -> Result<ApplicationArguments, ArgParseError>` run once at the run-pipeline parse-args step; owned `ApplicationArguments { source: Arc<[String]>, options: IndexMap<String,Vec<String>>, non_options: Vec<String> }` with Spring-mirroring accessors; `option_values(name) -> Option<&[String]>` where `Some(&[])`=present-valueless-flag, `None`=absent — encoding flag-present vs absent at the type level; thin `CommandLineArgsPropertySource(Arc<ApplicationArguments>)` impl of [property-sources]'s `PropertySource`+`EnumerablePropertySource`, multi-value→CSV + synthesized indexed keys, valueless-flag→present-empty; the SAME `Arc<ApplicationArguments>` shared as: injectable singleton, ApplicationRunner argument, and property-source backing — no re-parse; `Origin::CommandLine{ token_index }` on every returned PropertyValue for [origin-tracking]; position-hint DATA placing the source at the highest operational rung via [property-sources] add_first/before(name) vocabulary (never link order); isolated `args_os()` acquisition in a thin `from_env()`; tests/embedded pass explicit `Vec<String>`; one hard `ArgParseError{ token, position, reason }` for `--=value` (empty option name); lossy-vs-strict OsString decode decided at parse

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** The `ApplicationArguments` type, the `ArgParseError`, and the `CommandLineArgsPropertySource` adapter are kernel types in leaf-core (or leaf-boot, per charter §6 the bootstrap layer) — the parse is a SINGLE owned object the run pipeline constructs, so it needs NO cross-crate registration of its own (unlike config-data's source-CONTRIBUTORS). Cross-crate enters only at two seams: (a) the property-source adapter is registered into [property-sources] via the SAME source-provider descriptor substrate config-data uses (Phase-2-undecided: linkme distributed-slice / build-codegen / explicit), but here it is a SINGLE always-present built-in source the pipeline adds directly, so it sidesteps the DCE hazard (the run pipeline path-references it — Layer 0 is satisfied by construction, no force-link needed); (b) the injectable singleton must be registered into [container-core]'s registry as a pre-built singleton (Spring's `registerSingleton(springApplicationArguments)`), which is a direct register call by the run pipeline, again not a discovered contribution. The grammar/value-object is a STABLE public surface (downstream beans `@Autowired ApplicationArguments`, integration crates may read it), so its accessor signatures + the `commandLineArgs` source name + the `Origin::CommandLine` shape become an ABI-ish commitment, like spring-application-run's run-listener event-name taxonomy. CRITICAL R1 limitation surfaced by T1: because the grammar is fixed in core with no parser seam, an integration crate that wants clap-style parsing cannot CONTRIBUTE a parser — it can only consume `source_args()` and re-parse independently, creating a second argv interpretation the property source doesn't know about (the cross-crate cost of no extensibility seam, which R2 addresses). Origin-agnostic by the property-source contract: the adapter is just a `dyn PropertySource`, indistinguishable to the stack from a native/file/WASM source.

**T2 — execution context:** Entirely COLD-PATH, synchronous (charter §2.3): the parse runs once on the bootstrap task at the run-pipeline's parse-args step (before prepare_environment, mirroring Spring), is pure CPU over an in-memory `Vec<OsString>`, never awaits, never blocks, never spawns. The ONLY OS interaction is `std::env::args_os()` in `from_env()`, isolated so the parse function itself is a pure `Vec<OsString> -> Result` (testable, embeddable, deterministic). The resulting `Arc<ApplicationArguments>` is `Send+Sync` and immutable after parse, so it crosses `.await`/threads freely as a cheap Arc clone — shared by the property source (read on the synchronous, lock-free, hot config read path — the adapter's `get()` is a non-blocking IndexMap lookup, NEVER async, honoring [property-sources]' no-block-on-read discipline), the singleton bean (resolved on demand), and the ApplicationRunner argument (read in the runners window). No global lock (charter §2.5): the value is constructed once and frozen; no mutation after the parse step, so reads are lock-free by immutability. Cancellation: the parse is a bounded, non-cancellable cold step; if it errors it routes into spring-application-run's handle_run_failure as a RunFailure carrying the offending token/position (and a FailureAnalyzer-analogue can render 'malformed command-line argument --=foo at position 2'). No async Drop concern (the value is plain owned data). Errors propagate as `ArgParseError` with the full token context (charter §1.7).

#### R2 — Parser-SPI + neutral parsed model: an origin-agnostic ArgumentParser trait produces a neutral ParsedArguments (the value object + the property-source projection), so the default `--key=value` grammar is one swappable implementation and clap/getopt-style parsers plug in identically
Question whether the OPTION GRAMMAR must be hard-coded. Separate WHAT-is-parsed (a neutral parsed model the rest of leaf consumes) from HOW-argv-is-parsed (a swappable parser). Define an origin-agnostic SPI:
```rust
pub trait ArgumentParser: Send + Sync {
    fn parse(&self, argv: &[OsString]) -> Result<ParsedArguments, ArgParseError>;
}
pub struct ParsedArguments {           // the NEUTRAL model every consumer reads
    source: Arc<[String]>,
    options: IndexMap<String, Vec<String>>,
    non_options: Vec<String>,
    // optional: a parser-supplied origin/diagnostics table
}
```
The DEFAULT parser `SimpleArgParser` ships in leaf-boot and implements exactly R1's Spring `--key[=value]` grammar — so out-of-the-box behaviour is identical to R1/Spring. But the parser is selected the same origin-agnostic, descriptor-driven way the rest of leaf selects participants (the spring-application-run AppType-Deducer / ContextFactory analogue): a single highest-priority `ArgumentParser` descriptor wins, with the default as the lowest-priority fallback, and an explicit `Application::set_argument_parser(..)` escape hatch. An integration crate (`leaf-clap`) contributes a `ClapArgumentParser<C: clap::Parser>` descriptor that runs clap's derive parsing and projects the result INTO `ParsedArguments` (every clap field becomes an option entry, positionals become non_options) — so clap's rich grammar (short flags, subcommands, value validation, `--key value`) drives the SAME property source and the SAME injectable value object, with NO second argv interpretation. `ApplicationArguments` becomes a thin public read facade over `ParsedArguments` (the Spring-named accessors), keeping R1's DX.
