The property-source adapter (`CommandLineArgsPropertySource`) wraps `ParsedArguments` exactly as in R1 (multi-value→CSV+indexed, flag→present-empty, enumerable keys = option names, the synthetic non-option key), placed at the highest operational rung. The injectable bean is the `ApplicationArguments` facade. Critically, because the parser is an SPI, the parser can ALSO project a richer typed result: a `leaf-clap` parser can register the user's clap-derived struct as its OWN injectable bean alongside the neutral `ApplicationArguments`, so a bean can inject either the neutral args or the typed clap struct — the parser owns the projection but the neutral model stays the contract the property source + binder rely on. The parse still runs once, cold, at the run-pipeline parse-args step; the only addition over R1 is the parser-selection indirection (resolve the winning `ArgumentParser` descriptor, call it).

**Pros:** Solves R1's central limitation — grammar extensibility — without sacrificing R1's defaults: the Spring `--key=value` grammar is the shipped fallback, but clap/getopt/custom parsers plug in via the SAME origin-agnostic descriptor mechanism the rest of leaf uses for AppType deducers/context factories, so 'I want clap' is a starter-crate add, not a fork (charter §1 DX, §6 pluggable-everything-else, §11 unification).; ONE argv interpretation, not two (the cross-crate fidelity win): because clap (or any parser) projects INTO the neutral `ParsedArguments` that backs the property source AND the injectable bean AND the runner argument, a `--server.port` parsed by clap flows through leaf's config precedence identically to the default parser — no divergence between 'what clap saw' and 'what the property source exposes', which R1's re-parse path would create.; Maximal unification (charter §11): the parser is selected by the SAME descriptor/priority/fallback substrate as spring-application-run's AppType deducer and context factory — one discovery primitive, one escape-hatch shape (`set_argument_parser`), one anti-DCE concern, rather than a bespoke arg mechanism.; The neutral `ParsedArguments` keeps [property-sources], [relaxed-binding], and [config-data] decoupled from the parser: they bind over the neutral options map and never know whether clap or the default grammar produced it — the never-blend / first-source-wins / enumerable contracts hold regardless of parser (clean boundary).; Richer typed projection is possible without polluting the core: a clap parser can ALSO register the user's typed `#[derive(Parser)] struct Cli` as its own injectable bean, giving a bean the choice of the neutral `ApplicationArguments` or the strongly-typed CLI struct — strictly more expressive than R1, while the neutral model remains the property-source contract.; Diagnostics improve: a parser SPI can return rich parse errors (clap's are excellent — 'unknown flag --prot, did you mean --port?'), routed through spring-application-run's FailureAnalyzer chain, serving charter §1.7 better than R1's single hard error.

**Cons:** Inherits the FULL cross-crate DCE hazard R1 sidestepped (charter T1): the parser is now a DISCOVERED contribution, so a `leaf-clap` parser in a crate the binary never force-links is SILENTLY absent → the app silently falls back to the default `--key=value` grammar, and the user's `-v`/subcommand args are silently mis-parsed as non-options. This is a QUIET failure (worse than a missing bean's loud resolution error), mandating the anti-DCE self-check (warn when an enabled parser crate contributes zero parsers) and the force-link discipline — a real cost the always-present R1 source avoids.; Parser SELECTION ambiguity: if two crates each contribute an `ArgumentParser` (clap AND getopt), which wins? A priority/last-wins rule must be defined and made loud (an ambiguous-parser diagnostic), and the 'default is lowest priority' fallback must be airtight — a class of footgun R1 (no selection) doesn't have.; The neutral-model projection is lossy in the OTHER direction now: clap's rich structure (typed fields, validated enums, subcommand trees) must FLATTEN into the string-keyed `options`/`non_options` map to feed the property source, so a clap subcommand `serve --port 8080` has a non-obvious projection (is `serve` a non-option? does `port` become a property?) — the projection contract is subtle and parser-author-facing, more surface than R1.; More machinery for the common case (charter §5 'justify with intent'): an app that just wants Spring's `--key=value` pays the parser-resolution indirection (resolve descriptor, dispatch through `dyn ArgumentParser`) it would never exercise — cold-path-cheap but real, and it pre-judges that parser-swappability is even wanted (a Phase-2 bias toward an SPI where a fixed grammar + a 'read source_args() and parse yourself' escape hatch might suffice).; Two injectable beans (neutral `ApplicationArguments` + the optional typed clap struct) risks confusion about which to inject and whether they can drift; the parser-owns-the-typed-projection rule must be crisp or beans get two not-quite-consistent views of argv.; `ArgumentParser::parse` returning `Result` through a `dyn` trait means the error type must be erased/boxed at the dyn edge (the AFIT/RPITIT-not-dyn-safe family, though parse is sync so it is only an error-type-erasure concern, not a future-boxing one) — a small but real dyn-edge tax R1's concrete fn avoids.

**Mechanisms considered:** origin-agnostic `trait ArgumentParser { fn parse(&self, &[OsString]) -> Result<ParsedArguments, ArgParseError> }` SPI; neutral `ParsedArguments { source, options: IndexMap<String,Vec<String>>, non_options }` as the contract every consumer (property source, bean, runner, binder) reads; default `SimpleArgParser` (R1's Spring `--key=value` grammar) shipped in leaf-boot as the lowest-priority fallback; parser selected via the SAME descriptor/priority/fallback substrate as spring-application-run's AppType deducer + context factory; explicit `Application::set_argument_parser(..)` escape hatch; `leaf-clap` integration crate contributing `ClapArgumentParser<C: clap::Parser>` that projects clap's parse INTO `ParsedArguments` (one argv interpretation); `ApplicationArguments` as a thin public read facade (Spring-named accessors) over `ParsedArguments` — the injectable bean; optional second injectable bean: the parser's typed projection (the user's `#[derive(Parser)] struct Cli`) registered alongside the neutral args; `CommandLineArgsPropertySource(Arc<ParsedArguments>)` adapter identical to R1, placed at highest operational rung via [property-sources] vocabulary; anti-DCE self-check + force-link discipline for the discovered parser (warn on enabled-parser-crate-zero-contributions); ambiguous-parser diagnostic when two parsers contend

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** This is the realization that turns argv parsing into a cross-crate EXTENSION POINT, so it inherits spring-application-run's full discovery story. leaf-boot defines `ArgumentParser`, `ParsedArguments`, `ApplicationArguments`, and the default `SimpleArgParser`. An integration crate (`leaf-clap`) depends only on leaf-boot/leaf-core and contributes a parser descriptor via the Phase-2-undecided catalog substrate (linkme/codegen/explicit) — the SAME substrate config-data's source-providers and spring-application-run's deducers/factories use (unification dividend). CRITICAL T1 hazard: unlike R1's always-present built-in source (path-referenced by the pipeline, Layer-0-safe), a contributed parser is subject to ALL THREE DCE layers — Layer 0 (the `leaf-clap` crate must be force-linked via the generated `use leaf_clap as _;` prelude, since a Cargo feature gates COMPILATION not LINKAGE), Layer A (rustc reachability pre-1.62), Layer B (`--gc-sections`/LLD pre-1.89). A silently-DCE'd parser yields a QUIET wrong-parse (the default grammar mis-handles clap-style args) — the worst failure mode the cross-crate doc warns about — so R2 MANDATES the anti-DCE self-check (expected-vs-found per declared parser crate, warn on zero contributions) and is a natural host for the force-link prelude + 'leaf doctor' surface. Parser selection must be ordering-as-DATA (priority field on the descriptor), NEVER link/section order. The neutral `ParsedArguments` + `ApplicationArguments` accessors + the `commandLineArgs` source name remain the stable cross-crate ABI; the parser SPI trait is an additional stable surface. Generics can't carry a 'static descriptor → a `register_argument_parser!(Concrete)` macro shim hard-errors on a generic parser (per the cross-crate doc's macro-hard-error guidance). Origin-agnostic throughout: a native, clap-backed, or WASM-module-contributed parser projects into the identical neutral model.

**T2 — execution context:** Same cold-path discipline as R1 plus a parser-selection step, all synchronous on the bootstrap task (charter §2.3). At the run-pipeline parse-args step: (1) resolve the winning `ArgumentParser` descriptor (a cold, synchronous, bounded lookup over the contributed parser set — no IO, no await); (2) call `parser.parse(&argv)` through the `dyn` edge — synchronous, pure CPU, never blocks/awaits/spawns (a parser that needed IO would violate the contract — parsers are pure argv→model). The resulting `Arc<ParsedArguments>` is `Send+Sync`, immutable, shared by the property source (lock-free non-blocking `get()` on the config read path), the bean(s), and the runner argument exactly as R1. No global lock (charter §2.5): construct-once-freeze, lock-free reads by immutability. The parser-selection ambiguity (two parsers) is resolved at this cold step with a loud diagnostic, not a lock. Cancellation: parse-args is a bounded non-cancellable cold step; a parse error (the default grammar's `--=foo`, or clap's rich 'unknown flag' error) routes into spring-application-run's handle_run_failure as a RunFailure carrying the parser's diagnostic, fed to the FailureAnalyzer chain (charter §1.7). The dyn-edge error type is erased/boxed (sync, so no future-boxing — only `Box<dyn Error>`-style erasure). No async Drop (plain owned data). The discovered parser's force-link/DCE concern is a BUILD/link-time matter (T1), not a runtime execution-context one.

#### R3 — Schema-bound declarative arguments: a typed @Arguments struct (relaxed-binding target) is the primary surface, argv parsed against a declared option SCHEMA with validation, and the raw value-object + property source are the lower-level fallback
Push leaf's DX-first + §1.7-diagnostics intent hardest by making the PRIMARY surface a DECLARED, TYPED, VALIDATED argument schema rather than a string-keyed bag — the rust-native analogue of how Spring users actually consume args (they rarely call `getOptionValues`; they bind args into `@ConfigurationProperties` via the command-line property source). The user declares a struct:
```rust
#[leaf::arguments(prefix = "")]   // a thin macro emitting a relaxed-binding target + a schema descriptor
struct CliArgs {
    server_port: Option<u16>,     // --server-port / --server.port
    #[arg(required)] input: PathBuf,
    #[arg(multi)] include: Vec<String>,   // --include a --include b
    verbose: bool,                // a present-valueless flag → true
}
```
The macro emits (thinly, charter §2.10 — all hand-writable) a `const ArgSchema` descriptor (declared option names, arities, required-ness, types, the prefix) AND the [relaxed-binding] `Bindable` impl. argv is parsed in TWO conceptual layers: (1) a low-level lexer produces the SAME neutral options/non-options model as R1/R2 (still exposed as `ApplicationArguments` + the `commandLineArgs` property source — the raw fallback NEVER disappears); (2) the declared `CliArgs` is then BOUND from the command-line property source through the EXISTING [relaxed-binding]/binder machinery (NOT a bespoke arg binder — args are 'just another property source' and the typed struct is 'just another @ConfigurationProperties target', the deepest unification with config) and VALIDATED against the schema: an unknown `--prot` (not in the schema) is a rich error ('unknown option --prot; known: --server-port, --input, --include, --verbose'), a missing `required` arg is a rich error, a `--server-port=notanumber` is a type-conversion error with the offending token — ALL rendered through the unified diagnostics / FailureAnalyzer surface (charter §1.7, the marquee bootstrap-layer diagnostic). The typed `CliArgs` is registered as an injectable bean; the raw `ApplicationArguments` + property source remain registered too (so low-level access and the precedence-override role survive). Validation is OPT-IN: with NO declared schema, behaviour is exactly R1 (lenient lexing, no unknown-option rejection — Spring's default, since Spring does NOT reject unknown args). With a declared schema, the app gets strict validation + typed binding + completion-ready metadata. This mirrors [config-metadata]: the schema descriptor can ALSO feed shell-completion generation and a `--help` renderer (a build-time-emittable artifact). The parse-against-schema runs at the run-pipeline parse-args step (lexing) + a validation pass right after prepare_environment (once the command-line source is on the stack and binder is available), so type errors surface as early as the richest diagnostic allows (charter §1.7 timing).

**Pros:** Best charter §1 DX + §1.7 diagnostics: the PRIMARY surface is a typed, validated struct (`cli.server_port`, not `option_values("server-port")`), unknown/missing/mistyped args fail with the COMPLETE actionable context (known options, expected type, offending token) — the marquee bootstrap-layer 'failure teaches' promise, and typed access beats Spring's stringly-typed `getOptionValues` for a rust-native feel.; Deepest unification (charter §11): args are 'just another property source' and the typed struct is 'just another relaxed-binding/@ConfigurationProperties target' — R3 reuses the ENTIRE existing [relaxed-binding]/[binder]/[config-properties] machinery rather than inventing an arg binder, so `--server.port`, `SERVER_PORT` env, and `server.port` in a file ALL bind to the same `server_port: u16` field through one code path, with command-line winning by precedence. This is the single biggest reuse dividend of the three.; Validation timing honors charter §1.7 precisely: the schema is known at the parse step (lexing) and binding/validation runs once the command-line source is on the stack — so a typed/unknown-option error is the EARLIEST richest diagnostic (a dedicated startup validation pass), not a deferred runtime surprise; and because the schema is a `const` descriptor, build-time validation (R3-of-spring-application-run's RunPlan lineage) could lift it even earlier.; Completion + `--help` for free (the [config-metadata] dividend): the declared schema is the metadata source a build-time pass emits shell-completion + a `--help` renderer from — a Spring-grade tooling story Spring's untyped args can't match, realizing 'the classpath/declaration is the configuration' for CLI surface.; The raw fallback NEVER disappears: `ApplicationArguments` + the `commandLineArgs` property source remain for low-level access and the precedence-override role (a `--leaf.profiles.active=dev` still works WITHOUT being in any schema, since the property source is schema-independent) — so R3 is strictly a typed LAYER on top of R1's model, not a replacement, preserving the override-everything-operational intent.; Schema-bound parsing makes the flag/multi/arity semantics DECLARED rather than inferred: `verbose: bool` declares a valueless flag, `include: Vec<String>` declares multi-valued, `input: PathBuf` declares an arity-1 positional — removing R1's lossy CSV-vs-indexed guesswork because the target type DECLARES the shape the binder expects.

**Cons:** Largest conceptual surface + a macro that does real work (tension with charter §2.10 thin-macros): `#[leaf::arguments]` must emit a schema descriptor + a Bindable impl + arity/required metadata — more than R1's near-zero macro. It must stay THIN (emit only hand-writable schema data + a derive a user could write), but the temptation to bake validation logic into the macro is real, and `cargo expand` must stay legible.; Pre-judges several deferred Phase-2 keystones HARD: it leans on [relaxed-binding]'s canonicalization, [binder]'s strict-vs-lenient mode, [config-properties]'s binding target shape, [config-metadata]'s descriptor format, AND the unified error/diagnostics model — so presenting R3 as THE realization risks biasing all of those Phase-2 calls; it must stay strictly a CANDIDATE, and its value is bounded by those neighbours' eventual shapes.; Strict validation contradicts Spring's deliberate leniency: Spring does NOT reject unknown command-line args (they just become available options nobody reads). R3's schema-validation, when a schema is declared, REJECTS unknown args — a behaviour change that, while better DX, diverges from intent-parity and could surprise users who pass ad-hoc `--leaf.main.*` overrides not in their `CliArgs` schema (mitigated by 'unknown args are allowed if they match a KNOWN property prefix' — but that rule is subtle and is itself a new contract to pin).; Two surfaces (typed `CliArgs` bean + raw `ApplicationArguments` bean + the property source) is the most to reason about: which is authoritative when they disagree (e.g. the typed field validated/converted vs the raw string option)? The binder-derives-from-the-property-source rule must be crisp or users get two inconsistent views, and the typed struct can lag the raw source if rebinding semantics aren't pinned.; Overkill for a tiny CLI / library-embedded app that just wants `args_os()` parsed: R3's full schema/validation/metadata machinery is unwanted weight where R1's bag suffices, so the no-schema fallback (== R1) MUST be airtight and zero-overhead, or R3 taxes the simple case for the rich one.; Couples arg validation to binder availability + ordering: the validation pass can only run AFTER the command-line source is on the stack AND the binder is constructed, which constrains where in the run pipeline it sits (after prepare_environment) and creates an ordering dependency on [config-data]/[environment] sealing — a subtle pipeline-placement constraint R1/R2 (parse-only-at-parse-step) don't have.

**Mechanisms considered:** `#[leaf::arguments]` thin macro emitting a `const ArgSchema` descriptor (option names, arities, required, types, prefix) + a [relaxed-binding] `Bindable` impl; two-layer parse: low-level lexer → neutral options/non-options model (R1's `ApplicationArguments` + `commandLineArgs` property source, the raw fallback) → bind typed `CliArgs` from that source via EXISTING [relaxed-binding]/[binder] machinery; schema validation: unknown-option / missing-required / type-mismatch as rich errors through the unified diagnostics / FailureAnalyzer surface (charter §1.7); opt-in: no declared schema ⇒ behaviour identical to R1 (lenient, no unknown-option rejection, Spring-faithful default); typed `CliArgs` registered as an injectable bean ALONGSIDE the raw `ApplicationArguments` bean + property source (raw fallback never disappears); declared-type-drives-shape: `bool`→valueless flag, `Vec<T>`→multi-valued, `PathBuf`→arity-1 positional — removing R1's CSV-vs-indexed guesswork; schema descriptor feeds build-time shell-completion + `--help` rendering (the [config-metadata] dividend); validation timing: lexing at run-pipeline parse-args step + binding/validation pass after prepare_environment (earliest richest diagnostic, charter §1.7); 'unknown arg allowed if it matches a known property prefix' rule to reconcile schema-strictness with Spring's allow-arbitrary-override leniency

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** The `#[leaf::arguments]` macro lives in leaf-macros (proc-macro=true, emits only thin code via absolute paths per the cross-crate doc's strict split); the schema descriptor type, `ArgSchema`, `ApplicationArguments`, and the validation/binding logic live in leaf-boot/leaf-core. A user's `CliArgs` is declared in the BINARY crate (or any crate), and its schema descriptor must be discoverable for the validation pass + the bean registration + completion generation — so it joins the SAME component/config-properties discovery substrate (Phase-2-undecided linkme/codegen/explicit) that [config-properties] targets use, inheriting their DCE story (a `CliArgs` in an unreferenced crate is silently absent — but typically `CliArgs` is in the binary crate, Layer-0-safe). The raw command-line property source is always-present (R1's Layer-0-safe path). R3's distinctive cross-crate surface is the SCHEMA-as-metadata: like [config-metadata], the `const ArgSchema` descriptors across the linked crates can be collected at the final binary (link-time or build-codegen) to emit a unified `--help`/completion artifact — the sqlx/Architecture-C build-time pattern the cross-crate doc favors for deterministic, platform-independent generation. This WIDENS the stable ABI: the `ArgSchema` descriptor format + the `#[leaf::arguments]` attribute grammar + the binding contract become versioned public surface (must version cleanly), on top of R1's `ApplicationArguments` accessors + `commandLineArgs` source name. Generics in an arguments struct → the macro hard-errors (no 'static descriptor for a generic). Origin-agnostic: a `CliArgs` declared in a native, integration, or test crate binds identically through the property source.

**T2 — execution context:** Two cold-path execution moments on the bootstrap task (charter §2.3), both synchronous. (1) LEXING at the run-pipeline parse-args step: identical to R1 — pure synchronous argv→neutral-model, the only OS touch is the isolated `args_os()`, producing the `Arc<ApplicationArguments>` + the property source. (2) BIND+VALIDATE pass after prepare_environment (once the command-line source is on the stack and the binder is available): synchronous binding of `CliArgs` from the command-line property source through [binder] (in-memory, non-blocking — the binder reads the lock-free sealed config stack), then schema validation (unknown-option/required/type checks) — pure CPU, no await/IO/spawn. Type-conversion of arg values (`--server-port=8080`→u16) is synchronous via [type-conversion]. Both passes are bounded, non-cancellable cold steps. The resulting `Arc<CliArgs>` (and the raw `Arc<ApplicationArguments>`) are `Send+Sync` immutable, crossing `.await`/threads freely, read lock-free by beans/runners. No global lock (charter §2.5): construct-once-freeze. Cancellation/errors: a lexing error (R1's `--=foo`) or a validation/binding error (unknown `--prot`, missing required `--input`, mistyped `--server-port`) routes into spring-application-run's handle_run_failure as a RunFailure carrying the offending token + the schema context, rendered by the FailureAnalyzer chain — the earliest richest diagnostic (charter §1.7). Because the schema is a `const` descriptor, R3 is the realization most amenable to lifting validation to BUILD time (sync, off the bootstrap task entirely) for declared-but-statically-checkable constraints — the strongest fail-even-earlier story. No async Drop (plain owned data). The post-prepare-environment placement of the validation pass is an explicit execution-context boundary the run pipeline must honor (validate after the source is sealed onto the stack, before runners).

### Rust clashes
- No global argv / no JVM `String[] args` plumbed by the runtime. Spring's `main(String[] args)` hands argv to `SpringApplication.run(args)` and it flows everywhere. Rust's `std::env::args_os()` yields `OsString` (potentially non-UTF8) and is a global the program reads itself — leaf must acquire argv ONCE in a thin `from_env()` (the `#[leaf::main]`-emitted or hand-written entry), isolate it from the pure parse fn (so tests/embedded pass explicit args), and decide an OsString→String decode policy (lossy mangles non-UTF8 silently; strict errors). There is no ambient args the framework can re-read; the value object must be the single owned plumbed truth.
- Spring's `getOptionValues` returns `List<String>` and conflates 'absent option' (null) with 'present valueless flag' (empty list) only by careful API reading. Rust models this SHARPER and must STATE the contract: `option_values(name) -> Option<&[String]>` where `None`=ABSENT (falls through first-source-wins) and `Some(&[])`=PRESENT-valueless-flag (a present-empty value that WINS first-source-wins and does NOT fall through). This makes the flag-present-vs-absent and the null-never-overrides invariant a type-level fact rather than a documented convention — a clarity win, but the present-empty-WINS rule must be loud or users expect `--debug` (valueless) to fall through to a lower source (it must not).
- Spring's `CommandLinePropertySource` adapts multi-valued options to a CSV string by default while the binder ALSO wants indexed `foo[0]`/`foo[1]` forms for list binding. There is no single right rust mapping for `--foo=a --foo=b` → property keys; leaf must pin a contract (CSV `foo=a,b` AND/OR enumerable indexed keys) coupled to [relaxed-binding]'s list/index conventions, and the never-blend invariant means the command-line source returns ONE value per key — so the CSV-vs-indexed choice is a real adaptation decision, not a transcription.
- Spring exposes non-option (positional) args under a synthetic `nonOptionArgs` property-source key as CSV. This is a JVM-shaped convention (positional args as a magic property) that may not be rust-native intent — porting it blindly risks a 'why is there a nonOptionArgs property' surprise. leaf should re-judge whether positional args belong in the property source at all, or only on the `ApplicationArguments.non_option_args()` accessor (intent-vs-mechanism, charter §2.2).
- Spring's `springApplicationArguments` singleton is registered into a GC'd container by reference and shared freely. In Rust, the SAME parsed value backs three consumers (the injectable bean, the ApplicationRunner argument, AND the command-line property source) — so it must be an `Arc<ApplicationArguments>` shared across the [container-core] singleton store and the [property-sources] adapter, NOT three copies; the ownership/handle shape (Arc vs the eventual scope/lifetime keystone's handle) is a deferred Phase-2 decision this feature must not pre-bake but must flag as needing a shared-immutable handle.
- Spring does NOT reject unknown command-line args (leniency by design — any `--whatever` becomes an available option). A rust-native typed/schema-bound approach (R3) is TEMPTED to reject unknown args for better DX (charter §1.7), which DIVERGES from intent-parity. The strict-vs-lenient choice for args is a real clash: leaf must keep the no-schema path lenient (Spring-faithful) and make schema-strictness opt-in, OR explicitly choose to diverge — and reconcile 'reject unknown' with the legitimate need to pass ad-hoc `--leaf.main.*`/`--leaf.profiles.active` overrides that are NOT in any declared schema (they must still work via the property source, schema-independently).
- Spring's parser grammar (`--key[=value]`, `--` terminator) is hard-coded in `SimpleCommandLineArgsParser`. Real Rust CLI apps overwhelmingly use `clap` (short flags, subcommands, `--key value`, typed validation). leaf faces a clash: a fixed core grammar (R1, faithful but forces a second argv interpretation for clap users) vs a parser SPI (R2, idiomatic but inherits the cross-crate DCE silent-fallback hazard). Either way leaf must avoid TWO argv interpretations (the framework's property source disagreeing with the user's clap parse) — the neutral-model-fed-by-the-chosen-parser shape (R2/R3) is the rust-native resolution, but it is not a transcription of Spring's fixed parser.
- The command-line property source's PRECEDENCE (Spring's rung 11, highest operational, above env/system-properties/SPRING_APPLICATION_JSON-analogue, below test overrides) must be expressed as DATA (a position-hint on the source descriptor applied by [property-sources]' add_first/before(name) vocabulary), NEVER as link/section order (unspecified per the cross-crate doc). Spring fixes this order in `configureEnvironment` imperatively; leaf must carry it as a deterministic descriptor-sorted placement, coordinated with [config-data]'s overall precedence-order policy (which owns the rung ordering).

### Interactions
- **spring-application-run** — OWNER OF PLACEMENT + LIFECYCLE. The run pipeline's parse-args step (Spring's 'build DefaultApplicationArguments', between listeners.starting and prepare_environment) is where THIS feature's parse runs; the run pipeline then (a) hands the parsed `ApplicationArguments` to the ApplicationRunner-analogue in call_runners (and `source_args()` to the CommandLineRunner-analogue), and (b) registers the `applicationArguments` singleton in prepare_context (Spring's register `springApplicationArguments`). A parse error routes into the run pipeline's handle_run_failure → FailureAnalyzer chain. This feature owns the parse + value object + property-source adaptation; the run pipeline owns WHERE/WHEN the parse runs, the runner argument handoff, and the singleton registration timing.
- **property-sources** — PRIMARY CONSUMER/PRODUCER SEAM. The command-line args are adapted into a `CommandLineArgsPropertySource` (origin-agnostic `dyn PropertySource` + `EnumerablePropertySource`) added to [property-sources]' ordered stack via its add_first/position-hint vocabulary, honoring first-source-wins (an option value entirely replaces a lower source), never-blend (one value per key), null-never-overrides (absent option = `None` fall-through; valueless flag = present-empty that WINS), and name-as-identity (`commandLineArgs`). This feature provides the SOURCE; [property-sources] owns the stack mechanics, the ordering vocabulary, and the lookup primitive.
- **config-data** — PRECEDENCE-ORDER COORDINATION. [config-data] owns the overall externalized-config PRECEDENCE-ORDER policy (the analogue of Boot's 15-rung order where command-line sits at rung 11, highest operational). This feature's command-line source carries a position-hint as DATA that [config-data]'s/the run pipeline's precedence assembly places at that rung — above env/system-properties/SPRING_APPLICATION_JSON-analogue, below test overrides. config-data does NOT load command-line args (those come from argv, not files), but it owns the rung-ordering this source slots into.
- **profiles** — OVERRIDE CHANNEL. A `--leaf.profiles.active=dev` command-line arg activates profiles by resolving `leaf.profiles.active` THROUGH the command-line property source via first-source-wins — so a CLI switch overrides a file-declared active-profile set (Spring's '--spring.profiles.active=dev,hsqldb can replace what a file declared'). [profiles] owns the active/include/group levers and the expression grammar; this feature is merely the highest-operational source those reserved keys resolve through, and the activation read happens during prepare_environment after this source is on the stack.
- **relaxed-binding** — ENUMERABLE + CANONICALIZATION SEAM. The command-line source must expose its option names as the `EnumerablePropertySource::keys()` so [relaxed-binding] can canonicalize (`--server-port` / `--server.port` → canonical `server.port`) and bind list/map forms; the multi-valued option → indexed-key (`foo[0]`/`foo[1]`) adaptation feeds relaxed-binding's list-binding conventions. relaxed-binding owns the canonical-form mapping; this feature owns exposing the enumerable key set and the multi-value→indexed adaptation contract. (R3 binds a typed args struct entirely through this seam.)
- **origin-tracking** — PROVENANCE PRODUCER. Every value the command-line source returns carries `Origin::CommandLine{ token_index }` (the coarse origin is the `commandLineArgs` source name; the fine origin is the argv token index), so diagnostics can attribute 'server.port = 8080 came from command-line arg #3 (--server.port=8080)'. The single-traceable-origin guarantee survives the never-blend short-circuit (the winning source's origin is returned untouched). origin-tracking owns the provenance wrapping; this feature supplies the command-line-specific origin.
- **container-core** — BEAN REGISTRATION. The parsed `ApplicationArguments` (and, in R3, the typed `CliArgs`) is registered as a pre-built injectable singleton into [container-core]'s registry (Spring's `registerSingleton(springApplicationArguments)`) by the run pipeline in prepare_context, so any bean can inject it. It is an `Arc`-shared singleton (also referenced by the property-source adapter), not a freshly-constructed bean. container-core owns the singleton store and the injection resolution; this feature supplies the pre-built value and the run pipeline performs the registration.
- **environment** — SOURCE ADDED THROUGH THE MUTATE SEAM. The command-line source is added to the stack during the cold pre-seal customize phase through [environment]'s ConfigurableEnvironment mutate seam (the same seam config-data uses), then frozen into the read view beans see. environment owns the read/mutate segregation and seal timing; this feature is a source added through that seam at a specific (highest-operational) position before seal.
- **type-conversion** — TYPED-READ DOWNSTREAM. The command-line source returns RAW string `PropertyValue`s; a typed read (`get_property_as::<u16>("server.port")` or R3's binding `--server-port=8080`→`u16`) coerces via [type-conversion] at the read/binder seam. This feature stays string-typed and never blends; conversion (and its rich type-mismatch error carrying the offending token) is layered downstream. Especially load-bearing in R3 where the typed `CliArgs` struct's fields drive conversion + validation.
- **binder** — BINDING TARGET (R3-CENTRAL). In R3 the typed `#[leaf::arguments]` struct is bound from the command-line property source through the EXISTING [binder]/[config-properties] machinery (args are 'just another property source', the struct is 'just another binding target') — the deepest unification, reusing relaxed-binding + type-conversion + strict-vs-lenient mode rather than a bespoke arg binder. binder owns the binding engine and the strict-vs-lenient policy; this feature (R3) supplies the source + the schema/Bindable target.
- **config-metadata** — SCHEMA-METADATA DIVIDEND (R3). In R3 the declared `const ArgSchema` descriptors across linked crates are the metadata source a build-time pass collects (like [config-metadata]) to emit shell-completion + a `--help` renderer — the rust-native 'declaration is the configuration' tooling story. config-metadata owns the descriptor-collection/emission pattern; this feature (R3) contributes arg-schema descriptors into it.

### Open questions for Phase 2
- Is leaf's argv parser a FIXED Spring-faithful `--key[=value]` grammar in core (R1, faithful + always-present + Layer-0-safe, but forces clap users into a second argv interpretation), a swappable origin-agnostic ArgumentParser SPI with the default grammar as fallback (R2, idiomatic + clap plugs in via the same discovery substrate, but inherits the cross-crate DCE silent-wrong-parse hazard), or a typed schema-bound declarative surface over the raw model (R3, best DX/diagnostics + deepest binder unification, but pre-judges the relaxed-binding/binder/config-metadata/diagnostics keystones)? Downstream of the cross-crate composition substrate + the unified-diagnostics keystones — must stay a candidate.
- How is the multi-valued option → property-source key adaptation pinned: CSV (`--foo=a --foo=b` → `foo=a,b`, Spring's default), enumerable indexed keys (`foo[0]`/`foo[1]` for binder list-binding), or both — and how does this coexist with [relaxed-binding]'s list/index conventions and the never-blend invariant (one value per key)? This is a cross-feature contract (this feature + relaxed-binding + binder) with no single right answer, unresolved here.
- What is the OsString→String decode policy for argv (lossy vs strict, and is it per-token — option keys must be UTF8 but a positional file path might legitimately be non-UTF8)? This couples to the broader encoding/error policy and the unified error model; left unresolved.
- Should leaf reject UNKNOWN command-line args (R3's schema-strictness, better DX, charter §1.7) or stay lenient (Spring-faithful — unknown args become available options nobody reads)? If strict, how is the legitimate need to pass ad-hoc `--leaf.main.*`/`--leaf.profiles.active` overrides NOT in any declared schema reconciled (they must still work via the property source, schema-independently)? A strict-vs-lenient + intent-parity-vs-DX tension shared with [binder]'s strict-vs-lenient keystone.
- Does the synthetic `nonOptionArgs` property-source key (Spring's mechanism exposing positional args as a CSV property) belong in leaf's command-line property source at all, or should positional args live ONLY on the `ApplicationArguments.non_option_args()` accessor (intent-vs-mechanism, charter §2.2 — re-judge a JVM-shaped convention)?
- What is the shared-immutable HANDLE shape for the parsed value that backs three consumers (the injectable singleton bean, the ApplicationRunner argument, AND the command-line property source) without copying — `Arc<ApplicationArguments>` vs the eventual scope/lifetime/ownership keystone's bean-handle? This is the deferred ownership-model keystone applied to a singleton that is also a property source, not this feature's call.
- If parser selection is an SPI (R2), how is parser DISCOVERY (which crate's parser wins) and the anti-DCE silent-fallback hazard handled — the same link-time-registry/build-codegen/explicit substrate + force-link discipline + zero-contribution self-check that config-data's source-providers and spring-application-run's deducers need? A silently-DCE'd parser yields a QUIET wrong-parse, the worst failure mode — must share ONE discovery substrate, decided uniformly across all discovery features.
- Where exactly in the run pipeline does R3's schema VALIDATION/binding pass sit (it can only run after the command-line source is on the stack AND the binder is constructed, i.e. after prepare_environment) — and can statically-checkable schema constraints be lifted to BUILD time (the RunPlan/AOT lineage) for an even-earlier diagnostic? A pipeline-placement + compile-vs-runtime-split question coupled to spring-application-run's R3 and the [binder]/[environment] sealing order.

### Notes
Scope discipline: this feature is the argv→typed-value parse + its DUAL exposure (an injectable `ApplicationArguments` value object AND a highest-operational-precedence command-line `PropertySource`), strictly plugging into — never redesigning — [property-sources] (the stack/lookup/ordering vocabulary it adds a source to), [environment] (the mutate seam + seal), [config-data] (the precedence-rung ORDER policy), [profiles] (which it overrides via the source), [relaxed-binding]/[binder]/[type-conversion] (typed/list binding downstream), [origin-tracking] (provenance), [container-core] (singleton registration), and spring-application-run (which owns WHERE/WHEN it parses, the runner-argument handoff, and the singleton-registration timing). It owns ONLY: the option/non-option grammar (`--key[=value]`, `--` terminator, multi-valued, flag-present-vs-absent), the `ApplicationArguments` value-object shape, the argv→PropertySource adaptation (multi-value→CSV/indexed, valueless-flag→present-empty, enumerable option-name keys, the `commandLineArgs` source name, `Origin::CommandLine`), and (R3) the optional typed schema layer. This was an EXPLICIT Phase-1 gap: 02-configuration-environment.md's top-level summary names 'command-line args' as a concrete SOURCE TYPE 'not a generic Map' with 'its own grammar/behavior' that 'has no owner inside this area' — this design fills it. All three realizations stay implementation-agnostic and hold the deferred §3 keystones (cross-crate discovery substrate, metadata/codegen boundary, compile-vs-runtime split, unified error/diagnostics model, scope/lifetime/ownership handle, relaxed-binding canonicalization, strict-vs-lenient default) as CANDIDATES: R1 leans Spring-faithful/fixed-grammar/always-present (Layer-0-safe, no DCE hazard), R2 leans extensible-via-parser-SPI (clap plugs in, inherits the cross-crate DCE silent-fallback hazard), R3 leans typed/schema-bound/binder-unified (best DX + diagnostics + completion, pre-judges the most neighbours) — deliberately spanning the fixed-vs-extensible-vs-typed axis so Phase 2's signal stays unbiased. Provider/registry abstractions kept ORIGIN-AGNOSTIC throughout (the command-line source is just a `dyn PropertySource`; R2's parser is an origin-agnostic SPI a native/clap/WASM-module parser implements identically). Charter alignment: parsing is pure cold-path synchronous (§2.3 — the only OS touch, `args_os()`, is isolated for testability), reads are lock-free by immutability (§2.4/§2.5 — construct-once-freeze, no global lock), the value is an `Arc`-shared single owned truth across three consumers (§5 memory discipline, no triple-copy), the macro is thin or absent (§2.10 — `from_env()` and even R3's `#[leaf::arguments]` are hand-writable, emitting only schema DATA), and the parse error / R3's validation realize §1.7 (offending token + position + known-options, rendered through spring-application-run's FailureAnalyzer chain). Three JVM-shaped mechanics flagged for the Phase-3 re-unify intent-vs-mechanism re-judgement (charter §2.2): the synthetic `nonOptionArgs` property key (positional args as a magic property — may not be rust-native intent), the CSV multi-value adaptation (the binder may prefer indexed keys exclusively), and Spring's deliberate accept-unknown-args leniency (which R3's typed strictness tempts diverging from). The single highest-leverage decision is whether the argv parser is fixed (R1) or an SPI (R2/R3), because real Rust apps use clap and leaf must AVOID two divergent argv interpretations (the framework's property source disagreeing with the user's clap parse) — the neutral-model-fed-by-the-chosen-parser shape is the rust-native resolution but inherits the discovery/DCE story. Grounding fully cross-checked: spring-boot-4-di-design.md lines 244 (build DefaultApplicationArguments), 258 (configureEnvironment adds CommandLinePropertySource + activates profiles), 293 (register springApplicationArguments singleton), 307 (CommandLineRunner raw vs ApplicationRunner parsed), 1296 (CommandLinePropertySource as an EnumerablePropertySource subtype), 1429/1435 (command-line at precedence rung 11, highest operational, the per-invocation-most-explicit-wins intent); 02-configuration-environment.md [property-sources] (the origin-agnostic source trait, first-source-wins, never-blend, null-never-overrides, enumerable facet, position-as-data) and its explicit command-line-args gap; the cross-crate doc (Layer 0/A/B DCE, force-link, ordering-as-data, the macro-emits-thin-descriptor rule); the nightly envelope (no nightly needed — Option/Arc/IndexMap/object-safe traits cover it; R2's dyn parser SPI is sync so only error-type-erasure, not future-boxing); and the run-pipeline design this sits inside (parse-args step, singleton registration in prepare_context, the runners-after-started-before-ready window consuming the parsed args).

## Context Initializers (ApplicationContextInitializer equivalent)  `[context-initializers]`

leaf's realization of Spring's ApplicationContextInitializer hook — the ordered, discoverable set of programmatic customizations applied to the freshly-created context AFTER its environment is set and the context is post-processed, but BEFORE definition sources load and BEFORE refresh runs. Per spring-boot-4-di-design.md §"ApplicationContextInitializer" (lines 287-293) and §"prepareContext" (291-293): initializers are loaded in the constructor via getSpringFactoriesInstances, then applied in prepareContext()'s applyInitializers(context) — after setEnvironment + postProcessApplicationContext (bean-name generator, resource loader, conversion service), but before sources load and before refresh; ApplicationContextInitializedEvent / contextPrepared fires immediately after. The INTENT: a precise, stable, ordered window for programmatic container customization before the container is built — the canonical things an initializer does are (a) register a BeanFactoryPostProcessor-analogue (post-processor-spi's definition-tier processor) so it runs at refresh, (b) set/activate profiles or push extra property sources onto the Environment, (c) tweak engine policy (allow-override, allow-circular, lazy-init), (d) register pre-refresh singletons or aware-state. Two origins compose in ONE @Order-sorted stream: USER initializers (registered programmatically on the Application, or via the run-hook for tests) and LIBRARY initializers (contributed by integration crates, the auto-discovery analogue of spring.factories). This feature owns ONLY the initializer hook surface — the trait/descriptor shape, the capability scope of what an initializer may legally touch (origin-agnostic, since a WASM-module or test-double initializer must participate identically), the discovery+ordering of the user+library streams, and the failure semantics — NOT the run orchestration (spring-application-run owns WHEN applyInitializers fires and the surrounding event sequence), NOT the BFPP contract an initializer registers into (post-processor-spi owns that), NOT refresh (refresh-lifecycle). It sits squarely on the run-pipeline's prepare_context() step as a contributable, ordered, capability-scoped extension point. Notably this is ALSO the seam Spring's AOT fork uses (a generated <Main>__ApplicationContextInitializer injected first, spring-boot-4-di-design.md line 321) — so the realization must accommodate a generated/codegen initializer as a first-class member of the same stream.

### Candidate realizations

#### R1 — Literal ordered initializer trait + capability-scoped ContextCustomizer handle, two origin-agnostic descriptor streams merged into one @Order-sorted application pass
Mirror ApplicationContextInitializer directly as one async trait the run-pipeline's prepare_context() drives at the canonical point. `trait ContextInitializer { fn order(&self) -> Order; async fn initialize(&self, cx: &mut ContextCustomizer<'_>) -> Result<(), InitError>; }` where ContextCustomizer is a PHASE-TYPED capability handle scoped to exactly what is legal between create_context and load_sources: it exposes (a) `register_definition_processor(desc)` to add a definition-tier (BFPP-analogue) post-processor descriptor that refresh-lifecycle will run later (post-processor-spi owns the contract; the initializer only ENQUEUES it — the literal 'register a BFPP' Spring use case); (b) `environment_mut()` returning the ConfigurableEnvironment read/mutate seam (activate profiles, push a property source); (c) `engine_policy_mut()` for the override/circular/lazy toggles container-core parks on the engine; (d) `register_singleton(name, ErasedBean)` for the pre-refresh aware-state/arg-injection use case. Crucially the handle exposes NO `get_bean()` / instance access — 'definitions not yet loaded, no bean exists' is an API-shape guarantee, not a convention (mirrors post-processor-spi R1's definition-handle). Discovery: each initializer is collected as a thin origin-agnostic `const InitializerDescriptor { order: Order, origin: Origin, make: fn(&BootstrapContext) -> BoxFuture<Result<ErasedInitializer, InitError>> }` from the SAME catalog substrate post-processor-spi/auto-configuration use (Phase-2-undecided: linkme/codegen/explicit). TWO origin streams feed ONE descriptor list: USER initializers added programmatically (`Application::add_initializer(impl ContextInitializer)` — the addInitializers analogue, the §2.10 escape hatch + the withHook single-run test injection), and LIBRARY initializers contributed by integration crates via the catalog (the spring.factories analogue). The two are MERGED then @Order-sorted into one stream (AnnotationAwareOrderComparator parity) — origin is metadata for diagnostics, not a precedence tier. The make() closure receives the transient BootstrapContext so an initializer can read a pre-container shared singleton (an expensive client a registry-initializer parked). The run-pipeline calls `apply_initializers(cx).await` which awaits each in @Order; a throw aborts the run into handle_run_failure with a rich InitError naming the initializer (by origin+order+id) and which customization it was applying. The generated-AOT initializer (the <Main>__ApplicationContextInitializer analogue) is just one more descriptor in the stream, conventionally ordered FIRST (highest precedence) — codegen emits it via the same const descriptor shape. `#[leaf::initializer]` is a THIN macro emitting a hand-writable `ContextInitializer` impl + its const descriptor with the declared Order; nothing hidden.

**Pros:** Highest intent fidelity: applyInitializers → one async pass over an @Order-sorted stream of ContextInitializer is a 1:1 map to Spring, and the capability handle's four affordances (register-BFPP, mutate-env, tweak-engine-policy, register-singleton) ARE exactly the documented things a Spring initializer does — a cargo expand / stepped trace reads like prepareContext (DX #1, §2.10 legibility, intent-not-mechanism parity).; The phase-typed ContextCustomizer enforces the load-bearing invariant ('the context exists, env is set, but NO definitions are loaded and NO bean exists') as an API SHAPE: the handle simply has no get_bean(), so 'an initializer must not instantiate beans / must only register what runs later' becomes a compile-time guarantee, not a runtime warning — directly serving §2.9 (the illegal operation is unrepresentable, the earliest possible failure).; Two-origin-into-one-sorted-stream cleanly realizes 'user + library initializers compose by @Order': origin is diagnostic metadata, not a precedence class, so a library initializer and a user initializer interleave by Order exactly as Spring's single sorted collection — and the user-programmatic path (add_initializer) is the always-works escape hatch (§2.10) that doubles as the withHook single-run test injection lane.; Origin-agnostic descriptor + ErasedInitializer keeps the surface neutral: a native, a generated-AOT (<Main>__ApplicationContextInitializer analogue, just the first-ordered descriptor), a WASM-module, or a test-double initializer all participate through the identical const-descriptor shape — no web/ecosystem knowledge leaks in, and the AOT seam Spring uses is a first-class member rather than a fork.; Delegates rather than reinvents: the initializer only ENQUEUES a definition-processor descriptor (post-processor-spi owns the BFPP contract + when it runs at refresh), mutates the Environment via environment's existing read/mutate seam, and toggles engine policy container-core already parks — so this feature stays a thin, well-bounded hook surface (§2.11) whose only owned machinery is the trait + capability handle + the two-stream merge/sort.; Async initialize() is honest: an initializer that reads remote config to decide a profile, or builds a processor from an async factory, awaits naturally on the cold bootstrap task — and because it runs single-threaded before any bean exists, the &mut ContextCustomizer held across .await is safe by execution context (no global lock, §2.5), the same discipline post-processor-spi's definition phase uses.

**Cons:** A single concrete async trait + one fixed capability handle commits early to 'these four affordances, this shape' — a future legitimate initializer need (e.g. registering an instance-tier processor, or adding a definition source directly) is a capability-handle widening (a core edit), and the handle risks either being too narrow (forcing escape hatches) or too wide (re-exposing things the phase should forbid).; The capability handle's affordances are a DUPLICATE projection of surfaces other features own (environment's mutate seam, post-processor-spi's register-processor, container-core's engine policy) — keeping ContextCustomizer coherent with those as they evolve is real coupling, and a naive design risks two ways to do the same thing (e.g. mutate env here vs at the EnvironmentPrepared hook the run already fired).; Boxed-future initialize() at the dyn boundary (AFIT not dyn-safe; the chain MUST be dyn — heterogeneous, cross-crate, origin-agnostic) is an alloc per initializer — negligible on this cold path (a handful of initializers, once per boot), but it does mean the trait surface carries Pin<Box<dyn Future + Send>> via trait_variant/hand-emitted boxing, a small ABI commitment.; Inherits the silent-DCE hazard acutely and QUIETLY: a library initializer in a crate the binary never force-links is silently absent (Layer 0), and unlike a missing bean (loud at resolution) a skipped initializer just means a tweak silently didn't happen (a profile not activated, a processor not registered) — a worse-than-the-container failure mode that mandates the anti-DCE self-check (expected-vs-found per source crate).; The 'register a singleton before refresh' affordance (Spring registers springApplicationArguments + springBootBanner here) is awkward in Rust ownership: an ErasedBean handed in pre-refresh must be promoted into the engine's singleton store at the right point, and reconciling 'who owns it until then' with the bootstrap-context-promotion the run-pipeline already does risks two promotion paths.; Order is a single number-line shared across user + library + generated-AOT initializers, but the generated-AOT one must be FIRST by convention — encoding 'this one always wins' as a reserved Order band (vs a structural 'generated runs first' rule) is a subtle precedence contract a user could accidentally collide with, a footgun the type system won't catch.

**Mechanisms considered:** one async `trait ContextInitializer { fn order(&self)->Order; async fn initialize(&self, cx:&mut ContextCustomizer) -> Result<(),InitError> }` driven by the run-pipeline's prepare_context() at the canonical applyInitializers point; phase-typed `ContextCustomizer<'_>` capability handle exposing ONLY the legal pre-refresh affordances (register_definition_processor / environment_mut / engine_policy_mut / register_singleton) and deliberately NO get_bean() — 'no instance exists yet' as an API shape; thin origin-agnostic `const InitializerDescriptor { order, origin, make }` collected via the SAME catalog substrate as post-processor-spi/auto-config (Phase-2-undecided linkme/codegen/explicit), addressed by role not a runtime type-scan; TWO origin streams (USER via Application::add_initializer / withHook single-run injection; LIBRARY via the catalog) MERGED into ONE @Order-sorted stream — origin is diagnostic metadata, not a precedence tier (AnnotationAwareOrderComparator parity); make(&BootstrapContext) so an initializer can read a pre-container shared singleton parked by a registry-initializer; the generated-AOT initializer (<Main>__ApplicationContextInitializer analogue) as one more const descriptor in the stream, conventionally ordered FIRST; boxed-future initialize() at the dyn boundary (trait_variant/hand-emitted Pin<Box<dyn Future+Send>>); cold-path alloc tolerated; thin `#[leaf::initializer]` macro emitting a hand-writable impl + its const descriptor with the declared Order; throw → abort run into handle_run_failure with a rich InitError naming initializer (origin+order+id) + which customization

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** leaf-core/leaf-boot defines the ContextInitializer trait, the InitializerDescriptor, the ContextCustomizer capability handle traits, the Order enum, and InitError; per charter §6 this is part of the leaf-boot bootstrap layer (the prepareContext step). Each initializer is collected as a thin const descriptor from the SAME catalog substrate post-processor-spi/auto-configuration/refresh-lifecycle use (Phase-2-undecided: linkme distributed-slice / build.rs codegen / explicit with(); cross-crate doc Architectures A-D) — never a runtime spring.factories scan. The TWO-ORIGIN model maps directly to the cross-crate doc's two-source duality: the LIBRARY stream is the static link-time 'classpath' (a contributing crate emits a #[distributed_slice(leaf::INITIALIZERS)] descriptor via the thin macro, with absolute paths), and the USER stream is explicit programmatic registration (Architecture D, the always-works escape hatch). This feature inherits the silent-DCE hazard QUIETLY: a library initializer in a crate the binary never force-links contributes zero (Layer 0), or is DCE'd (Layer A pre-1.62 / Layer B under LLD pre-1.89) — and a missing initializer is a SILENT skipped-tweak (worse than a loud missing-bean), so this feature participates in the entry point's mandated anti-DCE self-check (expected-vs-found initializer count per source crate, warn on enabled-feature-zero-contributions; the run-pipeline hosts the check). Generics can't carry a 'static descriptor → the macro hard-errors with a register_initializer!(Concrete) shim. The generated-AOT initializer is leaf-codegen's natural output (the <Main>__ApplicationContextInitializer analogue) emitted as the first-ordered const descriptor — so the AOT seam rides the SAME stream, not a fork. Stable cross-crate surface: the ContextInitializer trait + ContextCustomizer capability traits + Order live in leaf-core as an ABI-ish commitment the thin macro targets with absolute paths. Origin-agnostic throughout: a WASM-module-contributed initializer's make() bridges into the module and the run pipeline cannot tell it from a native one. The withHook single-run test injection is process-local (one run), threaded explicitly, not cross-crate.

**T2 — execution context:** Entirely COLD-PATH on the bootstrap task — apply_initializers runs once, between create_context and load_sources, sequentially in @Order, each initialize() an explicit .await point under the run-pipeline's startup discipline (§2.3). Because it runs single-threaded before any application bean exists, the `&mut ContextCustomizer` held across .await is safe by EXECUTION CONTEXT, not a lock — the same sidestep post-processor-spi's definition phase uses (no global lock, §2.5). An initializer may .await (read remote config to decide a profile, build a processor from an async factory) but MUST NOT block the executor (blocking work → spawn_blocking, documented discipline). It registers a definition-processor descriptor that runs LATER (at refresh-lifecycle's invokeBeanFactoryPostProcessors) — the initializer does not run it, it only enqueues, so no premature instantiation and no cross-phase aliasing. PARENT LINKAGE: apply_initializers is a child step under the run root span (startup-instrumentation), carried explicitly (no ambient thread-local current-phase across .await, the §2.3 fix). ERRORS: an initialize() throw aborts the whole pass all-or-nothing and routes to the run's handle_run_failure with a rich InitError (which initializer by origin+order+id, which customization, the cause chain) — and because nothing is instantiated yet, the abort surface is small (no beans to tear down; teardown is the run's cancelRefresh/no-context-close path). NO async Drop: an initializer holding a resource participates in the explicit awaited teardown, never Drop. CANCELLATION of the bootstrap task mid-pass unwinds the in-flight initialize() and routes to the run's pre-refresh failure path. The ContextInitializedEvent the run fires immediately after this pass dispatches on the run's standalone early-multicaster (the context's multicaster does not exist yet) — ordered, not busy-waiting (§2.4).

#### R2 — Unified ContextCustomizer 'contribution' over a single capability-scoped CustomizeCtx, sharing post-processor-spi's contributor primitive — the initializer is just a definition-stage contributor running at a pre-refresh stage
Question whether the initializer deserves its OWN trait at all. Spring keeps ApplicationContextInitializer separate from BeanFactoryPostProcessor only because they run at different lifecycle points (initializer in prepareContext, BFPP at refresh) — but BOTH 'mutate the not-yet-built container'. So UNIFY: model the initializer as a contribution at a NEW pre-refresh STAGE of the SAME contributor pipeline post-processor-spi R3 proposes. Reuse that feature's `Contributor` primitive (one trait, one ordered list, one discovery path, stages-as-data) and add a `Stage::ContextInitialize` that fires in prepare_context() BEFORE Stage::RegistryEdit/DefinitionEdit (which fire at refresh). `trait Contributor { fn id(&self)->ContributorId; fn stages(&self)->StageSet; fn order(&self)->Order; async fn run(&self, stage: Stage, cx:&mut StageCtx<'_>) -> Result<(),PpError>; }` — an 'initializer' is simply a Contributor whose StageSet contains ContextInitialize. At that stage StageCtx is the capability-typed handle exposing the pre-refresh affordances (env mutate, engine policy, register a singleton, AND — uniquely possible because it is the same primitive — enqueue itself or another contributor for a LATER stage). The run-pipeline's prepare_context() runs `contributors.run_stage(ContextInitialize, cx).await` over the @Order-sorted subset whose StageSet opted into that stage. The killer property: leaf's OWN pre-refresh setup (register the args/banner singletons, install the standard infrastructure-processor descriptors, the generated-AOT wiring) and a user/library initializer are the SAME Contributor type at the SAME stage with the SAME ordering — perfectly symmetric dogfooding, ONE discovery path, ONE self-check surface for the whole container-extension space (initializers + BFPPs + BPPs). A user 'initializer that registers a BFPP' becomes a Contributor that opts into BOTH ContextInitialize (to do early env work) AND RegistryEdit (to add defs) — or, more idiomatically, the ContextInitialize-stage run() simply marks another contributor active, since they share the list. `#[leaf::initializer]` and `#[leaf::component(post_processor)]` both emit a Contributor descriptor differing only in their StageSet.

**Pros:** Maximal unification (§2.11, the charter's stated goal): initializers and post-processors stop being two discovery paths, two self-check surfaces, two ordering models — they are ONE Contributor pipeline where 'initializer' vs 'BFPP' vs 'BPP' is a StageSet flag. The smallest stable kernel ABI the macros target, and the fewest concepts to learn (DX #1): 'a contribution runs at the stage(s) it declares'.; ONE ordered list with a single global Order makes cross-cutting precedence reason about one number line: a user wanting their ContextInitialize work to precede a library's, and their RegistryEdit to follow the framework's, expresses both with Order on one contributor — no separate initializer-order vs processor-order regimes to reconcile (a real simplification over R1's two streams + post-processor-spi's separate ordering).; Perfectly symmetric dogfooding: leaf's own pre-refresh setup (args/banner singleton registration, standard infrastructure-processor installation, the AOT wiring) uses the IDENTICAL mechanism a user/library initializer uses — no privileged path, the exact 'extend the framework with the mechanism the framework uses on itself' property Spring prizes, extended to the initializer point Spring left as a separate trait.; ONE catalog/discovery path means ONE anti-DCE self-check (expected-vs-found contributors by stage, with per-source provenance) covers initializers AND processors — instead of R1 needing a separate initializer self-check on top of post-processor-spi's processor self-check. The entry point's worst silent-failure trap gets a single defense surface.; Naturally subsumes the AOT seam: the generated <Main>__ApplicationContextInitializer is a generated Contributor with StageSet={ContextInitialize}, conventionally first-ordered — no special fork, it is the same primitive leaf-codegen emits for any contributor (post-processor-spi R2/R3 already contemplate codegen contributors).; Future pre-refresh extension points are a new Stage variant + StageCtx case (e.g. a post-environment-prepared stage, a post-load-sources stage) rather than a new trait + a new discovery path — the SPI is open to new lifecycle hooks without churning the surface, exactly post-processor-spi R3's evolvability dividend extended to the run pipeline.

**Cons:** Hard PRE-DECIDES post-processor-spi's open question (do the tiers unify into one Contributor primitive — R3 — or stay distinct traits — R1?): this realization only works if post-processor-spi chose unification, so adopting it HERE biases that Phase-2 keystone, exactly the §3 pre-judgment the charter forbids. It must stay strictly a CANDIDATE contingent on post-processor-spi R3.; Collapses a distinction Spring deliberately keeps: ApplicationContextInitializer and BeanFactoryPostProcessor are conceptually different (programmatic-customization-of-the-context vs definition-rewriting) and run in different phases for a reason. A single Contributor-with-a-stage-tag risks blurring 'I customize the context' vs 'I rewrite definitions', weakening the teachable mental model for the entry point — the place users most need a crisp story.; StageCtx as a stage-tagged capability enum means every initializer's run() matches on the stage it expects and must handle wrong-stage arms (the recurring uniformity-vs-type-safety tradeoff post-processor-spi R3 itself flags) — a class of unreachable-but-must-handle arms a dedicated ContextInitializer trait (R1) avoids, cutting against DX for the simple single-stage initializer.; A single run(stage, cx) is LESS type-safe than R1's dedicated initialize(): a contributor that mishandles the ContextInitialize stage it tagged fails at runtime, not compile time — a §2.9 cost (later, less-legible failure) at the bootstrap layer where rich-early diagnostics matter most.; Coupling the initializer surface to post-processor-spi's contributor lifecycle means this feature can't be designed/shipped independently — it inherits all of post-processor-spi R3's open questions (the boxed-future standard, the two-source duality, the stage-enum-as-wide-ABI commitment) plus the run-pipeline's, a larger blast radius for a feature that is conceptually a thin hook.; The 'one contributor opts into both ContextInitialize and RegistryEdit' idiom is powerful but subtle: a contributor doing early env work at ContextInitialize AND adding defs at RegistryEdit must reason about TWO phase contexts and the time gap between them (initialize runs in prepare_context, RegistryEdit at refresh) — re-introducing the cross-phase reasoning the separate-trait model keeps simple.

**Mechanisms considered:** reuse post-processor-spi R3's single `Contributor` primitive (one trait, one ordered list, one discovery path, stages-as-data) and add a `Stage::ContextInitialize` firing in prepare_context() before the refresh-time stages; an 'initializer' = a Contributor whose StageSet contains ContextInitialize; 'BFPP' = StageSet contains RegistryEdit/DefinitionEdit — tiers as data; stage-typed StageCtx at ContextInitialize exposing the pre-refresh affordances (env mutate / engine policy / register singleton / enqueue another contributor for a later stage); run-pipeline prepare_context() runs contributors.run_stage(ContextInitialize, cx).await over the @Order-sorted opted-in subset; ONE global Order across all contributors and all stages — initializer-order and processor-order on one number line; leaf's own pre-refresh setup (args/banner singletons, standard infra-processor install, AOT wiring) as ordinary Contributors at ContextInitialize — symmetric dogfooding; the generated-AOT initializer as a generated Contributor with StageSet={ContextInitialize}, first-ordered; ONE catalog discovery path + ONE anti-DCE self-check (contributors-by-stage) covering initializers AND processors; #[leaf::initializer] and #[leaf::component(post_processor)] both emit a Contributor descriptor differing only in StageSet; boxed-future run() at the dyn boundary (AFIT not dyn-safe), sync fast-paths reserved for post-processor-spi's per-bean hot sub-hooks (not relevant to ContextInitialize)

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** Strongest unification fit for the cross-crate doc: leaf-core defines ONE Contributor trait + the Stage/StageCtx/Order/ContributorId vocabulary (shared with post-processor-spi), so there is ONE descriptor stream, ONE catalog substrate (Phase-2 linkme/codegen/explicit), and ONE anti-DCE self-check surface covering initializers AND processors — the smallest stable kernel ABI the thin macros target (a contributor descriptor with a StageSet differing only in which stages it opts into). A library initializer is a Contributor descriptor contributed by an integration crate (the static link-time 'classpath'); a user initializer is explicit programmatic registration (Architecture D); the generated-AOT initializer is leaf-codegen's emitted Contributor — all three feed the ONE stream, origin-agnostic (a WASM-module contributor's run() bridges into the module identically). This INHERITS post-processor-spi's open question as a hard dependency: the realization is only valid if post-processor-spi unifies (R3); adopting it here pre-judges that keystone, so it is a CANDIDATE contingent on that choice (a phase2Question). The silent-DCE hazard is shared with the whole contributor space — but the single self-check is a dividend (expected-vs-found contributors by stage, per-source provenance, fail/warn loud) rather than a separate initializer check. The wide cost: the Stage enum becomes a wider ABI commitment (adding ContextInitialize, and any future pre-refresh stage, extends the enum the whole workspace's contributors match on) — a semver surface that must version cleanly. Generics can't register a contributor (no 'static symbol until instantiated) → macro hard-errors with a register-concrete shim. CANDIDATES throughout, not a decision; the run-pipeline still hosts the force-link discipline + the self-check.

**T2 — execution context:** COLD-PATH on the bootstrap task, identical execution discipline to R1: the run-pipeline's prepare_context() drives run_stage(ContextInitialize) once, sequentially in global Order, each run() an .await point single-threaded before any application bean exists — so the &mut StageCtx held across .await is safe by execution context (no global lock, §2.5), the same sidestep post-processor-spi's definition stages use. The ContextInitialize stage runs STRICTLY before the refresh-time stages (RegistryEdit/DefinitionEdit at invokeBeanFactoryPostProcessors), so a contributor opting into both runs its early work now and its def-rewriting later — the engine's stage-phase sequencing enforces the gap (post-processor-spi R3's RegistryEdit-before-DefinitionEdit policy extended with ContextInitialize-before-everything). A contributor may .await but MUST NOT block (spawn_blocking otherwise, §2.3). PARENT LINKAGE: the stage is a child step under the run root span (startup-instrumentation), carried explicitly. ERRORS: a run() throw at ContextInitialize aborts all-or-nothing into the run's handle_run_failure with a rich PpError naming the contributor id + stage + which customization (§2.9) — small abort surface (nothing instantiated yet). NO async Drop → a contributor holding a resource participates in explicit awaited teardown. CANCELLATION mid-stage unwinds the in-flight run() into the run's pre-refresh failure path. Because run() at ContextInitialize is async/boxed at the dyn boundary, there is one alloc per initializer per boot — negligible cold-path cost. The ContextInitializedEvent the run fires after this stage dispatches on the standalone early-multicaster (context's multicaster not yet built), ordered, not busy-waiting (§2.4).

#### R3 — Declarative customization-record initializers: an initializer DECLARES a typed set of CustomizationOps (data) rather than imperatively mutating a handle; the run applies the ops, enabling a build-time-frozen initializer plan + a runtime overlay lane
Push the AOT/declarative lineage hardest and question whether an initializer should be imperative code at all. Most real initializers do a SMALL, ENUMERABLE set of things: activate profiles, add a property source, register a definition-processor descriptor, set an engine-policy toggle, register a pre-refresh singleton. So model an initializer as a function that RETURNS a typed `Customization { profile_activations: Vec<Profile>, property_sources: Vec<PropertySourceDesc>, processor_descriptors: Vec<DefinitionProcessorDesc>, engine_policy: PolicyOverlay, pre_refresh_singletons: Vec<(BeanName, ErasedBean)> }` — a DECLARATIVE record of WHAT to customize, not imperative mutation of a handle. `trait ContextInitializer { fn order(&self)->Order; async fn customize(&self, cx:&CustomizeInput<'_>) -> Result<Customization, InitError>; }` where CustomizeInput is a READ-ONLY view (the prepared Environment, the BootstrapContext shared singletons, the deduced app-type) — the initializer reads, decides, and returns a record; the RUN-PIPELINE applies the merged-and-ordered records to the context. The win: the customization records are INSPECTABLE DATA. A build-time/codegen pass (leaf-codegen reading the resolved feature graph) can pre-compute the records of all statically-knowable initializers (most library initializers are pure given the feature set), merge+order them, validate them (no two property sources collide, every processor descriptor resolves, profile activations are consistent), and FREEZE an `InitializerPlan` artifact (Architecture C, sqlx model) the runtime simply applies — so the ordering, validation, and the bulk of the work move to BUILD time, and the runtime apply is a thin data-driven pass. Initializers whose customize() genuinely needs runtime values (reads the now-loaded Environment, an async remote read) run at runtime and their records OVERLAY the frozen plan in @Order. A user initializer (programmatic / withHook) is always a runtime-overlay record. Validation moves EARLIEST: a colliding/contradictory customization (two initializers both setting incompatible engine policy, a property source that shadows another, a profile activation that contradicts a profile group) fails at BUILD or at a dedicated startup-validation pass with complete context and ZERO side effects. `#[leaf::initializer]` emits the customize() impl; a const-foldable customize() (one returning a fixed record) is detected and its record baked into the plan.

**Pros:** Most declarative + inspectable: an initializer's effect is a typed DATA record, not opaque imperative mutation — 'what does this initializer do to my context' is readable data a test can assert over and a tool can dump (the sqlx --check lineage, §2.10 thin-macro legibility), instead of emergent runtime behaviour. The bootstrap layer's customization becomes auditable.; Earliest + richest fail-fast (§2.9, charter §1.7): because customizations are data, the build/plan pass can VALIDATE the merged set — colliding property sources, contradictory engine-policy overlays, an unresolvable processor descriptor, inconsistent profile activations — at BUILD time (or a startup-validation pass) BEFORE any side effect, with complete context. The predictable initializer mistakes surface as a build error, the purest 'a context that started is a context that works'.; Best fit for the AOT lineage + §3 compile-vs-runtime keystone applied to THIS seam: Spring's AOT fork already injects a generated initializer first (line 321); R3 generalizes that — the ordering, merge, and validation of the WHOLE initializer set move to build time, the runtime apply is a thin data-driven pass over a frozen InitializerPlan, and the generated-AOT initializer is just the plan itself rather than a special member.; Sidesteps the &mut-handle-across-await aliasing entirely: customize() takes a READ-ONLY CustomizeInput and returns an owned record, so there is no shared mutable context handle held across .await — the run-pipeline applies the records single-threaded afterward. The cleanest answer to the aliasing clash R1/R2 resolve only by execution context.; Strongest cross-crate determinism (Architecture C / sqlx model — the cross-crate doc's most-reliable, fully platform-independent path incl. wasm): a build-time cargo-metadata-driven plan ENUMERATES declared integration crates' initializers and emits them as frozen records, sidestepping all three DCE layers — the anti-DCE self-check becomes a build-time manifest cross-check (--check-able in CI) rather than a fragile runtime count, turning the entry point's worst silent-failure trap into a deterministic build gate.; The merge step makes user+library composition EXPLICIT and analyzable: 'user initializer overlays library initializer at this Order' is a visible merge in the plan, and a runtime-overlay record (a user/withHook initializer the plan didn't anticipate) is a clearly-marked overlay lane — composition is data, not interleaved imperative side effects.

**Cons:** Diverges MOST from Spring's imperative ApplicationContextInitializer mental model and pre-judges the §3 compile-vs-runtime AND metadata/codegen keystones the hardest — presenting a frozen-plan declarative initializer as THE shape strongly biases Phase-2's signal; must be held strictly as a CANDIDATE, and its value is only as large as the fraction of initializers expressible as a fixed CustomizationOp set.; The enumerable Customization record is a CLOSED set of op kinds (activate profile / add property source / register processor / set policy / register singleton) — an initializer that wants to do something OUTSIDE that set (a genuinely novel context mutation) has no slot and must fall back to an imperative escape hatch, partly defeating the declarative shape; choosing the op vocabulary completely is itself a design risk (too narrow = escape hatches everywhere; too wide = re-imperative).; Several initializer effects are inherently runtime: an initializer that reads the now-loaded Environment (post-EnvironmentPrepared) to decide a profile, or builds a processor from an async remote read, cannot be frozen — so the plan needs a runtime-overlay lane plus a conservative build-time over-approximation, partially reintroducing the dynamism it sought to eliminate, and the two computation modes (build-time-frozen + runtime-overlay) must produce coherent results.; Two authoring/computation models (a const-foldable customize() baked into the plan vs a runtime customize() returning an overlay record) is more total machinery and more concepts than R1's single imperative pass — and keeping the frozen plan and the runtime overlay coherent (same merge order, same validation) is a real burden for a feature that is conceptually a thin hook.; The dynamic WASM-module / withHook test initializer has NO build-time presence, so it can only contribute through the runtime-overlay lane — a direct tension with the freeze-at-build shape, forcing a runtime re-merge that erodes the frozen-plan simplicity for exactly the test/plugin cases (the same tension the run-pipeline R3 flags).; The InitializerPlan + the Customization record format become a stable ABI/format commitment that must version cleanly across leaf releases — a heavier surface than R1's trait, and overkill for a small CLI app whose two initializers could trivially run imperatively.
