**Mechanisms considered:** initializer DECLARES a typed `Customization` record (profile_activations / property_sources / processor_descriptors / engine_policy overlay / pre_refresh_singletons) rather than imperatively mutating a handle; `trait ContextInitializer { fn order(&self)->Order; async fn customize(&self, cx:&CustomizeInput) -> Result<Customization,InitError> }` where CustomizeInput is READ-ONLY (env view, bootstrap singletons, app-type); run-pipeline applies the merged-and-@Order-ed customization records to the context after collecting them — a thin data-driven apply pass; build-time/codegen pass (leaf-codegen over the resolved feature graph) pre-computes statically-knowable initializers' records, merges+orders+validates them, and FREEZES an InitializerPlan (Architecture C, sqlx model); runtime-overlay lane: initializers needing runtime values (loaded env, async read) run at runtime and their records overlay the frozen plan in @Order; user/withHook initializers are always overlay records; build/plan-time VALIDATION: colliding property sources, contradictory engine-policy overlays, unresolvable processor descriptors, inconsistent profile activations fail with complete context, zero side effects; const-foldable customize() (returning a fixed record) detected and baked into the plan; non-const customize() deferred to the overlay lane; the generated-AOT initializer subsumed as the plan itself (not a special stream member); #[leaf::initializer] emits the customize() impl; closed CustomizationOp vocabulary as the typed surface

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** This is the realization confronting 'discover library initializers without a classpath' via the cross-crate doc's most-reliable path (Architecture C, sqlx model). A build.rs / cargo-leaf-prepare in the binary crate reads the resolved dependency graph (cargo metadata) + a manifest convention, computes the statically-knowable initializers' Customization records, merges+orders+validates them, and emits a frozen InitializerPlan into OUT_DIR (or a checked-in --check-able artifact), include!'d into the binary — sidestepping Layer 0 (the plan ENUMERATES declared integration crates and emits force-link references), Layer A (rustc reachability), and Layer B (--gc-sections) ENTIRELY, and being platform-independent incl. wasm/embedded where linkme fails. The anti-DCE self-check becomes a BUILD-TIME manifest cross-check (expected-vs-found initializer per declared crate, --check fails CI on a silently-lost contribution) — strictly more reliable than R1/R2's runtime count, turning the entry point's worst silent-failure trap into a deterministic gate. Ordering+merge+validation are plan-time, so link/registration order is irrelevant (honouring §170: never rely on link order). BUT it cannot scan crates the build doesn't know about: it enumerates DECLARED integration crates via metadata, not a true classpath; a dynamic WASM-module source or a withHook test initializer has NO build-time presence → it contributes through a runtime-overlay lane (a phase2Question). Origin-agnostic: a declared native and a build-known integration initializer are planned identically; a runtime-overlay (WASM-module / test) initializer joins via the same apply pass but bypasses the plan. The InitializerPlan format + the Customization record + the ContextInitializer trait in leaf-core/leaf-boot become a stable ABI/format commitment (must version cleanly). leaf-codegen (proc-macro/build crates isolated from runtime, charter §6) owns plan emission; leaf-boot owns the apply pass. This pre-judges the metadata/codegen + compile-vs-runtime keystones hardest — CANDIDATE only, its scope bounded to the statically-knowable initializer fraction.

**T2 — execution context:** The PLAN phase is SYNCHRONOUS cold-path/build-time work (single-threaded, no IO into the running app, before the binary runs or in a dedicated runtime validation pass) — pure analysis producing the InitializerPlan + the earliest (build-time) diagnostics. The runtime side: customize() of runtime-overlay initializers runs async on the bootstrap task (an initializer reading the loaded Environment or doing a remote read awaits; blocking → spawn_blocking, §2.3), but because customize() takes a READ-ONLY CustomizeInput and returns an OWNED Customization record, there is NO shared mutable context handle held across .await — the aliasing clash R1/R2 resolve only by execution context is sidestepped structurally. The run-pipeline then APPLIES the merged plan-plus-overlay records to the context single-threaded, in @Order, after all customize() calls complete — a thin synchronous data-driven pass (apply profile activations, push property sources, enqueue processor descriptors, set engine policy, register pre-refresh singletons), no .await, no lock (§2.5). PARENT LINKAGE: the apply pass is a child step under the run root span (startup-instrumentation), explicit. ERRORS: build/plan-time validation failures are compile/prepare errors with complete context; a runtime customize() throw or an apply-time conflict aborts all-or-nothing into the run's handle_run_failure with a rich InitError (which initializer, which CustomizationOp, the conflict) — small abort surface (nothing instantiated). NO async Drop → an initializer holding a resource participates in explicit awaited teardown. CANCELLATION mid-customize() unwinds the in-flight read into the run's pre-refresh failure path; because apply is synchronous and post-collection, a cancellation never leaves a half-applied context. The ContextInitializedEvent the run fires after apply dispatches on the standalone early-multicaster, ordered, not busy-waiting (§2.4).

### Rust clashes
- No spring.factories runtime SPI loading + no runtime classpath. Spring loads ApplicationContextInitializers in the SpringApplication constructor via getSpringFactoriesInstances (a spring.factories scan), then applies them in prepareContext — a classpath query Rust cannot do (no global classpath, no runtime reflection). leaf must collect each initializer as a thin origin-agnostic 'static const descriptor from a SCOPED catalog (static link-time registry for the LIBRARY stream + optional dynamic source; Phase-2-undecided linkme/codegen/explicit) PLUS explicit programmatic registration for the USER stream, addressed by ROLE, never a runtime type-scan. This inherits the silent-DCE failure mode QUIETLY: a missing initializer is a silently-skipped tweak (a profile not activated, a processor not registered), worse than a loud missing-bean — mandating the anti-DCE self-check.
- No CGLIB/proxy and the initializer must only ENQUEUE, never instantiate. Spring's initializer registers a BeanFactoryPostProcessor that runs LATER at refresh; it must NOT instantiate beans (definitions are not loaded yet). In leaf this 'register what runs later, touch no instance' rule must be an API SHAPE: the capability handle (R1 ContextCustomizer / R2 StageCtx) exposes NO get_bean(), so 'no instance exists yet' is unrepresentable rather than a runtime warning — and the registered definition-processor descriptor (post-processor-spi's contract) is enqueued origin-agnostically so a WASM-module/test-double processor is enqueued identically.
- &mut context handle across .await over a not-yet-built container. Spring's initializer freely mutates the live ConfigurableApplicationContext; an async leaf initializer holding &mut ContextCustomizer across an .await collides with Rust aliasing/Send. R1/R2 resolve this by EXECUTION CONTEXT (the apply pass runs single-threaded on the cold path before any bean exists, so the &mut handle is never aliased), the same sidestep post-processor-spi's definition phase uses; R3 sidesteps it STRUCTURALLY (customize() takes a read-only input and returns an owned record, no shared mutable handle). Either way leaf must NOT reach for a global lock (§2.5).
- async fn in traits is not dyn-compatible, but the initializer chain MUST be dyn. The stream is heterogeneous, cross-crate-contributed, and origin-agnostic (incl. WASM-module sources), so the async initialize()/customize()/run() hook at the dyn boundary must return a boxed future (Pin<Box<dyn Future + Send>> via trait_variant or hand-emitted boxing — AFIT/RPITIT desugar to opaque non-object-safe types). This is one alloc per initializer per boot — negligible on this cold path (a handful of initializers, once), but it is a real ABI shape the thin macro emits and a small stable commitment.
- No GC-mopped failed init; no async Drop. Spring can rely on GC to clean up if an initializer throws mid-prepareContext. In Rust there is no GC AND no async Drop (nightly doc: AsyncDrop experimental-incomplete with tokio-shutdown crashes — avoid), so an initializer that throws aborts the run all-or-nothing into the run-pipeline's handle_run_failure, and any resource an initializer opened is torn down via the explicit awaited container-driven pass (the run's pre-refresh cancelRefresh path) — never a Drop, never a forget. Because nothing is instantiated yet at applyInitializers, the abort surface is small.
- The generated-AOT initializer (<Main>__ApplicationContextInitializer) must be a first-class member of the SAME stream, not a fork. Spring's AOT fork injects a generated initializer FIRST (line 321). In leaf the generated/codegen initializer (leaf-codegen's natural output) must ride the identical const-descriptor / contributor / plan shape as native+library initializers, conventionally first-ordered — so the AOT seam is one more member of the ordered stream (R1/R2) or the plan itself (R3), never special-cased machinery the user can't inspect (§2.10).
- The withHook single-run test initializer must be threaded explicitly, not via a thread-local across .await. Spring's getRunListeners consults a thread-local SpringApplicationHook to inject a single-run participant; a thread-local read at an arbitrary .await suspension point is hazardous in async Rust (the §2.3 ThreadLocal-across-await concern). leaf must carry the single-run initializer (the test-slice injection lane) as an EXPLICIT value threaded through the run (or a task-local with documented semantics), joined into the @Order-sorted stream as a runtime-overlay member — not an ambient thread-local read.
- User-vs-library ordering is ONE @Order number-line, not a precedence tier — but no link/registration order may be trusted. Spring sorts ALL initializers (constructor-loaded library + addInitializers user) as one AnnotationAwareOrderComparator stream. The cross-crate doc warns link-time/constructor order is UNSPECIFIED (may be deliberately randomized), so leaf must encode order as DATA (an Order field on each descriptor) resolved by an explicit sort, never inferred from registration order — a stricter discipline than Spring needs, and origin (user/library/generated) is diagnostic metadata, NOT a precedence class.
- The capability surface duplicates seams other features own — must stay a thin projection, origin-agnostic. The legal pre-refresh affordances (mutate the Environment, register a definition-processor, toggle engine policy, register a pre-refresh singleton) are projections of environment's read/mutate seam, post-processor-spi's register-processor contract, and container-core's engine policy. leaf must expose them as a coherent capability-scoped handle without creating a SECOND way to do the same thing (e.g. mutate env here vs at the EnvironmentPrepared hook the run already fired) — and the handle/record must stay origin-agnostic so a WASM-module/test-double initializer customizes identically.
- The ContextInitializer trait / contributor stage / InitializerPlan format becomes a cross-crate ABI with no classpath to anchor it. Spring's initializer interface is agreed by convention within one JVM. In leaf, integration crates depend on the trait (R1), the shared contributor primitive + Stage enum (R2), or the Customization record + InitializerPlan format (R3), so leaf must PUBLISH them as a versioned public surface (an ABI-ish commitment in leaf-core/leaf-boot) — like the run-listener event-name taxonomy, but for the initializer surface.

### Interactions
- **spring-application-run** — PRIMARY PARENT / the orchestrator that drives this hook. The run-pipeline's prepare_context() step calls apply_initializers(cx).await at the canonical point — AFTER set_environment + post_process_context (name-generator/conversion-service), BEFORE load_sources, BEFORE refresh — and fires ContextInitialized/Prepared immediately after. This feature owns the initializer HOOK SURFACE (the trait/descriptor, capability scope, two-stream merge+sort, failure semantics); the run owns WHEN it fires, the surrounding event sequence, the BootstrapContext the initializer reads, the force-link discipline + anti-DCE self-check, and routing an initializer throw into handle_run_failure. The USER stream is the run's add_initializer/withHook surface; the LIBRARY stream is the run's catalog.
- **post-processor-spi** — PRIMARY DOWNSTREAM / the contract an initializer registers into. The canonical initializer use case is registering a definition-tier (BFPP-analogue) post-processor that refresh-lifecycle runs later — so the capability handle's register_definition_processor enqueues a post-processor-spi descriptor; the initializer only ENQUEUES, never runs it. R2 goes further: it UNIFIES the initializer onto post-processor-spi R3's single Contributor primitive (initializer = a contributor at a new Stage::ContextInitialize) — making R2 contingent on post-processor-spi choosing unification. This feature stays proxy/processor-mechanism-neutral; post-processor-spi owns the BFPP/BPP contract and when it fires.
- **environment** — MUTATED via the capability handle. A core initializer affordance is activating profiles and pushing extra property sources onto the Environment using environment's ConfigurableEnvironment read/mutate seam — but this fires LATER than the run's prepare_environment/EnvironmentPrepared hook (where config-data ran), so the initializer sees a fully-prepared Environment and adds late, programmatic tweaks. The clash to avoid: two ways to mutate env (here vs at EnvironmentPrepared). environment owns the abstraction; this feature owns the pre-refresh mutate window.
- **profiles** — ACTIVATED via an initializer (one of the documented uses). An initializer may set active profiles programmatically before definitions load — feeding profiles' active/include/group levers so the active-profile set is decided before the container filters @Profile-gated beans at refresh. Activation is itself a property read through the same stack; this feature provides the pre-refresh programmatic activation slot, profiles owns the activation semantics.
- **container-core** — the context the initializer customizes + engine-policy toggles. The initializer's capability handle toggles the engine policies container-core parks on the engine (allow-override, allow-circular, lazy-init) before refresh — the prepareContext step that configures the bean factory before sources load. container-core fixes the engine-vs-facade split and where the policies live; this feature provides the pre-refresh window to set them programmatically, origin-agnostically.
- **refresh-lifecycle** — DOWNSTREAM consumer of what the initializer enqueued. Everything an initializer registers (a definition-processor descriptor, an engine policy, an activated profile) takes effect when refresh-lifecycle runs its fixed-order template AFTER apply_initializers returns — the enqueued BFPP-analogue runs at invokeBeanFactoryPostProcessors, the policy gates the bean factory, the profile filters @Profile beans. refresh-lifecycle never sees initializers directly; it consumes their effects. The initializer pass is strictly before refresh; refresh is all-or-nothing after.
- **auto-configuration** — SIBLING discovery + the library-initializer origin. Library initializers are contributed by integration crates exactly as auto-configurations are — the same catalog substrate, the same force-link discipline, the same 'adding a starter (Cargo feature) expresses intent + must link the crate' mental model, and the same anti-DCE self-check. An auto-configuration's enabling wiring and a library initializer often ship in the same integration crate; both key off the resolved capability/feature set. This feature shares auto-configuration's two-source duality and silent-DCE hazard.
- **events** — OBSERVED via the event the run fires after this pass. The run fires ContextInitialized/Prepared immediately after apply_initializers, on the run's STANDALONE early-multicaster (the context's multicaster does not exist yet — early listeners cannot be beans). This feature does not fire the event itself (the run does) but its completion IS the trigger; the early-vs-context multicaster handoff and early-event-buffering concern are shared with the run-pipeline and refresh-lifecycle. Whether the run reuses events' substrate or a distinct early channel is a deferred events meta-question.
- **startup-instrumentation** — INSTRUMENTED as a child step. apply_initializers is a named child step (e.g. leaf.context.apply-initializers) under the run root span; each initializer's run can nest as a sub-step so a slow library initializer is visible in the startup trace. Parent linkage is carried explicitly (no ambient thread-local current-phase across .await, the §2.3 fix). On an initializer failure the in-flight step is tagged with the outcome for boot-failure forensics — sharing the diagnostics spirit with the run's FailureAnalysis.
- **context-close** — TEARDOWN on the failure path (indirect, via the run). Because there is no async Drop, an initializer that opened a resource and then the pass (or a later phase) fails participates in the explicit awaited teardown the run drives — but since apply_initializers runs BEFORE refresh, a failure here routes to the run's pre-refresh cancelRefresh path (no ContextClosedEvent, nothing instantiated to destroy), NOT the full context-close. context-close owns the post-Refreshed teardown; this feature's failures are pre-Refreshed.
- **task-execution** — EXECUTION-CONTEXT SOURCE. apply_initializers runs on the bootstrap task; an initializer that awaits (remote read to decide a profile, async processor factory) uses task-execution's executor, and a blocking initializer must spawn_blocking (explicit execution-context discipline the run documents and threads through, §2.3). This is a cold-path, single-threaded pass — no concurrency among initializers (they run sequentially in @Order), so no creation guard is involved here.

### Open questions for Phase 2
- Is the initializer its OWN dedicated trait (R1 — highest intent fidelity, crisp 'customize the context' surface, but a second discovery+ordering+self-check path alongside post-processor-spi) or UNIFIED onto post-processor-spi's single Contributor primitive as a new pre-refresh Stage::ContextInitialize (R2 — maximal unification §2.11, one discovery path, one self-check, but HARD-DEPENDS on post-processor-spi choosing R3 unification and blurs Spring's deliberate initializer-vs-BFPP distinction) or a DECLARATIVE customization-record that enables a build-time-frozen InitializerPlan (R3 — AOT/sqlx determinism + earliest fail-fast + structurally avoids the &mut-across-await clash, but pre-judges the compile-vs-runtime keystone hardest and needs a runtime-overlay lane for dynamic/test initializers)? This is the initializer-surface shape, downstream of the §3 compile-vs-runtime + metadata/codegen keystones AND of post-processor-spi's own unify-or-not question — must stay a candidate.
- Does the initializer surface UNIFY with post-processor-spi (R2's bet), and is that decision made HERE or there? R2 only works if post-processor-spi unified its tiers into one Contributor primitive (its own R3); adopting R2 here would pre-judge that keystone. Conversely if post-processor-spi stays two distinct traits (its R1), the initializer naturally wants its own trait (R1 here). The two features' unify-or-not decisions are coupled and must be resolved together, not independently — a cross-feature meta-architecture call on whether 'customize the context' and 'rewrite definitions' are one extension primitive or two.
- Which cross-crate substrate collects the LIBRARY initializer stream (and is it the SAME one post-processor-spi/auto-configuration/the run-participant registries use)? linkme (zero-cost, DCE-sensitive, no wasm), inventory (DCE-robust, wasm, but life-before-main is hostile to async registration), build-time codegen (Architecture C, deterministic, R3's natural fit + the force-link + build-time anti-DCE manifest), or explicit with() (Architecture D, the universal escape hatch the USER stream already uses)? The entry point hosts the force-link discipline + the mandated anti-DCE self-check, and a missing initializer is a QUIETLY-skipped tweak — so the self-check matters acutely here. Cross-cuts the run-pipeline, auto-configuration, and every discovery feature.
- What is the exact CAPABILITY SCOPE of the pre-refresh customization handle, and how is it kept a thin origin-agnostic projection of the seams other features own (environment's mutate seam, post-processor-spi's register-processor, container-core's engine policy) WITHOUT creating a second way to do the same thing? R3 forces this into a closed CustomizationOp vocabulary (analyzable but possibly too narrow); R1/R2 expose an imperative handle (flexible but risks drift). The op-set-vs-imperative-handle choice cross-cuts the metadata/codegen boundary and the unified diagnostics model.
- How is the &mut-context-handle-across-.await aliasing clash resolved — by EXECUTION CONTEXT (R1/R2: single-threaded cold-path apply, the post-processor-spi definition-phase sidestep) or STRUCTURALLY (R3: read-only input + owned returned record, no shared mutable handle)? This is the same clash post-processor-spi's definition phase faces; resolving it once for both (a shared 'pre-refresh customization runs single-threaded' discipline vs a 'customizations are returned data' discipline) is the unifying call. Cross-cuts post-processor-spi, environment, and the async-context model.
- How are the user (programmatic / withHook single-run) and library (catalog) and generated-AOT initializer streams MERGED into one @Order stream, and where does the generated-AOT initializer's 'always first' precedence live — a reserved Order band (collidable) or a structural 'generated runs first' rule? And how is the withHook single-run test initializer threaded WITHOUT an ambient thread-local read across .await (the §2.3 hazard)? Cross-cuts the testing story, the run-pipeline's withHook/Abandoned mechanics, and task-execution.
- Does a DYNAMIC (WASM-module / runtime) initializer source contribute, and at what timing relative to apply_initializers — especially under R3 where dynamically-sourced initializers have no build-time presence and need a runtime-overlay lane that erodes the frozen plan? The two-source duality (static link-time + optional dynamic) applies to initializers exactly as to beans, processors, and run-participants; the timing/overlay semantics are unresolved. Cross-cuts auto-configuration and post-processor-spi's same duality.
- What is the unified error/diagnostics model an initializer failure (and R3's plan-time customization-conflict validation) realizes (the §1.7/§2.9 keystone)? An initializer that throws, a colliding property source, a contradictory engine-policy overlay, or an unresolvable enqueued processor descriptor should fail with complete context (which initializer by origin+order+id, which customization, the cause chain) — but whether that surfaces at build time (R3), a startup-validation pass, or runtime, and the error representation, depend on the deferred unified error model and the compile-vs-runtime split. Cross-cuts the run-pipeline's FailureAnalysis and condition-report.
- How much of the JVM-shaped initializer machinery is even rust-native intent vs scaffolding to design OUT — specifically the 'register a pre-refresh singleton' affordance (Spring registers springApplicationArguments/springBootBanner here): does leaf NEED a pre-refresh singleton-registration path on the initializer handle, or do those go through the bootstrap-context-promotion the run-pipeline already does, or through ordinary bean definitions? Avoiding two promotion paths is a rust-native simplification to judge in Phase 3, flagged so it isn't ported blindly.

### Notes
Scope boundary honoured: this feature is the INITIALIZER HOOK SURFACE only — the ApplicationContextInitializer analogue at the run-pipeline's prepare_context()/apply_initializers step (spring-boot-4-di-design.md lines 287-293). It is strictly DOWNSTREAM of spring-application-run (which owns WHEN apply_initializers fires, the surrounding event sequence, the BootstrapContext, the force-link/anti-DCE discipline, and routing failures into handle_run_failure) and strictly UPSTREAM of post-processor-spi (the BFPP contract an initializer enqueues) and refresh-lifecycle (which consumes the enqueued effects). It owns ONLY: the initializer trait/descriptor shape, the capability scope of what an initializer may legally touch pre-refresh (origin-agnostic), the discovery+@Order-merge of the USER + LIBRARY (+ generated-AOT) streams, and the pass's failure semantics. It does NOT own the run orchestration, the BFPP/BPP contracts, the Environment abstraction, profiles activation semantics, or the engine-vs-facade split — those are named neighbours. All three realizations stay implementation-agnostic and hold the deferred §3 keystones (metadata/codegen boundary, compile-vs-runtime split, dependency-based auto-config, unified error/diagnostics, cross-crate composition substrate, async-context-propagation) as CANDIDATES — R1 leans intent-faithful/dedicated-trait, R2 leans unify-onto-post-processor-spi's-Contributor (and is explicitly CONTINGENT on that feature's own unify decision — flagged so it doesn't pre-judge), R3 leans AOT/build-time-frozen-declarative, deliberately spanning the compile-vs-runtime axis so Phase 2's signal stays unbiased. Provider/registry abstractions kept ORIGIN-AGNOSTIC throughout (a native, generated-AOT, WASM-module, or test-double initializer participates identically). Grounding fully cross-checked: spring-boot-4-di-design.md §ApplicationContextInitializer (287-293, the apply-after-setEnvironment/postProcess-before-sources-before-refresh window + the register-BFPP/set-profiles uses + contextPrepared/ApplicationContextInitializedEvent firing after), §prepareContext (291-293, the full step incl. register-singleton + policy toggles), §bootstrap context (295-299, the BootstrapContext an initializer reads), the AOT pipeline fork (321, the generated <Main>__ApplicationContextInitializer injected first), the run-listener event sequence + standalone early-multicaster (266-285); the run-pipeline design handed in (the apply_initializers step, the two-stream descriptor model, the withHook/Abandoned mechanics, the standalone early-multicaster handoff); the upstream Phase-1 post-processor-spi design (its R1 two-traits / R3 one-Contributor / capability-handle-with-no-get_bean / role-as-data / the &mut-across-await-by-execution-context resolution / the silent-DCE self-check mandate) which this hook sits directly on top of and whose unify-or-not question this feature inherits; the nightly envelope (AsyncDrop avoid → explicit awaited teardown; AFIT/RPITIT not dyn-safe → boxed futures at the dyn edge; linkme/inventory tradeoffs; no async-context primitives → explicit threading of the withHook single-run initializer); and the cross-crate doc (the three DCE layers, the force-link/anti-DCE-self-check mandate, Architectures A-D, §170 ordering-as-data, the two-source duality, the charter §6 leaf-core/leaf-boot/leaf-macros/leaf-codegen topology). Notable tension to flag for Phase 3: the capability-scope handle is the highest-risk-of-blind-porting surface (it duplicates seams environment/post-processor-spi/container-core own — must be a thin coherent projection, not a second way to do the same thing), and the 'register a pre-refresh singleton' affordance may be JVM scaffolding to design out in favour of the bootstrap-context-promotion the run already does. The single highest-leverage Phase-2 coupling is the unify-or-not question SHARED with post-processor-spi: R2's viability is entirely contingent on that, so the two features' shapes must be decided together. I wrote no files. Relevant absolute paths: /home/jan/projects/testing/leaf/docs/research/spring-boot-4-di-design.md (287-321 the initializer + prepareContext + bootstrap-context + AOT-fork + run-listener sequence); /home/jan/projects/testing/leaf/docs/design/phase1/01-container-beans.md (378-468 post-processor-spi R1/R2/R3, the capability-handle + role-as-data + &mut-by-execution-context + self-check this hook builds on); /home/jan/projects/testing/leaf/docs/design/phase1/05-events-lifecycle.md (refresh-lifecycle fixed-order template + the standalone early-multicaster handoff); /home/jan/projects/testing/leaf/docs/research/rust-cross-crate-composition.md (DCE layers, Architectures A-D, §170 ordering-as-data, two-source duality, self-check mandate); /home/jan/projects/testing/leaf/docs/research/rust-nightly-features-tradeoffs.md (AFIT/RPITIT not dyn-safe → boxing; AsyncDrop avoid; linkme/inventory).

## Run Listeners & the Bootstrap Event Sequence  `[run-listeners-events]`

This feature is the SpringApplicationRunListener analogue plus the fixed, named bootstrap event sequence — NARROWER than (and sitting inside) the `spring-application-run` pipeline design. The run pipeline OWNS the ordered run() orchestration (timer, bootstrap-context, prepare-environment, create/prepare-context, refresh, runners, ready); THIS feature owns the OBSERVATION TAXONOMY that pipeline fires through: (a) the RunListener contract (Spring's SpringApplicationRunListener callbacks starting/environmentPrepared/contextPrepared/contextLoaded/started/ready/failed — doc 264-283), realized as a stable, named, ordered phase vocabulary; (b) the FIXED, named startup event sequence and its exact ordering (ApplicationStarting → EnvironmentPrepared → ContextInitialized → Prepared → [ContextRefreshed/ServerInitialized during refresh] → Started → AvailabilityChange(Liveness CORRECT) → [runners] → Ready → AvailabilityChange(Readiness ACCEPTING_TRAFFIC) | Failed-on-throw — doc 268-279, 1887), where the design intent is 'startup is a state machine with well-defined, STABLE observation points' giving extension authors precise hooks and the framework one uniform place to layer cross-cutting concerns (doc 281); (c) THE marquee rust-native concern — the STANDALONE EARLY MULTICASTER: the first four events fire before/around context creation through a standalone multicaster (Spring's `initialMulticaster`), and only at contextLoaded are the application's listeners attached to the LIVE context's multicaster and ApplicationPrepared published (doc 283) — which is PRECISELY WHY early listeners CANNOT be ordinary beans (no context exists yet to host them; doc 1889), so they must be registered on the Application or via descriptors; (d) the early-vs-context multicaster HANDOFF and early-event buffering; (e) availability-as-CORE publication (Liveness CORRECT with Started, Readiness ACCEPTING_TRAFFIC with Ready — doc 285) routed through this taxonomy; (f) the run HOOK (withHook thread-local single-run RunListener for test-slicing) and the failed callback that precedes FailureAnalysis. Per the run-pipeline design and charter §6, this lives in leaf-boot atop leaf-framework's events/event-multicaster/lifecycle-events substrate. The intent must be realized WITHOUT JVM lineage: no spring.factories runtime SPI loading of run listeners (descriptors from a scoped link/codegen/explicit catalog instead), no ambient thread-local current-phase across the eager-singleton/background fan-out (parent linkage carried explicitly), no thread-local withHook read at an arbitrary await point, and the early-vs-context handoff must reconcile with the events/event-multicaster neighbour's eventual (typed-channel vs erased-bus vs hybrid) design rather than assume a single erased bus. Scope discipline: this feature owns the run-event TAXONOMY + the RunListener contract + the standalone early multicaster + the early-vs-context handoff/buffering + WHO fires WHICH event at WHICH run-phase + the withHook single-run injection seam; it does NOT own the run() orchestration order (spring-application-run), the general bus engine (events/event-multicaster), the availability STATE model (lifecycle-events), the refresh-internal events (refresh-lifecycle/runtime-lifecycle), or FailureAnalysis rendering (spring-application-run).

### Candidate realizations

#### R1 — Standalone early-multicaster + a context-handoff at contextLoaded: the run fires a fixed named-event sequence through a pre-context EarlyEventChannel, then transfers application listeners onto the live context's multicaster, mirroring Spring's two-multicaster split literally
Port Spring's actual mechanism faithfully. The Application owns a list of explicitly-registered RunListener descriptors (the `addListeners`/spring.factories analogue, here a scoped catalog — Phase-2-undecided linkme/codegen/explicit) PLUS a process-local single-run withHook injection. A single concrete `RunListeners` aggregate (the EventPublishingRunListener analogue) is built once at the top of run() and holds a STANDALONE early multicaster — a deliberately lightweight, pre-context dispatch channel (`EarlyEventChannel`) that exists BEFORE the real container/its event-multicaster. The fixed named events fire as explicit calls the run pipeline makes at each phase boundary: `run_listeners.starting(&bootstrap_ctx)` → publishes ApplicationStarting on the EarlyEventChannel; `environment_prepared(&bootstrap_ctx, &env)` → EnvironmentPrepared (the hook where config-data/EnvironmentPostProcessor-analogues run); `context_prepared(&ctx)` → ContextInitialized; `context_loaded(&ctx)` → THE HANDOFF: iterate the Application's registered ApplicationListeners, attach each to the now-live context's event-multicaster (the events/event-multicaster neighbour), THEN publish ApplicationPrepared (so a prepared-listener registered as a context bean can observe it, but the first three events were standalone-only — exactly Spring's reason early listeners can't be beans); `started(&ctx, startup_duration)` → ContextRefreshed already fired during refresh on the context's multicaster, now Started + AvailabilityChange(Liveness CORRECT) publish on the CONTEXT's multicaster; `ready(&ctx, duration)` → Ready + AvailabilityChange(Readiness ACCEPTING_TRAFFIC); `failed(&ctx?, &err)` → ApplicationFailed (which may fire on EITHER channel depending on how far bring-up got — standalone if pre-context, context if post). The event TYPES are a fixed leaf-published vocabulary (RunPhaseEvent enum or distinct typed events carrying the Application handle, the BootstrapContext for the first two, the context for later ones, and parent-trace linkage). Early-event buffering: any listener attaching late (e.g. an app listener that should have seen Starting) is handled by the EarlyEventChannel optionally retaining-and-replaying the early facts at handoff — a per-event-name buffer drained at contextLoaded (the registerListeners-flush analogue). The withHook single-run RunListener is threaded EXPLICITLY into the RunListeners aggregate at construction (not read from an ambient thread-local at dispatch) so it participates in every phase callback for exactly this run. Each phase callback is `async` and awaited inline on the bootstrap task; the EarlyEventChannel dispatches sequentially in registration/Order so the named sequence stays totally ordered. The two channels are coherent because the run pipeline owns the single handoff point (contextLoaded) and never fires a 'context' event before it nor a 'standalone' event after.

**Pros:** Highest intent fidelity to the doc's two-multicaster reality (283): the standalone-early-channel + the contextLoaded-attach-listeners-then-publish-Prepared handoff map 1:1, so 'early listeners cannot be beans' is realized for the RIGHT structural reason (there is literally no context yet) rather than as an arbitrary rule — maximally teachable (DX #1, §2.10), and a Spring developer recognizes the exact sequence.; The fixed named-event sequence is a concrete, ordered set of explicit phase-callback calls the run pipeline makes — each event has a single, obvious emission point, so 'the canonical sequence fired in order' is legible in a stepped trace and the named vocabulary (the RunListener phase names) is a stable, tool-friendly taxonomy extension authors and startup-instrumentation key off (doc 281, parity with startup-instrumentation's stable name vocabulary).; Cleanly SEPARATES the pre-context concern (the EarlyEventChannel, a tiny leaf-boot-owned channel) from the general bus (events/event-multicaster, leaf-framework): the first events do not need the full bus to exist, dissolving Spring's awkward 'multicaster bean isn't created until refresh but we need to fire events before that' tension — the early channel is purpose-built and the handoff is the one seam where the two meet.; Async-first and reactive (§2.3/§2.4): each phase callback is an inline `.await` on the bootstrap task preserving total ordering; the early channel dispatches sequentially (no busy-wait); availability publication routes Started/Ready facts through the context multicaster as reactive notifications (the lifecycle-events availability-state holder is woken, not polled).; The withHook single-run RunListener is threaded as an EXPLICIT value into the RunListeners aggregate, directly dissolving the §2.3 thread-local-across-await hazard (Spring's getRunListeners reads a thread-local) — test-slicing/observe-and-abort works without an ambient read at an arbitrary suspension point.; Origin-agnostic and DCE-honest: RunListener descriptors and ApplicationListeners come from a scoped catalog (native, WASM-module, or test-double register identically); the contextLoaded handoff is the natural place for the anti-DCE self-check (expected-vs-found run-listeners/early-listeners per source), turning a silently-absent listener into a loud diagnostic.

**Cons:** TWO dispatch channels (the standalone EarlyEventChannel and the context's event-multicaster) is a genuine coherence burden: the run pipeline must guarantee no 'context' event fires before the handoff and no 'standalone' event after, and the handoff itself (attach-listeners-then-publish-Prepared) is an ordering subtlety that must stay correct as the events/event-multicaster neighbour's design evolves — a missed/mis-ordered fire is a correctness bug with no structural guard beyond convention.; Porting Spring's two-multicaster split risks carrying JVM-shaped scaffolding the charter (§2.2) says to question: if leaf's event-multicaster is ALWAYS present (not a refresh-created bean) or events are typed channels rather than an erased bus, a separate EarlyEventChannel may be unnecessary — the early events could just go on the always-present bus with a 'no context-bean listeners attached yet' note, making this realization's central mechanism redundant scaffolding.; Early-event buffering/replay-at-handoff is a real semantic decision baked in here (buffer-and-replay vs lose-early-events-for-late-listeners) that properly belongs to the events neighbour's early-buffer design — R1 commits to a per-event-name retain-and-replay that may conflict with how refresh-lifecycle and lifecycle-events want early facts handled, risking double-buffering.; The event vocabulary (the RunListener phase names + the typed event set) becomes a stable cross-crate ABI with no classpath to anchor it; getting the named taxonomy complete and correctly ordered up front, and versioning it cleanly, is a commitment — and the early-vs-context split means some events (ApplicationFailed) can fire on EITHER channel, complicating the 'which listener sees what' contract.; ApplicationFailed firing on either channel depending on bring-up progress means a failure-observing listener must be registered as a RunListener/early-listener (not a context bean) to reliably see pre-context failures — a subtle gotcha that mirrors but slightly worsens Spring's, and couples to the run pipeline's handle_run_failure routing.

**Mechanisms considered:** a single concrete `RunListeners` aggregate (the EventPublishingRunListener analogue) built once at run() top, holding a standalone pre-context `EarlyEventChannel` + the live context's event-multicaster after handoff; fixed named phase callbacks the run pipeline calls explicitly at each boundary (starting/environment_prepared/context_prepared/context_loaded/started/ready/failed), each publishing its named event; contextLoaded as THE handoff: iterate the Application's registered ApplicationListeners → attach each to the live context's event-multicaster → THEN publish ApplicationPrepared (Spring's exact reason early listeners can't be beans); event TYPES as a fixed leaf-published vocabulary (typed run-phase events carrying the Application/BootstrapContext/context handle as appropriate + explicit parent-trace linkage); per-event-name early-event buffer on the EarlyEventChannel, drained/replayed at the contextLoaded handoff (the registerListeners-flush analogue); withHook single-run RunListener threaded EXPLICITLY into the RunListeners aggregate at construction (not an ambient thread-local read at dispatch) — dissolving the §2.3 hazard; availability publication (Liveness CORRECT with Started, Readiness ACCEPTING_TRAFFIC with Ready) routed through the context multicaster as reactive facts into lifecycle-events' state holder; run-listener/early-listener descriptors from a scoped catalog (linkme/codegen/explicit, Phase-2-undecided), addressed by role; anti-DCE self-check at the handoff

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** leaf-boot defines the RunListener trait/contract, the fixed run-event-name TAXONOMY (an ABI-ish const vocabulary like startup-instrumentation's), the typed run-phase event set, and the RunListeners aggregate + EarlyEventChannel; the general bus it hands off to (event-multicaster) lives in leaf-framework. RunListener descriptors and pre-context ApplicationListeners are collected from the SAME scoped catalog substrate the rest of leaf uses (Phase-2-undecided linkme distributed-slice / build.rs codegen / explicit register; cross-crate doc Architectures A-D), addressed by ROLE, never a runtime spring.factories type-scan. Because early listeners CANNOT be context beans, their ONLY discovery path is this catalog (or explicit Application::add_listener) — so the silent-DCE failure mode is acute and asymmetric: a context-bean listener that's DCE'd is at least loud at bean resolution, but a DCE'd EARLY run-listener is silently absent (no Starting/EnvironmentPrepared observation, no failure-on-pre-context-error), indistinguishable from a legitimately-unregistered listener — MANDATING the anti-DCE self-check (expected-vs-found run-listeners per source crate, warn on enabled-feature-zero-contributions) which the contextLoaded handoff naturally hosts. The Layer-0 force-link discipline applies (a run-listener-only crate the binary never references contributes nothing unless the generated app-root emits `use leaf_x as _;`). The run-event-name taxonomy + the RunListener trait + the typed event set are emitted with absolute `::leaf_boot::`/`::leaf_framework::` paths by the thin `#[run_listener]`/`#[event_listener]` macros and held in leaf-boot/leaf-framework for ABI stability; macros carry zero dispatch logic and hard-error on generic listener types (no 'static symbol until concrete) with a register-concrete shim. The two-source duality applies to BOTH run-listeners and the eventual context-bean listeners: the static link-time set is the default 'classpath'; an optional dynamic/WASM-module source contributing run-listener descriptors (whose phase-callbacks bridge into the module) feeds the SAME RunListeners aggregate — origin-agnostic because the aggregate only ever sees an erased phase-callback. The withHook single-run hook is process-local (one run), not cross-crate. CRITICAL coupling: the early-vs-context multicaster handoff is a cross-crate seam between leaf-boot's EarlyEventChannel and leaf-framework's event-multicaster — its shape depends on the events neighbour's typed-vs-erased-vs-hybrid decision (deferred), so this feature must keep the handoff a thin, swappable adapter, not assume a single erased bus.

**T2 — execution context:** Entirely a COLD-PATH concern on the bootstrap task — the run pipeline fires the named sequence synchronously-in-order via inline `.await`s at each phase boundary. The standalone EarlyEventChannel dispatches the first events (Starting/EnvironmentPrepared/ContextInitialized) SEQUENTIALLY on the bootstrap task before the container/its multicaster exist — ordered, never busy-waiting (§2.4). At the contextLoaded handoff, the Application's listeners attach to the context's event-multicaster (the events neighbour's dispatch seam), and from Prepared onward events dispatch through THAT (sync-by-default-inline-on-the-bootstrap-task per the multicaster's contract). PARENT LINKAGE for the startup trace is carried EXPLICITLY in each event (the run is the root span; refresh-internal events nest under it) — never read off an ambient thread-local current-phase across the eager-singleton/background fan-out (the §2.3 fix shared with startup-instrumentation). NO GLOBAL LOCK (§2.5): the EarlyEventChannel guards only its own sequential-dispatch cursor; no lock is held across a listener `.await`. ERROR PROPAGATION is non-uniform and load-bearing (the lifecycle-events 'Ready-listener failure can fail startup' intent): an ordinary early-event listener failure may isolate, but a started/ready milestone listener failure must route into the run pipeline's handle_run_failure (fire `failed`, then FailureAnalysis) — a per-phase error policy the channel must express. The withHook single-run RunListener participates in every phase callback as an explicit value (no thread-local read across `.await`); an AbandonedRunException-analogue signalled by the hook short-circuits to a rethrow WITHOUT analysis/close (a defined run-pipeline outcome). CANCELLATION: cancelling the bootstrap task mid-sequence stops further phase callbacks; the run pipeline's teardown (cancelRefresh/context-close) handles cleanup — there is no async Drop, so the EarlyEventChannel and any retained early-buffer are dropped explicitly. Availability publication (Liveness/Readiness) is a reactive notification into lifecycle-events' state holder (woken subscribers, never polled), with the runners-complete-before-ACCEPTING_TRAFFIC ordering an explicit execution-context boundary the run pipeline honours.

#### R2 — Unified bus from the start, no standalone early channel: the run-event sequence is a fixed ordered list of named milestones published on leaf's ONE always-present event-multicaster, with pre-context listeners as descriptor-attached non-bean subscribers and a retained-fact replay for late attachers
Question whether leaf NEEDS Spring's standalone early multicaster at all (a JVM artifact of the multicaster being a refresh-created bean). Make leaf's event-multicaster ALWAYS PRESENT from the very start of run() (it is created/handed to the run pipeline before any event fires — it is not a context bean that only exists after refresh). The fixed named run-event sequence is then a single ordered list of MILESTONE publications on that ONE bus: the run pipeline calls `bus.publish(ApplicationStarting{..})`, `…EnvironmentPrepared{..}`, `…ContextInitialized{..}`, `…ApplicationPrepared{..}`, `…(ContextRefreshed during refresh)`, `…ApplicationStarted{..}`, `…AvailabilityChange(Liveness CORRECT)`, `…ApplicationReady{..}`, `…AvailabilityChange(Readiness ACCEPTING_TRAFFIC)`, or `…ApplicationFailed{..}` on throw — all through the SAME publish path app code uses. The distinction 'early listeners cannot be beans' is preserved as a TIMING fact, not a separate channel: a listener that wants to observe the FIRST milestones must be registered as a pre-context descriptor (a RunListener / Application-registered ApplicationListener from the scoped catalog) because no CONTEXT exists yet to host a bean — but it subscribes to the SAME bus. Context-bean listeners are attached to the bus at the normal refresh-lifecycle registerListeners phase; they therefore miss the pre-refresh milestones unless the bus offers RETAINED-FACT replay. R2 leans on the lifecycle-events availability-state insight generalized: the run-milestone events are published normally, AND the most recent of each milestone is RETAINED (last-write-wins per milestone name) so a listener attaching late (a context bean, or a dynamically-loaded subscriber) can OPTIONALLY replay the milestones it missed — the early-event-buffering intent realized as retained-latest on the bus rather than a separate buffer drained at handoff. The RunListener phase-callback contract (starting/environmentPrepared/…) becomes a THIN convenience facade over `bus.subscribe(milestone)` — a RunListener is just a bundle of milestone subscriptions with the stable phase names; it is NOT a privileged separate dispatch path. The withHook single-run listener is an explicit per-run subscription added to the bus for this run and removed at run end. Availability is published as ordinary AvailabilityChange events on the same bus (dogfooding lifecycle-events).

**Pros:** Maximal unification (§2.11): there is ONE event substrate (the events/event-multicaster bus) and the run-event sequence is just a fixed ordered set of publications on it — no bespoke standalone channel, no two-multicaster handoff to keep coherent, no separate early-buffer mechanism. The RunListener contract is a thin facade over bus subscription, so run-events, lifecycle facts, and app events all share one dispatch engine, error policy, and ordering — the cleanest Phase-2-friendly shape.; Directly questions the JVM-shaped standalone multicaster (charter §2.2 intent-not-mechanism): Spring needs `initialMulticaster` only because its real multicaster is a refresh-created bean; if leaf's bus is always-present, that scaffolding is unnecessary, and 'early listeners can't be beans' reduces to the HONEST timing fact (no context exists yet to host a bean) rather than a separate-channel artifact — a more rust-native, smaller-surface realization.; Retained-latest milestone facts elegantly solve early-event-buffering AND the late-attacher problem with ONE mechanism, and reuse exactly the lifecycle-events availability-state insight (a retained, queryable, replayable current value) — a context bean attaching at registerListeners can replay the Starting/EnvironmentPrepared milestones it structurally missed, dissolving Spring's 'context beans never see early events' limitation as a deliberate, opt-in capability.; Async-first/reactive and no two-channel coherence risk (§2.3/§2.4): a single ordered publish path on the bootstrap task, sync-by-default inline awaits, availability as reactive notifications; the named sequence's ordering is the publish order on one channel, far simpler to keep totally ordered and trace than R1's two-channel split.; withHook as an explicit per-run subscription added/removed on the bus avoids any thread-local-across-await hazard (§2.3) and is uniform with how any dynamic listener attaches — no special single-run dispatch path.; Origin-agnostic and dual-classpath-clean: pre-context RunListeners (catalog/Application-registered), context-bean listeners (registered at refresh), and dynamic/WASM-module subscribers all attach to the SAME bus — the run-milestone events meet all subscriber origins at one publish path.

**Cons:** Pre-commits to a strong property of the (deferred) events/event-multicaster keystone — that the bus is ALWAYS PRESENT before run() rather than a refresh-created context service — and to RETAINED-LATEST milestone semantics on the bus; both are exactly the events-neighbour decisions the charter defers (§3 type-erasure/registry substrate; lifecycle-events' retained-state-vs-retained-events fork), so presenting R2 as THE shape risks biasing Phase-2 signal and must stay a candidate.; Retained-latest milestone replay AMPLIFIES the multi-fire/stale-fact footgun the lifecycle-events design flagged: a late subscriber replaying a retained Starting/EnvironmentPrepared could act on a stale milestone, and for a refreshable/restartable context the retained run-milestones could be replayed inappropriately — the one-time-vs-every-time consumption semantics become a load-bearing decision this realization forces early.; Loses some intent fidelity / teachability versus Spring: a developer who knows Spring's two-multicaster split will look for it and not find it; the 'RunListener is a thin facade over bus subscription' framing, while cleaner, is further from the documented mechanism (a fidelity cost the charter tolerates but that surprises Spring users at the entry point — the place predictability matters most).; If the events neighbour lands on TYPED CHANNELS (not an erased bus), 'always-present bus before any context' plus 'retained-latest per milestone' needs typed milestone channels wired before the container exists, and the retention machinery pushes stateful storage into a dispatch engine the events design may want stateless — a real tension with the typed-channel realization (events R1) that R2 glosses.; An ApplicationReady/Started milestone-listener failure that must FAIL startup (the lifecycle-events non-uniform error intent) is harder to express when the milestone is 'just another publish' on the general bus with a default isolation policy — R2 must layer a per-milestone error policy onto the unified bus, partially reintroducing the special-casing it sought to avoid.; Pre-context RunListeners subscribing to the 'same bus' before the bus is wired into a context is conceptually clean but means the bus has a lifecycle phase (pre-context → context-attached → closed) that must be defined — a different complexity than R1's explicit handoff, not obviously less.

**Mechanisms considered:** leaf's event-multicaster made ALWAYS PRESENT from the top of run() (handed to the run pipeline before any event fires), NOT a refresh-created context bean; the fixed named run-event sequence as a single ordered list of milestone publications on the ONE bus (Starting/EnvironmentPrepared/ContextInitialized/Prepared/Started/Liveness/Ready/Readiness | Failed); 'early listeners cannot be beans' preserved as a TIMING fact (no context exists yet to host a bean) — pre-context listeners are catalog/Application-registered descriptors subscribing to the same bus; RETAINED-LATEST per-milestone facts so a late-attaching listener (context bean, dynamic subscriber) can OPTIONALLY replay the milestones it missed (early-buffering as retained-latest, reusing the lifecycle-events availability-state insight); the RunListener phase-callback contract (starting/environmentPrepared/…) as a THIN facade over bus.subscribe(milestone) with the stable phase names — not a privileged separate dispatch path; withHook single-run listener as an explicit per-run subscription added/removed on the bus for this run; availability published as ordinary AvailabilityChange events on the same bus (dogfooding lifecycle-events); per-milestone error policy layered on the unified bus for the 'Ready-listener failure fails startup' non-uniform contract

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** leaf-boot defines the fixed run-event-name taxonomy + the typed milestone event set + the thin RunListener facade; the always-present event-multicaster + the retained-latest mechanism live in leaf-framework (events/event-multicaster + lifecycle-events). Because there is NO separate early channel, the cross-crate surface is smaller: everything is bus subscription. Pre-context RunListeners and context-bean listeners are collected from the SAME scoped catalog substrate (Phase-2-undecided linkme/codegen/explicit) — but R2 makes the run-milestone events reachable by BOTH pre-context descriptors and (via retained-latest replay) context beans, so the discovery story partly UNIFIES with the events neighbour's general listener-discovery (one substrate for all listeners, run-milestone or app). The silent-DCE hazard is identical in severity to R1 but the diagnosis is uniform (the events-neighbour self-check covers run-milestone subscribers too): a DCE'd pre-context RunListener is silently absent; the mandated anti-DCE self-check (expected-vs-found per source) and the leaf-doctor discovery listing apply, now reporting run-milestone subscriptions alongside app-event subscriptions. Layer-0 force-link discipline applies. The retained-latest milestone state is a single owned holder (leaf-framework) — no classpath duality on the WRITE side (the run pipeline writes milestones), while the SUBSCRIBER side inherits the static-link-time-plus-optional-dynamic-source duality (a WASM-module subscriber attaching late replays retained milestones identically to a native one — origin-agnostic). The run-event taxonomy + typed milestone set + thin RunListener facade are the stable ABI, emitted with absolute paths by thin macros; macros hard-error on generic listener types. HARD coupling: R2 PRESUPPOSES the events neighbour decides (a) the bus is always-present pre-context and (b) retained-latest is available — both deferred §3 keystone calls, so this is the most coupled-to-events-neighbour realization and must stay a candidate. The withHook hook is process-local. The Cargo-feature-as-starter / force-link discipline still applies for pulling RunListener-contributing crates onto the link graph.

**T2 — execution context:** COLD-PATH on the bootstrap task. The run pipeline publishes the milestone sequence in fixed order via inline `.await`s on the ONE always-present bus — sync-by-default inline-on-the-bootstrap-task dispatch (the event-multicaster's contract), totally ordered because it is one channel's publish order (no two-channel coherence concern, the §2.4 reactive win). PARENT LINKAGE for the startup trace is carried EXPLICITLY in each milestone event (the run is the root; refresh-internal events nest), never an ambient thread-local current-phase across the eager-singleton/background fan-out (§2.3). RETAINED-LATEST milestone state is held behind leaf's reactive state primitive (the deferred watch/seqlock-shaped cell shared with lifecycle-events) so a late subscriber's replay is a cold-path read + reactive notification, never a poll (§2.4); the retention write is a single owned cell, no global lock (§2.5). NON-UNIFORM ERROR POLICY: ordinary milestone-listener failures isolate per the bus's error policy, but a Started/Ready milestone failure routes into the run pipeline's handle_run_failure (the lifecycle-events 'Ready-listener failure fails startup' intent) — a per-milestone error policy on the bus the bootstrap task observes. withHook is an explicit per-run subscription (no thread-local-across-await read); an AbandonedRunException-analogue short-circuits to rethrow without analysis/close. CANCELLATION: cancelling the bootstrap task stops further publications; no async Drop, so the bus's pre-context state and any retained milestones are torn down explicitly via the run pipeline's teardown. Availability (Liveness/Readiness) publishes as reactive AvailabilityChange notifications into lifecycle-events' state holder; the runners-complete-before-ACCEPTING_TRAFFIC ordering is an explicit execution-context boundary. The bus's lifecycle phases (pre-context → context-attached at registerListeners → closed) are explicit cold-path transitions the run pipeline + refresh-lifecycle drive.

#### R3 — Typed run-phase state machine emits the named events as transition side-effects: a RunPhase enum advancing on the bootstrap task fires each named event exactly once as a verified transition, with RunListeners as phase-transition observers and a pluggable early-vs-context dispatch sink
Make the FIXED NAMED SEQUENCE a structural property rather than a hand-fired convention, building directly on the run-pipeline R1's typed RunPhase enum (Created → Starting → EnvironmentPrepared → ContextCreated → ContextInitialized → ContextPrepared/Loaded → Refreshing → Refreshed → Started → RunnersInvoked → Ready | Failed). Each phase TRANSITION is the single, verified emission point of its named event: the run pipeline's typed state machine advances the phase, and advancing it FIRES the corresponding named run-event EXACTLY ONCE as a transition side-effect — so 'fire ApplicationStarting' is not a call the pipeline must remember to make, it is what `transition_to(Starting)` DOES, and the type system guarantees a phase (hence its event) cannot fire twice, out of order, or be skipped (each transition asserts its predecessor phase). RunListeners are modeled as phase-transition OBSERVERS: a RunListener is `async fn on_phase(&self, transition: &RunTransition)` (or the typed per-phase callbacks as sugar), invoked by the state machine at each transition with the typed transition payload (from-phase, to-phase, the event, the relevant handle — BootstrapContext for early phases, context for later, parent-trace linkage). The early-vs-context distinction becomes a property of the TRANSITION SINK, not a separate channel the pipeline juggles: the state machine owns a `RunEventSink` that, for pre-ContextLoaded transitions, dispatches to pre-context observers (catalog/Application-registered RunListeners — the only thing that exists), and for post-ContextLoaded transitions, ALSO dispatches to the live context's event-multicaster — the handoff is a state-machine-internal sink capability transition at the ContextLoaded phase (mirroring refresh-lifecycle R1's typed RefreshState gating). This makes the whole bootstrap event sequence + the early-multicaster handoff a TOTAL, verified state machine: every (phase, event) pairing is enumerated, the Failed transition is reachable from any phase carrying the failing phase context, and the run-pipeline's handle_run_failure is the `→ Failed` transition. The withHook single-run RunListener is an explicit extra observer registered on the state machine for this run. Availability publication (Liveness CORRECT, Readiness ACCEPTING_TRAFFIC) are themselves transition side-effects of the Started and Ready transitions. This is the lifecycle-events R3 'state-transition-side-effects' insight applied specifically to the BOOTSTRAP event sequence, unifying the run-phase state machine, the named-event sequence, and the early-vs-context handoff into one verified machine.

**Pros:** Makes the fixed named sequence a STRUCTURAL guarantee (the strongest §2.9 win): because each event fires only as a typed phase transition that asserts its predecessor, the sequence provably cannot be mis-ordered, double-fired, or skipped — the exact 'startup is a state machine with well-defined observation points' intent (doc 281) realized as an actual checked state machine rather than a hand-maintained list of publish calls (R1/R2's weakness).; Unifies tightly with the run-pipeline R1 (the shared typed RunPhase enum) and with lifecycle-events R3 (events-as-transition-side-effects): one typed state machine drives the run() phases, the named event sequence, the early-vs-context handoff, AND the availability publications — maximal unification (§2.11), and a single inspectable run-state value answers 'what is bootstrap doing right now' (superb diagnostic/test surface).; The early-vs-context handoff becomes a TYPED SINK capability transition at the ContextLoaded phase (like refresh-lifecycle R1's RefreshState gating / R2's phase-typed RefreshCx): 'pre-context transitions dispatch only to pre-context observers; post-context transitions also dispatch to the context bus' is a property of the sink handed in at each phase, holding for all observers — dissolving R1's hand-coded two-channel coherence risk into a checked transition.; The Failed event/transition is reachable from ANY phase and structurally carries the failing-phase context (which phase, what was being assembled) — the richest possible failure context for the run-pipeline's handle_run_failure/FailureAnalysis (charter §1.7/§2.9), and the AbandonedRunException short-circuit is a defined transition outcome, not an exceptional code path.; Availability (Liveness/Readiness) as transition side-effects of Started/Ready is exact and unmissable: the K8s readiness-gate window (runners complete BEFORE the Ready transition flips ACCEPTING_TRAFFIC) is encoded as the RunnersInvoked→Ready transition boundary, an execution-context boundary the machine enforces rather than a comment.; withHook as an explicit per-run observer on the state machine avoids the thread-local-across-await hazard (§2.3) and slots into the same observer-dispatch path as catalog RunListeners — uniform, no privileged single-run channel.

**Cons:** Heaviest machinery and the largest conceptual surface for THIS narrow feature: a total, verified run-phase state machine with a phase-typed event sink is more than 'fire a fixed sequence of named events', and it tightly couples this feature to the run-pipeline's R1 (the shared RunPhase enum) and to lifecycle-events' R3 — if Phase 2 picks the run-pipeline R2 (re-orderable stages) or R3 (frozen plan), the 'phase transition IS the event' framing must be re-expressed, so R3 partly pre-judges the run-orchestration shape keystone.; Totality is a specification BURDEN: enumerating every (phase, event) pairing AND the early-vs-context sink behavior at each, plus the Failed-from-any-phase transitions and the Abandoned short-circuit, is a large correctness surface; an incompletely-specified machine LOOKS total but has gaps (the recurring totality footgun from runtime-lifecycle R3 / lifecycle-events R3).; Events-as-transition-side-effects couples the named-event firing to the state-machine substrate AND to the events/event-multicaster dispatch sink: if the events neighbour lands on typed channels vs an erased bus, the 'sink' adapter must bridge to either — and the retained/early-buffering concern (how a late context-bean listener sees pre-context events) is NOT solved by the state machine alone, still needing the events-neighbour's early-buffer or a retained-latest mechanism (so R3 inherits R1's or R2's buffering decision anyway).; Modeling the bootstrap event sequence as a full typed state machine is FURTHER from Spring's mechanism (a list of run-listener callbacks the run() method invokes) than R1 — a fidelity/teachability cost, and the 'event = transition side-effect' indirection can make 'where exactly does ApplicationStarting fire' less obvious than R2's literal publish call, despite the stronger guarantee.; The state machine is the run pipeline's concern (RunPhase belongs to spring-application-run); building THIS feature ON that enum risks blurring the scope boundary — the named-event taxonomy + early-multicaster ought to be expressible independently of whichever run-orchestration shape wins, but R3 binds them to one shape.; Per-phase non-uniform error policy (a Ready-transition observer failure must fail startup, an early-phase observer failure may isolate) must be encoded into the transition table — defined and total, but a larger surface than R1/R2's per-event policy and entangled with the run pipeline's handle_run_failure.

**Mechanisms considered:** a typed RunPhase enum (shared with run-pipeline R1) whose transitions FIRE the named run-events exactly once as verified side-effects (transition asserts predecessor phase → no double-fire/skip/mis-order); RunListeners as phase-transition observers: `async fn on_phase(&self, &RunTransition)` (typed per-phase callbacks as sugar) invoked at each transition with the typed payload (from/to phase, event, relevant handle, parent-trace linkage); a phase-typed `RunEventSink` capability: pre-ContextLoaded transitions dispatch only to pre-context observers; post-ContextLoaded transitions ALSO dispatch to the live context's event-multicaster — the early-vs-context handoff as a sink capability transition at ContextLoaded; the Failed event as a transition reachable from ANY phase, structurally carrying the failing-phase context (feeding handle_run_failure/FailureAnalysis); the AbandonedRunException short-circuit as a defined transition outcome; availability publication (Liveness CORRECT on Started transition, Readiness ACCEPTING_TRAFFIC on Ready transition) as transition side-effects; the RunnersInvoked→Ready boundary encoding the K8s readiness-gate window; withHook single-run RunListener as an explicit per-run observer registered on the state machine (no thread-local-across-await read); the lifecycle-events R3 'events-are-the-state-machine's-output' pattern applied to the bootstrap event sequence specifically; early-buffering/retained-latest for late context-bean listeners inherited from R1's buffer or R2's retained-latest (the state machine does not solve it alone)

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** leaf-boot defines the RunPhase enum (shared with the run-pipeline feature), the RunTransition payload type, the RunListener observer trait, the fixed run-event taxonomy + typed event set, and the phase-typed RunEventSink; the context event-multicaster the sink bridges to lives in leaf-framework. RunListener observers are collected from the SAME scoped catalog substrate (Phase-2-undecided linkme/codegen/explicit), addressed by role; because pre-context observers are the ONLY thing that can see early-phase transitions, the silent-DCE hazard is acute and asymmetric exactly as in R1 — a DCE'd pre-context RunListener silently misses early transitions — MANDATING the anti-DCE self-check (expected-vs-found observers per source), which the state machine can run at the Starting transition (assert expected pre-context observers present) and at the ContextLoaded sink-transition (assert expected context-attachable observers). Layer-0 force-link discipline applies. The RunPhase enum + RunTransition + RunListener trait + run-event taxonomy become a stable cross-crate ABI emitted with absolute paths by thin macros (zero dispatch logic, hard-error on generic observers). The phase-typed sink is the cross-crate seam between leaf-boot's state machine and leaf-framework's event-multicaster — its shape depends on the deferred events neighbour decision (typed channels vs erased bus), so the sink must be a thin swappable adapter. Two-source duality: static link-time RunListener observers are the default; an optional dynamic/WASM-module source contributes observers whose on_phase bridges into the module — origin-agnostic because the state machine only ever invokes an erased on_phase. The DEEPEST T1 tension is that R3 binds this feature's cross-crate surface to the run-pipeline's RunPhase enum (the run-orchestration shape keystone): if Phase 2 picks the run-pipeline R2/R3, this feature's ABI must be re-expressed — so the RunPhase coupling must stay a candidate. The withHook hook is process-local. AOT-friendliness: the transition table + the per-phase sink behavior could be a const-emitted schedule a build-time pass freezes (Architecture C), but that widens the stable surface (the RunPhase/transition vocabulary becomes ABI).

**T2 — execution context:** The state machine runs on the bootstrap task (COLD PATH); each transition is an explicit `.await` point that dispatches its named event to the phase-appropriate observers via the RunEventSink before advancing. Pre-ContextLoaded transitions dispatch to pre-context observers sequentially on the bootstrap task (ordered, no busy-wait, §2.4); at the ContextLoaded sink-capability transition the context's event-multicaster becomes a dispatch target and post-context transitions ALSO route through it (the events neighbour's sync-by-default inline-on-the-bootstrap-task contract). The single-threaded-cold-path execution context means the &mut state machine + the phase-typed sink are held without aliasing-across-await issues by execution context, NOT a lock (§2.5) — no global lock; only the per-container bring-up guard serializes concurrent run/close. PARENT LINKAGE is carried EXPLICITLY in each RunTransition (the run is the root span; refresh-internal events nest), never an ambient thread-local current-phase across the eager-singleton/background fan-out (§2.3). NON-UNIFORM ERROR POLICY is encoded in the transition table: an early-phase observer failure may isolate; a Started/Ready-transition observer failure routes to the `→ Failed` transition (handle_run_failure); the Abandoned short-circuit is a defined transition that rethrows WITHOUT analysis/close. CANCELLATION: cancelling the bootstrap task mid-transition routes to the `→ Failed` transition (or the run-pipeline's cancelRefresh/context-close per how far bring-up got), carrying the failing phase; no async Drop, so any pre-context sink state + retained early-buffer is torn down explicitly on the unwind. Availability (Liveness CORRECT on the Started transition, Readiness ACCEPTING_TRAFFIC on the Ready transition) are reactive notifications into lifecycle-events' state holder (woken subscribers, never polled); the RunnersInvoked→Ready transition boundary is the explicit execution-context boundary after which the app accepts traffic, with runners (data load/migration) completing on the bootstrap task BEFORE the flip. withHook is an explicit per-run observer (no thread-local read across `.await`).

### Rust clashes
- No spring.factories runtime SPI loading of RunListeners/ApplicationListeners; no runtime classpath. Spring loads SpringApplicationRunListener (the EventPublishingRunListener) and the application's early ApplicationListeners via SpringFactoriesLoader at runtime — a classpath scan Rust cannot do. Every RunListener and pre-context ApplicationListener must instead be a thin origin-agnostic descriptor from a SCOPED catalog (static link-time registry + optional dynamic source; Phase-2-undecided linkme/codegen/explicit), addressed by ROLE, never a runtime type-scan. Because early listeners CANNOT be context beans (no context exists yet — doc 1889), this catalog is their ONLY discovery path, so the silent-DCE failure mode is acute and ASYMMETRIC: a DCE'd early run-listener is silently absent (no Starting/EnvironmentPrepared observation, no failure-on-pre-context-error) and indistinguishable from a legitimately-unregistered one — mandating the anti-DCE self-check.
- The standalone early multicaster + early-listeners-cannot-be-beans is a JVM-shaped mechanism that must be re-judged, not ported blindly. Spring's first four events fire before/around context creation via a standalone SimpleApplicationEventMulticaster (initialMulticaster), and contextLoaded then attaches the application's listeners to the LIVE context's multicaster before publishing ApplicationPrepared (doc 283). This two-multicaster split exists ONLY because Spring's real multicaster is a refresh-created bean. In leaf the question (charter §2.2) is whether a separate early channel is even needed: if leaf's event-multicaster is always-present (not a refresh-created bean), the early events could ride the one bus and 'early listeners can't be beans' reduces to the honest timing fact that no context exists yet to host a bean. The early-vs-context handoff must reconcile with the events/event-multicaster neighbour's eventual (typed-channel vs erased-bus vs hybrid) design — it cannot assume a single erased bus.
- No ambient thread-local 'current phase' across the eager-singleton/background fan-out. Spring's run-listener dispatch and startup tracing lean on a single synchronous call stack with an ambient current-step/current-phase. In async leaf, bring-up fans out into concurrent eager-singleton waves / background-bootstrap futures, so parent linkage for the startup trace and the run-phase context must be carried EXPLICITLY in each fired event (the run is the root span; refresh-internal events nest under it), never read off an ambient thread-local at an arbitrary .await point (the §2.3 fix shared with startup-instrumentation).
- The withHook thread-local single-run RunListener is hazardous across .await. Spring's getRunListeners consults a thread-local SpringApplicationHook to inject a single-run RunListener (the mechanism behind test-context bootstrapping / SpringApplication.withHook — doc 317). A thread-local read at an arbitrary suspension point is the §2.3 ThreadLocal-across-await hazard; leaf must thread the single-run hook as an EXPLICIT value into the RunListeners aggregate / state machine for exactly this run (or a task-local with documented semantics), and the AbandonedRunException-analogue short-circuit (rethrow WITHOUT analysis/close — doc 315) must be a defined signal threaded through, not an ambient throw.
- Availability is CORE (not actuator) and must be published REACTIVELY. Spring publishes LivenessState.CORRECT (with ApplicationStarted) and ReadinessState.ACCEPTING_TRAFFIC (with ApplicationReady) from the core run listener itself (doc 285). In leaf these availability transitions ride this run-event taxonomy but feed lifecycle-events' RETAINED, queryable availability STATE holder; probes must observe it reactively (a watch/notify on a transition, §2.4), never busy-poll a flag — and the runners-complete-BEFORE-ACCEPTING_TRAFFIC ordering (the K8s readiness-gate window — doc 307) is an explicit execution-context boundary the async sequence must honour, not a comment.
- The run-event sequence's error contract is NON-UNIFORM and cannot be Spring's GC-forgiving model. Spring's ApplicationReady-listener failure can FAIL startup (routed through run-failure handling, not merely logged — lifecycle-events intent), whereas ordinary early-event listener failures isolate. leaf must express a PER-PHASE error policy (some milestone-listener failures abort startup and route into the run pipeline's handle_run_failure → fire `failed` → FailureAnalysis; ordinary ones isolate) — and because there is no async Drop and no GC, a failed bring-up's teardown after a milestone-listener failure is the explicit awaited container-driven pass (cancelRefresh/context-close), never a Drop.
- The fixed named event vocabulary + the RunListener phase-name taxonomy become a cross-crate ABI with no classpath to anchor them. Spring's run-event names + the SpringApplicationRunListener callback names are agreed by convention within one JVM. In leaf, downstream/integration crates (and startup-instrumentation, which keys off a stable name vocabulary) depend on them, so leaf must PUBLISH the run-event-name taxonomy + the typed event set + the RunListener trait as a versioned public surface (an ABI-ish commitment, like startup-instrumentation's stable name taxonomy) — emitted with absolute paths by thin macros that carry zero dispatch logic.
- RunListener/observer async dispatch must box at the dyn boundary. A RunListener invoked across a dyn boundary with `async fn on_phase`/`async fn starting` is not dyn-compatible on stable (AFIT/RPITIT NOT dyn-safe — nightly doc), so the dyn-erased run-listener path must use trait_variant Send-variant + a dynosaur-style bridge OR hand-emit Pin<Box<dyn Future + Send>> per phase callback — a boxing cost acceptable on this cold bootstrap path, but a fixed workaround until RTN stabilizes.
- Early-event buffering has no implicit container-managed restart/reset. Spring buffers events fired before the multicaster exists and flushes them at registerListeners.
