In leaf there is no implicit container restart/reset, so whether a late-attaching listener (a context bean, or a dynamic subscriber) can observe the pre-context milestones it structurally missed must be an EXPLICIT decision — a per-event early-buffer drained at the handoff (R1), a retained-latest milestone mechanism on the bus (R2, reusing the lifecycle-events availability-state insight, but amplifying the stale-fact footgun), or nothing — and it must be reconciled with the events/refresh-lifecycle/lifecycle-events early-buffer designs to avoid double-buffering.
- Generic RunListeners can't be link-time-registered. There is no 'static symbol until a generic is concrete (cross-crate doc §153), so the run-listener descriptor catalog holds only concrete observer types; the thin macro must hard-error on a generic RunListener with a register_run_listener!(Concrete) shim escape hatch.

### Interactions
- **spring-application-run** — PARENT / the orchestration this taxonomy is fired BY. The run pipeline owns the ordered run() sequence and calls this feature's named phase callbacks (starting/environmentPrepared/contextPrepared/contextLoaded/started/ready/failed) at each boundary; THIS feature owns WHAT those events are, the standalone early multicaster + the contextLoaded handoff, the early-vs-context split, and the withHook/Abandoned single-run seam. R3 explicitly shares the run-pipeline R1's typed RunPhase enum (events as transition side-effects). The run pipeline's handle_run_failure is the consumer of the `failed` event; the run pipeline owns FailureAnalysis rendering (this feature only fires `failed`).
- **event-multicaster** — THE dispatch SEAM the post-handoff events flow through, and the substrate the standalone early channel must reconcile with. From ApplicationPrepared onward, events dispatch through the context's event-multicaster (sync-by-default inline-on-the-bootstrap-task, per-dispatch error policy). The CRITICAL coupling: the early-vs-context handoff (R1's two channels / R2's always-present bus / R3's phase-typed sink) depends on whether the multicaster is always-present and whether it is typed-channels vs erased-bus vs hybrid — a deferred decision this feature must keep a thin swappable adapter over. The non-uniform 'Ready-listener failure fails startup' error policy must be expressible by the multicaster's error-policy seam.
- **events** — UPSTREAM — the publish/subscribe MODEL and listener authoring the post-handoff run-events and the context-attached listeners use. The RunListener phase callbacks are (in R2) a thin facade over bus subscription; context-bean listeners that observe Prepared/Refreshed/Started/Ready are ordinary #[event_listener] beans attached at registerListeners. This feature inherits events' typed-vs-erased bus shape, its early-event-buffering design, and its cross-crate listener-discovery substrate + mandatory silent-DCE self-check.
- **lifecycle-events** — OVERLAPPING PUBLISHER + availability-state sink. The bootstrap event sequence this feature owns IS largely the same ordered run sequence lifecycle-events catalogs (Starting → … → Ready); the boundary: this feature owns the RunListener contract + the standalone early multicaster + the run-phase firing; lifecycle-events owns the availability STATE model (retained, queryable Liveness/Readiness) and the catalog of context lifecycle facts. The Liveness CORRECT / Readiness ACCEPTING_TRAFFIC publications fired here feed lifecycle-events' retained state holder. The early-pre-context-fact buffering and the cancel-vs-close fact distinction (a failed bring-up fires Failed, NOT Refreshed/Closed) are shared concerns; R2/R3 reuse lifecycle-events' retained-latest / state-transition-side-effect insights.
- **refresh-lifecycle** — FIRES events DURING the run sequence's refresh window + drains the early-event buffer. ContextRefreshed (and any ServerInitialized) fire DURING refresh on the context's multicaster — BETWEEN this feature's ContextPrepared (fired before refresh) and Started (fired after). refresh-lifecycle's registerListeners phase is where the Application's listeners attach to the context multicaster and the early-event buffer is drained (the contextLoaded handoff this feature defines lands at / coordinates with that phase). refresh-lifecycle's cancelRefresh (a pre-Refreshed failure) routes into this feature's `failed` firing.
- **runtime-lifecycle** — its auto-start completes BEFORE the Started event fires. refresh-lifecycle's finish_refresh auto-starts SmartLifecycle beans by ascending phase; only AFTER that does this feature fire ApplicationStarted + Liveness CORRECT. This feature does not start lifecycle beans — it fires the Started milestone (and the availability transition) once runtime-lifecycle's auto-start has completed, and the Ready milestone after runners; runtime-lifecycle owns the running-state machine, this feature owns the Started/Ready milestone firing layered on top.
- **context-close** — COLLABORATOR on the failure path + the close-time availability transition. On a post-Refreshed failure, this feature's `failed` firing precedes the run pipeline driving context-close (clean close: flip Readiness REFUSING_TRAFFIC first, publish Closed, stop, destroy). A pre-Refreshed failure routes to refresh-lifecycle's cancelRefresh instead (Failed fired, NOT Closed). The Abandoned short-circuit rethrows WITHOUT analysis or close. This feature owns firing `failed`; context-close owns the ordered teardown it does not.
- **startup-instrumentation** — COMPLEMENTARY observation surface + shared stable name taxonomy. This feature's fixed named run-event sequence is the EXTERNAL reactive-milestone view; startup-instrumentation is the INTERNAL timed step-tree view — both observe the same bring-up. They share the stable, .-namespaced name vocabulary discipline (this feature's run-event names + RunListener phase names are an ABI-ish vocabulary like startup-instrumentation's step names), and both must carry parent-trace linkage EXPLICITLY (not an ambient thread-local) across the async fan-out — the run is the root span both nest under.
- **environment** — the EnvironmentPrepared event is THE hook where config-data/EnvironmentPostProcessor-analogues run. This feature fires EnvironmentPrepared carrying the BootstrapContext + the Environment after the run pipeline's prepare_environment has created the Environment and added the command-line source; the firing is the precise moment config-data loading + profile activation observe-and-mutate the environment. This feature owns the EnvironmentPrepared milestone + that it carries the BootstrapContext; environment/config-data/profiles own what runs in response.
- **config-data** — RUNS AT the EnvironmentPrepared milestone this feature fires. config-data's deterministic file/import loading + multi-document activation executes as the response to EnvironmentPrepared (the EnvironmentPostProcessor moment), populating the property-source stack before the context is created. The async file/network IO config-data fences off is awaited on the bootstrap task within this run-phase window.
- **auto-configuration** — shares the scoped-catalog + force-link discipline for participant discovery. RunListeners and auto-configurations are both discovered via the same scoped catalog (link-time + optional dynamic, never a runtime classpath scan) and both depend on the Cargo-feature-as-starter + force-link discipline (a feature must gate compilation AND cause the app-root to emit `use leaf_x as _;`). The kill-switch + starter-as-feature mental model live in the run pipeline / auto-configuration; this feature inherits the same anti-DCE self-check obligation for its run-listener catalog.
- **task-execution** — EXECUTION-CONTEXT SOURCE for the bootstrap task + any async listener dispatch. The named-event sequence fires on the bootstrap task; if a post-handoff event is dispatched async (the multicaster's opt-in async path), that uses task-execution's executor, and a blocking RunListener must spawn_blocking — explicit execution-context discipline this feature documents and threads through (§2.3).

### Open questions for Phase 2
- Does leaf NEED Spring's standalone early multicaster at all, or does an always-present event-multicaster make it unnecessary scaffolding? R1 ports the two-multicaster split literally (a standalone EarlyEventChannel + a contextLoaded handoff); R2 makes the one bus always-present and reduces 'early listeners can't be beans' to the honest timing fact; R3 makes it a phase-typed sink capability transition. This is downstream of the events/event-multicaster keystone (is the multicaster a refresh-created bean or always-present? typed-channels vs erased-bus vs hybrid?) and cannot be settled per-feature — it dictates whether the early-multicaster mechanic is real machinery or designed out (charter §2.2).
- How is early-event buffering for late-attaching listeners realized — a per-event buffer drained at the contextLoaded handoff (R1), a retained-latest-per-milestone mechanism on the bus (R2, reusing the lifecycle-events availability-state insight but amplifying the stale/multi-fire footgun), or nothing (context beans simply never see pre-context milestones, matching Spring)? Shares the events neighbour's early-buffer design, refresh-lifecycle's registerListeners-flush, and lifecycle-events' retained-state-vs-retained-events fork; the answer determines whether pre-bring-up extension hooks observable by later beans are first-class.
- Which cross-crate substrate collects the RunListener / pre-context ApplicationListener descriptors, and how is the acute, ASYMMETRIC silent-DCE failure handled (a DCE'd early run-listener is silently absent with no loud resolution failure, unlike a missing context bean)? linkme (zero-cost, DCE-sensitive, no wasm), inventory (life-before-main, hostile to async), build-time codegen (Architecture C, deterministic, the entry point's natural force-link + anti-DCE-manifest home), or explicit register (Architecture D). The mandated anti-DCE self-check (expected-vs-found run-listeners per source) and leaf-doctor discovery listing are non-negotiable here. Cross-cuts the cross-crate composition meta-concept and every discovery feature.
- How is the run-event sequence's NON-UNIFORM error contract expressed — some milestone-listener failures (Started/Ready) abort startup and route into handle_run_failure → `failed` → FailureAnalysis, while ordinary early-event listener failures isolate? This needs a per-phase/per-milestone error policy on whatever dispatch seam Phase 2 picks, and depends on the deferred unified error/diagnostics model (§2.9) and the event-multicaster error-policy decision; it is the same non-uniform-error question lifecycle-events flagged for the Ready-listener-fails-startup case.
- How are the withHook single-run RunListener + the AbandonedRunException-analogue carried across .await without an ambient thread-local read at an arbitrary suspension point (the §2.3 ThreadLocal-across-await hazard)? Test-context bootstrapping / test slicing depend on this; the answer (an explicit value threaded into the RunListeners aggregate / state machine vs a documented task-local) is downstream of the deferred async-context-propagation model. Cross-cuts the testing story, task-execution, and the run pipeline's Abandoned short-circuit.
- Is the bootstrap event sequence a hand-fired ordered list of named publications (R1/R2) or a TYPED phase-transition state machine where each event fires exactly once as a verified transition side-effect (R3)? R3 gives the strongest structural guarantee that the fixed named sequence cannot be mis-ordered/double-fired/skipped, but binds this feature to the run-pipeline's RunPhase-enum shape (the run-orchestration keystone — fixed-fn vs re-orderable-stages vs frozen-plan) and to lifecycle-events' events-as-transition-side-effects. Must stay a candidate; cross-cuts spring-application-run and lifecycle-events.
- Does a dynamic (WASM-module / runtime) participant source contribute RunListeners / pre-context ApplicationListeners, and at what timing relative to the run sequence — given early listeners must exist before the FIRST event fires (Starting), a stricter timing constraint than context-bean listeners? The static-link-time-plus-optional-dynamic-source duality applies to run-participants exactly as to definitions; the timing/overlay semantics (especially under a frozen-plan run pipeline where dynamically-sourced participants have no build-time presence) are unresolved. Cross-cuts refresh-lifecycle and auto-configuration's same duality.
- How much of the SpringApplicationRunListener / event-sequence surface is rust-native intent vs JVM-shaped scaffolding to design OUT? Candidates to question against intent-parity (charter §2.2): the standalone early multicaster (above), the BootstrapContext-carrying first-two-callbacks (does leaf need a transient pre-container registry passed to early listeners, or is that a JVM artifact?), and whether the seven-callback RunListener contract should survive as-is or collapse into bus subscriptions (R2). Belongs to the per-feature Phase-3 re-unify, flagged so it isn't ported blindly.
- Does the run-event-name taxonomy + the typed run-phase event set + the RunListener trait constitute a versioned cross-crate ABI, and how does it stay coherent with startup-instrumentation's stable step-name taxonomy and lifecycle-events' fact catalog (three overlapping name vocabularies for one bring-up)? With no classpath to anchor them, downstream/integration crates depend on these names; the unification (one shared milestone vocabulary vs three) is a §2.11 question that cannot be decided for this feature alone.

### Notes
Scope discipline: I treated this feature as the NARROW sub-feature the brief names — the SpringApplicationRunListener analogue + the fixed named bootstrap event sequence + the standalone early multicaster + why earliest listeners cannot be beans + the early-vs-context handoff/buffering + the withHook single-run seam + availability-as-core publication — sitting INSIDE the supplied spring-application-run pipeline design. I deliberately did NOT re-own: the run() orchestration ORDER (spring-application-run), the general bus engine/dispatch/error-isolation (events/event-multicaster), the availability STATE model (lifecycle-events), the refresh-internal ContextRefreshed/ServerInitialized firing (refresh-lifecycle/runtime-lifecycle), or FailureAnalysis rendering (spring-application-run owns it; this feature only fires the `failed` event). The three realizations are genuinely divergent on the axis that matters HERE — the early-vs-context dispatch SHAPE: R1 ports Spring's two-multicaster split literally (highest fidelity, two-channel coherence burden); R2 unifies on one always-present bus with retained-latest replay (max unification, questions the standalone-multicaster as JVM scaffolding, but pre-commits to events-neighbour keystone calls); R3 makes the named sequence a verified phase-transition state machine (strongest structural guarantee, but binds to the run-pipeline RunPhase shape). They deliberately span the 'faithful-port vs design-it-out vs structurally-verify' spectrum so Phase-2 signal stays unbiased. All three hold the deferred §3 keystones (events type-erasure/registry substrate, the always-present-vs-refresh-created-multicaster question, the reactive-state primitive for availability, the unified error model for the non-uniform Ready-fails-startup policy, the cross-crate composition substrate, async-context-propagation for withHook) as CANDIDATES. Provider/registry abstractions kept ORIGIN-AGNOSTIC throughout (native, WASM-module, test-double RunListeners participate identically). The single most important rust-native insight: Spring's standalone early multicaster is the prime candidate to be designed OUT (charter §2.2) — it exists only because Spring's real multicaster is a refresh-created bean, and if leaf's bus is always-present, 'early listeners cannot be beans' collapses to the honest timing fact that no context exists yet; I refused to settle this (it is downstream of the events keystone) and made it the first phase2Question. Two clashes dominate and belong to Phase 2: the early-vs-context dispatch shape (inherited from events/event-multicaster) and the non-uniform error contract (the Ready-listener-fails-startup case, shared with lifecycle-events). The acute, ASYMMETRIC silent-DCE hazard is the sharpest T1 concern: a DCE'd EARLY run-listener is silently absent (no Starting observation, no failure-on-pre-context-error) and — unlike a missing context bean loud at resolution — indistinguishable from a legitimately-unregistered listener, so the anti-DCE self-check is non-negotiable and this feature is a natural host for the leaf-doctor / startup-report. Grounding fully cross-checked: spring-boot-4-di-design.md (run sequence 244-321 esp. the SpringApplicationRunListener/event-sequence 264-285, the standalone early multicaster + early-listeners-cannot-be-beans 283/1889, availability-as-core 285, the K8s runner window 307, withHook 317, AbandonedRunException 315, the full ordered sequence 268-279/1887); the supplied spring-application-run pipeline design (R1/R2/R3, the rustClashes, the run-phase taxonomy); the Phase-1 neighbour designs (refresh-lifecycle R1/R2/R3, context-close, runtime-lifecycle R1/R2/R3, events R1/R2/R3, event-multicaster, lifecycle-events R1/R2/R3 incl. the availability-state-vs-retained-events fork and the Ready-fails-startup non-uniform error intent, startup-instrumentation, environment/config-data/profiles, auto-configuration); the nightly envelope (no async Drop → explicit awaited teardown; AFIT/RPITIT NOT dyn-safe → box/trait_variant/dynosaur at the dyn run-listener boundary; thread-local-across-await hazard for withHook; no async-context primitives); and the cross-crate doc (Layer 0/A/B DCE, the force-link/anti-DCE-self-check mandate, Architectures A-D, ordering-as-data, the charter §6 leaf-framework/leaf-boot/leaf-macros/leaf-codegen topology — this feature lives in leaf-boot atop leaf-framework's bus). Notable tension flagged for Phase 3: the standalone early multicaster, the BootstrapContext-carrying first-two-callbacks, and the withHook thread-local are the three JVM-shaped mechanics most at risk of being ported blindly — each must be re-judged for rust-native necessity. Names used (RunListener, RunListeners aggregate, EarlyEventChannel, RunEventSink, RunPhase/RunTransition, run-event taxonomy) are Phase-1 placeholders only. I wrote no files. Grounding paths (all absolute): /home/jan/projects/testing/leaf/docs/research/spring-boot-4-di-design.md, /home/jan/projects/testing/leaf/docs/superpowers/specs/2026-06-14-leaf-charter-design.md, /home/jan/projects/testing/leaf/docs/research/rust-nightly-features-tradeoffs.md, /home/jan/projects/testing/leaf/docs/research/rust-cross-crate-composition.md, /home/jan/projects/testing/leaf/docs/design/phase1/05-events-lifecycle.md, /home/jan/projects/testing/leaf/docs/design/phase1/01-container-beans.md, /home/jan/projects/testing/leaf/docs/design/phase1/02-configuration-environment.md, /home/jan/projects/testing/leaf/docs/design/phase1/03-conditions-auto-configuration.md.

## Application Runners (ApplicationRunner / CommandLineRunner)  `[runners]`

The readiness-gating callback window. Per spring-boot-4-di-design.md §305-309 ("Runners: ApplicationRunner / CommandLineRunner") and the run-sequence at §244, callRunners() executes in a PRECISE window: AFTER refreshContext() and listeners.started() (the container is fully built, eager singletons constructed, SmartLifecycle auto-started, Liveness=CORRECT published), but BEFORE listeners.ready() and the AvailabilityChangeEvent(ReadinessState.ACCEPTING_TRAFFIC). The intent of THIS window is deliberate (§307): it lets startup data loading and migrations complete BEFORE readiness probes pass, so a Kubernetes-style readiness gate sees the pod as not-ready-for-traffic until the runners finish — the app starts, loads its caches / runs its DB migrations / warms its connections, and only THEN flips to accepting traffic. Runners are ordered callbacks: both ApplicationRunner (receives parsed ApplicationArguments — options/non-option args) and CommandLineRunner (receives raw args) extend a common Runner marker, and callRunners() collects ALL Runner beans and sorts them as ONE single @Order-stream (AnnotationAwareOrderComparator), so the two kinds interleave by order — this single-ordered-stream is NOT new in Boot 4 (Runner marker arrived in 2.7; the behavior is unchanged through 3.x/4.x). A runner that throws wraps in IllegalStateException and ABORTS startup (the run routes to handleRunFailure → FailureAnalyzer → close). leaf owns ONLY this sub-feature: the Runner callback contract(s), the args-shape distinction, the single-ordered-stream collection+sort, the await-each-in-order execution, the throw-aborts-startup semantics, and the precise execution-context boundary that the readiness flip sits behind. It does NOT own the run sequence itself (spring-application-run), the Started/Ready milestones or AvailabilityState publication mechanism (runtime-lifecycle / lifecycle-events), or refresh (refresh-lifecycle) — it is the contributed-callback family that the run-pipeline's call_runners() step drives, plus the ordered-await + abort discipline of that step. Realizing the intent WITHOUT JVM lineage: no spring.factories runtime scan to find Runner beans (Runners are resolved from the container as a typed, origin-agnostic collection), no IllegalStateException wrap (a rust-native RunFailure carrying which runner + cause), no sync-around-main (each runner is awaited on the bootstrap task with explicit execution-context discipline; a blocking runner must spawn_blocking), and the readiness flip is an explicit awaited boundary (await all runners, THEN publish ACCEPTING_TRAFFIC) rather than an ambient sequencing assumption.

### Candidate realizations

#### R1 — Two async-trait callbacks + a single @Order-merged await loop: ApplicationRunner/CommandLineRunner as distinct origin-agnostic descriptor traits, collected from the container into ONE order-sorted stream the call_runners() step awaits sequentially, a throw aborting into RunFailure
Mirror Spring's shape literally but rust-native. Two thin async-trait callbacks: `trait ApplicationRunner { async fn run(&self, args: &ApplicationArguments) -> Result<(), RunnerError>; }` and `trait CommandLineRunner { async fn run(&self, raw: &[String]) -> Result<(), RunnerError>; }`. Both are reduced at collection time to a common internal `RunnerEntry { order: Order, id: RunnerId, invoke: BoxFuture-producing closure capturing the typed args-shape }` — the rust-native analogue of the package-private Runner marker: not a shared supertrait the user implements, but a uniform internal entry the call_runners() step iterates. `ApplicationArguments` is a typed parse of the CLI (options as key→values multimap + ordered non-option args) shared with the run-pipeline's ParseArgs step; CommandLineRunner gets the raw &[String] the run already holds. COLLECTION: at the call_runners() step (after refresh+started), resolve BOTH runner kinds from the container as origin-agnostic collections (every Runner is a normal container bean — discovered via the container's get-all-of-type, NOT a separate runtime scan), assign each an Order (a #[runner(order=N)] attribute → descriptor metadata, default 0, stable tie-break by registration/id), MERGE the two kinds into ONE Vec<RunnerEntry>, and STABLE-sort by ascending order — so an ApplicationRunner(order=10) and a CommandLineRunner(order=5) interleave correctly (the single-ordered-stream intent). EXECUTION: await each entry's invoke() IN ORDER on the bootstrap task — strictly sequential (Spring runs them in sequence; a later migration runner may depend on an earlier cache-load runner, so sequential-by-default is the safe intent), each await an explicit execution-context point. A runner returning Err (or panicking, caught at the entry boundary) STOPS the loop immediately and wraps into a RunFailure { phase: CallRunners, runner: RunnerId, order, cause } that the run-pipeline routes to handle_run_failure (FailureAnalyzer chain + context-close) — the rust-native replacement for IllegalStateException-wrap-and-abort, carrying WHICH runner failed at WHAT order (richer than Spring's wrap). The call_runners() step itself is the readiness boundary: it returns Ok only when ALL runners completed; the run-pipeline then fires Ready + flips Readiness=ACCEPTING_TRAFFIC (runtime-lifecycle/lifecycle-events). A blocking runner (a sync migration lib) is documented to spawn_blocking inside its run(). Thin macros: #[application_runner]/#[command_line_runner] (or #[runner] picking the kind by the run() signature) emit the trait impl + a const RunnerDescriptor registration into the same catalog substrate beans use; nothing hidden, hand-writable as Application::register_runner(MyRunner).

**Pros:** Highest intent fidelity to §305-309: two callback kinds (parsed-args vs raw-args), one @Order-merged stream, sequential await, throw-aborts-startup — a reader who knows Spring's callRunners() recognizes it 1:1, and cargo expand of #[runner] reads as a plain trait impl + a descriptor registration (DX #1, §2.10, intent-not-mechanism parity).; Async-first and execution-context-explicit by construction (§2.3): each runner is awaited on the bootstrap task at an explicit .await point; the readiness flip is the precise execution boundary AFTER the await-all completes — the K8s readiness-gate intent (data load / migrations finish before ACCEPTING_TRAFFIC) becomes a literal awaited sequence, dissolving Spring's sync-around-main assumption.; Sequential-by-default is the correct safe intent: Spring runs runners in sequence and users routinely order migration-then-seed; a later runner may depend on an earlier one's side effects, so NOT parallelizing by default avoids a silent ordering hazard (R3 explores opting into parallelism for declared-independent runners).; Rich failure context (charter §1.7/§2.9): a failing runner produces RunFailure carrying the runner id + order + the full cause-chain, strictly richer than Spring's IllegalStateException wrap — and it is the natural input to a 'runner X failed during startup data load, after refresh, before ready' FailureAnalysis, exactly the bootstrap-layer complete-context promise.; Origin-agnostic + minimal new surface: runners are ordinary container beans collected by type, so a native, WASM-module, or test-double runner participates identically; the only NEW surface is the two callback traits + the ApplicationArguments type + the merge-and-sort step, everything else delegates (args from ParseArgs, ordering from the shared Order primitive, abort from the run-pipeline's handle_run_failure).; The two-trait + uniform-internal-entry split is the honest rust port of Spring's two-public-interfaces-one-package-private-marker design — users implement the kind that fits their args need, while the engine sees one homogeneous ordered list, avoiding both a leaky shared supertrait and a duplicated execution loop.

**Cons:** Two callback traits for what is almost the same thing risks DX confusion ('which do I implement?') — Spring carries both only because CommandLineRunner predates typed args; a rust-native design might collapse to ONE runner trait taking ApplicationArguments (raw args reachable from it), questioning whether CommandLineRunner is JVM-lineage scaffolding to design OUT (a §2.2 intent-parity judgement, flagged).; Sequential await means a slow runner blocks all later runners and delays the readiness flip — correct for dependent runners but a latency cost for genuinely independent ones (a 30s migration + a 30s cache-warm run as 60s of not-ready even when they could overlap); R1 offers no opt-in concurrency, pushing that to R3.; 'Resolve all Runner beans from the container' inherits the cross-crate DCE hazard (Layer 0/A/B): a runner in a crate the binary never force-links is SILENTLY absent — and unlike a missing required bean (loud at resolution), a missing runner just means a migration silently never runs, a quieter and more dangerous failure (data corruption vs a crash). Mandates the anti-DCE self-check at the runner registry.; Order is a flat integer (Spring's @Order): two runners with the same order have only a tie-break (registration/id) deciding their relative order, so cross-crate 'my seed must run after their migration' is expressed by magic-number coordination, not a declared dependency edge — fragile when runners come from independent integration crates (R2/R3 address this with declared edges).; Panic-catching at the entry boundary (to convert a panicking runner into RunFailure rather than unwinding the bootstrap task) needs a defined catch_unwind/abort policy and couples to leaf's unified error model — a runner that panics mid-migration leaves partial side effects the framework cannot roll back (only context-close can tear down beans, not undo a half-run migration), an inherent limit worth stating.; The args-shape distinction (parsed ApplicationArguments vs raw &[String]) presumes a CLI-argument model leaf must own (option syntax, multimap semantics) shared with the run-pipeline's ParseArgs — for a non-CLI app (a server with no meaningful argv) this is near-empty ceremony, so the ApplicationArguments richness must scale down to 'no args' cleanly.

**Mechanisms considered:** two async-trait callbacks `ApplicationRunner::run(&ApplicationArguments)` and `CommandLineRunner::run(&[String])`, reduced to a common internal `RunnerEntry { order, id, invoke }` (the rust analogue of Spring's package-private Runner marker); collect BOTH kinds from the container as origin-agnostic typed collections (get-all-of-type, not a separate runtime scan), assign Order from a #[runner(order=N)] attribute, MERGE into one Vec and STABLE-sort ascending — the single-ordered-stream; await each entry IN ORDER on the bootstrap task, strictly sequential by default, each an explicit .await point; a runner Err / caught-panic STOPS the loop and wraps into RunFailure { phase: CallRunners, runner, order, cause } routed to the run-pipeline's handle_run_failure (FailureAnalyzer + context-close) — replacing IllegalStateException-wrap-abort; call_runners() returning Ok is the readiness boundary: the run-pipeline fires Ready + flips Readiness=ACCEPTING_TRAFFIC only after ALL runners complete; blocking runner → documented spawn_blocking inside run() (execution-context discipline §2.3); thin #[application_runner]/#[command_line_runner]/#[runner] macros emitting trait impl + const RunnerDescriptor registration into the same catalog substrate beans use; hand-writable register_runner(Concrete) escape hatch; ApplicationArguments = typed CLI parse (options multimap + ordered non-option args) shared with the run-pipeline ParseArgs step; CommandLineRunner gets the raw slice the run already holds; considered collapsing to ONE runner trait (ApplicationArguments-only, raw reachable from it) — flagged as an intent-parity question rather than adopted, to keep R1 faithful

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** Runners are origin-agnostic container beans, so the discovery substrate is the SAME one beans/auto-configuration use (Phase-2-undecided: linkme distributed-slice / inventory / build-time codegen / explicit with(); cross-crate doc Architectures A-D). The Runner callback traits + the ApplicationArguments type + the RunnerDescriptor (order + id + invoke-factory) live in leaf-core (or leaf-boot alongside the run-pipeline, charter §6 topology) so any downstream/integration crate can contribute a runner depending only on leaf-core. This feature INHERITS the DCE story but with a QUIETER failure mode than the container's: a runner in a crate the binary never force-links is silently absent (Layer 0), or DCE'd (Layer A pre-1.62 / Layer B under LLD pre-1.89), and a missing runner means a migration/seed SILENTLY never runs (no crash, possibly data corruption) — strictly more dangerous than a missing required bean (loud at resolution). So runners are a prime consumer of the mandated anti-DCE self-check (expected-vs-found per source crate, warn on enabled-feature-zero-contributions) and a natural line item in 'leaf doctor'/the startup report ('3 runners discovered: migrate@10 from leaf-flyway, seed@20 from app, warm-cache@30 from app'). Generics can't carry a 'static descriptor → the #[runner] macro hard-errors with a register_runner!(Concrete) shim for generic runner types. The Order primitive is the SHARED cross-crate ordering vocabulary (the same one runtime-lifecycle phases, auto-config ordering, and the event/listener order use — §170 ordering-as-data: never rely on link/registration order, always sort by declared order at runtime). Stable cross-crate surface: the two callback trait signatures + ApplicationArguments shape + the RunnerId/Order vocabulary become an ABI-ish public commitment (a runner contributed by leaf-flyway must compile against a stable Runner contract), emitted with absolute paths by the thin macros. A dynamic (WASM-module) runner source contributes runners through the same RunnerDescriptor at the same collection point — timing relative to the call_runners() step is the two-source-duality question (flagged, not resolved).

**T2 — execution context:** Entirely a COLD-PATH step on the bootstrap task, but it is the LAST cold-path work before the app goes hot, so its execution boundary matters acutely (§2.3). The merge-and-sort is synchronous cold analysis (one Vec stable-sort over RunnerEntry, single-threaded, before any runner runs). EXECUTION: each runner is awaited sequentially on the bootstrap task — an explicit .await point; a runner may await freely (a DB migration's async queries, an async cache load); a BLOCKING runner (a sync migration crate) MUST spawn_blocking (documented execution-context discipline) so it never blocks the bootstrap reactor. NO GLOBAL LOCK (§2.5): runners run after refresh with the container fully built and no creation guard held, so a runner resolving beans / awaiting freely cannot deadlock a guarded worker. The READINESS FLIP is the precise execution-context boundary this feature exists to define: the call_runners() step awaits ALL runners to completion, and only then does the run-pipeline publish Readiness=ACCEPTING_TRAFFIC (reactively, via lifecycle-events' watch/notify state — never a polled flag, §2.4) — so a K8s readiness probe observing that state sees not-ready until migrations/data-load finish. CANCELLATION: cancelling the bootstrap task mid-runners drops the in-flight runner future; because there is no async Drop, a runner holding async resources must clean up explicitly on its own cancel path, and the run routes to handle_run_failure (context-close for the already-Refreshed container — runners run post-Refresh, so the teardown path is close, not cancelRefresh). A runner's partial side effects (a half-applied migration) are NOT rollback-able by the framework (only the runner's own transaction can) — an inherent limit. ERRORS: a runner Err / caught-panic aborts the loop and surfaces as RunFailure carrying the failing RunnerId + order + cause-chain (§2.9). PARENT LINKAGE: the call_runners() step is a child startup-instrumentation span under the run root; each runner is a named child step, so a slow/failing runner is visible in the boot trace.

#### R2 — One unified Runner contract over a typed ApplicationArguments, ordered by declared dependency EDGES (after/before RunnerId) topo-sorted, awaited sequentially: collapse the two-trait JVM lineage, replace magic-number @Order with cross-crate-safe edges
Question two JVM-shaped choices: (a) whether TWO runner traits are real intent or CommandLineRunner is lineage scaffolding, and (b) whether a flat integer @Order is adequate for cross-crate runner coordination. Collapse to ONE async-trait: `trait Runner { async fn run(&self, args: &ApplicationArguments) -> Result<(), RunnerError>; }` where ApplicationArguments exposes BOTH the parsed view (options multimap + non-option args) AND the raw &[String] (so a 'CommandLineRunner-style' runner just reads args.raw()) — one contract, the args-shape distinction becomes a method on the args object, not a second trait. Replace the flat @Order with DECLARED EDGES: each runner descriptor carries `{ id: RunnerId, after: &[RunnerId], before: &[RunnerId], order: Option<Order> }`, and call_runners() TOPO-SORTS the runners by their edges (with a stable secondary sort by optional order then id for unconstrained pairs), detecting cycles as an early rich diagnostic BEFORE any runner runs. So 'seed-data must run after db-migrate' is a declared edge (after = [DbMigrate::ID]) that holds even when db-migrate comes from leaf-flyway and seed from the app crate — no magic-number coordination across crate boundaries. EXECUTION stays sequential await on the bootstrap task in the topo-resolved order (the safe default; R3 layers concurrency onto the SAME edge graph). The readiness flip, the abort-on-throw (→ RunFailure), the spawn_blocking discipline, and the descriptor/catalog substrate are as R1. The cycle/missing-edge-target detection runs at the start of call_runners() (or earlier, see R3) and is itself a FailureAnalysis-grade diagnostic ('runner cycle: migrate → seed → migrate' / 'seed declares after=warm-cache but no runner warm-cache is registered — did you enable the cache starter?'). Thin macro: #[runner(after(DbMigrate), before(StartTraffic))] emits the impl + a descriptor with the edges resolved to RunnerId consts; the escape hatch is register_runner(MyRunner).with_after(...).

**Pros:** Cross-crate-safe ordering (T1 strength): declared after/before edges over RunnerId mean a runner in leaf-flyway and a runner in the app crate coordinate by a NAMED dependency, not a coincidental integer — the §170 'ordering-as-data, never rely on link/registration order' principle realized for runners, and the SAME topo-sort primitive refresh-lifecycle/auto-config-ordering/the run-pipeline R2 mandate (the unification dividend, §2.11).; Collapsing to one Runner trait is a clean §2.2 intent-parity win IF CommandLineRunner is judged lineage: one contract, the raw-vs-parsed distinction as a method on ApplicationArguments — less DX confusion ('which trait?'), one execution loop, and the args object is the single source for both views. The two-trait split in Spring exists for historical reasons (CommandLineRunner predates typed args), not a real semantic need.; Earliest + richest failure for ordering mistakes (§2.9): a cycle or a dangling after/before target is caught at sort time BEFORE any runner runs (zero side effects), with a complete diagnostic naming the unsatisfiable edge and the suspected missing starter — strictly better than R1's flat order (which can silently place runners in a surprising relative order with no error), and a much better story than Spring (which has no cross-runner dependency concept at all).; Extensible without magic numbers: an integration crate adds a runner that must slot 'after migrations, before traffic-accept' by declaring edges, and it lands correctly regardless of what other runners exist or what integer they chose — the open-set cross-crate runner story Spring's flat @Order handles poorly.; Keeps the safe sequential-await default (dependent runners are common) while making the dependency structure EXPLICIT and inspectable — the topo order is data you can dump ('resolved runner order: migrate, seed, warm-cache') in the startup report, better debuggability than an emergent integer sort.; Reuses the shared ordering/topo-sort engine, so runners do not invent a bespoke ordering mechanism — directly serving unification and giving the anti-DCE self-check a richer hook (a missing expected runner shows up as a dangling edge target, naming which contribution is absent, not just a count mismatch).

**Cons:** Diverges from Spring's deliberately simple flat-@Order model — more machinery (edges + topo-sort + cycle detection) for the common case where an app has 2-3 runners and a flat order is plenty; risks over-engineering a small surface (a CLI app with one runner pays topo-sort it never needs), and the DX of declaring edges is heavier than slapping order=10.; Collapsing the two traits PRE-JUDGES the §2.2 intent question (is CommandLineRunner real or lineage?) — if some users genuinely want the raw-args contract as a distinct type (clearer intent, narrower signature), one-trait-with-a-method is a slight expressiveness loss; this should arguably be a phase2Question, not baked into a realization (flagged).; Edges over RunnerId make RunnerId a cross-crate ABI surface (a runner referencing DbMigrate::ID couples to leaf-flyway's published const) — a tighter coupling than R1's standalone integer, and a renamed/removed runner id in a dependency becomes a compile or sort-time break in dependents (semver burden on the runner-id vocabulary).; Under-constrained runners still need a stable fallback (optional order, then id): two runners with no edges between them have an arbitrary-but-stable relative order, so the 'declare your real dependencies' discipline is advisory — an author who forgets an edge gets a surprising-but-stable order, a quieter footgun the topo-sort cannot catch (same class as R1's tie-break, just relocated).; The cycle/dangling-target detection must run at a defined point (start of call_runners(), or earlier in a validation pass) and its diagnostic quality depends on the deferred unified error model — the 'did you enable the cache starter?' hint requires the registry to know expected-but-absent runner ids, coupling to the anti-DCE manifest (good synergy, but another dependency).; Sequential-only execution (like R1) still serializes genuinely-independent runners; R2 makes the dependency graph explicit but does NOT itself use it to parallelize — so the latency cost of independent runners remains, deferred to R3 which builds on R2's edges.

**Mechanisms considered:** ONE `trait Runner { async fn run(&self, args: &ApplicationArguments) -> Result<(), RunnerError>; }`; ApplicationArguments exposes BOTH parsed (options multimap + non-option args) AND raw &[String] — the args-shape distinction as a method, not a second trait; runner descriptor carries `{ id: RunnerId, after: &[RunnerId], before: &[RunnerId], order: Option<Order> }`; call_runners() TOPO-SORTS by edges with stable secondary sort (order then id) for unconstrained pairs; cycle + dangling-edge-target detection at sort time, BEFORE any runner runs — a FailureAnalysis-grade early diagnostic naming the unsatisfiable edge + suspected missing starter; sequential await on the bootstrap task in topo-resolved order (safe default; concurrency deferred to R3 over the same edge graph); readiness flip / abort-on-throw→RunFailure / spawn_blocking discipline / catalog descriptor substrate as R1; thin #[runner(after(DbMigrate), before(StartTraffic))] macro emitting impl + edge-bearing descriptor (edges = RunnerId consts); register_runner(MyRunner).with_after(...) escape hatch; considered keeping a flat Order alongside edges as the simple-case path (edges optional, default empty) so a one-runner app pays nothing — order as the unconstrained-tie-break, edges for real cross-crate dependencies; considered whether collapsing the two traits should be a realization choice or a phase2Question — flagged as a question, surfaced explicitly

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** This is the realization built FOR cross-crate runner coordination. The Runner trait + ApplicationArguments + the edge-bearing RunnerDescriptor live in leaf-core/leaf-boot; integration crates contribute runners depending only on leaf-core. The after/before edges over RunnerId are the §170 ordering-as-data answer applied to runners: a leaf-flyway DbMigrate runner publishes DbMigrate::ID as a stable const, and an app's seed runner declares after(DbMigrate) — the order holds regardless of link/registration order (never rely on it). This MAKES RunnerId a cross-crate ABI commitment (the published id vocabulary must version cleanly; a removed/renamed id breaks dependents at compile or sort time — a tighter but more honest coupling than R1's integers). The topo-sort is the SAME engine the run-pipeline R2 / refresh-lifecycle R2 / auto-config-ordering want — one shared scheduling primitive across the whole bring-up (the unification dividend). The discovery substrate is the shared bean/catalog one (Phase-2-undecided linkme/inventory/codegen/explicit), so the DCE hazard is inherited acutely with the same QUIET failure mode as R1 (a missing runner = a migration silently skipped) — but R2 turns it into a RICHER signal: a silently-DCE'd runner crate shows up as a DANGLING after/before edge target ('seed declares after=migrate, but no runner migrate is registered'), naming the absent contribution rather than a count-only mismatch. So the anti-DCE self-check + the edge-target validation are the same check, hosted at sort time, and feed 'leaf doctor'. Generics → register_runner!(Concrete) macro shim (no 'static descriptor for a generic). A dynamic (WASM-module) runner source contributes edge-bearing descriptors at the same collection point; its edges referencing static-crate RunnerIds (and vice-versa) is the two-source-duality timing question (flagged, not resolved). Origin-agnostic throughout: a native, WASM-module, or test-double runner with edges participates identically.

**T2 — execution context:** As R1 — a COLD-PATH step on the bootstrap task, the last cold work before the app goes hot. The topo-sort + cycle/dangling-target detection is SYNCHRONOUS cold analysis over the runner descriptors (single-threaded, before any runner runs) producing the resolved order + the earliest diagnostics. EXECUTION is sequential await in topo order on the bootstrap task — each runner an explicit .await point; async runners await freely, blocking runners MUST spawn_blocking (§2.3). NO GLOBAL LOCK (§2.5): runners run post-Refresh with no creation guard held. The READINESS FLIP is the same precise boundary: await ALL runners, THEN publish Readiness=ACCEPTING_TRAFFIC reactively via lifecycle-events (watch/notify, never polled, §2.4) — migrations/data-load (now correctly ORDERED by edges) finish before a K8s readiness probe sees ready. CANCELLATION: cancelling mid-runners drops the in-flight future; no async Drop, so a runner cleans up its async resources explicitly on cancel; the run routes to handle_run_failure → context-close (post-Refresh teardown path). A cycle/dangling-target detected at sort time aborts BEFORE any side effect (the earliest, richest abort); a runtime runner Err/caught-panic aborts the sequential loop and surfaces as RunFailure carrying the failing RunnerId + the resolved-order context + cause-chain (§2.9). PARENT LINKAGE: call_runners() is a child startup-instrumentation span; the resolved topo order is recorded so the boot trace shows runners in their actual execution order with their declared edges — a forensic for 'why did seed run before migrate?' (answer: a missing edge).

#### R3 — Build-time-frozen runner SCHEDULE + thin async executor with declared-independence concurrency: resolve the runner set, the topo order, and the parallelizable groups once into an inspectable RunnerPlan; run() awaits the frozen schedule, overlapping declared-independent runners while honoring the readiness gate
Push the AOT/plan lineage (shared with the run-pipeline R3 / refresh-lifecycle R3) onto the runner step, AND exploit the explicit dependency edges (from R2) to safely parallelize. Separate the runner step's STRUCTURE from its EXECUTION. A PLAN phase (build-time codegen via leaf-codegen reading cargo metadata + resolved features, OR a runtime startup-validation pass when not AOT) resolves everything statically knowable about runners: the runner SET (collected, deduped from the resolved feature graph), the topo order over after/before edges, cycle/dangling-target detection (fails the BUILD with complete context, zero runtime side effects), and — the new lever — the PARALLELIZABLE GROUPS: runners with no transitive edge between them form a concurrency WAVE that may overlap, while edges force sequencing between waves. It emits a `RunnerPlan { ordered_waves: Vec<Vec<RunnerId>>, edges, expected_source_crates }` as a checked-in/const artifact (sqlx model, Architecture C, fused with the run-pipeline's RunPlan). The RUNTIME call_runners() is then a THIN executor: consume the frozen RunnerPlan and, wave by wave, instantiate+invoke the wave's runners — each wave a bounded structured-concurrency fan-out (independent runners overlap, e.g. a 30s migration and a 30s cache-warm run concurrently = 30s not 60s of not-ready), join the wave before starting the next (edges respected), and on the final wave's completion the run-pipeline flips Readiness=ACCEPTING_TRAFFIC. Validation moves EARLIEST: the plan validates the runner graph (no cycle, every edge target present, every expected runner-source crate linked) at BUILD time — so a missing-runner (DCE'd migration crate) or a cycle is a BUILD error, not a silent skip at runtime. The runtime failure path (a runner Errs/panics) cancels its wave's structured scope (sibling in-flight runners in the same wave are cancelled), unwinds, and surfaces RunFailure routed to handle_run_failure → context-close. A withHook/test-slice or WASM-module runner the plan didn't anticipate joins via an explicit runtime-overlay lane (appended as a final serial wave, or merged with declared edges if it carries them). Same executor serves AOT-emitted and runtime-computed plans (no bimodality).

**Pros:** Solves the latency cost R1/R2 leave open: declared-independent runners OVERLAP within a wave (structured concurrency), so an app whose migration and cache-warm are truly independent reaches readiness in max(durations) not sum — directly serving the readiness-gate intent (minimize the not-ready window) while STILL honoring edges (dependent runners stay sequenced across waves). The safe-by-default ordering of R1/R2 plus opt-in-via-honest-edges parallelism.; Best fit for the §3 compile-vs-runtime keystone + the AOT lineage applied to the runner step: the runner SET, order, and wave structure are statically knowable, so the collection + topo-sort + cycle/dangling-target detection move to BUILD time — a thin readable runtime executor, and the runner schedule is an INSPECTABLE artifact ('wave 0: migrate; wave 1: seed, warm-cache (parallel)') not emergent behavior (§2.10 legibility).; Earliest + richest fail-fast for the DCE trap taken to its limit (charter §1.7, §2.9): a DCE'd migration runner (the dangerous silent-skip of R1/R2) becomes a BUILD error ('expected runner-source crate leaf-flyway contributed 0 runners — feature enabled but crate not force-linked') via the build-time manifest cross-check — turning runners' worst silent-failure mode (a migration that silently never runs → data corruption) into a deterministic CI gate, the purest realization of the readiness-gate's safety intent.; Directly addresses the cross-crate doc's strongest recommendation (Architecture C / sqlx model, the deterministic platform-independent path incl. wasm): a build-time cargo-metadata-driven runner plan sidesteps all three DCE layers AND non-deterministic DCE entirely — the anti-DCE self-check is a build-time manifest cross-check, not a fragile runtime count.; Identical executor across AOT-emitted and runtime-computed plans = one runner-step code path for optimized and dev builds (no bimodality), and wasm/embedded (where link-time discovery fails) get a first-class runner path — the cross-crate doc's identical-runtime-API goal.; Wave-based structured concurrency gives clean cancellation semantics (§2.3): a failing runner cancels its wave's siblings via the structured scope and unwinds, and the readiness flip is the precise boundary after the final wave — a mechanically-derived failure/teardown path rather than hand-coded which-runner-failed bookkeeping.

**Cons:** Diverges MOST from Spring's runtime-dynamism + simple-sequential model and pre-judges the §3 compile-vs-runtime + metadata/codegen keystones the hardest — presenting a frozen RunnerPlan + parallel waves as THE realization risks biasing Phase 2; must stay strictly a CANDIDATE, and its payoff is bounded by how much of the runner set is statically knowable (profile/condition-gated runners, dynamic/WASM runners are not).; Parallelizing runners is a SEMANTIC HAZARD if edges are under-declared: two runners the plan believes independent (no edge) but which actually share state (both touch the same table) now race — Spring's always-sequential model never has this, so R3 trades the latency win for a new correctness footgun that the safe-default of R1/R2 avoids. The 'declare your real dependencies or get a data race' burden is heavier than 'declare or get a surprising order'.; Profile/condition/feature-gated runners (a runner that only applies under a profile, or whose enabling condition is runtime) are not fully knowable at plan time — the plan needs a conservative over-approximation + runtime re-resolution, partially reintroducing the dynamism it sought to eliminate, and the withHook/test-slice/WASM-module overlay lane (runners the plan didn't anticipate) erodes the frozen-plan simplicity for exactly the test/dynamic cases.; Heaviest machinery for a small surface: a whole RunnerPlan IR (ordered waves + edges + expected-source-crates) + a build-time plan phase + a structured-concurrency wave executor — overkill for the overwhelmingly common case of 1-3 sequential runners, and the RunnerPlan becomes a stable artifact/format commitment that must version with leaf and stay coherent with the fused RunPlan.; Two computation modes (build-time codegen + runtime-computed) that must produce IDENTICAL runner schedules, plus the runtime overlay lane, is essentially R2's topo-sort + a wave grouping anyway — so the incremental payoff over R2 (build-time validation + concurrency) is real but bounded, and keeping the modes coherent is a maintenance burden.; Structured-concurrency wave execution means the readiness-flip boundary now depends on ALL runners in the final wave completing, and a single slow runner in an otherwise-fast wave still gates the flip — plus concurrent runners sharing the bootstrap reactor need careful spawn_blocking discipline (two blocking runners in one wave must BOTH spawn_blocking or they serialize on the reactor anyway), a subtler execution-context story than the sequential R1/R2.

**Mechanisms considered:** PLAN phase (build-time codegen via leaf-codegen reading cargo metadata + resolved features, OR runtime startup-validation pass) resolving the runner SET, topo order, cycle/dangling-target detection, AND parallelizable groups — WITHOUT running any runner; `RunnerPlan { ordered_waves: Vec<Vec<RunnerId>>, edges, expected_source_crates }` as a checked-in/const artifact (sqlx model, Architecture C), fused with the run-pipeline RunPlan; thin async executor: wave by wave, instantiate+invoke a wave's runners as a bounded structured-concurrency fan-out (independent runners overlap), join before the next wave (edges respected); final-wave completion → Readiness=ACCEPTING_TRAFFIC; build-time validation: no cycle, every edge target present, every expected runner-source crate force-linked → BUILD error with complete context, zero runtime side effects (the DCE'd-migration silent-skip becomes a CI gate); runtime failure: a runner Err/panic cancels its wave's structured scope (sibling in-flight runners cancelled), unwinds, surfaces RunFailure → handle_run_failure → context-close; runtime-overlay lane for withHook/test-slice/WASM-module runners the plan didn't anticipate (appended serial wave, or merged via their declared edges); identical executor across AOT-emitted and runtime-computed plans (sqlx --check lineage); plan checked-in + --check-able as the build-time anti-DCE manifest for runners; conservative over-approximation + runtime re-resolution for profile/condition/feature-gated runners the plan can't fully fix; spawn_blocking discipline within a wave: concurrent blocking runners must each spawn_blocking or they serialize on the bootstrap reactor — documented execution-context rule

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** The realization that confronts the runner DCE trap most directly via the cross-crate doc's most-reliable path (Architecture C, sqlx model). A build.rs / `cargo leaf prepare` in the binary crate reads the resolved dependency graph (cargo metadata) + a manifest convention, ENUMERATES the runner-contributing crates, emits the force-link references AND the RunnerPlan into OUT_DIR (or a checked-in --check-able artifact) include!'d into the binary — sidestepping Layer 0 (the plan enumerates declared runner-source crates and force-links them), Layer A (rustc reachability), and Layer B (--gc-sections) ENTIRELY, fully platform-independent incl. wasm/embedded where linkme fails. The anti-DCE self-check becomes a BUILD-TIME manifest cross-check for runners specifically (expected-vs-found per declared runner-source crate; --check fails CI on a silently-lost migration runner) — strictly more reliable than R1/R2's runtime detection, turning runners' worst silent-failure trap (a migration that never runs) into a deterministic gate. The topo order + wave grouping are resolved at plan time so registration/link order is irrelevant (§170). BUT it cannot see runners in crates the build doesn't know about (enumerates DECLARED crates via metadata, not a classpath), and a dynamic WASM-module runner has NO build-time presence → it joins via the runtime-overlay lane (a phase2Question). RunnerId remains a cross-crate ABI (edges reference it) and the RunnerPlan format + the Runner trait + ApplicationArguments become a stable format/ABI commitment (must version cleanly, fused with the RunPlan). leaf-codegen (proc-macro/build crates isolated from runtime, charter §6) owns plan emission; leaf-boot owns the executor. Origin-agnostic: a declared native crate and a build-known integration crate are planned identically; a runtime-overlay (WASM/test) runner joins the same executor but bypasses the plan. CANDIDATES, not a decision — the plan's scope is exactly the statically-knowable fraction of the runner set.

**T2 — execution context:** The PLAN phase is SYNCHRONOUS cold-path/build-time work (single-threaded, no IO into the running app, before the binary runs or in a dedicated runtime validation pass) — pure analysis producing the RunnerPlan + the earliest (build-time) diagnostics. The runtime EXECUTOR is async on the bootstrap task: it runs the frozen waves, each wave a bounded structured-concurrency fan-out where declared-independent runners OVERLAP (a failure/cancel in one node cancels the wave and unwinds cleanly, §2.3); a blocking runner within a wave MUST spawn_blocking (else concurrent blocking runners serialize on the reactor — a documented execution-context rule sharper than the sequential R1/R2). Edges force sequencing across waves (a later wave's runner reads the prior wave's committed side effects). NO GLOBAL LOCK (§2.5): runners run post-Refresh, no creation guard held. The READINESS FLIP is the precise boundary after the FINAL wave joins: the run-pipeline publishes Readiness=ACCEPTING_TRAFFIC reactively via lifecycle-events (watch/notify, never polled, §2.4) — overlapping-independent + sequenced-dependent runners all complete before a K8s probe sees ready, minimizing the not-ready window. CANCELLATION: cancelling the bootstrap task cancels the active wave's structured scope → in-flight runner futures drop; no async Drop, so each runner cleans up async resources explicitly on cancel; the run routes to handle_run_failure → context-close (post-Refresh). A build-time plan-validation failure (cycle, dangling edge, missing runner-source crate) aborts at COMPILE/PREPARE time with complete context (zero side effects); a runtime runner failure cancels its wave, surfaces RunFailure carrying the failing RunnerId + wave + cause-chain (§2.9). The runtime-overlay lane (withHook/test/WASM runners) runs on the same bootstrap task, joined into the executor as a final serial wave or merged by its edges. PARENT LINKAGE: call_runners() is a child startup-instrumentation span; each wave + each runner is a named child step, so the boot trace shows the wave structure and any overlap.

### Rust clashes
- No spring.factories runtime SPI loading / no runtime classpath to find Runner beans. Spring's callRunners() collects Runner beans from the container (which were themselves wired via component-scan / spring.factories). Rust has no global classpath and no runtime type-scan, so runners must be collected as origin-agnostic 'static descriptors from the SAME scoped catalog substrate beans use (Phase-2-undecided linkme/inventory/codegen/explicit), addressed by ROLE (the Runner contract), never a runtime scan. This inherits the silent-DCE failure mode, and for runners it is ACUTELY dangerous: a missing runner is a migration/seed that SILENTLY never runs (data corruption), not a loud load error — quieter and worse than a missing required bean. Mandates the anti-DCE self-check at the runner registry.
- No IllegalStateException wrap; rust-native typed failure instead. Spring wraps a throwing runner in IllegalStateException and aborts. Rust has no exception type to wrap into — a runner returns Result<(), RunnerError> (or panics, caught at the entry boundary), and the abort is a rich RunFailure { phase: CallRunners, runner: RunnerId, order/wave, cause-chain } routed to the run-pipeline's handle_run_failure → FailureAnalyzer → context-close. This is STRICTLY richer than Spring's wrap (which loses which-runner context) and is exactly the charter §1.7/§2.9 complete-context-failure surface — but the analyzer-matching mechanism couples to the deferred unified error model (downcast over a typed error enum vs Any vs pattern-matched cause-chain), so the RunnerError representation must stay a candidate.
- No sync-around-main; each runner is awaited with explicit execution-context discipline. Spring runs runners synchronously on the main thread. In async Rust each runner is an `.await` on the bootstrap task; an async runner (async DB migration) awaits freely, but a BLOCKING runner (a sync migration crate) MUST spawn_blocking or it stalls the bootstrap reactor — a documented execution-context rule (§2.3) Spring never needs. Under R3's concurrent waves this sharpens: two blocking runners in one wave must BOTH spawn_blocking or they serialize on the reactor anyway.
- No async Drop; a cancelled/failed runner's teardown is explicit. Spring relies on GC + sync teardown. In Rust there is no async Drop (nightly: experimental-incomplete, tokio-shutdown crashes — avoid), so cancelling the bootstrap task mid-runner drops the in-flight future and the runner must clean up its own async resources explicitly on its cancel path; the framework's teardown is the explicit awaited context-close (runners run POST-Refresh, so close, not cancelRefresh). Crucially, a runner's partial SIDE EFFECTS (a half-applied migration) are NOT framework-rollback-able — only the runner's own transaction can undo them, an inherent limit to state explicitly.
- The two-trait-one-marker shape is JVM lineage to RE-JUDGE, not port blindly. Spring carries ApplicationRunner + CommandLineRunner over a package-private Runner marker largely for historical reasons (CommandLineRunner predates typed ApplicationArguments). The rust-native question (§2.2 intent-parity): is the raw-args-vs-parsed-args distinction real intent (two traits) or scaffolding (one Runner trait taking an ApplicationArguments that exposes both views)? R1 ports both faithfully; R2/R3 collapse to one — this must be a deliberate judgement, not an automatic port.
- Flat @Order is fragile across crate boundaries; declared edges are the rust-native ordering. Spring's AnnotationAwareOrderComparator sorts the single Runner stream by an integer @Order — fine within one app, fragile when runners come from independent integration crates (magic-number coordination). The rust-native answer (R2/R3) is declared after/before edges over RunnerId topo-sorted (the §170 ordering-as-data principle: never rely on link/registration order, always sort by declared dependency at runtime) — but this makes RunnerId a cross-crate ABI vocabulary that must version cleanly.
- The Runner contract + ApplicationArguments + RunnerId/Order vocabulary (+ R3's RunnerPlan format) become a cross-crate ABI with no classpath to anchor them. In one JVM these are agreed by convention; in leaf, integration crates (leaf-flyway etc.) depend on them, so leaf must PUBLISH them as a versioned public surface emitted with absolute paths by the thin macros — an ABI-ish commitment like the run-pipeline's event-name taxonomy.
- The readiness flip must be a reactive state transition, not a polled flag. The whole point of the runners window is that Readiness=ACCEPTING_TRAFFIC flips AFTER runners complete so K8s readiness probes gate traffic. leaf must publish that availability state reactively (a watch/notify transition consumed by probes, §2.4), never busy-poll a flag, and the await-all-runners-THEN-flip ordering is an explicit execution-context boundary (§2.3) the async pipeline honors — Spring's sequencing was an implicit consequence of synchronous ordering.

### Interactions
- **spring-application-run** — PARENT / the step that OWNS this feature. call_runners() is one named step in the run-pipeline's fixed sequence (after refresh_context() + Started+Liveness, before Ready+Readiness=ACCEPTING_TRAFFIC). This feature provides the Runner contract(s), the collect+merge+order logic, the await-each discipline, and the abort-to-RunFailure semantics that the run-pipeline's call_runners() step invokes; the run-pipeline owns WHERE the step sits and routes a runner failure into handle_run_failure (FailureAnalyzer + teardown). The args this feature consumes (ApplicationArguments / raw &[String]) come from the run-pipeline's ParseArgs step. Strictly a sub-feature of the run-pipeline.
- **refresh-lifecycle** — UPSTREAM precondition. Runners run STRICTLY after refresh-lifecycle's refresh() has completed (the container fully built, all eager singletons constructed, ContextRefreshed fired) — so a runner can resolve and use any singleton bean, with no creation guard held. A refresh failure aborts BEFORE runners ever run (they are post-Refresh), which is also why a runner-failure teardown path is context-close (clean close of a built container), not refresh-lifecycle's cancelRefresh.
- **runtime-lifecycle** — BRACKETING milestones + availability. runtime-lifecycle's finish_refresh auto-starts SmartLifecycle beans and the run fires Started+Liveness=CORRECT BEFORE runners; runners then run; only after ALL runners complete does the run fire Ready and runtime-lifecycle/lifecycle-events publish Readiness=ACCEPTING_TRAFFIC. This feature owns the await-all boundary; runtime-lifecycle/lifecycle-events own the AvailabilityState publication (reactive watch/notify) that the readiness flip drives.
- **lifecycle-events** — DOWNSTREAM readiness signal. The completion of the runner step is the trigger for the run-pipeline to fire the Ready event and the AvailabilityChangeEvent(ReadinessState.ACCEPTING_TRAFFIC) that lifecycle-events defines and routes. This feature does not publish those itself — it provides the awaited boundary after which they fire. The availability state must be observed reactively by probes (§2.4).
- **container-core** — SOURCE of runner instances. Runners are ordinary container beans resolved from container-core's context at the call_runners() step (get-all-of-type for each Runner kind). A runner may itself resolve other beans during its run() (the container is fully built and running), so container-core is both where runners come from and what they operate against.
- **context-close** — TEARDOWN on runner failure. A runner that Errs/panics aborts startup; because runners run post-Refresh, the run-pipeline drives context-close (clean ordered teardown of the built container) — NOT refresh-lifecycle's cancelRefresh. context-close models exactly the post-Refreshed clean-close path this feature's failure routes to. Note: context-close tears down beans, but cannot roll back a runner's already-applied side effects (a half-run migration).
- **startup-instrumentation** — INSTRUMENTED. The call_runners() step is a child startup span under the run root; each runner (and under R3 each wave) is a named child step, so a slow or failing runner is visible in the boot trace with its order/wave. Parent linkage is carried explicitly (the §2.3 fix). On failure the in-flight runner step is tagged with the outcome for boot-failure forensics.
- **auto-configuration** — POTENTIAL CONTRIBUTOR + feature-keying. Integration starters (the 'classpath is the configuration' / starter-as-Cargo-feature model) commonly contribute runners (e.g. a leaf-flyway starter contributes a DbMigrate runner). Whether a runner is present keys off the resolved capability/feature set + the force-link discipline — the same mechanism auto-configuration uses, and the same DCE hazard (an enabled-but-unlinked starter contributes a SILENTLY-absent runner).

### Open questions for Phase 2
- Is the runner family TWO traits (ApplicationRunner parsed-args + CommandLineRunner raw-args, faithful to Spring's two-public-one-marker shape, R1) or ONE Runner trait over an ApplicationArguments that exposes both views (collapsing CommandLineRunner as JVM lineage, R2/R3)? This is a §2.2 intent-parity judgement (is the raw-vs-parsed distinction real intent or historical scaffolding?) that affects the public API surface and the args model leaf must own. Belongs to the per-feature Phase-3 re-unify; flagged so it isn't ported blindly.
- Is runner ORDERING a flat @Order integer (R1, Spring-faithful, fragile across crates) or declared after/before dependency EDGES over RunnerId topo-sorted (R2/R3, cross-crate-safe, but makes RunnerId an ABI and adds machinery)? This is downstream of the unified ORDERING primitive keystone (the same topo-sort-over-edges question refresh-lifecycle, auto-config-ordering, the run-pipeline, and the event/listener order all raise) — must be resolved ONCE for the whole framework, not per-feature.
- Do runners run STRICTLY SEQUENTIALLY (R1/R2, the safe Spring-faithful default — a later runner may depend on an earlier's side effects) or may declared-INDEPENDENT runners OVERLAP in concurrency waves (R3, minimizing the not-ready window but introducing a data-race footgun if edges are under-declared)? This trades readiness-window latency against a new correctness hazard Spring never has, and depends on whether the dependency structure is declared explicitly enough to trust. Cross-cuts the §3 compile-vs-runtime keystone.
- Is the runner step's STRUCTURE (set, order, waves, expected-source crates) computed at RUNTIME (R1/R2) or FROZEN at build time into an inspectable RunnerPlan + thin executor (R3, AOT/sqlx determinism + earliest fail-fast + the DCE'd-migration-becomes-a-build-error gate, but pre-judges the compile-vs-runtime + metadata/codegen keystones hardest and struggles with profile/condition/dynamic runners)? Must stay a CANDIDATE; it is the runner-step shape downstream of the §3 keystones.
- Which cross-crate substrate collects the runner registry (linkme / inventory / build-time codegen / explicit with()), and how is the runner-specific DCE failure mode (a SILENTLY-absent migration runner = data corruption, quieter and more dangerous than a missing bean) handled by the mandated anti-DCE self-check? The runner registry is a prime consumer of the force-link discipline + the expected-vs-found manifest cross-check (and 'leaf doctor'). Cross-cuts auto-configuration and every discovery feature; resolved once for the whole framework.
- What is the RunnerError representation and how does it feed the unified error/diagnostics model (FailureAnalysis)? The abort-on-throw → RunFailure { runner, order, cause } is the charter §1.7/§2.9 surface for 'runner X failed during startup data load, after refresh, before ready', but the analyzer-matching mechanism (downcast over a typed error enum vs Any vs pattern-matched cause-chain) and the catch-policy for a PANICKING runner (catch_unwind vs abort) depend on the deferred unified error model. Cross-cuts the run-pipeline's FailureAnalyzer and condition-report.
- How rich must the ApplicationArguments model be, and does it scale DOWN cleanly to apps with no meaningful argv (a server vs a CLI)? The parsed-options-multimap + non-option-args + raw-slice shape is shared with the run-pipeline's ParseArgs step; for a non-CLI app it is near-empty, so the model must not impose ceremony on the no-args case. Belongs to the run-pipeline / args meta-design, flagged here as the consumer.
- Can a DYNAMIC (WASM-module / runtime) source contribute runners, and at what TIMING relative to the call_runners() step — especially under R3 where dynamically-sourced runners have no build-time presence and need a runtime-overlay lane (appended wave / merged edges) that erodes the frozen plan? The two-source duality (static link-time + optional dynamic) applies to runners exactly as to beans/definitions; the overlay timing + how a dynamic runner's edges reference static RunnerIds (and vice-versa) is unresolved. Cross-cuts refresh-lifecycle and auto-configuration's same duality.

### Notes
Scope boundary honoured: this feature is the RUNNER FAMILY ONLY — the ApplicationRunner/CommandLineRunner callback contract(s), the single-ordered-stream collect+merge+sort, the await-each-in-order execution, the throw-aborts-startup semantics, and the precise readiness-gate execution boundary the runners window defines. It is a SUB-FEATURE of spring-application-run, which owns the run sequence, WHERE call_runners() sits, and the handle_run_failure routing; it delegates the readiness/availability publication to runtime-lifecycle + lifecycle-events, the container to container-core, the prior refresh to refresh-lifecycle, and the failure teardown to context-close. The marquee intent (spring-boot-4-di-design.md §307) is the K8s readiness-gate window: runners (data load / migrations) complete on the bootstrap task BEFORE Readiness=ACCEPTING_TRAFFIC flips — realized here as an explicit awaited execution-context boundary. The three realizations deliberately span the axis Phase 2 must decide: R1 is Spring-faithful (two traits, flat @Order, sequential), R2 collapses the two-trait lineage + replaces @Order with cross-crate-safe declared edges (unify-via-shared-topo-sort), R3 freezes the runner schedule at build time + adds declared-independence concurrency waves (AOT/determinism + earliest fail-fast, the strongest answer to runners' uniquely-dangerous silent-DCE failure mode). All hold the deferred §3 keystones (unified ordering primitive, cross-crate composition substrate, compile-vs-runtime split, unified error/diagnostics model, metadata/codegen boundary) as CANDIDATES; provider/registry abstractions kept ORIGIN-AGNOSTIC throughout (native, WASM-module, test-double runners participate identically). Two notable tensions to flag for Phase 3: (1) the two-trait shape (ApplicationRunner + CommandLineRunner) is the JVM-lineage mechanic most at risk of being ported blindly — it must be re-judged for rust-native necessity (§2.2); (2) runner concurrency (R3) is the single place where minimizing the readiness window (intent) collides with a new data-race correctness hazard absent from Spring's always-sequential model — the safe default is sequential, parallelism only over honestly-declared independence. The uniquely-dangerous property of THIS feature vs the rest of the bootstrap layer: a silently-DCE'd runner is not a loud failure but a migration that NEVER RUNS (data corruption) — so the anti-DCE self-check / force-link discipline is not optional polish here, it is correctness-critical, and R3's build-time manifest gate is the strongest realization of that. Grounding cross-checked: spring-boot-4-di-design.md §244 (run sequence placement), §305-309 (Runner marker provenance — NOT new in v4, single-ordered-stream since 2.6/2.7; the readiness-gate window; ApplicationRunner-parsed vs CommandLineRunner-raw; throw-wraps-IllegalStateException-aborts), §1858 (Boot docs: use runners not listeners for lengthy startup tasks — confirms the runners window is the sanctioned long-task slot); the run-pipeline design (call_runners as the after-refresh+started/before-ready step, RunFailure routing, ParseArgs/ApplicationArguments, Order primitive); the nightly envelope (AsyncDrop avoid → explicit awaited teardown + no side-effect rollback; AFIT/RPITIT for the async Runner trait, boxed at the dyn edge; inventory/linkme tradeoffs); the cross-crate doc (the three DCE layers + the SILENT-failure-is-worst trait acutely relevant to silently-skipped migrations, force-link/anti-DCE-self-check mandate, Architectures A-D, §170 ordering-as-data, charter §6 topology); refresh-lifecycle (runners are post-Refresh, hence close-not-cancel on failure) and the events-lifecycle availability/runtime-lifecycle sections (Readiness=ACCEPTING_TRAFFIC as reactive core state).

## Startup Failure Analysis (FailureAnalyzer equivalent)  `[failure-analysis]`

leaf's realization of the boot-layer "a startup failure should TEACH, not dump a stack trace" surface — the FailureAnalyzer to FailureAnalysis SPI carved out of the run pipeline's handle_run_failure terminal. Its intent (spring-boot-4-di-design.md lines 311-321 and 2200-2215): the predictable boot failures (port-in-use, missing/ambiguous bean, bad property binding, bean-definition-override) are KNOWN failure shapes, so a startup Throwable is fed through an ORDERED chain of pluggable analyzers; the FIRST analyzer that RECOGNIZES the cause returns a non-null FailureAnalysis(description, action, cause) — returning nothing is a chain-of-responsibility "pass"; a FailureAnalysisReporter then RENDERS that analysis into a clean, human-facing "Description: / Action:" diagnostic (vs the raw trace). It owns ONLY the failure-DIAGNOSIS surface, not the run orchestration: (1) the FailureAnalyzer SPI + its origin-agnostic discovery/ordering, keyed by ROLE not a runtime type-scan; (2) the chain-of-responsibility match-or-pass + first-non-null-wins; (3) the FailureAnalysis(description, action, cause) value shape — the precise place charter 1.7/2.9 fail-with-complete-context lands at the boot layer; (4) the FailureAnalysisReporter rendering seam (human-facing presentation kept SEPARATE from the precise machine error the framework throws — Spring's UI-agnostic-framework / opinionated-Boot-report split); (5) the cause-MATCHING mechanism (Spring's AbstractFailureAnalyzer<T> matches a specific exception TYPE via generics+reflection — leaf must match over a rust-native error model). INVOKED BY spring-application-run's handle_run_failure (after Failed fires, before/driving context-close); the AbandonedRunException short-circuit (rethrow WITHOUT analysis) lives in the run, not here. Crucial Spring detail to port honestly: analyzers are NOT beans and run BEFORE the context is usable, so they receive container state (Environment, the partial registry, the resolved condition-report) by EXPLICIT construction/threading, never @Autowired.
