Must replicate the INTENT WITHOUT JVM lineage: no spring.factories runtime SPI load, no reflective instantiation, no generics+reflection cause-type match (Any/downcast or pattern-matched cause-chain instead), no GC-mopped failed context (teardown is the explicit container-driven async close the run drives), and the analyzer registry is a SCOPED origin-agnostic catalog (static link-time + optional dynamic), never implicitly global.

### Candidate realizations

#### R1 - Ordered analyzer chain over a rust-native cause-chain, matched by downcast: a FailureAnalyzer trait (analyze(&FailureContext) -> Option<FailureAnalysis>) collected as origin-agnostic descriptors, walked first-non-null-wins, rendered by a pluggable reporter
Mirror Spring's FailureAnalyzers chain literally as a rust-native chain-of-responsibility. Define trait FailureAnalyzer { fn analyze(&self, ctx: &FailureContext) -> Option<FailureAnalysis>; } where returning None is the 'pass' (the next analyzer gets a chance) and the FIRST Some wins - exactly Spring's first-non-null semantics. FailureContext is the explicit-handoff bundle that REPLACES Spring's constructor-injected container state + reflective instantiation: it carries the root failure as a typed &BootError (the run's RunFailure cause-chain), the failing RunPhase, a read-only &Environment (already prepared by then), an optional &PartialContext handle (whatever of the registry was built - for missing/ambiguous-bean analyzers), and the resolved &ConditionReport (so a 'bean backed off' analyzer can explain WHY a needed bean is absent - the condition-report loud-later bridge). FailureAnalysis { description: String, action: String, cause: Option<&dyn BootError> } is the value shape. The cause-MATCHING (Spring's AbstractFailureAnalyzer<T> generic+reflection) becomes a rust-native walk: each analyzer pattern-matches / downcasts over the typed boot-error cause-chain (a `for cause in ctx.error.chain()` walking Error::source() + (&dyn Any).downcast_ref::<PortInUse>() style probe), so a PortInUseAnalyzer matches BindError, a MissingBeanAnalyzer matches NoSuchBean, a BadBindingAnalyzer matches a config-binding error - each is a small pure fn over the cause-chain. A thin AbstractFailureAnalyzer<T>-analogue helper (impl<A: CauseAnalyzer<E>> FailureAnalyzer for A) auto-walks the chain looking for the first E cause and hands it to the analyzer, so authors write fn analyze_cause(&self, e: &PortInUse, ctx) without re-implementing the walk. Analyzers are collected as thin origin-agnostic const descriptors from the SAME catalog substrate the rest of leaf uses (Phase-2-undecided: linkme/codegen/explicit), ordered by an @Order-analogue, walked in order. The default reporter is a FailureAnalysisReporter trait (default LoggingFailureAnalysisReporter-analogue rendering 'Description:/Action:' to the configured diagnostic sink); the reporter is the pluggable presentation seam kept SEPARATE from analysis (framework-throws-precise / Boot-renders-human split). If NO analyzer matches, the reporter falls back to a full structured dump of the BootError cause-chain (charter 1.7 'full causal chain' is the floor, the FailureAnalysis is the polish on top). leaf ships the predictable built-ins (port-in-use, missing/ambiguous bean, bean-definition-override, bad config binding, ambiguous app-type, enabled-starter-contributed-nothing). #[leaf::failure_analyzer] is a THIN macro emitting the descriptor + the cause-match shim; everything is hand-writable as Application::add_failure_analyzer(MyAnalyzer).

**Pros:** Highest INTENT fidelity: the trait + Option-is-pass + first-Some-wins + separate reporter map 1:1 to FailureAnalyzers / FailureAnalysis / FailureAnalysisReporter / 'returning null is a pass' - a reader who knows Spring's diagnostics layer recognizes it instantly (DX #1, intent-not-mechanism parity), and the chain-of-responsibility is the genuinely-portable kernel of the feature (Rust has no JVM lineage to fight here).; Realizes charter 1.7/2.9 as the marquee surface: FailureAnalysis(description, action, cause) is exactly the 'what broke / what to DO about it' shape, the FailureContext carries the full causal chain (failing phase + partial-build state + environment + condition-report + cause-chain), and the no-match fallback to a structured cause-chain dump makes 'rich complete context' the FLOOR with the actionable diagnosis as polish - the cleanest place in the whole framework for the complete-context-failure promise.; The explicit FailureContext handoff is the honest rust-native port of Spring's 'analyzers are NOT beans, receive state via constructor args, run before the context is usable': leaf threads the (partial) container state in by value/reference at the failure site, sidestepping both reflective instantiation AND the @Autowired-into-a-half-dead-context hazard - and the analyzer signature cannot accidentally depend on a live running context it does not have.; Cold-path-pure and async-trivial: analyzers are synchronous pure fns over already-captured state (no IO, no await, no spawn), so the dyn-trait boxing/AFIT concerns that plague hot paths do not arise - the chain runs once, synchronously, on the bootstrap task inside handle_run_failure, after the failure is already in hand (2.3 execution context is trivial; no spawn, no blocking).; The condition-report integration is first-class: a MissingBeanAnalyzer can consult the resolved ConditionReport in the FailureContext to turn 'NoSuchBean X' into 'X was not registered because @ConditionalOnProperty(foo) evaluated false - set foo=true or provide X yourself' - directly closing the 'condition-not-met and wiring-broken are distinct, time-separated failures' gap (the loud-later bridge the conditions doc flags) that is the single highest-value boot diagnostic.; Thin-macro / fully-hand-writable (2.10): #[leaf::failure_analyzer] only emits the descriptor + the AbstractFailureAnalyzer-analogue cause-walk shim, and the whole thing degrades to add_failure_analyzer(MyAnalyzer) - nothing hidden, cargo expand reads as the hand-written chain.

**Cons:** The cause-MATCHING mechanism (downcast over a typed BootError cause-chain) PRE-DECIDES part of the deferred unified-error/diagnostics 3 keystone: whether boot errors are a single typed enum, an Arc<dyn BootError> with Error::source() + downcast, or an Any-tagged context bag is exactly the meta-decision this analyzer-match mechanism rides on - so the analyze() signature and the cause-walk MUST stay a candidate, and a wrong guess here ripples to condition-report, startup-instrumentation, and every fail-with-context feature.; downcast_ref over dyn Any/dyn Error is more brittle than Spring's generic AbstractFailureAnalyzer<T>: a cause wrapped/boxed by an intermediate layer (a binding error nested inside a bean-creation error inside a refresh error) is only matchable if the cause-chain is faithfully preserved and downcastable at every hop - the run/refresh/container error-wrapping discipline becomes load-bearing for analysis to work at all, and a lost source() link silently disables an analyzer (a worse diagnostic, not a crash).; Analyzer discovery inherits the full silent-DCE hazard (Layer 0/A/B) and the failure mode is QUIETER than a missing bean: a PortInUseAnalyzer in a crate the binary never force-links is silently absent, so the user gets the raw bind-error dump instead of the actionable message - a degraded diagnostic, not a loud failure, which is the WORST kind of silent loss (the user does not know they were supposed to get help). Mandates the anti-DCE self-check + a startup-report listing registered analyzers.; Chain ORDER matters (a broad analyzer that matches a supertype-ish cause can shadow a more specific one - Spring's first-non-null is order-sensitive too) but there is no structural guard: an under-ordered analyzer set can yield a less-specific diagnosis than an available better one, and getting the @Order-analogue of the built-ins right (specific-before-general) is a hand-maintained property.; The FailureContext shape is a coupling magnet: as more analyzers want more partial-build state (which beans were under construction, which property source a bad value came from via origin-tracking, which auto-config backed off), FailureContext accretes references into half-built subsystems - and exposing a &PartialContext of a FAILED bring-up is inherently a 'what is even valid to read here' hazard (the container is mid-teardown).; Spring's reporter is a logging side-effect; leaf must decide the rendering SINK (stderr? the diagnostic/tracing pipeline? a returned structured value?) and that couples to the (undecided) unified diagnostics model - rendering 'Description/Action' as a log line vs returning it as structured data in the RunFailure vs both is itself a small keystone the reporter seam cannot fully resolve alone.

**Mechanisms considered:** trait FailureAnalyzer { fn analyze(&self, ctx: &FailureContext) -> Option<FailureAnalysis>; } - None = chain 'pass', first Some wins (Spring first-non-null); FailureContext explicit-handoff bundle (typed &BootError cause-chain + failing RunPhase + &Environment + optional &PartialContext + &ConditionReport) REPLACING Spring's reflective-instantiation + constructor-injected container state; FailureAnalysis { description, action, cause } value type - the charter 1.7/2.9 complete-context-failure shape; cause-matching by walking the typed cause-chain (Error::source() + downcast_ref::<ConcreteCause>) - the rust-native answer to AbstractFailureAnalyzer<T> generic+reflection; thin AbstractFailureAnalyzer<T>-analogue blanket impl that auto-walks the chain for the first E cause so authors write analyze_cause(&self, e: &E, ctx) without re-walking; FailureAnalysisReporter trait (default Logging Reporter rendering 'Description:/Action:') as the pluggable presentation seam, SEPARATE from analysis (framework-precise vs Boot-human split); no-match fallback: full structured BootError cause-chain dump (rich-complete-context is the FLOOR; FailureAnalysis is the polish); analyzers collected as origin-agnostic const descriptors + @Order from the shared catalog substrate (Phase-2-undecided linkme/codegen/explicit), walked in order; ship predictable built-ins: port-in-use, missing/ambiguous bean, bean-definition-override, bad config binding, ambiguous app-type, enabled-starter-contributed-nothing; ConditionReport-consulting analyzer turning NoSuchBean into 'backed off because <condition> - do X' (the conditions-doc loud-later bridge); thin #[leaf::failure_analyzer] macro emitting descriptor + cause-match shim; hand-writable add_failure_analyzer(MyAnalyzer) escape hatch

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** leaf-boot (the SpringApplication-equivalent layer, charter 6) defines the FailureAnalyzer trait, FailureContext, FailureAnalysis, the FailureAnalysisReporter trait + default, and the BootError cause-chain contract; built-in analyzers ship in leaf-boot, and integration crates (leaf-tokio's port-in-use richer variant, a leaf-axum binding-error analyzer) contribute additional analyzers. Each analyzer is collected as a thin origin-agnostic const descriptor from the SAME catalog substrate auto-configuration/refresh-lifecycle/the run-participant registries use (Phase-2-undecided: linkme distributed-slice / build.rs codegen / explicit add_failure_analyzer; cross-crate doc Arch A-D) - never a runtime spring.factories scan, never reflective instantiation. INHERITS the DCE story but with the QUIETEST failure mode in the whole bootstrap: a silently-DCE'd analyzer (Layer 0 unreferenced crate / Layer A reachability / Layer B --gc-sections pre-1.89) yields a DEGRADED diagnostic (raw dump instead of the actionable message) - never a crash, never an empty-result the user notices - so this feature is a PRIMARY consumer of the mandated anti-DCE self-check (expected-vs-found analyzers per source crate) and the natural content for a 'leaf doctor'/startup-report line listing registered analyzers (so a user can SEE that the port-in-use analyzer is present). The cross-crate STABLE surface is acute and unusual: the FailureAnalysis(description,action,cause) shape, the FailureContext fields, AND - load-bearing - the typed BootError cause-chain VOCABULARY that analyzers downcast against (PortInUse, NoSuchBean, AmbiguousBean, BadBinding, BeanDefinitionOverride) become an ABI-ish public contract every contributing crate matches over, anchored by no classpath - so leaf must PUBLISH the boot-error type taxonomy as a versioned public surface (like startup-instrumentation's stable step-name taxonomy and the run-listener event names). Generics cannot carry a 'static descriptor -> the macro hard-errors with a register_failure_analyzer!(Concrete) shim. Origin-agnostic throughout: a native, WASM-module, or test-double analyzer participates identically; the dynamic-source timing question (a WASM-module analyzer registering before the failure path runs) is a phase2Question. Shares the anti-DCE-self-check + cross-tier-report machinery with condition-report (the conditions doc flags this duplication explicitly).

**T2 — execution context:** Entirely a COLD-PATH, synchronous-analysis concern on the bootstrap task, invoked once by the run's handle_run_failure AFTER the failure is already captured: the analyzer chain is pure synchronous fns over already-materialized FailureContext state (no IO, no await, no spawn) - so the dyn-trait async-boxing / AFIT / RPITIT concerns that bite hot paths simply DO NOT arise here (analyze() is fn, not async fn). NO GLOBAL LOCK (2.5): the chain walk is single-threaded read-only over captured state. The chain runs BEFORE the explicit container-driven teardown (the run's handle_run_failure: fire Failed -> run THIS analyzer chain -> render -> drive context-close/cancelRefresh) - because there is no async Drop and no GC, the failed context's teardown is a separate explicit awaited pass the RUN owns (not this feature), and the analyzer chain must complete its read of the &PartialContext BEFORE teardown begins (an ordering constraint between this feature and context-close). The AbandonedRunException short-circuit (rethrow WITHOUT analysis or close) is decided by the RUN before this chain is ever entered - so this feature never sees an abandoned run. ERRORS within an analyzer: an analyzer that itself panics/errors must NOT mask the original failure - the chain isolates a faulty analyzer (catch/skip -> treat as a 'pass') and continues, because the WHOLE point is to diagnose the original error, never to introduce a second one (charter 2.9 - the diagnostician must not crash the diagnosis). Reactivity (2.4) is N/A - there is nothing to wake on; this is the terminal cold path. Parent linkage (2.3): the analysis is tagged onto the in-flight startup-instrumentation step's failure outcome so the recorded trace carries the diagnosis (sharing the diagnostics spirit), carried explicitly, not read off an ambient thread-local. The reporter's render is a synchronous write to the configured sink (a log/diagnostic line) - if that sink is async, the render result is a value the run awaits-writing, not the analyzer's concern.

#### R2 - Pattern-registry / declarative failure catalog: analyzers are DATA (a typed cause-matcher + a description/action template) keyed in a catalog the diagnoser indexes by cause-type, plus a thin imperative escape hatch - diagnosis becomes table lookup over the cause-chain rather than a hand-walked chain
Question whether failure analysis needs a free-form imperative chain at all for the PREDICTABLE cases. Most built-in analyzers are 'IF the cause-chain contains a PortInUse THEN description=fmt!(port, addr), action=fixed-advice' - pure data. So model the common case as a DECLARATIVE catalog: FailurePattern { matches: CauseKey, severity, build: fn(&MatchedCause, &FailureContext) -> FailureAnalysis } registered into a catalog INDEXED by the cause-type key (a TypeId-keyed map, leaning on const TypeId::of + Any downcast, stable), so the diagnoser walks the cause-chain ONCE and for each cause does an O(1) catalog lookup for a registered pattern (specificity/order breaking ties) rather than asking every analyzer in turn. This makes 'which analyzer handles which cause' INSPECTABLE data (a leaf doctor can dump 'these cause-types have a registered diagnosis; these do not'), and the registration is uniform with the rest of leaf's metadata/registry substrate (the same TypeId-keyed table the bean registry uses). The imperative FailureAnalyzer trait from R1 STILL exists as the escape hatch for analyzers that need cross-cutting logic (look at the environment + the condition-report + multiple causes together - e.g. 'ambiguous app-type because both web features enabled') - those register as 'wildcard' patterns consulted after the keyed lookups. The description/action templates can be authored as #[failure(matches = PortInUse, action = ...)]-style declarative attributes (a thin macro emitting the FailurePattern + the typed matcher), pushing the predictable cases fully declarative. The reporter seam and the no-match structured-dump fallback are identical to R1. Crucially this leans into the deferred type-erasure/registry 3 keystone: failure patterns are just another row in leaf's TypeId-keyed registry, so the SAME substrate (and the same anti-DCE self-check) covers beans, conditions, and failure diagnoses.

**Pros:** Strongest UNIFICATION (2.11): failure analysis becomes another consumer of leaf's TypeId-keyed registry substrate rather than a bespoke chain - the same metadata/codegen/anti-DCE machinery that registers beans and conditions registers failure patterns, and 'what can leaf diagnose' is INSPECTABLE catalog data (a first-class leaf doctor dump: which cause-types have a registered actionable diagnosis), which is itself a charter 2.9 legibility win.; O(1) keyed lookup per cause instead of asking every analyzer in turn: for a large analyzer set (every integration crate contributing port/binding/connection-pool diagnoses) the diagnoser indexes by cause-TypeId and only consults patterns that could match - cheaper and, more importantly, makes the match DETERMINISTIC and explainable ('cause X is handled by pattern from crate Y') rather than order-dependent first-non-null.; Most of the predictable built-ins (the port-in-use / override / bad-binding cases the feature EXISTS for) become pure DATA - a matches+description+action template - so contributing a new actionable diagnosis is a declarative one-liner, not an imperative analyzer, which is the lowest-ceremony authoring story (DX #1) and keeps the description/action wording reviewable as data.; The keyed catalog gives a structural completeness check Spring lacks: leaf can warn at build/startup that a known-thrown boot-error type has NO registered diagnosis ('NoSuchBean has no FailurePattern - it will fall back to a raw dump'), turning 'we forgot to write the helpful message' into a detectable gap rather than a silent worse-diagnostic - directly serving the teach-don't-dump intent.; Retains R1's imperative trait as the wildcard/cross-cutting escape hatch, so the cases that genuinely need to look at environment+condition-report+multiple-causes together (ambiguous app-type, enabled-starter-contributed-nothing) are NOT forced into the table - best-of-both, declarative-common-case + imperative-escape-hatch (2.10).; Leans into and validates the deferred type-erasure/registry keystone with a concrete second consumer (after beans), giving Phase 2 a stronger signal about whether one TypeId-keyed substrate serves the whole framework.

**Cons:** Pre-decides the type-erasure/registry 3 keystone HARDER than R1: a TypeId-keyed FailurePattern catalog assumes the unified-error model exposes a stable per-cause TypeId to key on (and that wrapped causes are downcastable at the right hop) - if the unified error model lands on a single big enum or an opaque dyn Error without clean per-variant TypeId keys, the whole keyed-lookup premise weakens, so it must stay strictly a candidate and is the MOST coupled to two undecided keystones at once (error model AND registry substrate).; A keyed-by-cause-type catalog handles 'this exact cause type' well but is awkward for the genuinely cross-cutting diagnoses that are the HIGHEST value (a missing-bean explanation that needs the condition-report, an ambiguous-app-type that needs the feature graph) - those all fall to the wildcard escape hatch, so the 'declarative table' may cover only the SIMPLE half and the hard/valuable half stays imperative anyway, partly defeating the unification claim.; Two registration shapes (declarative FailurePattern + imperative wildcard FailureAnalyzer) plus the index is MORE machinery than R1's single chain for a strictly cold path that runs at most once per process - the O(1)-lookup performance argument is near-worthless on a path that fires only on a fatal failure, so the catalog's payoff is legibility/unification, NOT speed, and the speed framing would be a mis-sell.; Cause-chain wrapping makes keyed lookup subtle: a cause is only found if the diagnoser walks to the right hop AND the wrapping layer preserved the downcastable type - so the keyed table still depends on the same faithful-cause-chain discipline as R1, and an index miss (wrong hop) silently falls through to the dump, same quiet-degradation hazard.; Declarative description/action templates are less expressive than imperative formatting for rich diagnoses (e.g. listing the candidate beans considered for an ambiguous injection, or the property-source origins via origin-tracking) - so the valuable, context-rich messages push back to imperative builders, and the attribute-template sugar mainly helps the already-simple cases.; Inspectable-catalog completeness checks ('NoSuchBean has no pattern') require leaf to ENUMERATE the known boot-error types - re-raising the stable-error-taxonomy ABI commitment even more strongly than R1 (the catalog's keys ARE the published taxonomy), tightening the cross-crate versioning surface.

**Mechanisms considered:** FailurePattern { matches: CauseKey, severity, build: fn(&MatchedCause, &FailureContext) -> FailureAnalysis } registered into a catalog INDEXED by cause-TypeId (const TypeId::of + Any downcast, stable); diagnoser walks the cause-chain once; per cause does O(1) catalog lookup (specificity/order tie-break) instead of asking every analyzer; declarative #[failure(matches = PortInUse, action = ...)] attribute sugar - thin macro emitting the FailurePattern + typed matcher, pushing predictable cases fully declarative; imperative FailureAnalyzer trait RETAINED as the wildcard/cross-cutting escape hatch (environment + condition-report + multi-cause), consulted after keyed lookups; failure patterns as just-another-row in leaf's TypeId-keyed registry substrate (the SAME table beans/conditions use) - the unification bet; structural completeness check: warn when a known boot-error type has NO registered FailurePattern (will fall back to raw dump); reporter seam + no-match structured-dump fallback identical to R1; shared anti-DCE self-check + cross-tier report machinery with condition-report and the bean registry

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** Same leaf-boot ownership as R1, but the cross-crate surface is the CATALOG + its keys rather than a trait chain. The FailurePattern catalog is registered through the SAME catalog substrate as everything else (Phase-2-undecided linkme/codegen/explicit; cross-crate doc Arch A-D), and because patterns are keyed by cause-TypeId, the registration is uniform with the bean registry's TypeId-keyed rows - the unification dividend the conditions doc hints at (the 'duplicated cross-tier-report/anti-DCE-self-check mechanism' two features reach for becomes ONE shared mechanism). The published-taxonomy ABI commitment is STRONGER than R1: the catalog's KEYS are the boot-error type taxonomy, so the set of diagnosable cause-types is an explicit versioned public surface, and const TypeId::of (stable 1.91) makes the keys const-promotable into static catalog rows. DCE story identical (quiet degraded-diagnostic on a dropped pattern) but the keyed catalog makes the anti-DCE self-check RICHER: it can assert 'expected pattern for cause-type T from crate C is present' per known key, strictly more precise than R1's count. The TypeId-keyed lookup is fully platform-independent given a build-time-emitted catalog (Arch C / sqlx model - the deterministic path incl. wasm). A dynamic WASM-module pattern source registering before the failure path is the same timing phase2Question. Generics cannot register -> register_failure_pattern!(Concrete) macro shim. Origin-agnostic: native/WASM/test patterns key identically.

**T2 — execution context:** Identical cold-path/synchronous profile to R1 - the catalog lookup + template build are pure synchronous fns over captured state, run once on the bootstrap task inside handle_run_failure, before the explicit awaited teardown. The O(1)-keyed-lookup is a cold-path nicety with negligible runtime relevance (it fires at most once per process on a fatal failure) - its value is determinism/legibility, NOT throughput (be honest: 2.4 reactivity and 2.3 hot-path discipline are simply not engaged here). NO GLOBAL LOCK - the catalog is read-only at failure time (built once, immutable). Faulty-pattern isolation identical to R1 (a panicking build fn is caught and treated as a pass, never masking the original failure). No async Drop, so teardown remains the run's explicit awaited pass after diagnosis. Same parent-linkage-into-startup-instrumentation discipline. The only T2 delta vs R1: the catalog is BUILT (indexed) at registration time (cold, once) rather than walked per-failure, but since failure is at-most-once this is immaterial.

#### R3 - Result-typed self-diagnosing errors (intent-faithful, mechanism-divergent): boot errors carry their OWN diagnosis via a Diagnose trait, the analyzer chain is reframed as the OVERRIDE/enrichment layer, and analysis is a property of the error type rather than an external chain - questioning whether an external SPI is even rust-native
Question the external-SPI shape itself (charter 2.2 / intent-not-mechanism): Spring NEEDS an external FailureAnalyzer chain because its framework exceptions are deliberately UI-agnostic and it cannot make the framework depend on Boot's presentation - but in leaf, where the boot-error types and the diagnosis layer can live in the same workspace, the most rust-native shape may be that an error KNOWS how to diagnose itself. Define trait Diagnose { fn diagnose(&self, ctx: &FailureContext) -> Option<FailureAnalysis>; } implemented BY the boot-error types themselves (PortInUse::diagnose returns its own description/action; NoSuchBean::diagnose consults ctx.condition_report) - so the PREDICTABLE diagnoses live next to the errors that need them, type-checked, no downcast, no discovery needed for built-ins (the error variant IS the dispatch). The run's handle_run_failure walks the cause-chain and calls .diagnose(ctx) on the most-specific cause that implements it - first Some wins. The EXTERNAL analyzer chain (R1's trait) is then REFRAMED as the ENRICHMENT/OVERRIDE layer: a registered FailureAnalyzer can (a) diagnose a cause whose error type leaf does not own (a third-party error from an integration crate that cannot impl leaf's Diagnose), or (b) OVERRIDE/augment a built-in diagnosis (a deployment-specific 'Action: in OUR cluster, do X'). Resolution order: external override analyzers -> the error's own Diagnose -> external fallback analyzers -> structured dump. This keeps the SPI for genuine extension/foreign-error cases but makes the common case (leaf's own predictable failures) a zero-discovery, downcast-free, compile-checked property of the error - sidestepping the silent-DCE hazard ENTIRELY for built-ins (they are not registered, they are impl'd) and only paying discovery for true third-party/override extension. The FailureAnalysis shape and reporter seam are identical to R1.

**Pros:** Sidesteps the silent-DCE hazard ENTIRELY for the BUILT-IN predictable diagnoses (the feature's whole reason to exist): port-in-use / missing-bean / override / bad-binding diagnoses are impl'd ON the error types in leaf-boot, not registered into a discoverable catalog - so they CANNOT be DCE'd away or left unlinked, removing the 'quiet degraded-diagnostic' worst-failure-mode for exactly the cases that matter most (a huge reliability win vs R1/R2 where every built-in is a discovery-fragile descriptor).; Most rust-native and compile-checked: the predictable diagnosis is a Diagnose impl on a concrete error type - no downcast, no TypeId keying, no reflection-analogue, the compiler verifies every owned boot-error variant either has a diagnosis or is explicitly opted out (an exhaustiveness story Spring's reflective chain cannot give), directly serving charter 2.2 'realize the intent in idiomatic Rust, possibly completely differently' and the teach-don't-dump completeness goal.; Keeps the external SPI EXACTLY where it is genuinely needed - foreign errors leaf does not own (an integration crate's connection error it cannot impl Diagnose on) and deployment-specific OVERRIDES - so the discovery-fragile path is paid ONLY for true extension, not for the built-ins, which is the right cost allocation (the common case is free and robust; the rare case keeps full pluggability).; The diagnosis lives NEXT TO the error definition, so it stays in sync: when someone adds a new boot-error variant, the Diagnose impl is right there to fill in (or the exhaustiveness check flags it) - vs R1/R2 where the analyzer/pattern is in a separate file/crate and can drift out of date with the error it is supposed to recognize (the analyzer-drifts-from-its-error hazard R1's cons names).; Cleanest cause-chain story: .diagnose() is called on the typed cause directly (no downcast-at-the-right-hop guessing) - the cause-chain walk just asks each typed cause 'can you diagnose yourself?', so a wrapped/nested cause is handled as long as it is reachable via source(), with no per-hop downcast brittleness.; Still honors 1.7/2.9 with the same FailureAnalysis(description, action, cause) shape, the same FailureContext, and the same no-match structured-dump floor - it changes only WHERE the predictable diagnosis lives (on the error vs in a chain), not the user-facing promise.

**Cons:** DIVERGES MOST from Spring's intent-MECHANISM and risks losing the clean 'framework throws precise / Boot renders human' SEPARATION that is itself part of the design intent (lines 2215): putting diagnosis ON the error type couples the error definition to presentation/remediation wording, which is exactly what Spring deliberately split apart - so R3 trades discoverability-robustness for a presentation/error coupling that may be the wrong call (a charter 2.2 judgment that must NOT be pre-made here).; Pre-decides the unified-error 3 keystone the HARDEST of the three: Diagnose-on-the-error assumes boot errors are leaf-owned named TYPES (not an opaque dyn Error / anyhow-style erased chain) that leaf can impl a trait on - if the unified error model lands on type-erased or third-party-heavy errors, the 'error diagnoses itself' premise collapses for most causes and everything falls back to the external chain anyway, making R3 effectively R1 with extra coupling.; The override-vs-self-vs-fallback resolution order (external override -> self -> external fallback -> dump) is MORE complex than R1's single first-non-null chain and introduces a genuinely tricky question: when does an external analyzer get to OVERRIDE an error's own diagnosis vs only supplement a missing one? Mis-specifying this yields surprising 'why did not my custom analyzer win' / 'why did it win' confusion - a subtle precedence model Spring does not have.; Foreign errors (the integration-crate connection error leaf cannot impl Diagnose on) STILL need the full discovery-fragile external-analyzer path, so the silent-DCE hazard is not eliminated - only narrowed to third-party/override analyzers; for an ecosystem where MOST interesting failures originate in integration crates (db pools, http servers), the 'built-ins are robust' win may cover a smaller fraction of real-world failures than it appears.; Couples the boot-error crate to the FailureContext + FailureAnalysis + condition-report types (since errors now reference them in their Diagnose impls), pulling presentation/diagnosis dependencies DOWN into the error-definition layer - a layering inversion (errors depending on the diagnosis/report machinery) that fights the clean dependency-points-inward topology (6) and could create awkward crate-graph pressure.; Loses R2's inspectable catalog: 'what can leaf diagnose' is now scattered across Diagnose impls on error types rather than a single enumerable table, so the 'leaf doctor: here are the diagnosable failures' legibility win is weaker (it is a trait-impl audit, not a data dump).

**Mechanisms considered:** trait Diagnose { fn diagnose(&self, ctx: &FailureContext) -> Option<FailureAnalysis>; } impl'd BY the boot-error types themselves - the error variant IS the dispatch, no downcast/discovery for built-ins; handle_run_failure walks the cause-chain and calls .diagnose(ctx) on the most-specific implementing cause; first Some wins; external FailureAnalyzer chain (R1's trait) REFRAMED as the enrichment/override layer for foreign errors leaf cannot impl Diagnose on + deployment-specific overrides; resolution order: external override analyzers -> error's own Diagnose -> external fallback analyzers -> structured dump; compile-time exhaustiveness: every owned boot-error variant either has a Diagnose or is explicitly opted out (a completeness story the reflective chain cannot give); FailureAnalysis shape + FailureContext + reporter seam + no-match dump floor identical to R1; built-ins are NOT registered (so cannot be DCE'd) - only true third-party/override analyzers use the discovery substrate; diagnosis co-located with the error definition so it stays in sync (vs drifting analyzer in a separate crate)

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** Inverts the cross-crate story vs R1/R2 for the common case: the PREDICTABLE built-in diagnoses are Diagnose impls on leaf-boot's own error types - NO discovery, NO catalog, NO descriptor, so they sidestep all three DCE layers ENTIRELY (they are ordinary trait impls compiled with the error types, force-linked because the error types are always referenced on the failure path). Only the EXTENSION cases use the discovery substrate (Phase-2-undecided linkme/codegen/explicit): a third-party-error analyzer or a deployment-override analyzer, contributed by an integration/app crate, IS a discoverable descriptor and DOES inherit the DCE hazard + anti-DCE self-check - but the blast radius is narrowed to genuine extensions, and a dropped override analyzer degrades to the built-in self-diagnosis (a SANE fallback, not a raw dump - strictly better than R1's degrade-to-dump). The crate-graph cost is the layering tension: the boot-error types must reference FailureContext/FailureAnalysis/ConditionReport to impl Diagnose, pulling diagnosis-layer types down toward the error-definition layer - a dependency-direction pressure Phase 3 topology must resolve (errors-depend-on-diagnosis vs a separate boot-error-diagnostics crate). The published-taxonomy ABI surface is SMALLER (built-ins are not a cross-crate registry, they are impls) but the Diagnose trait + FailureContext + FailureAnalysis become the stable surface foreign analyzers compile against. const TypeId not needed for built-ins (no keying). Origin-agnostic for the extension lane only. Generics/foreign-error analyzers still need a register shim.

**T2 — execution context:** Cold-path/synchronous identical to R1/R2: .diagnose() and external analyzers are pure synchronous fns over captured FailureContext, run once on the bootstrap task in handle_run_failure before the explicit awaited teardown. NO GLOBAL LOCK; read-only over captured state. The resolution-order walk (override -> self -> fallback -> dump) is a synchronous cold sequence. Faulty-diagnoser isolation identical (a panicking .diagnose()/analyzer is caught and treated as a pass, never masking the original failure - and here it is especially important since a built-in's own Diagnose panicking must still let the external/dump path produce SOMETHING). No async Drop -> teardown is the run's explicit awaited pass after diagnosis; the .diagnose() read of &PartialContext must precede teardown (same ordering constraint with context-close as R1). Parent-linkage-into-startup-instrumentation identical. The one T2 nuance: because built-in diagnosis is a trait method on the error, it is invoked directly with zero discovery/lookup latency (even more trivially cold than R1's chain walk), reinforcing that this whole feature is a terminal cold path where 2.3 hot-path / 2.4 reactive disciplines are not engaged.

### Rust clashes
- No spring.factories runtime SPI loading + no reflective instantiation. Spring's FailureAnalyzers loads FailureAnalyzer beans from META-INF/spring.factories (the diagnostics key did NOT migrate to .imports in Boot 3 - still spring.factories in Boot 4) and instantiates them REFLECTIVELY during the failure path. Rust has no runtime classpath scan and no reflective instantiation; analyzers must be collected as thin origin-agnostic 'static descriptors from a SCOPED catalog (static link-time + optional dynamic; Phase-2-undecided linkme/codegen/explicit), addressed by ROLE, and constructed by ordinary code - never a runtime type-scan. Inherits the silent-DCE failure mode, and uniquely the QUIETEST one in the bootstrap (a missing analyzer = a worse diagnostic, not a crash).
- No generics+reflection cause-type matching. Spring's AbstractFailureAnalyzer<T extends Throwable> uses the generic type parameter + reflection to match a specific cause TYPE. Rust generics are erased at the dyn boundary and there is no runtime generic reflection - so cause-matching must be a rust-native walk over a typed error model: downcast_ref over the boot-error cause-chain (Error::source() + Any/downcast, all stable) OR pattern-matching a typed error enum OR (R3) a Diagnose trait on the error itself. The matching mechanism RIDES the deferred unified-error/diagnostics 3 keystone and must stay a candidate, not bake in a specific error representation.
- Analyzers run BEFORE the context is usable, and are NOT beans. Spring's analyzers cannot be @Autowired (they run on the failure path, before/while the context is unusable) and must receive container state via CONSTRUCTOR ARGS (BeanFactory/Environment as params; the *Aware path was deprecated in 2.7). leaf must port this as an EXPLICIT FailureContext handoff threaded into analyze() (the partial registry, the prepared Environment, the resolved ConditionReport, the failing phase, the cause-chain) - never an injected dependency, never a read off a live running context that does not exist. The container is mid-FAILURE, so 'what is valid to read' from the partial state is itself a hazard.
- No GC-mopped failed context; no async Drop. Spring can let the GC clean a half-built failed context after handleRunFailure closes it. Rust has no GC AND no async Drop (nightly doc: AsyncDrop experimental-incomplete with tokio-shutdown crashes - avoid). The analyzer chain runs FIRST (read-only over the partial state), THEN the run drives an explicit, awaited, container-driven teardown (refresh-lifecycle's cancelRefresh pre-Refreshed / context-close post-Refreshed) - never a Drop, never a forget. The chain must finish reading the partial context BEFORE teardown begins (an ordering constraint with context-close).
- The diagnostician must not crash the diagnosis. Spring's chain is forgiving (a non-matching analyzer returns null = pass). leaf must additionally ISOLATE a FAULTY analyzer: an analyzer that panics/errors while inspecting a half-built failed state must NOT mask the ORIGINAL failure - it is caught and treated as a 'pass', and the chain continues, because introducing a second error while diagnosing the first violates charter 2.9. This is sharper in Rust where a panic across the cold failure path could otherwise abort the rich-context reporting.
- FailureAnalysis 'Action:' wording is presentation; keep it separate from the precise machine error (Spring's framework-precise / Boot-human split). Spring deliberately keeps Spring Framework UI-agnostic (throws precise, machine-meaningful exceptions) while Boot owns the human-facing FailureAnalysisReporter presentation. leaf must preserve this seam: the reporter (rendering 'Description:/Action:') is pluggable and SEPARATE from both the typed BootError and the FailureAnalysis value - and must decide the rendering SINK (stderr / the diagnostics-tracing pipeline / a returned structured value) without baking it into analysis. R3's error-diagnoses-itself shape is in direct TENSION with this separation (a clash to weigh, not resolve).
- The boot-error TYPE TAXONOMY becomes a cross-crate ABI with no classpath to anchor it. Spring's analyzers match cause types agreed within one JVM. In leaf, integration-crate analyzers downcast/match over leaf's published boot-error types (PortInUse, NoSuchBean, AmbiguousBean, BadBinding, BeanDefinitionOverride), so leaf must PUBLISH this error-type taxonomy + the FailureAnalysis/FailureContext shape as a versioned public surface (an ABI-ish commitment, like startup-instrumentation's stable step-name taxonomy and the run-listener event names) - the analyzers' match keys ARE that taxonomy.
- Cause-chain fidelity is load-bearing for analysis to work at all. Downcast/match-based analysis only succeeds if every wrapping layer (run -> refresh -> bean-creation -> binding) PRESERVES a faithful, downcastable Error::source() link to the originating cause. A lost or non-downcastable hop SILENTLY disables the matching analyzer (degraded diagnostic, not a crash) - so the framework-wide error-wrapping discipline (preserve, never flatten, the cause-chain) is a precondition this feature depends on but does not own.
- AbandonedRunException short-circuit lives in the RUN, not here. Spring's handleRunFailure checks AbandonedRunException FIRST and rethrows WITHOUT analysis or close (test-slicing / withHook abort). In leaf this short-circuit is the run-pipeline's decision (spring-application-run), made BEFORE the analyzer chain is entered - so this feature never sees an abandoned run, but the boundary (the run owns 'should we even analyze?') must be explicit, and the abandon signal is carried as an explicit value, not an ambient thread-local read (the 2.3 ThreadLocal-across-await hazard).

### Interactions
- **spring-application-run** — PRIMARY HOST / the thing that invokes this. This feature IS the FailureAnalyzer chain inside the run pipeline's handle_run_failure terminal: the run fires Failed, then INVOKES this chain over the captured failure, takes the resulting FailureAnalysis (or no-match dump), renders it, and THEN drives teardown. The run owns the AbandonedRunException short-circuit (rethrow WITHOUT analysis), the failing-RunPhase capture, and the cause-chain assembly that becomes this feature's input; this feature owns ONLY the analyze-and-render step. The boundary: run = orchestration + which-teardown-on-which-failure; this feature = turn the captured failure into an actionable diagnosis.
- **condition-report** — HIGHEST-VALUE COLLABORATOR + shared machinery. The condition-report records every match/no-match with a human-readable reason; a MissingBeanAnalyzer consults the resolved ConditionReport (threaded in via FailureContext) to turn a bare NoSuchBean into 'X backed off because @ConditionalOnProperty(foo)=false - set foo or provide X' - closing the conditions-doc's flagged 'condition-not-met and wiring-broken are distinct, time-separated failures' gap. The conditions doc explicitly names the 'FailureAnalyzer loud-later rendering side of the report bridge' and a 'duplicated cross-tier-report/anti-DCE-self-check mechanism that two features both reach for' - so this feature and condition-report SHARE the anti-DCE self-check + report-rendering machinery (a Phase-2 unification target).
- **context-close** — TEARDOWN ORDERING CONSTRAINT. Because there is no async Drop, the failed context's teardown is context-close's explicit awaited pass (clean close post-Refreshed) OR refresh-lifecycle's cancelRefresh (partial, pre-Refreshed) - driven by the RUN. This feature's analyzer chain reads the &PartialContext BEFORE that teardown begins, so the run must sequence analyze -> render -> teardown: the analysis must complete its read of the half-built state while it is still readable, never racing the destroy pass.
- **refresh-lifecycle** — FAILURE SOURCE + cause-chain provider. Most predictable boot failures (missing/ambiguous bean, bean-definition-override, eager-singleton creation failure) ORIGINATE in refresh-lifecycle's eager fail-fast bring-up. refresh-lifecycle must surface these as typed, downcastable boot-error causes (preserving the cause-chain through bean-creation -> refresh) so the analyzers can match them - refresh's error-wrapping discipline is a precondition this feature consumes; refresh owns the throw, this feature owns the diagnosis.
- **environment** — DIAGNOSIS INPUT. The prepared Environment is threaded into FailureContext (read-only) so a bad-binding analyzer can show the offending property, its resolved value, and - via origin-tracking - which property source/file:line it came from, making the 'bad property binding' diagnosis carry the full provenance (charter 1.7 'where'). The Environment is fully prepared by the time any analyzable failure occurs (failures after prepare_environment), so it is a safe read.
- **startup-instrumentation** — DIAGNOSTICS SIBLING / failure-tag consumer. On a boot failure the run tags the in-flight startup step with the failure outcome; this feature's resulting FailureAnalysis is attached to that recorded step so the startup trace becomes a boot-failure forensic (what phase, what step was running, plus the actionable diagnosis). Shares the diagnostics spirit and the stable-name-taxonomy ABI pattern (startup-instrumentation's step names ~ this feature's boot-error-type taxonomy). Parent linkage is carried explicitly (the 2.3 fix), not read off an ambient thread-local.
- **auto-configuration** — DIAGNOSIS INPUT + a built-in analyzer's subject. An 'enabled-starter-contributed-nothing' analyzer (the rust-native analogue catching the silent-DCE / unlinked-auto-config-crate case the cross-crate doc warns about) and an 'ambiguous app-type' analyzer key off the resolved capability/feature set + the condition/auto-config outcome. auto-configuration's back-off model means many 'missing bean' failures trace to an auto-config that backed off - the analyzer explains that via the condition-report, turning a silent back-off into an actionable message.
- **container-core** — PARTIAL-STATE SOURCE. The optional &PartialContext in FailureContext is container-core's (half-built) registry - a missing/ambiguous-bean analyzer reads which definitions were registered, which candidates were considered for an unsatisfied injection point, and the bean-creation cause-chain. container-core owns the registry + the precise BeansException-analogue throws; this feature reads the partial registry read-only to enrich the diagnosis (the 'candidates considered' part of charter 1.7).
- **lifecycle-events** — COORDINATION via the Failed milestone. The run fires the Failed event (on lifecycle-events / the early-vs-context multicaster) as part of handle_run_failure, distinct from running this analyzer chain - Failed is the OBSERVABLE fact (listeners/probes react), the FailureAnalysis is the human-facing diagnosis. The two are complementary: Failed says 'it failed', this feature says 'here is why and what to do'. AvailabilityState never reaches ACCEPTING_TRAFFIC on a failed run.

### Open questions for Phase 2
- What is the unified error/diagnostics model (the deferred 3 keystone) that FailureAnalysis/FailureAnalyzer realizes, and specifically how do analyzers MATCH a cause - downcast over an Arc<dyn BootError>/Error::source() chain (R1), a TypeId-keyed catalog over named error variants (R2), or a Diagnose trait impl'd on the error types themselves (R3)? The matching mechanism is the single most coupled-to-the-error-model decision; it cross-cuts condition-report, startup-instrumentation, container-core's BeansException-analogue, and every fail-with-context feature, and must be resolved ONCE for the whole diagnostics surface, not per-feature.
- Is failure analysis an EXTERNAL pluggable SPI (R1/R2 - analyzers discovered as descriptors, faithful to Spring's framework-precise/Boot-human separation, but discovery-fragile and downcast-brittle) or an INTERNAL property of self-diagnosing error types (R3 - robust, compile-checked, no DCE hazard for built-ins, but couples error definitions to presentation and diverges from Spring's deliberate separation)? This is the core shape decision and is a charter 2.2 'realize the intent, possibly completely differently' judgment that must NOT be pre-made in Phase 1.
- Which cross-crate substrate collects the analyzer/pattern descriptors (linkme zero-cost-but-DCE-sensitive-no-wasm / inventory DCE-robust-wasm-but-life-before-main / build-time codegen Arch C deterministic-portable / explicit add_failure_analyzer Arch D)? The QUIET degraded-diagnostic failure mode (a dropped analyzer = a worse message, never a crash) makes this feature a primary driver of the mandated anti-DCE self-check, and it SHARES that self-check + the cross-tier report-rendering machinery with condition-report (the conditions doc flags this duplication) - so the substrate choice must be made jointly across the diagnostics features.
- What is the rendering SINK and shape for a FailureAnalysis - a stderr/log line (Spring's LoggingFailureAnalysisReporter), a structured value carried back in the RunFailure for programmatic consumers, an entry in the diagnostics/tracing pipeline, or all three? This couples to the unified diagnostics model and to how the run's RunFailure is surfaced; the FailureAnalysisReporter seam can be defined but the sink/shape cannot be fully resolved without the diagnostics keystone.
- Does a dynamic (WASM-module / runtime) source contribute failure analyzers, and at what timing relative to the failure path - given a dynamically-sourced analyzer has no build-time presence and the failure path runs late? The two-source duality (static link-time + optional dynamic) applies to analyzers as to every other run-participant; the registration-before-failure timing is unresolved. Cross-cuts the same duality in refresh-lifecycle and auto-configuration.
- How much of the boot-error type TAXONOMY (the analyzers' match keys / the published ABI surface) is fixed in leaf-core vs leaf-boot vs contributed by integration crates, and how does it version cleanly across leaf releases without a classpath to anchor it? The taxonomy is a load-bearing cross-crate contract every contributing analyzer matches over; its ownership and versioning is a topology question downstream of the crate decomposition (a Phase 3 output).
- Is the framework-wide error-wrapping discipline (every layer preserves a faithful, downcastable Error::source() cause-chain) a global invariant the diagnostics keystone enforces, or a per-feature responsibility? Downcast/match-based analysis silently fails if any wrapping hop flattens or non-downcastably erases the cause - so 'never lose the cause-chain' must be decided as a framework-wide rule, not left to each throwing feature; cross-cuts container-core, refresh-lifecycle, config-data, and the run.

### Notes
Scope boundary honoured: this feature owns ONLY the failure-DIAGNOSIS surface carved out of spring-application-run's handle_run_failure terminal - the FailureAnalyzer SPI + chain-of-responsibility match-or-pass + first-non-null-wins, the FailureAnalysis(description, action, cause) value shape, the FailureContext explicit-handoff that replaces Spring's reflective-instantiation+constructor-injection, the cause-matching mechanism, and the FailureAnalysisReporter rendering seam. It does NOT own: the run orchestration, the AbandonedRunException short-circuit, the failing-phase capture, the which-teardown-on-which-failure fork, or the Failed event (all spring-application-run + context-close + lifecycle-events). It DELEGATES the cause-chain it analyzes to whatever threw (refresh-lifecycle, container-core, config-data, environment) and CONSUMES condition-report (the loud-later bridge), startup-instrumentation (failure-tagging), and the Environment+PartialContext as read-only diagnosis inputs. All three realizations stay implementation-agnostic and hold the deferred 3 keystones (unified error/diagnostics model, type-erasure/registry substrate, cross-crate composition substrate, async-context-propagation) as CANDIDATES - R1 leans intent-faithful-external-chain, R2 leans unify-via-keyed-catalog, R3 leans rust-native-self-diagnosing-error, deliberately spanning the external-SPI-vs-internal-property axis AND the error-model coupling axis so Phase 2's signal stays unbiased. Provider/registry abstractions kept ORIGIN-AGNOSTIC throughout (a native, WASM-module, or test-double analyzer participates identically). The THREE highest-leverage observations to carry into Phase 2/3: (1) this is the single most concentrated place in the framework for charter 1.7/2.9 'fail with rich, complete, actionable context' - the no-match structured-cause-chain dump is the FLOOR and the FailureAnalysis is the polish, so the unified diagnostics model should be designed with THIS surface as its marquee consumer; (2) the QUIET degraded-diagnostic DCE failure mode (a dropped analyzer yields a worse message, never a crash, so the user never knows they were supposed to get help) is uniquely insidious and makes the anti-DCE self-check + a 'leaf doctor'-style registered-analyzers listing non-optional - and R3's self-diagnosing-error shape is the only realization that eliminates this hazard for the built-ins (a strong Phase-2 signal worth weighing against its error/presentation coupling); (3) cause-chain fidelity (faithful downcastable Error::source() at every wrapping hop) is a framework-wide precondition this feature depends on but cannot enforce alone - it should be elevated to a global invariant of the unified error model. The condition-report doc's explicitly-flagged tensions (the FailureAnalyzer 'loud-later' rendering side of the report bridge, and the duplicated cross-tier-report/anti-DCE-self-check two features reach for) are confirmed here and point to a SHARED diagnostics-machinery unification in Phase 2. Grounding fully cross-checked: spring-boot-4-di-design.md lines 311-321 + 2200-2215 (the FailureAnalyzer/FailureAnalysis/FailureAnalysisReporter chain, first-non-null-pass semantics, AbstractFailureAnalyzer<T> generic+reflection match, analyzers-are-not-beans/constructor-injected/run-before-context-usable, spring.factories-still-not-migrated, AbandonedRunException short-circuit, framework-precise/Boot-human separation intent); the run-pipeline parent design (handle_run_failure as the host); the four Phase-1 upstream docs (condition-report's loud-later bridge + duplicated-self-check tension, refresh-lifecycle eager fail-fast as the failure source, context-close cancel-vs-close teardown, environment+origin-tracking provenance, startup-instrumentation failure-tagging); the nightly envelope (Any+downcast + const TypeId stable; AsyncDrop avoid -> explicit awaited teardown; no generic reflection; inventory/linkme tradeoffs); and the cross-crate doc (the three DCE layers, the silent-empty-iterable worst-trait, the force-link/anti-DCE-self-check mandate, Architectures A-D, the stable-taxonomy-as-ABI pattern). Notable Phase-3 flag: R3's 'error diagnoses itself' is the most rust-native and DCE-robust but its coupling of error-definition to presentation directly fights Spring's deliberate framework-precise/Boot-human separation - a genuine 2.2 tension to re-judge, not port blindly.

## Startup Banner  `[banner]`

leaf's configurable startup banner — the SpringApplicationBannerPrinter/printBanner analogue (spring-boot-4-di-design.md §"Banner", lines 301-303, fired at line 244's printBanner() step, after prepareEnvironment, before createApplicationContext). Its intent: a single, opinionated, late-bound bring-up step that emits a banner the user can override, with THREE knobs to replicate as INTENT (not JVM mechanism): (1) a MODE tri-state — console (write to the process stdout/console), log (route through the logging/diagnostics channel), or off (suppress) — controlled by spring.main.banner-mode / setBannerMode and (critically) bound back from externalized config via bindToApplication, so config overrides the programmatic setter; (2) a resolvable BANNER SOURCE — a default leaf-figlet-style text banner, an overridable text resource (Spring's banner.txt / spring.banner.location), and a programmatic Banner SPI (an object that renders itself given the Environment + an output target), with PLACEHOLDER substitution (${application.version}, ${leaf.version}-analogue of spring-boot.version, ${application.title}) resolved against the prepared Environment, plus ANSI/color styling; (3) the rendered banner is captured and REGISTERED as a container singleton (Spring's springBootBanner) so it is itself an injectable/queryable bean after the context exists. Within the run-pipeline (spring-application-run) this feature owns ONLY the print_banner() step: WHEN it fires (after EnvironmentPrepared+bindToApplication, before create_context), the mode resolution, the banner-source resolution + placeholder/ANSI rendering, the choice of output channel, and the deferred registration of the rendered banner as a singleton during prepare_context. It does NOT own the run sequence (spring-application-run), the Environment / property-resolution walk it reads placeholders from (environment/property-resolution), the spring.main.* bind mechanism (spring-application-run's bind_to_application), resource loading primitives (resource-loading neighbour), the logging/tracing channel (startup-instrumentation/the diagnostics substrate), or the singleton registry it registers into (container-core). The marquee rust-native question per charter §2.2: is the banner even native leaf intent, or JVM-shaped scaffolding (a print-a-figlet step) that a rust-native design slims down? It is deliberately a SMALL feature — the value is intent-parity on the three knobs + clean integration with the run step's execution-context and the cross-crate override story, NOT new machinery.

### Candidate realizations

#### R1 — Runtime Banner SPI + ordered banner-source chain: a `Banner` trait whose `render(&self, env, mode, out) -> Result<RenderedBanner>` is invoked by the print_banner() run step; the source is selected from an origin-agnostic descriptor chain (programmatic > text-resource > default), mode is a tri-state read from the bound config, and the output target is a mode-selected async writer
Mirror Spring's SpringApplicationBannerPrinter as a runtime SPI. Define `trait Banner { async fn render(&self, env: &dyn PropertyResolver, mode: BannerMode, out: &mut dyn BannerSink) -> Result<RenderedBanner, BannerError>; }` and `enum BannerMode { Console, Log, Off }`. The print_banner() run step (a single `.await` point in spring-application-run, fired AFTER EnvironmentPrepared + bind_to_application, BEFORE create_context) does: (1) read the resolved BannerMode — default Console, overridden by the programmatic `Application::banner_mode(..)` setter, in turn overridden by `leaf.main.banner-mode` bound from the Environment (the bind_to_application seam); if Off, return immediately (the un-instrumented fast path is a single enum check + early return). (2) Select the active Banner by walking an ORDERED, origin-agnostic `BannerSource` descriptor chain — first non-None wins, exactly like Spring's image>text>default precedence: a programmatically-set Banner (`Application::banner(my_banner)`) beats a discovered text-resource banner (the `banner.txt`/`leaf.banner.location`-analogue, resolved via the resource-loading neighbour) beats the built-in `DefaultLeafBanner` (a const figlet-ish string + version line). (3) Construct the mode-appropriate `BannerSink`: for Console, an async writer over the process stdout (an `AsyncWrite`-shaped sink from task-execution); for Log, a sink that routes each rendered line into the diagnostics/tracing channel (startup-instrumentation's leaf-owned target) rather than stdout. (4) `banner.render(env, mode, sink)` does placeholder substitution by calling `env.resolve_placeholders(template)` (property-resolution) — so `${application.version}`, `${leaf.version}`, `${application.title}` resolve against the prepared Environment's ApplicationInfo-analogue source — and applies ANSI styling (a small const palette) gated on a `BannerSink::supports_ansi()` capability (so Log/non-tty sinks get plain text). render() returns a `RenderedBanner { text: String, char_count, .. }`. (5) The print_banner() step stashes the RenderedBanner so prepare_context() can register it as the `leafBanner` singleton (container-core) — the deferred registration matches Spring's springBootBanner. BannerError (resource-not-found, placeholder-unresolved-in-strict-mode, IO-write-failure) folds into the run's RunFailure / FailureAnalysis chain (charter §1.7) — though a banner failure is non-fatal by intent (degrade to no-banner + a warning, since a cosmetic banner must never abort a boot). The `Banner`, `BannerSource`, and `BannerSink` are origin-agnostic: a native crate, an integration crate, or a test double contributes a custom Banner identically. The built-in DefaultLeafBanner and the text-resource BannerSource are themselves descriptors in the chain (dogfooding). `#[leaf::main]` need emit nothing banner-specific (the default chain is always present); a custom banner is `Application::banner(..)` or a contributed descriptor.

**Pros:** Highest Spring intent-fidelity for all three knobs: the Banner SPI (render-yourself-given-env-and-output), the mode tri-state, the ordered source precedence (programmatic > resource > default), the placeholder substitution against the live Environment, and the deferred singleton registration all map 1:1 to SpringApplicationBannerPrinter — a user who knows Spring's banner finds the same shape (DX #1, intent-not-mechanism parity §2.2).; The banner is REPLACEABLE and INSPECTABLE exactly as Spring intends: a user swaps the whole Banner via `Application::banner(..)`, contributes a custom BannerSource descriptor, or queries the registered `leafBanner` singleton after refresh — the extensibility surface is a clean trait + descriptor chain, not baked-in behaviour.; Clean separation of the three concerns the banner genuinely has: WHAT to render (Banner), WHERE it comes from (BannerSource chain), and WHERE it goes (BannerSink, mode-selected) — so the console-vs-log distinction becomes a sink choice rather than scattered if/else, and placeholder/ANSI is render's job delegating to property-resolution. This factoring is the rust-native answer to Spring's monolithic printer.; The mode tri-state with an early Off return makes the un-banner path nearly free (one enum check), honouring overhead #2 — and the Log sink routing through startup-instrumentation's tracing target unifies the 'banner in logs' case with the rest of leaf's diagnostics rather than a bespoke logger.; Async-correct by construction (§2.3): render() and the sink write are `.await` points on the bootstrap task, so a Console write to a slow/piped stdout or a Log route through an async subscriber never blocks the bootstrap task synchronously — and a custom Banner that does real work (resolves a remote MOTD) awaits cleanly.; Non-fatal-by-intent failure handling (degrade to no-banner + warn) is the right charter §1.7 posture for a COSMETIC step: a missing banner.txt or an unresolved placeholder produces a rich diagnostic but does not abort the boot — the banner is the one run step where fail-fast would be user-hostile, and R1 makes that an explicit policy.

**Cons:** The Banner SPI is JVM-shaped scaffolding the charter (§2.2) tells us to question: an async `render` trait + a BannerSink abstraction + a descriptor chain is real machinery for what is, in most apps, 'print a const string once'. The risk is porting Spring's full printer architecture for a feature that a rust-native design (R2) could collapse to a const + a writeln.; The BannerSource chain inherits the cross-crate DCE story (Layer 0/A/B): a custom BannerSource in a crate the binary never force-links is SILENTLY absent — and unlike a missing bean (loud at resolution) a missing banner source just silently falls through to the default, the quietest possible failure. For a cosmetic feature this is low-stakes, but it still mandates the same anti-DCE discipline as every discovery surface, which is heavy for a banner.; The text-resource BannerSource (banner.txt / leaf.banner.location) presupposes a resource-loading abstraction (load a named resource relative to the binary/working-dir) that leaf may not have settled — and the JVM's classpath-relative banner.txt has no clean Rust analogue (no classpath; a file path is working-dir-relative and brittle, an embedded resource needs include_str!/build-time embedding). This forces an early, possibly premature, resource-loading-shaped decision onto a cosmetic feature.; The BannerSink async-writer abstraction over stdout couples the banner to whatever async-IO/writer shape task-execution settles on; a synchronous println would be simpler and (for a one-shot cold-path write) arguably correct, so the async sink may be over-engineering the §2.3 discipline for a single startup write.; ANSI styling + tty-detection (supports_ansi) is a per-sink capability that drags in terminal-detection concerns (is stdout a tty, NO_COLOR env honoured, Windows console modes) — real but peripheral surface that a const-string banner with no color (R2's slim path) sidesteps entirely.; Registering the RenderedBanner as a singleton (the springBootBanner analogue) is of dubious rust-native value: Spring registers it so it is injectable, but who injects a banner? This may be JVM ceremony to design OUT (a phase2 §2.2 judgement) rather than faithfully port.

**Mechanisms considered:** `trait Banner { async fn render(&self, env: &dyn PropertyResolver, mode: BannerMode, out: &mut dyn BannerSink) -> Result<RenderedBanner, BannerError>; }` invoked at the print_banner() run step; `enum BannerMode { Console, Log, Off }` resolved by precedence: default Console < programmatic `Application::banner_mode` < `leaf.main.banner-mode` bound from the Environment (bind_to_application seam); ordered origin-agnostic `BannerSource` descriptor chain (programmatic Banner > text-resource banner via resource-loading > built-in DefaultLeafBanner), first-non-None-wins, mirroring Spring's image>text>default precedence; mode-selected `BannerSink`: a Console async-writer over process stdout vs a Log sink routing lines into startup-instrumentation's leaf-owned tracing target; `supports_ansi()` capability gates color; placeholder substitution by delegating the template to `env.resolve_placeholders(..)` (property-resolution), resolving ${application.version}/${leaf.version}/${application.title} against the prepared Environment's ApplicationInfo-analogue source; ANSI styling via a small const palette, applied only when the sink supports it (tty / NO_COLOR honoured); deferred registration of the `RenderedBanner` as the `leafBanner` singleton during prepare_context (container-core), mirroring springBootBanner; non-fatal failure policy: BannerError degrades to no-banner + a warning into the diagnostics channel, never aborts the boot (a cosmetic step must not fail the run); built-in DefaultLeafBanner + text-resource source are themselves descriptors in the chain (dogfooding); thin macros emit nothing banner-specific

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** leaf-boot owns the print_banner() run step, the BannerMode enum, the Banner/BannerSource/BannerSink traits, and BannerError; the built-in DefaultLeafBanner + text-resource BannerSource ship as default descriptors. Per charter §6 the banner is part of the bootstrap layer (leaf-boot, the SpringApplication-equivalent). The BannerSource chain is an additional cross-crate discovery surface collected from the SAME catalog substrate the rest of leaf uses (Phase-2-undecided: linkme distributed-slice / build.rs codegen / explicit with(); cross-crate doc Arch A-D) — never a runtime classpath scan for banner.txt. It INHERITS the full DCE story but at the LOWEST stakes of any discovery feature: a silently-DCE'd custom BannerSource just falls through to the default banner (a cosmetic degradation, not a crash or wrong behaviour), so while the anti-DCE self-check applies uniformly, the banner is the feature where a missing contribution matters least — useful as a low-risk canary for the discovery substrate. The text-resource banner is the cross-crate sharp edge: there is NO classpath, so the JVM's classpath-relative banner.txt becomes either a working-dir-relative file path (resolved at runtime, brittle) or a build-time-embedded resource (include_str!/build.rs, the rust-native analogue of 'on the classpath') — this couples to the resource-loading neighbour's eventual decision and to whether 'a banner shipped by an integration crate' is even a use case (likely not; banners are app-level). The placeholder path is cross-crate-INERT (it consumes the env read view, registers no descriptor) — like value-injection's value path, it compiles and links wherever invoked with zero DCE exposure and full wasm support. Generics can't carry a 'static descriptor → a contributed Banner registers via a thin register_banner!(Concrete) shim, hard-erroring on generics. The mode-knob name (leaf.main.banner-mode) and the placeholder vocabulary (application.version/title, leaf.version) become a small stable cross-crate config surface. The Console sink writes the PROCESS stdout (a single process-global resource — the only global the banner touches, and only at one cold-path moment, so no global-lock concern).

**T2 — execution context:** Entirely a COLD-PATH single-shot step on the bootstrap task, fired once between EnvironmentPrepared and create_context. The whole print_banner() is one `.await` point: mode resolution is a synchronous in-memory read (env.get for leaf.main.banner-mode + the programmatic setter), source selection is a synchronous descriptor-chain walk, render() awaits (placeholder resolution is a synchronous in-memory env walk per property-resolution's contract; a custom Banner MAY await real work), and the sink write awaits (a Console write to stdout or a Log route through the async tracing subscriber). NO GLOBAL LOCK (§2.5): the only shared resource is process stdout, written once at one cold moment (no contention — the bootstrap task is the sole writer at this phase). The Console sink must be an async writer (or a spawn_blocking around a synchronous stdout write if the writer would block on a piped/full stdout — documented execution-context discipline §2.3), never a naked blocking println that stalls the bootstrap task. The Log sink is reactive (§2.4): it emits into startup-instrumentation's channel, not a busy-wait. PARENT LINKAGE: the print_banner step is a child startup-step under the run root (leaf.application.run > leaf.banner.print), nested explicitly, not via an ambient thread-local. CANCELLATION: a cancelled bootstrap task mid-banner simply drops the partial write (the banner is idempotent-cosmetic, no teardown needed — there is nothing to async-Drop). ERRORS: BannerError is a rich Result (resource path searched, unresolved placeholder + sources consulted, IO error) but by the non-fatal policy it degrades to no-banner + a warning rather than propagating as a RunFailure — the deliberate exception to fail-fast for a cosmetic step. The RenderedBanner stashed for later singleton registration is a plain owned String moved into prepare_context (no cross-thread sharing until it becomes a singleton).

#### R2 — Compile-time-lowered slim banner: a thin macro/const path where the banner is a `const &str` (default or user-embedded via include_str!), placeholders are split at macro time, and the print step is a hand-writable mode-match over write-to-stdout vs emit-to-tracing — questioning whether the Banner SPI is needed at all
Take charter §2.2 ('does leaf NEED Spring's mechanism, or does a rust-native design make it unnecessary') seriously and SLIM the banner to its essence: in the overwhelming common case a banner is a fixed string printed once. Model it as a COMPILE-TIME-resolved const + a thin runtime emit, eliminating the Banner trait, the BannerSource chain, and the BannerSink abstraction. The banner template is a `const BANNER: &str` — either leaf's built-in default (a const figlet-ish art + a version line) or the user's, supplied as `Application::banner_text(include_str!("banner.txt"))` (the rust-native 'on the classpath' = embed at compile time via include_str!, NO runtime resource loading, NO file IO, NO classpath analogue). A thin macro splits the template's placeholders at MACRO TIME (like value-injection R1's grammar split): `${application.version}` etc. become a const segment list (Literal | Placeholder{key}) so the runtime never re-parses the banner's structure — it only resolves the placeholder keys against the prepared Environment. The print step is then a hand-writable function a user could have written: `match banner_mode { Off => return, Console => { let s = render(&segments, env)?; write_stdout(s).await }, Log => { let s = render(&segments, env)?; tracing::info!(target: "leaf.banner", "{s}") } }` where render() walks the const segments calling env.resolve_placeholders only on the placeholder segments and applies ANSI from a const palette (or strips it for Log/non-tty). BannerMode is the same tri-state read by the same precedence (default < programmatic < bound config). There is NO Banner trait and NO descriptor chain: a custom banner is just a different const string (the common case) OR — for the rare programmatic/dynamic banner — an explicit escape-hatch closure `Application::banner_fn(|env| async move { .. })` the print step awaits (covering the 'I need to compute my banner at runtime' case without a discovered SPI). The rendered string MAY be registered as a singleton, but R2 questions whether that ceremony is worth it (likely dropped — see cons). `#[leaf::main]` emits nothing; the macro only does the placeholder split when `banner_text!`/`#[banner(..)]` is used. This is the thin-macro, low-overhead, cross-crate-inert realization: the banner path links wherever the app is built with ZERO DCE exposure and full wasm support, because there is no registry to discover.

**Pros:** Thinnest possible realization honouring charter §2.2 (intent parity, not mechanism parity) + §2.10 (thin macros): the banner is a const string + a hand-writable mode-match, with the macro doing ONLY a placeholder split a user could inspect via cargo expand — no Banner trait, no Sink abstraction, no descriptor chain. This is the rust-native answer to 'a print-a-figlet step' the run-pipeline openNotes explicitly flag as JVM-shaped scaffolding to question.; Lowest overhead by far (overhead #2): a const banner, a compile-time segment split, an early Off return, and a single write — no trait-object dispatch, no descriptor-chain walk, no async-render boxing. The un-banner path is one enum check; the banner path is a const-driven write.; ZERO cross-crate/DCE exposure (the major T1 win, shared with value-injection R1): the banner path consumes the env read view and a const string — it registers NO descriptor, so there is no silent-empty-registry hazard, no force-link discipline, no anti-DCE self-check, and FULL wasm/embedded support out of the box. For a cosmetic feature this avoids dragging the most fragile part of leaf's infrastructure into a banner.; include_str! is the HONEST rust-native analogue of Spring's classpath-relative banner.txt: 'the banner that ships with the app' is embedded at compile time, deterministically, with no runtime file IO, no working-dir brittleness, and no premature resource-loading-abstraction decision. The escape-hatch banner_fn closure cleanly covers the genuinely-dynamic case without an SPI.; Routing Log mode straight to `tracing::info!(target: "leaf.banner")` unifies the banner-in-logs case with startup-instrumentation's tracing-native posture (events-lifecycle startup-instrumentation R1) for free — no bespoke BannerSink, the subscriber already configured for leaf's diagnostics handles it.; Earliest diagnostics (charter §1.7): a malformed placeholder (`${unbalanced`) is a COMPILE error at the macro span (like value-injection R1), and a missing embedded banner is impossible (include_str! fails at compile time if the file is absent) — so the whole class of 'banner.txt not found at runtime' failures Spring has simply cannot occur.

**Cons:** Lowest Spring-mechanism parity: there is no inspectable/replaceable Banner bean, no banner-source precedence chain, no springBootBanner singleton — a user porting from Spring who relied on a programmatic `Banner` implementation or a discovered banner finds a different (escape-hatch closure) shape. This is intent-preserving but mechanism-diverging, the deliberate §2.2 tradeoff R1 avoids.; A RUNTIME-authored banner (a banner string loaded from config/DB at runtime, or a banner.txt at an operator-supplied path resolved at runtime — both real in Spring via spring.banner.location pointing at an external file) is impossible in the const-lowered form; it must fall back to the banner_fn closure with a runtime-loaded string, reintroducing exactly the runtime-resolution path R2 sought to eliminate (R1 territory) for that case.; Dropping the banner-source descriptor chain means an integration crate CANNOT contribute a banner (e.g. a 'leaf-fancy-banner' crate) without the app explicitly calling banner_text/banner_fn — losing the auto-discovery DX for the (admittedly rare) cross-crate banner case. R2 trades the discovery story for simplicity, which is right for banners but inconsistent with how every other contribution works.; ANSI styling as a const palette stripped for non-tty still needs SOME runtime tty/NO_COLOR detection at the write site (or it ships color into piped logs) — so a sliver of the terminal-detection concern survives even in the slim path; fully avoiding it means no color (acceptable, but a parity loss vs Spring's Ansi support).; If the rendered-banner-as-singleton ceremony IS actually wanted by some downstream feature (e.g. an actuator-analogue /info endpoint echoing the banner), R2's instinct to drop it would have to be reversed, re-adding a registration step — so R2 pre-judges that the singleton is unnecessary, which is a §2.2 call that belongs in phase 2, not baked into the realization.; The compile-time placeholder split means the placeholder VOCABULARY is fixed at macro time against keys it must know exist (application.version etc.); a user placeholder referencing an arbitrary runtime property works (it is just a Placeholder{key} resolved at runtime), but the macro cannot validate the key exists at compile time — so the 'earliest diagnostics' win is partial (malformed grammar yes, unknown-but-well-formed key no).
