- No GC fallback for a forgotten close, and no async Drop. Spring's standalone teardown is already opt-in (close()/registerShutdownHook), but a forgotten close is eventually GC-mopped. leaf has no GC AND no async Drop (nightly doc: experimental-incomplete, tokio-shutdown crash, no dyn story — avoid), so the shutdown this feature triggers is the SOLE teardown: the explicit awaited context-close pass (stop runtime-lifecycle then reverse-order destroy under per-bean timeouts). This sharpens Spring's 'developers wrongly assume process exit handles it' footgun into a hard requirement — skipping the hook AND skipping an explicit close leaks async resources with no safety net.
- Spring's startupShutdownLock (ReentrantLock) + isStartupShutdownThreadStuck interrupt clashes with §2.5 no-global-lock + async cancellation. Spring guards close/refresh with a lock and interrupts a shutdown-hook thread stuck WAITING (e.g. user System.exit during startup). In leaf the hook-vs-explicit-close race is dissolved by context-close's idempotent CAS / state machine (a second trigger is a defined no-op or awaits the in-flight close via a watch/notify), never a contended mutex; a hung teardown is bounded by context-close's per-bean/per-phase timeouts + async cancellation and surfaces a rich 'which bean stalled' diagnostic, never an interrupted OS thread or a deadlocked hook.
- The exit-code AGGREGATION rule is a JVM-convention with no structural guard. Spring's getExitCode aggregates multiple generators as 'the highest absolute value wins' (max of positives, min of negatives), else 0. This is a hand-maintained arithmetic convention; leaf must port it explicitly and test it, and a contributor returning a surprising sign/magnitude can silently dominate the final code — the same opacity Spring has, now leaf's. (R3 additionally faces std::process::ExitCode's narrower 0-255 portable space not matching Spring's arbitrary-i32, possibly forcing a leaf-defined ExitCode.)
- Exit-code contributors inherit the cross-crate DCE silent-failure hazard in its QUIETEST form. A contributor/mapper in a crate the binary never force-links (Layer 0) or that is DCE'd (Layer A pre-1.62 / Layer B under LLD pre-1.89) is silently absent — and unlike a missing bean (loud at resolution) a missing exit-code contributor just yields a WRONG (often zero) exit code that won't surface in lib tests, only in the final-binary exit status. This mandates the run pipeline's anti-DCE self-check and final-binary testing of the exit status. (R3 mitigates this for the dominant failure path by carrying the code ON the error value, off the registry entirely.)
- ExitCodeEvent + the exit-code role traits become a small stable cross-crate ABI with no classpath to anchor them. The ExitCodeEvent name, the ExitCodeContributor/ExceptionExitMapper signatures, and (R2) the TerminationState vocabulary are agreed by convention within one JVM in Spring; in leaf downstream/integration crates depend on them, so leaf must PUBLISH them as a versioned public surface (an ABI-ish commitment), emitted with absolute paths by the thin macros — like the run-listener event-name taxonomy.

### Interactions
- **context-close** — PRIMARY DOWNSTREAM / the lifecycle this feature DRIVES (and the explicit boundary). This feature is the APP-LEVEL coordinator ABOVE context-close: the shutdown hook it arms TRIGGERS context-close's idempotent close-once teardown, and the exit()/termination coordinator AWAITS context-close (which owns stop-then-destroy reverse-order teardown, the CAS close-once gate, the cancel-vs-close fork, per-bean timeouts, and the ShutdownReport) as one unit before computing the exit code. This feature NEVER tears down beans itself — it decides WHEN/WHETHER to arm the hook, on WHAT signals, and computes the exit code AROUND the close. The hook-vs-explicit-close race resolves to a defined no-op via context-close's CAS. The intent-distinction the FEATURE id calls out is exactly this: app-level exit-code + hook-arming + teardown-ordering coordination, DISTINCT from the container close lifecycle it drives.
- **spring-application-run** — HOST PIPELINE / two integration points. The run pipeline ARMS the hook (this feature) at its early 'enable shutdown hook' step (gated by the bound leaf.main.register-shutdown-hook knob, armed early but firing only once a RunningContext exists), and on failure routes through handle_run_failure where handle_exit_code (this feature) computes the failure-derived code BEFORE context-close, in Spring's handleExitCode→failed→reportFailure→close order. The AbandonedRunException short-circuit (test-slice/withHook abort) skips BOTH failure analysis AND exit-code/close. This feature builds concretely on the run pipeline's RunFailure/RunningContext types and its FailureAnalyzer chain (the exit code and the FailureAnalysis are sibling outputs of the same failure).
- **runtime-lifecycle** — INDIRECT DOWNSTREAM (via context-close). This feature's triggered shutdown causes context-close to call runtime-lifecycle's stop_all() FIRST (reverse-phase graceful drain, per-phase timeout) before any destruction — so the app-level shutdown this feature coordinates ultimately drives the graceful drain. runtime-lifecycle owns the phase-grouped stop choreography + the spring.lifecycle.timeout-per-shutdown-phase knob; this feature only initiates the close that triggers it and observes completion to compute the code.
- **events** — PUBLISHER. This feature publishes ExitCodeEvent (the computed code) via the events substrate — exit-code-as-CORE, like availability, not an actuator add-on — for listeners that want to observe/log/report the final code. In R2 the ExitCodeEvent is literally the ExitCodeComputed→Terminated state-transition side-effect; in R3 it is a non-load-bearing observe-only lifecycle event (the code's source of truth is the typed result's Termination). Whether the event reuses the general bus or a lightweight channel is the shared events meta-question.
- **environment** — CONFIGURED BY (the bound knob). The decision to arm the shutdown hook is gated by leaf.main.register-shutdown-hook, a spring.main.* knob bound via the run pipeline's bind_to_application step onto the live Application from the prepared Environment — so externalized config can override a programmatic setter. This feature READS that bound knob to decide whether to arm; environment + the bind_to_application seam own HOW the knob is sourced and bound.
- **lifecycle-events** — SIBLING / availability-at-shutdown. lifecycle-events owns the liveness/readiness availability state and its reactive watch/notify model; this feature's shutdown trigger is the point at which the app transitions out of ACCEPTING_TRAFFIC (a readiness flip on shutdown), and exit-code-as-core mirrors lifecycle-events' availability-as-core posture. In R2 both share the same observable-state-machine + watch substrate (the unification opportunity). lifecycle-events models the availability fact; this feature models the termination/exit-code fact.
- **startup-instrumentation** — INSTRUMENTED (shutdown forensic). The shutdown/teardown pass this feature triggers is a recordable cold-path step under the run's root span (symmetric with bring-up instrumentation), and on a failure the exit-code derivation shares the diagnostics spirit with FailureAnalysis — the recorded trace + the FailureAnalysis + the exit code together form the boot/shutdown forensic. Carries parent linkage explicitly into the close fan-out (the §2.3 no-ambient-thread-local fix shared across the lifecycle features).

### Open questions for Phase 2
- Is application-shutdown-coordination + exit-code best modeled as (R1) three thin roles + an exit() coordinator delegating to context-close — intent-faithful, smallest divergence; or (R2) a single observable Termination state-machine over a reactive watch channel — first-class race/idempotency/abandoned transitions + observable shutdown, but heavier and pre-judging the reactive-state substrate; or (R3) a leaf-native typed-result + std::process::Termination with exit-code folded into the unified error model — most rust-native and smallest surface, but pre-judges the error-model keystone hardest and handles the success/controlled-shutdown exit-code awkwardly? This is the shutdown-coordination shape, downstream of the §3 unified-error-model + async-execution keystones — must stay a candidate.
- Are runtime-lifecycle R3 (RunState), context-close R3 (RunDown), and this feature R2 (TerminationState) ONE unified application-lifecycle state machine over ONE reactive-state primitive, or three layered/distinct machines? Three lifecycle features each propose a controller-state-machine-over-watch variant; if the reactive-state substrate is adopted in Phase 2 they must be RECONCILED in Phase 3 (one machine spanning bring-up→running→draining→terminated, or a composed stack) — presenting three separate machines risks redundancy (§2.11 working against itself). Belongs to the lifecycle meta-design, not this feature.
- What is the unified error/diagnostics model that the exit-code-from-failure mapping rides (the §1.7/§2.9 keystone), and does exit-code derivation FOLD INTO it (R3 — the error carries its own code, reusing the FailureAnalysis taxonomy) or stay a SEPARATE ExceptionExitMapper SPI (R1/R2)? The mapper's signature (downcast over a typed enum vs Any vs pattern-matched cause-chain) and whether 'port-in-use → analysis + action + a conventional exit code' is one coherent value or two parallel SPIs depend on the deferred error model. Cross-cuts the run pipeline's FailureAnalyzer, condition-report, and every feature that fails with context.
- Which cross-crate substrate collects the success-path exit-code contributors (and any link-time-contributed ExceptionExitMappers)? linkme / inventory / build-time codegen / explicit with() — and given the QUIET failure mode (a DCE'd contributor yields a wrong exit code, not a crash, invisible in lib tests), how is the run pipeline's mandated anti-DCE self-check + final-binary exit-status testing extended to cover it? R3 notably moves the load-bearing failure-path code OFF the registry (onto the error value); how much of the contributor surface even needs cross-crate discovery is itself open. Cross-cuts the cross-crate composition keystone and the run pipeline's discovery surfaces.
- Where does the runtime-specific signal-listener (the registerShutdownHook analogue) live, and what is the core's runtime-agnostic ShutdownTrigger contract? tokio::signal is runtime-specific so the listener belongs in an integration crate (leaf-tokio), but the core must define a seam that bridges multiple signal sources (and a no-runtime/core-only binary has no auto-hook). The exact contract + whether SIGTERM/ctrl-c/custom signals are configurable + how it composes with the chosen async-runtime keystone is unresolved. Cross-cuts task-execution and the runtime-pluggability invariant (§2.6).
- Does leaf adopt std::process::Termination/ExitCode (R3) for the process-exit boundary, accepting its narrower portable 0-255 code space, or define a leaf ExitCode newtype to preserve Spring's arbitrary-i32 + highest-magnitude-aggregation semantics? And is the exit-code's source of truth the typed result's Termination (R3) or the published ExitCodeEvent (R1/R2) — i.e. does the surface that OBSERVES the code match the one that COMPUTES it? This shapes the macro-emitted main signature and the public exit-code type. Cross-cuts the thin-macro story and the run pipeline's #[leaf::main].
- How much of Spring's exit-code surface is genuine rust-native intent vs JVM-shaped scaffolding to be designed OUT (charter §2.2)? Candidates to re-judge: whether ExitCodeExceptionMapper is even needed as a distinct SPI (vs 'the error knows its code', R3); whether SpringApplication.exit() as a standalone static coordinator survives (vs returning a Termination from main); and whether ExitCodeEvent is load-bearing or merely observe-only. Belongs to the per-feature Phase-3 re-unify, but flagged so the JVM surface isn't ported blindly.

### Notes
Scope boundary honoured precisely per the FEATURE intent: this feature is the APPLICATION-LEVEL exit-code-generation + shutdown-coordination layer (charter §6 leaf-boot), strictly ABOVE and DISTINCT FROM the container close lifecycle (context-close) it DRIVES. It owns ONLY: (1) arming the shutdown hook (the registerShutdownHook analogue — an opt-in runtime-specific signal-listener task that triggers context-close once, gated by the bound leaf.main.register-shutdown-hook knob); (2) the exit-code roles (ExitCodeContributor↔ExitCodeGenerator, ExceptionExitMapper↔ExitCodeExceptionMapper) + the aggregation rule (highest-magnitude wins) + ExitCodeEvent-as-CORE; (3) the app-level teardown-ordering coordinator (the SpringApplication.exit() analogue: trigger close → compute code → publish event → return code); and (4) the EXPLICIT caller-owned process-exit boundary (never process::exit inside the framework). It DELEGATES to: context-close (stop-then-destroy reverse-order teardown, CAS close-once, cancel-vs-close fork, per-bean timeouts, ShutdownReport), runtime-lifecycle (the phased graceful drain context-close triggers first), the spring-application-run pipeline (which hosts the hook-arm step + handle_exit_code on the failure path + the RunFailure/RunningContext/FailureAnalyzer types this builds on), environment (the bound knob), and events/lifecycle-events (ExitCodeEvent + availability-at-shutdown). All three realizations stay implementation-agnostic and hold the deferred §3 keystones (unified error/diagnostics model, reactive-state/async-execution substrate, cross-crate composition substrate, metadata/codegen boundary) as CANDIDATES — R1 leans literal-Spring-surface/delegation, R2 leans unify-via-observable-state-machine (sharing the substrate with runtime-lifecycle R3 + context-close R3), R3 leans most-rust-native (typed-result + std::Termination + fold-into-error-model), deliberately spanning the bespoke-machinery-vs-fold-into-existing-idioms axis so Phase 2's signal stays unbiased. Provider/registry abstractions kept ORIGIN-AGNOSTIC throughout (a native, WASM-module, or test-double exit-code contributor / mapper / shutdown trigger participates identically). The single highest-leverage Phase-3 consolidation to flag: exit-code-from-failure is the natural place where the unified error/diagnostics model (§1.7/§2.9) and the run pipeline's FailureAnalysis surface MEET — 'port-in-use → a clean diagnostic + an action + a conventional exit code' wants to be ONE coherent value (R3's bet), not two parallel SPIs; this should be coordinated with the error-model meta-design and the spring-application-run FailureAnalyzer chain. The three JVM-shaped mechanics most at risk of being ported blindly and flagged for rust-native re-judgement: the standalone ExitCodeExceptionMapper SPI (vs 'the error knows its code'), SpringApplication.exit() as a static coordinator (vs returning a std::process::Termination from main), and whether ExitCodeEvent is load-bearing or observe-only. Grounding cross-checked: spring-boot-4-di-design.md §244 (run() step 2 enable-shutdown-hook), §313-321 (handleRunFailure→handleExitCode→failed→reportFailure→close, AbandonedRunException short-circuit, withHook, StackWalker, AOT fork), §407-420/§888-890/§2400 (doClose sequence, registerShutdownHook, standalone-destruction-only-on-close-or-hook, startupShutdownLock/isStartupShutdownThreadStuck v6.1 provenance) + the confirmed SpringApplication.exit(context, generators) / ExitCodeGenerator / ExitCodeExceptionMapper / ExitCodeEvent contract (highest-magnitude aggregation; run() never calls System.exit; the caller passes the returned code to System.exit); the provided spring-application-run design (the host pipeline + RunFailure/FailureAnalyzer/handle_run_failure tangle); the four Phase-1 upstream docs (context-close R1/R2/R3 — the CAS close-once, the cancel-vs-close fork, the per-bean-timeout reverse-order drain, the opt-in signal-hook-as-trigger, the no-async-Drop-mandatory-teardown clash; runtime-lifecycle R1/R2/R3; lifecycle-events availability-as-core; environment's spring.main bind seam); the nightly envelope (AsyncDrop avoid → explicit awaited teardown; AFIT/RPITIT not dyn-safe → box at the dyn edge; tokio::signal runtime-specificity); the cross-crate doc (the three DCE layers, the QUIET-wrong-code failure mode, the anti-DCE self-check + final-binary-testing mandate, Architectures A-D, the runtime-specific-listener-in-integration-crate / core-defines-the-contract topology, §6 leaf-core/leaf-boot/leaf-macros/leaf-codegen). Sources for the confirmed Spring exit-code contract: https://www.baeldung.com/spring-boot-exit-codes and https://docs.spring.io/spring-boot/docs/current/api/org/springframework/boot/ExitCodeGenerator.html

## Bootstrap Context  `[bootstrap-context]`

leaf's TRANSIENT, PRE-CONTAINER registry — the ConfigurableBootstrapContext / BootstrapRegistry analogue (Spring intent: spring-boot-4-di-design.md §295-299 "The bootstrap context"; created first in run() at §244; BootstrapRegistryInitializer-initialized; promoted at prepareContext's bootstrapContext.close(context) at §293). Its WHOLE reason to exist: some bootstrap work must happen BEFORE the real container/Environment is sealed, must be SHAREABLE across bootstrap participants, and must be DISPOSABLE — Spring gives it a deliberately MINIMAL pre-container registry rather than letting that work prematurely instantiate the real context. The canonical motivating case (named verbatim in the Spring doc AND already cited by leaf's environment design's "BootstrapContext discipline"): an EXPENSIVE CLIENT (a remote-config HTTP/cloud-secrets client, a vault connection) that an EnvironmentPostProcessor-analogue needs at the EnvironmentPrepared hook to fetch config — created ONCE, lazily, shared across several EPPs, then either promoted into the container as a real bean (so the app keeps using the same warm client/connection pool) or disposed at close if nothing wants it. It owns: (a) the registry surface — a write side (BootstrapRegistry: register / registerIfAbsent of an instance OR a lazy InstanceSupplier, addCloseListener) and a read side (BootstrapContext: get / getOrElse / isRegistered); (b) the lazy-singleton-supplier semantics (a registered InstanceSupplier runs at most once, on first get, with a SINGLETON-vs-PROTOTYPE scope knob); (c) the BootstrapRegistryInitializer participant role (seed the registry before any run-listener fires); (d) the PROMOTE-AT-CLOSE seam (close-listeners fire; selected entries become real container singletons; a BootstrapContextClosedEvent-analogue announces it); (e) the lifetime guarantee that it is GONE after prepareContext (no reaching into it post-refresh). It sits INSIDE the spring-application-run pipeline (created at step 3, threaded read-only into the Starting + EnvironmentPrepared run-listener callbacks and the EnvironmentPostProcessor-analogues, closed during prepareContext as a capability transition). It is implementation-agnostic here: I compare registry/lazy/promotion MECHANISMS without picking leaf's meta-architecture, and hold the cross-cutting keystones (registry/type-erasure substrate, scope/ownership-handle shape, async-context-propagation, unified diagnostics) as Phase-2 candidates. Must replicate the INTENT without JVM lineage: no reflective type-keyed map relying on erasure-free Class objects, no GC-mopped disposal (explicit awaited close, no async Drop), no thread-local "current bootstrap context", and — critically — the lazy InstanceSupplier becomes an ASYNC-aware supplier on the cold bootstrap task whose result is fenced into a sync-usable handle before the env is sealed (the async pre-step → snapshot → sync-use pipeline the environment/value-injection designs already flagged).

### Candidate realizations

#### R1 — Literal typed pre-container registry object: a small owned BootstrapContext value with a write side (register / registerIfAbsent / addCloseListener) and a read side (get / getOrElse), TypeId-keyed heterogeneous storage of instances-or-lazy-suppliers, threaded read-only into the early run callbacks and promoted entry-by-entry at an explicit awaited close()
Mirror DefaultBootstrapContext as ONE concrete owned value `BootstrapContext` the run pipeline creates first (run-step 3) and holds by value/&mut through the pre-refresh phase. Two trait facets over the same value (the ConfigurableBootstrapContext split): a WRITE facet `BootstrapRegistry` exposing `register::<T>(supplier)`, `register_if_absent::<T>(supplier)`, `register_instance::<T>(value)`, `add_close_listener(f)`, `is_registered::<T>()` — and a READ facet `BootstrapContext` exposing `get::<T>() -> Result<Arc<T>, NotRegistered>`, `get_or_else::<T>(default)`, `get_registered_names()` (for diagnostics). Internally a `HashMap<TypeId, Entry>` where `Entry = Instance(Arc<dyn Any+Send+Sync>) | Lazy(BoxSupplier)` and the supplier memoizes on first resolve (a per-entry OnceCell, NOT a global lock — each get only touches its own entry). The SCOPE knob (Spring's Scope.SINGLETON default vs PROTOTYPE) is a flag on the entry: SINGLETON memoizes the first result; PROTOTYPE re-runs the supplier per get. Suppliers are ASYNC-aware: the supplier signature is `async fn(&BootstrapContext) -> Result<T, BootstrapError>` so an expensive remote-config client is constructed by awaiting on the cold bootstrap task; `get::<T>()` therefore has an async resolve path (`get(&self).await`) — but because all bootstrap-context use happens on the single cold bootstrap task before the env is sealed, no cross-task sharing of a half-built entry occurs. The run pipeline threads the read facet `&BootstrapContext` into `BootstrapRegistryInitializer` descriptors (run first, write-facet, to seed it), then into the Starting and EnvironmentPrepared run-listener callbacks and the EnvironmentPostProcessor-analogues (read-facet) — exactly Spring's `listeners.starting(bootstrapContext)` / `environmentPrepared(bootstrapContext, env)` signatures. CLOSE: during prepareContext the pipeline calls `bootstrap.close(&mut container_builder).await` — fire each registered close-listener (`BootstrapContextClosedEvent`-analogue carrying the bootstrap context + the new container handle so a listener can copy state across), then PROMOTE: each entry tagged `promote` is registered as a real container singleton (the warm client survives as a bean); un-promoted entries are dropped (explicit awaited disposal if they carry an async-close hook, since there is no async Drop). After close the value is consumed/moved-out so the type system forbids any post-refresh reach. BootstrapRegistryInitializer participants are collected as origin-agnostic const descriptors from the SAME catalog substrate the run pipeline uses (Phase-2-undecided: linkme / codegen / explicit). `register_component!`-style macro shim for the generic-target case (no 'static TypeId for `Foo<T>`).

**Pros:** Highest intent fidelity and teachability (DX #1, §2.10): the write/read facet split is exactly ConfigurableBootstrapContext-vs-BootstrapContext; register/registerIfAbsent/addCloseListener/get/getOrElse map 1:1; the threading into the early callbacks matches listeners.starting(bootstrapContext)/environmentPrepared(...); a Spring migrant reads it instantly and `cargo expand` of #[leaf::main] shows a plain owned value created then closed — nothing hidden.; The lazy InstanceSupplier with a per-entry OnceCell honours the marquee motivating case (an expensive client several EPPs share) with at-most-once construction AND no global lock (§2.5): each get touches only its own entry's cell, so concurrent-distinct-entry resolves never serialize — and the SINGLETON/PROTOTYPE scope knob is a one-field divergence per entry, faithfully porting Scope without machinery.; Async-aware suppliers resolve the central rust clash cleanly (§2.3): the expensive-client construction is an awaited cold-path step on the bootstrap task, and because all use is pre-seal on one task, the result is fenced into a sync-usable Arc<T> handle BEFORE the env is sealed — directly realizing the 'async pre-step → snapshot → sync-use' pipeline the environment/value-injection designs already named as the BootstrapContext-discipline owner.; Promote-at-close is a first-class, inspectable, AWAITED transition (no async Drop, charter rust-clash): close() fires close-listeners then moves promoted entries into the container builder and explicitly disposes the rest — the warm-client-survives-as-a-bean intent is literal, and a per-entry async-close hook handles disposal of un-promoted resources without relying on Drop.; Lifetime is enforced by ownership, not convention: the value is created in run(), borrowed read-only into the early callbacks, and CONSUMED at close — so 'you cannot reach into the bootstrap context after refresh' is a move/borrow-checker guarantee, exactly the transient-and-disposable invariant Spring documents but cannot enforce structurally.; Minimal, self-contained surface that delegates outward: it owns ONLY the registry + lazy + promote semantics; the participant-discovery rides the run pipeline's substrate, the EnvironmentPrepared timing is the run pipeline's, the closed-event rides events — so the feature stays a thin, honest object (§2.11).

**Cons:** TypeId-keyed `HashMap<TypeId, Arc<dyn Any+Send+Sync>>` PRE-DECIDES a slice of the deferred type-erasure / registry substrate keystone (§3): it bakes in Any-downcast + Arc as THE storage shape, which may conflict with whatever the container's registry substrate becomes — must be held as a candidate, not a commitment, and the `dyn Any` downcast loses the rich 'wrong type / not registered' diagnostic unless wrapped carefully.; Async `get(&self).await` on the read facet leaks async into a surface Spring made synchronous (BootstrapContext.get() is sync) — every EPP-analogue that reads the registry must be async, and an EPP that only wants an already-instance value still sits on an async fn; the ergonomic split between 'await a lazy supplier' and 'read an instance' needs care or it taxes the common case.; Threading `&BootstrapContext` (and the &mut write facet for initializers) through the run pipeline's early callbacks means the bootstrap context's borrow shape couples to the run-listener callback signatures — if those callbacks fan out (parallel initializers), a shared &mut write facet forces serialization or an interior-mutability cell, reintroducing a lock decision the per-entry OnceCell was meant to avoid.; Scope=PROTOTYPE (re-run supplier per get) is a faithful port of a Spring feature whose rust-native NEED is questionable in a pre-container phase — it may be JVM-shaped scaffolding (§2.2) that adds an entry-flag + a re-run branch for a case nobody hits before the container exists; keeping it risks porting blindly.; The generic-target gap (a `Foo<T>` has no monomorphized 'static TypeId until instantiated) forces a macro hard-error + register_component!(Concrete) shim, the same papercut as component discovery — acceptable but a real DX wrinkle that must be diagnosed loudly, not silently no-op.; Promotion-into-the-container couples the bootstrap context to container-core's singleton-registration seam BEFORE refresh (registering a ready instance as a definition/singleton) — getting 'a promoted warm client is a real bean with the right name/type and participates in close-time teardown' right is a real cross-feature contract, not just a map copy.

**Mechanisms considered:** one owned `BootstrapContext` value created first in run(), held by value/&mut through pre-refresh, consumed at close; two trait facets over the same value: write `BootstrapRegistry` (register/register_if_absent/register_instance/add_close_listener/is_registered) + read `BootstrapContext` (get/get_or_else/get_registered_names); internal `HashMap<TypeId, Entry>` where `Entry = Instance(Arc<dyn Any+Send+Sync>) | Lazy(BoxSupplier)`, each Lazy memoized by a PER-ENTRY OnceCell (no global lock); SINGLETON (memoize first result) vs PROTOTYPE (re-run per get) scope as a per-entry flag — the Scope.SINGLETON/PROTOTYPE port; ASYNC-aware supplier `async fn(&BootstrapContext) -> Result<T, BootstrapError>`; get has an async resolve path; all use is pre-seal on the single cold bootstrap task → result fenced into a sync Arc<T> before env seal; threaded read-only into the Starting + EnvironmentPrepared run-listener callbacks + the EnvironmentPostProcessor-analogues; write-facet only to BootstrapRegistryInitializer descriptors which run first; explicit awaited `close(&mut container_builder).await`: fire close-listeners (BootstrapContextClosedEvent-analogue carrying ctx + new container handle) → promote tagged entries as real container singletons → explicitly dispose un-promoted entries (per-entry async-close hook; no async Drop); BootstrapRegistryInitializer participants as origin-agnostic const descriptors from the shared run-pipeline catalog substrate (Phase-2-undecided); register_component!(Concrete) macro shim for generic targets lacking a monomorphized 'static TypeId

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** leaf-boot (charter §6 — the SpringApplication-equivalent layer) defines the `BootstrapContext`/`BootstrapRegistry` traits, the `Entry`/scope model, the `BootstrapRegistryInitializer` descriptor trait, and the `BootstrapContextClosedEvent`-analogue type. The TypeId-keyed map is process-local within a single run — it is NOT a cross-crate registry itself; the only cross-crate surface is WHO contributes BootstrapRegistryInitializers (and EPP-analogue readers), which ride the SAME participant-discovery substrate the run pipeline and environment's EnvCustomizer use (link-time linkme slice default + optional dynamic/WASM source; Architecture B/C/D candidates, never a runtime spring.factories scan). It therefore inherits the DCE story but in a MUTED form vs the container: a BootstrapRegistryInitializer in a crate the binary never force-links is silently absent (Layer 0) — its failure mode is 'an entry the EPP expected is missing' surfacing as a NotRegistered error at the EPP's get() (loud-ish, because get() returns Result), strictly better-signposted than a silently-skipped initializer. Still mandates the anti-DCE self-check (expected-vs-found initializers per source crate) and is a natural input to 'leaf doctor'. The registration ABI (the descriptor trait + the BootstrapContext trait pair) lives in leaf-boot/leaf-core and is emitted with absolute paths by thin macros; it is small and must stay ultra-stable since downstream EPP crates name it. Generics can't carry a 'static TypeId key → register_component!(Concrete) shim hard-errors on a generic target. The bootstrap context is created/closed entirely within the binary's run() so there is no link-order dependency on its lifetime; promotion writes into container-core's singleton seam (same binary). Origin-agnostic throughout: a native, WASM-module-, or test-double-contributed initializer/entry participates identically; a test can construct a BootstrapContext directly and register fakes (the test-double path) with no link-time machinery.

**T2 — execution context:** Entirely COLD-PATH on the single bootstrap task — this feature never touches a hot path (it is gone before the container is running). Creation is sync; BootstrapRegistryInitializers run sequentially (write facet) on the bootstrap task; the early run-listener callbacks read it on the same task. The async surface is the lazy supplier resolve: `get::<T>().await` may construct an expensive client by awaiting cold IO (remote config / vault) — a documented async-pre-step that MUST complete (the result fenced into an Arc<T> snapshot) before the env is sealed and before the container is built, so no half-built entry is ever observed by a sealed-env reader. Because all access is single-task pre-seal, the per-entry OnceCell needs no cross-thread synchronization beyond Send+Sync on the stored Arc (so a promoted client can later be shared across the running container's tasks). NO GLOBAL LOCK (§2.5): per-entry memoization only. A blocking client constructor inside a supplier must spawn_blocking (documented execution-context discipline §2.3). CANCELLATION: cancelling the bootstrap task mid-resolve aborts the in-flight supplier; any entries already constructed are disposed by the explicit close path the run pipeline drives on failure (refresh-lifecycle cancelRefresh / handle_run_failure), never by Drop — and a supplier that started external work must be cancel-safe or wrapped. close() is an AWAITED pass: fire close-listeners, await promotion writes, await per-entry async-close disposal of un-promoted resources; there is NO async Drop, so disposal is explicit and ordered. ERRORS propagate as a rich BootstrapError (which entry, which supplier, what was expected) into the run pipeline's RunFailure cause-chain (§2.9). No reactive/notify need — this layer is pure cold orchestration.

#### R2 — Bootstrap context AS the unsealed Environment-mutation phase: fold the pre-container registry into the same capability-token / EnvCustomizer customize window the environment design already defines, so a 'bootstrap-shared object' is just a token-scoped infrastructure object created during customize, with promotion = the seal/handoff transition rather than a separate registry
Question whether leaf needs a SECOND pre-container registry at all, given the environment design (02-configuration-environment R2) already defines a MutationToken-gated customize window with EnvCustomizer (EnvironmentPostProcessor-analogue) descriptors, an async pre-step that produces an in-memory source BEFORE customize, and a seal boundary after which mutation is forbidden. R2 UNIFIES: the 'bootstrap context' becomes the SHARED-CAPABILITY SCOPE of that customize window, not a distinct object. The MutationToken minted by the bootstrap owner carries (or gates access to) a small typed `BootstrapScope` side-table — `token.shared::<T>(|| async { ... })` returns an Arc<T> created at-most-once and cached on the token's scope, available to every customizer that holds the (borrowed) token for the rest of the customize phase. The expensive remote-config client is created via `token.shared::<VaultClient>(...)` by the first EPP that needs it and re-used by the rest — same intent, zero new registry type, riding the env design's existing async-pre-step → in-memory-source → sync-use pipeline. PROMOTION is reframed as the SEAL/HANDOFF: when the token is dropped (the env-seal boundary), any BootstrapScope entry tagged `promote` is handed to the container builder as a singleton (the warm client survives), and the rest are disposed by an explicit awaited drain. There is no separate 'bootstrap context closed' moment distinct from env-seal — the closed-event-analogue is folded into the seal transition (or co-fired with it). BootstrapRegistryInitializers fold into the SAME EnvCustomizer descriptor stream (a customizer that runs FIRST, before any source-contributing customizer, whose job is to pre-seed BootstrapScope) — one participant taxonomy, topo-ordered by data, instead of two. The read side is whatever customizers are handed: `&Environment` + `&BootstrapScope` (read) via the token. After seal the BootstrapScope is gone exactly as the token is gone — the transient lifetime falls out of the token's drop.

**Pros:** Maximal unification (§2.11), the charter's explicit goal: NO new registry primitive — the bootstrap context becomes a facet of the env-customize window the environment design ALREADY owns (MutationToken + EnvCustomizer + async-pre-step + seal). One participant taxonomy (EnvCustomizers), one lifetime boundary (token drop = seal), one async-pre-step pipeline — collapsing two Spring concepts (BootstrapContext + EnvironmentPostProcessor) that exist separately only because of JVM lineage into one rust-native phase.; Lifetime and 'no reach after refresh' are enforced by the SAME mechanism that already seals the environment: the BootstrapScope lives and dies with the MutationToken, so the transient-and-disposable invariant needs no separate ownership story — it is literally the env-seal boundary, and a stale BootstrapScope read after seal is the same Err(Sealed) the env already returns.; Tightest fit to the actual motivating case as the docs frame it: the expensive client exists SOLELY so an EnvironmentPostProcessor can fetch config — and EPPs ARE EnvCustomizers in leaf, so colocating the shared client with the customize phase that uses it is the most honest model; the client is created where it is used and handed off at the one seal boundary.; Async discipline is inherited wholesale (§2.3) rather than re-invented: the env design already specifies the async-pre-step (fetch remote config → in-memory source → sync customize) and that customizers are sync-non-blocking after the pre-step; token.shared resolution is that same pre-step, so there is exactly one place where bootstrap-phase async IO lives.; Fewest moving parts / least new ABI: no BootstrapContext/BootstrapRegistry trait pair, no separate descriptor taxonomy, no second closed-event — smaller stable surface for downstream crates to depend on, and the thinnest macro footprint (an EPP-analogue is already a registered EnvCustomizer).; Promotion-as-handoff is a clean single transition: the token-drop/seal moment both seals the env AND hands promoted shared objects to the container builder — one ordered awaited step, no separate close() to keep coherent with refresh-lifecycle's cancel-vs-close.

**Cons:** OVER-UNIFIES against a real intent boundary: Spring deliberately keeps BootstrapContext SEPARATE from the Environment because not every bootstrap-shared object is env-related (the doc says 'sharing singletons or lazily-created objects across the bootstrap phase' — broader than config). Folding it into the env-customize window scopes the bootstrap context to env-mutation time only, so a bootstrap-shared object needed by, say, a ContextInitializer (which runs AFTER env prep, in prepareContext) has no home — a genuine coverage gap.; Re-couples two concepts the upstream designs deliberately drew a boundary between: the environment design explicitly DEFERS 'where the async pre-materialization pipeline lives' and the profiles/value-injection designs name the BootstrapContext as a DISTINCT discipline — making the bootstrap context a sub-feature of environment pre-decides that boundary in environment's favour, biasing the Phase-2 'who owns the async pre-step' keystone.; The promote-at-close timing DIVERGES from Spring's: Spring closes the bootstrap context in prepareContext (AFTER createContext, alongside applyInitializers), not at env-seal (which is during prepareEnvironment, BEFORE the context exists). R2's seal-time handoff has no container to promote INTO yet — so either promotion must be deferred to a later step (re-introducing a separate close moment, defeating the unification) or the container builder must exist earlier than Spring's order, a real sequencing conflict with the run pipeline.; A MutationToken-scoped typed side-table is a narrower storage model than a free TypeId registry: token.shared::<T> is fine for a handful of well-known shared clients but awkward for the general 'register an arbitrary lazily-created object by type and let any participant get it' surface Spring offers — pushing some cases back toward R1's explicit registry anyway.; Couples the bootstrap context's fate to the environment design's still-open questions (the read/mutate seam mechanism, whether mutation is a token or a borrow) — if Phase 2 picks a different env-mutation model, the bootstrap context's whole shape moves with it, a fragile dependency for a feature that could stand alone.; Loses the explicit, separately-observable BootstrapContextClosedEvent seam (a real Spring extension point) by folding it into seal — a listener that specifically wants 'the bootstrap phase is ending, copy my state' now has to hook the env-seal moment, conflating two distinct observation points.

**Mechanisms considered:** NO separate registry: the bootstrap context = the shared-capability scope of the environment design's MutationToken-gated customize window; `token.shared::<T>(|| async { ... }) -> Arc<T>` — at-most-once creation cached on the token's BootstrapScope side-table, re-used by every customizer holding the borrowed token; BootstrapRegistryInitializers FOLDED into the EnvCustomizer descriptor stream as first-running customizers that pre-seed BootstrapScope (one participant taxonomy, topo-ordered by data); promotion = the SEAL/HANDOFF transition at token drop: promote-tagged BootstrapScope entries handed to the container builder as singletons; the rest drained by an explicit awaited disposal; async pre-step inherited from the env design (fetch remote config → in-memory source → sync customize) is the ONE place bootstrap-phase async IO lives; token.shared resolution rides it; read side = customizers handed `&Environment` + `&BootstrapScope` via the borrowed token; after seal both are gone (transient lifetime = token drop); closed-event-analogue folded into (or co-fired with) the env-seal transition rather than a separate close()

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** Strongest unification dividend: NO new cross-crate registry — BootstrapRegistryInitializers and EPP-analogues are BOTH EnvCustomizer descriptors riding the environment design's existing customizer-discovery substrate (link-time linkme slice default + optional dynamic/WASM source; const descriptors, runtime-evaluated, topo-ordered by DATA never link/section order). The MutationToken never crosses a crate boundary as data — only the customize fn is invoked with a borrowed token (the env design's stated 'no token smuggling'), so token.shared is a within-binary capability with no extra ABI. The stable surface SHRINKS vs R1: no BootstrapContext/BootstrapRegistry trait pair to publish — downstream crates depend only on the (already-published) EnvCustomizer descriptor + the token's shared API. DCE story is inherited verbatim from the env-customizer substrate (a customizer in an unreferenced crate is silently absent — Layer 0 — surfaced by the env design's self-check); no NEW DCE surface is introduced, which is precisely the unification win. RISK: this makes the bootstrap context's cross-crate shape a HOSTAGE to the environment design's still-open read/mutate-seam keystone — if Phase 2 picks a borrow-based seam instead of a token, token.shared has no home. Origin-agnostic: a native or WASM-module-contributed customizer pre-seeds BootstrapScope identically. The generic-target limitation still bites (a shared `Foo<T>` has no 'static key) → register_component!(Concrete) shim, shared with the env-customizer path. Promotion writes into container-core's singleton seam within the same binary — but the timing conflict (seal happens before the container exists in Spring's order) is a real cross-feature sequencing constraint flagged for Phase 2.

**T2 — execution context:** Inherits the environment design's T2 wholesale (the unification payoff): all bootstrap-context activity is COLD-PATH on the bootstrap task during the customize window; the MutationToken's drop is the seal boundary. token.shared resolution is the env design's documented async pre-step — fetch remote config by awaiting cold IO, fence the result into an Arc<T> snapshot BEFORE customizers run synchronously and BEFORE seal — so there is exactly ONE place bootstrap-phase async IO lives, and customizers themselves are sync-non-blocking (a blocking client constructor spawn_blocks, §2.3). NO GLOBAL LOCK (§2.5): token.shared memoizes per-type on the token's side-table within the single cold task; the env design's steady-state lock-free Arc<SealedEnv> read path is unaffected (the bootstrap context is gone by then). CANCELLATION: cancelling the bootstrap task during customize aborts in-flight token.shared work; entries already created are disposed by the explicit awaited drain at the seal/teardown boundary the run pipeline drives (no async Drop). The seal/handoff is an AWAITED transition: seal the env, hand promoted shared objects to the container builder, drain-dispose the rest. ERRORS during a customizer / token.shared resolution are aggregated and reported at the env design's bootstrap-validation gate with full provenance (which customizer, which shared object, which key) feeding the RunFailure cause-chain (§2.9). The one T2 tension vs Spring: because seal is during prepareEnvironment (before the context exists) the promotion-into-container step may need to be deferred to a later cold step on the bootstrap task, an explicit ordering boundary flagged for Phase 2. No reactive/notify need beyond the env design's existing profile-recompute notification.

#### R3 — Effect-typed bootstrap-resource graph: a build-time-/startup-resolved declarative DAG of typed bootstrap resources with declared promote-disposition and dependencies, where 'register an expensive client' is a node, lazy resolution is demand-driven over the DAG, and promotion/disposal are computed transitions of the resolved plan
Push the AOT / declarative lineage hardest (the run pipeline's R3 RunPlan shape + Spring 7's AOT fork, applied to the bootstrap context). Reframe the bootstrap context not as an imperative register/get registry but as a DECLARATIVE GRAPH of typed `BootstrapResource` nodes resolved once into a `BootstrapPlan`. Each resource is declared (by a const descriptor, contributed cross-crate) as `BootstrapResource { id, ty: TypeId, deps: &[ResourceId], scope: Singleton|Prototype, disposition: Promote|Transient, supplier: async fn(&ResolvedDeps) -> Result<T> }`. A PLAN phase (build-time codegen via leaf-codegen reading the resolved feature graph, OR a startup-validation pass when not AOT) resolves the DAG: validate that every declared dep is present and acyclic, compute a topological resolution order, and determine the promote-set (which resources become container singletons) and the transient-set (disposed at close) — ALL before any supplier runs, emitting an inspectable `BootstrapPlan` (which resources, in what order, who promotes, who disposes, the dep edges). The RUNTIME is then a thin demand-driven executor: when an EPP-analogue asks for `VaultClient`, the executor resolves it AND its declared deps in plan order, awaiting each supplier at most once (singleton) on the cold bootstrap task, memoizing into a typed slot. Because deps are declared, a resource that needs another bootstrap resource (the client needs a credentials-loader resource) is wired structurally, not by imperative get() calls inside the supplier. PROMOTION is a computed transition: at close, the plan's promote-set is handed to the container builder in dependency order (so a promoted client's promoted dependencies are registered first), and the transient-set is disposed in REVERSE dependency order by an explicit awaited drain. VALIDATION moves EARLIEST (charter §1.7): a missing dependency, a cycle, an ambiguous type, or a declared-but-unlinked resource fails the BUILD (or the startup-validation pass) with a complete diagnostic and ZERO side effects — before any client connects. The same executor serves AOT-emitted and runtime-computed plans (no bimodality). Imperative escape hatch: a programmatic `with_bootstrap_resource(...)` overlay lane for resources the plan didn't anticipate (test doubles, a withHook-injected fake), joined into the executor.

**Pros:** Earliest + richest fail-fast (charter §1.7/§2.9), the bootstrap layer's marquee surface: a missing/cyclic/ambiguous bootstrap-resource dependency or a declared-but-unlinked resource fails at BUILD/validation time with complete context (which resource, which missing dep, the dep path) BEFORE any expensive client connects or any IO runs — the purest 'a bootstrap that started is one that will complete', and the FailureAnalysis vocabulary applies at plan time.; Structural dependencies between bootstrap resources (the client needs a credentials-loader needs a region-resolver) are DECLARED and topologically resolved, not hand-wired via imperative get() calls inside suppliers — eliminating R1's risk of a supplier calling get() for an entry that isn't registered yet (an ordering footgun), and making the bootstrap phase's own mini-dependency-graph first-class and inspectable.; Best fit for the deferred compile-vs-runtime + metadata/codegen keystones (§3) and symmetric with the run pipeline's R3 RunPlan: the bootstrap-resource graph is exactly what a build-time pass can freeze, the most expensive analysis (dep resolution, promote-set computation, cycle check) moves off the startup path, and the executor is a thin demand-driven resolver — the cleanest AOT/wasm-friendly path (sidesteps DCE entirely by enumerating declared resources at build time).; Promotion and disposal become COMPUTED transitions of the resolved plan (promote-set in dep order, transient-set in reverse dep order) rather than per-entry flags checked imperatively — so 'a promoted client's promoted deps are registered first' and 'transients dispose before their deps' are mechanically derived, removing a class of ordering bugs and giving correct awaited teardown with no async Drop.; The BootstrapPlan is INSPECTABLE data (a generated/dumpable artifact): 'which bootstrap resources exist, what they depend on, who promotes into the container, who is transient' is a readable plan, not emergent runtime behaviour — excellent debuggability and a clean thin-macro story (the plan is hand-inspectable; charter §2.10), and the anti-DCE self-check becomes a build-time manifest cross-check (expected-vs-found resources per declared crate, --check-able in CI).; Origin-agnostic and overlay-friendly: a native, WASM-module-, or test-contributed resource descriptor participates identically in planning; the programmatic with_bootstrap_resource overlay lane cleanly handles test doubles / withHook-injected fakes the frozen plan didn't anticipate.

**Cons:** MASSIVELY over-engineers a deliberately MINIMAL Spring concept (the doc stresses 'a deliberately minimal pre-container registry'): a full effect-typed DAG with build-time planning, dep edges, promote-set computation, and an overlay lane is enormous machinery for what is usually 'create one expensive client and maybe keep it' — a direct tension with charter §2.2 (don't port JVM scaffolding, but also don't INVENT heavyweight scaffolding) and §5 (don't over-build).; Pre-judges the §3 compile-vs-runtime AND metadata/codegen keystones HARD for a feature that barely warrants influence over them — presenting a frozen BootstrapPlan as THE realization risks biasing Phase-2 signal far out of proportion to the feature's weight; it must be held strictly as a CANDIDATE, and its value is bounded by how much of the bootstrap-resource graph is even knowable at build time.; Most of what the plan freezes is genuinely runtime: WHICH bootstrap resources are needed often depends on resolved config (an EPP only needs a vault client IF spring.config.import names a vault: source), so the plan must conservatively over-approximate (plan every possibly-needed resource) or re-resolve at runtime — partially reintroducing the demand-driven dynamism it sought to eliminate, and demand-driven-resolution-over-a-frozen-plan is most of R1's executor anyway.; Declaring inter-resource DEPENDENCIES is a feature Spring's BootstrapRegistry does NOT have (Spring suppliers just call context.get() imperatively) — so the dep-DAG is a leaf INVENTION; it may be cleaner, but it is novel surface a Spring migrant must learn, and for the common single-resource case the dep edges are pure overhead.; Two computation modes (build-time codegen plan + runtime-computed plan) that must produce IDENTICAL plans, plus the overlay lane for unanticipated resources, is a real coherence burden for a transient phase that exists for at most a few hundred milliseconds — the payoff (faster startup, earlier validation) is small because the bootstrap context is tiny and short-lived.; The BootstrapPlan + BootstrapResource descriptor format becomes a stable ABI/format commitment that must version cleanly across leaf releases — a heavy, long-lived contract for an ephemeral feature, and the build-time path can't see runtime/WASM-contributed resources (forcing the overlay lane that erodes the frozen-plan simplicity).

**Mechanisms considered:** declarative graph of typed `BootstrapResource { id, ty, deps, scope, disposition: Promote|Transient, supplier: async fn(&ResolvedDeps)->Result<T> }` const descriptors, contributed cross-crate; PLAN phase (build-time leaf-codegen reading the resolved feature graph, OR a startup-validation pass): validate deps present + acyclic, compute topo resolution order, compute promote-set vs transient-set, emit an inspectable `BootstrapPlan` — before any supplier runs; thin demand-driven runtime executor: resolve a requested resource AND its declared deps in plan order, await each supplier at-most-once (singleton), memoize into a typed slot; structural inter-resource dependencies declared (not imperative get() inside suppliers) — the bootstrap phase's own mini dep-graph made first-class; promotion = computed transition: promote-set handed to the container builder in dependency order; transient-set disposed in REVERSE dependency order by explicit awaited drain (no async Drop); whole-graph validation at plan/build time (missing dep, cycle, ambiguous type, declared-but-unlinked resource) → BUILD/validation error with complete context, zero side effects; FailureAnalysis vocabulary applied at plan time; identical executor across AOT-emitted and runtime-computed plans (sqlx --check lineage); plan checked-in + --check-able as the anti-DCE manifest cross-check; conservative over-approximation + runtime re-resolution for config-dependent resource need (an EPP needs a vault client only if a vault: source is imported); programmatic `with_bootstrap_resource(...)` overlay lane for unanticipated resources (test doubles, withHook-injected fakes) joined into the executor; Architecture C (build-time codegen) substrate — platform-independent incl. wasm/embedded, sidestepping DCE layers

**T1 — cross-crate/tooling:** Confronts 'declared bootstrap resources across crates without a classpath' via the cross-crate doc's most-reliable path (Architecture C / sqlx model): a build.rs / `cargo leaf prepare` in the binary crate reads the resolved dependency graph (cargo metadata + a manifest convention), enumerates declared BootstrapResource descriptors, validates the DAG, and emits the BootstrapPlan into OUT_DIR (or a checked-in --check-able artifact) include!'d into the binary — sidestepping Layer 0 (the plan ENUMERATES declared resources and emits force-link references), Layer A (rustc reachability), and Layer B (--gc-sections) ENTIRELY, fully platform-independent incl. wasm where linkme fails. The anti-DCE self-check becomes a BUILD-TIME manifest cross-check (expected-vs-found resources per declared crate, --check fails CI on a silently-lost resource) — strictly more reliable than R1/R2's runtime presence check. BUT it cannot see resources the build doesn't know about: a dynamic WASM-module source or a test-injected fake has NO build-time presence and must contribute via the runtime overlay lane (a phase2Question). The BootstrapResource descriptor format + the BootstrapPlan format become a stable ABI/format commitment in leaf-boot/leaf-codegen (must version cleanly) — heavier than R1's trait pair, the cost of the AOT path. leaf-codegen (proc-macro/build crates isolated from runtime, charter §6) owns plan emission; leaf-boot owns the executor + the BootstrapResource descriptor trait + the promotion-into-container seam. Generics can't carry a 'static descriptor → register_component!(Concrete) shim. Origin-agnostic: a build-known native crate and a build-known integration crate plan identically; a runtime-overlay (WASM/test) resource joins via the same executor but bypasses the plan. CANDIDATES throughout — the plan's scope is exactly the statically-knowable fraction of the (tiny) bootstrap-resource graph.

**T2 — execution context:** The PLAN phase is SYNCHRONOUS cold/build-time work (single-threaded, no IO into the app, before the binary runs or in a dedicated startup-validation pass) — pure analysis over resource descriptors producing the BootstrapPlan + earliest diagnostics. The runtime EXECUTOR is async on the bootstrap task, demand-driven: resolving a requested resource awaits its declared deps' suppliers in plan order, each at-most-once (singleton), on the cold bootstrap task — the expensive-client IO (remote config / vault) is the genuinely-runtime async work, fenced into a typed slot/Arc<T> before the env is sealed and before the container is built. Because resolution order is planned, there is no imperative get()-ordering hazard. NO GLOBAL LOCK (§2.5): per-slot memoization on the single cold task; a blocking supplier spawn_blocks (§2.3). CANCELLATION: cancelling the bootstrap task mid-resolution aborts in-flight suppliers; because the plan validated the graph before any side effect, the abort surface is smaller (only IO/construction failures remain); resources already constructed are disposed by the explicit awaited drain in REVERSE dependency order the run pipeline drives on failure (no async Drop). PROMOTION/disposal are awaited transitions of the resolved plan (promote-set in dep order into the container builder, transient-set reverse-dep-order disposal). The config-dependent-need case needs a runtime RE-RESOLUTION step on the bootstrap task (cold, sync analysis over the plan + the now-loaded config) before suppliers run — an execution-context boundary reconciling the plan with runtime reality. The overlay lane (with_bootstrap_resource / test fakes) runs on the same bootstrap task, joined into the executor's resolution order. ERRORS: build-time plan failures are compile/prepare errors with complete context; runtime failures are a rich BootstrapError carrying the failing resource + dep path + FailureAnalysis into the RunFailure cause-chain (§2.9). No reactive/hot-path concern — wholly cold and gone before steady state.

### Rust clashes
- No reflective Class-keyed registry; no erasure-free type identity. Spring's DefaultBootstrapContext keys instances by Class<?> and relies on the JVM's reflective type identity + casts. Rust has no runtime reflection and TypeId works only for 'static types — so the registry must be TypeId-keyed over Arc<dyn Any + Send + Sync> with explicit downcast (R1), or a typed-slot/declared-graph model (R3). A generic `Foo<T>` has no monomorphized 'static TypeId until instantiated, so the macro must hard-error / demand register_component!(Concrete) — turning a silent no-op into a clear diagnostic.
- No GC-mopped disposal; no async Drop. Spring lets a never-promoted bootstrap object be silently garbage-collected and its close-listeners are best-effort. leaf has no GC AND no async Drop (nightly doc: AsyncDrop experimental-incomplete, tokio-shutdown crashes — avoid). So disposal of un-promoted bootstrap resources (closing an expensive client / connection pool that nothing wanted) MUST be an EXPLICIT, AWAITED drain at close — never a Drop, never a forget — with per-resource async-close hooks and error aggregation. This is the bootstrap-context-specific instance of the framework-wide explicit-teardown clash.
- The lazy InstanceSupplier is inherently async in leaf but sync in Spring. Spring's InstanceSupplier<T> is a synchronous Supplier resolved lazily on get(); the expensive client it builds is constructed with blocking JVM IO that Spring tolerates around main. leaf's async-first + no-blocking discipline (§2.3) means the supplier that builds a remote-config client must AWAIT cold IO on the bootstrap task — so 'get a bootstrap object' acquires an async resolve path, and the result must be FENCED into a sync-usable Arc<T> snapshot BEFORE the env is sealed (the async-pre-step → snapshot → sync-use pipeline the environment/value-injection/profiles designs already named as the BootstrapContext discipline). A sync get() can only return an already-resolved instance.
- No thread-local 'current bootstrap context'. Spring threads the ConfigurableBootstrapContext explicitly through listener callbacks (listeners.starting(bootstrapContext) / environmentPrepared(bootstrapContext, env)) — but any temptation to stash it in a thread-local for ambient access is hazardous across .await in async Rust (the §2.3 ThreadLocal-across-await concern). leaf must carry the bootstrap context as an EXPLICIT borrowed value threaded through the early run-listener callbacks and EPP-analogues, never an ambient read at an arbitrary suspension point.
- No runtime SPI scan for BootstrapRegistryInitializers. Spring loads BootstrapRegistryInitializer via SpringFactoriesLoader (a classpath/spring.factories scan). Rust has no classpath — initializers must be collected as origin-agnostic const descriptors from a SCOPED catalog substrate (link-time linkme slice + optional dynamic source; Phase-2-undecided), addressed by role, with the force-link discipline + anti-DCE self-check. An initializer in an unreferenced crate is silently absent (Layer 0) — though the failure mode is milder here (a downstream EPP's get() returns NotRegistered, which is loud-ish) than a silently-skipped container post-processor.
- Promotion into a not-yet-existing container is a sequencing clash. Spring closes the bootstrap context in prepareContext (AFTER createContext), so a real container exists to promote singletons INTO. If leaf folds the bootstrap context into the env-seal window (R2), seal happens during prepareEnvironment BEFORE the container exists — so promotion must be deferred to a later cold step, or the container builder must be brought up earlier. The promote-into-container singleton-registration seam also couples to container-core's pre-refresh definition/singleton model and to context-close's teardown participation (a promoted warm client must be torn down at container close).
- Ownership vs share-and-mutate. Spring's bootstrap context is a freely-aliased mutable object that any participant reads/writes. In Rust, a write side (register) wants &mut while many read sides (get) want &shared, and if the early callbacks fan out in parallel the &mut write facet forces serialization or interior mutability — a per-entry OnceCell (R1) or a token-scoped side-table (R2) resolves it without a global lock (§2.5), but the borrow shape must be designed deliberately rather than emerging.
- Scope.PROTOTYPE may be JVM-shaped scaffolding to design OUT. Spring's BootstrapRegistry.register supports a Scope (SINGLETON default / PROTOTYPE re-create-per-get). In a pre-container phase that exists for milliseconds and whose entire point is to SHARE a single expensive object, the rust-native NEED for a prototype-scoped bootstrap object is questionable (§2.2) — it must be judged for intent-parity, not ported reflexively as an entry flag + re-run branch.
- The BootstrapContext / BootstrapRegistry trait pair (and R3's BootstrapResource/BootstrapPlan format) become a cross-crate ABI with no classpath to anchor them. Downstream EPP/initializer crates name these by absolute path; leaf must PUBLISH them as a small, ultra-stable versioned surface (the emitted const descriptors hard-code paths to them), exactly like the run-listener event taxonomy — an ABI-ish commitment for a feature that is otherwise ephemeral at runtime.
- BootstrapContextClosedEvent rides the early-multicaster, not the container's. Spring fires BootstrapContextClosedEvent from close, but at that point (R1/Spring: during prepareContext) the container's multicaster exists, whereas the close-LISTENERS registered on the bootstrap context are NOT @Beans (the bootstrap context is gone before beans exist). leaf must dispatch the closed-event-analogue via the run pipeline's standalone early-multicaster + the bootstrap context's own addCloseListener list — reconciled with events/event-multicaster's eventual early-vs-context handoff design, not assumed to be on the live bean bus.

### Interactions
- **spring-application-run** — PRIMARY OWNER / host pipeline. The bootstrap context is created at run-step 3 (createBootstrapContext), seeded by BootstrapRegistryInitializer descriptors, threaded read-only into the Starting + EnvironmentPrepared run-listener callbacks, and CLOSED during prepareContext (promote + dispose) — exactly Spring's listeners.starting(bootstrapContext) / environmentPrepared(bootstrapContext, env) / bootstrapContext.close(context) sequence. This feature owns only the registry+lazy+promote+lifetime semantics; the run pipeline owns WHEN it is created, threaded, and closed, and routes its disposal into handle_run_failure on a boot failure.
- **environment** — DEEPEST collaborator — the BootstrapContext discipline. The environment design (R2) already names the bootstrap context as the home of the async pre-step that produces an in-memory property source BEFORE the MutationToken-gated customize window runs synchronously. R2 of THIS feature folds the bootstrap context INTO that customize window (token.shared). Either way, the expensive client lives here and feeds the EnvCustomizer/EPP-analogues that mutate the environment before seal; the bootstrap context's lifetime aligns with (R2: equals) the env-customize-then-seal boundary.
- **config-data** — CANONICAL CONSUMER. config-data's EnvironmentPostProcessor-analogue (the ordered infrastructure that loads config files/imports at EnvironmentPrepared) is the prototypical reader of the bootstrap context: a config-import that needs a remote/cloud/vault source constructs (or gets) the expensive client from the bootstrap context, shared across multiple imports, then promoted so the running app reuses the warm connection. config-data's async file/network IO is exactly the cold async-pre-step the bootstrap context's lazy supplier performs on the bootstrap task before seal.
- **context-close** — TEARDOWN SYMMETRY + promoted-bean fate. The bootstrap context's own close (promote + dispose un-promoted) is a distinct, EARLIER teardown than context-close's container teardown — but they share the no-async-Drop / explicit-awaited-drain discipline and the CAS-close-once idempotence pattern. A PROMOTED bootstrap object becomes a real container singleton, so context-close later tears IT down at container shutdown (the warm client gets a proper destroy callback); an un-promoted object is disposed at bootstrap-close and never reaches context-close. On a pre-refresh boot failure, the run pipeline disposes the bootstrap context as part of the cancel path.
- **container-core** — PROMOTION TARGET. close() promotes selected entries into container-core's pre-refresh singleton/definition seam (registering a ready instance as a real bean with a name/type before refresh) — the warm-client-survives-as-a-bean intent. This couples to container-core's facade for registering manual singletons before definitions load, and the promoted bean must then participate in normal DI, lifecycle callbacks, and close-time teardown like any other singleton.
- **events** — PUBLISHES the closed-event-analogue. close() fires a BootstrapContextClosedEvent-analogue (carrying the bootstrap context + the new container handle so a listener can copy state across the seam) plus the per-context addCloseListener callbacks. These fire BEFORE the live bean bus exists, so dispatch rides the run pipeline's standalone early-multicaster + the bootstrap context's own close-listener list — the early-vs-context multicaster handoff this area shares with refresh-lifecycle and spring-application-run.
- **post-processor-spi** — NEIGHBOUR via ApplicationContextInitializers. ApplicationContextInitializer-analogues run in prepareContext AROUND the same time the bootstrap context closes; an initializer may want to read a bootstrap object before it is disposed (a case R2's env-scoped folding cannot cover, since initializers run after env-seal — a coverage tension flagged in R2's cons). post-processor-spi owns the initializer/processor contracts; the bootstrap context owns the transient shared objects those initializers may consume during the close window.
- **profiles** — SHARES the async-pre-step pipeline. profiles' lever-harvesting and config-data's profile-conditional documents both run during the env-customize window the bootstrap context feeds; a bootstrap object (e.g. a client that resolves which profiles a remote source dictates) is the kind of shared pre-container object the bootstrap context exists to hold, consumed before resolve_active seals the ActiveProfiles.
- **task-execution** — EXECUTION-CONTEXT SOURCE. The bootstrap context's lazy supplier resolution (constructing an expensive client by awaiting cold IO) runs on the bootstrap task via task-execution's executor; a blocking client constructor must spawn_blocking. All bootstrap-context activity is cold-path before the container is running — task-execution provides the bootstrapExecutor the run pipeline uses.
- **startup-instrumentation** — INSTRUMENTED. Bootstrap-context creation, each lazy-supplier resolution (the expensive client construction), and close (promote + dispose) are child startup steps under the run's root span — making 'the vault client took 800ms to construct during bootstrap' a legible startup-trace entry, sharing the diagnostics spirit with the bootstrap layer's FailureAnalysis surface.

### Open questions for Phase 2
- Is leaf's bootstrap context a DISTINCT minimal registry object (R1, intent-faithful, covers shared objects beyond env including those a ContextInitializer needs) or FOLDED into the environment design's MutationToken/EnvCustomizer customize window (R2, maximal unification + one lifetime boundary, but scopes it to env-mutation time and pre-decides environment's open read/mutate-seam keystone) or a declarative build-time-resolved bootstrap-resource DAG (R3, earliest fail-fast + AOT determinism, but massively over-engineers a deliberately minimal concept)? This shape decision is downstream of the §3 metadata/codegen + compile-vs-runtime keystones and of the environment read/mutate-seam keystone — must stay a candidate.
- Which type-erasure / registry substrate stores heterogeneous bootstrap objects keyed by type — TypeId over Arc<dyn Any + Send + Sync> with downcast (R1), a token-scoped typed side-table (R2), or planned typed slots (R3)? This is a slice of the deferred type-erasure & registry-substrate keystone (§3) and should reuse whatever the container's registry substrate becomes rather than a bespoke bootstrap-only map; the choice also determines the richness of the wrong-type-vs-not-registered diagnostic.
- WHERE does the async pre-step (fetch remote config → snapshot → sync use) that the bootstrap context performs actually live, and who owns it framework-wide — the bootstrap context, the environment customize window, or a shared async-pre-materialization primitive? The environment, value-injection, and profiles designs ALL flag this same BootstrapContext-discipline pipeline as needing one framework-wide owner; it must align rather than be re-invented per feature, and it is downstream of the deferred async-execution / context-propagation model.
- Does the lazy InstanceSupplier need to be ASYNC (resolving an expensive client by awaiting cold IO) and if so does that make the read-side get() async, or is get() strictly sync over already-resolved instances with all async resolution forced into an explicit pre-step? This determines whether every EPP-analogue reader sits on an async fn, and is downstream of the async-context-propagation model — the sync-get-vs-async-resolve boundary must be pinned once for the bootstrap phase.
- Is the PROMOTE-AT-CLOSE timing Spring's (close during prepareContext, AFTER the container exists) or earlier (R2: at env-seal, before the container exists, forcing deferred promotion)? This sequencing decision cross-cuts the run pipeline's step order, container-core's pre-refresh singleton seam, and whether the bootstrap context can be folded into the env window at all — it constrains the whole-pipeline ordering Phase 2/3 must settle.
- Should the bootstrap context support Spring's Scope.PROTOTYPE (re-create-per-get) at all, or is it JVM-shaped scaffolding to design OUT (§2.2)? A pre-container phase whose entire purpose is to SHARE a single expensive object has a questionable need for prototype-scoped bootstrap objects — this is a per-feature Phase-3 intent-parity call (does leaf NEED it) flagged so it isn't ported reflexively.
- Does R3's inter-resource DEPENDENCY declaration (the bootstrap phase's own mini dep-graph) belong in leaf at all, given Spring's BootstrapRegistry has no such concept (suppliers just call get() imperatively)? It cleanly removes an ordering footgun but is novel surface; whether the bootstrap phase warrants its own dependency-resolution machinery vs a flat imperative registry is a scope/complexity judgment cross-cutting the §5 don't-over-build constraint.
- How does a dynamic (WASM-module / runtime / test-double) source contribute BootstrapRegistryInitializers / bootstrap resources, and at what timing — especially under R3 where dynamically-sourced resources have no build-time presence and need a runtime overlay lane that erodes the frozen plan? The static-link-time + optional-dynamic two-source duality applies to bootstrap participants exactly as it does to container definitions and run participants; the timing/overlay semantics are unresolved and cross-cut the cross-crate composition keystone.
- How is the BootstrapContextClosedEvent-analogue dispatched given it fires before the live bean bus exists — via the run pipeline's standalone early-multicaster, the bootstrap context's own close-listener list, or leaf's general event substrate? This is the same early-vs-context multicaster handoff + early-event-buffering question refresh-lifecycle, spring-application-run, and startup-instrumentation share, and belongs to the events meta-design, not this feature.
- What unified error/diagnostics model does a bootstrap-resource failure (an expensive client failed to connect, a missing/cyclic dependency) report into, and does the FailureAnalysis(description, action, cause) vocabulary apply at the bootstrap-context layer (R3: even at plan/build time)? This is the §1.7/§2.9 keystone surfacing again at the bootstrap layer; the analyzer-matching mechanism is downstream of the deferred unified error model and must stay a candidate.

### Notes
Scope boundary honoured: this feature is STRICTLY the transient pre-container registry — the ConfigurableBootstrapContext/BootstrapRegistry analogue (spring-boot-4-di-design.md §295-299) — and NOT the run pipeline that hosts it (spring-application-run, provided as the parent design and built on concretely here). It owns ONLY: (a) the write/read facet pair (register/register_if_absent/register_instance/add_close_listener vs get/get_or_else/is_registered); (b) the lazy InstanceSupplier with at-most-once memoization and the SINGLETON/PROTOTYPE scope knob; (c) the BootstrapRegistryInitializer participant role; (d) promote-at-close + the BootstrapContextClosedEvent-analogue + explicit awaited disposal of un-promoted entries; (e) the transient-and-disposable lifetime guarantee. It DELEGATES outward: participant-discovery to the run pipeline's catalog substrate, the EnvironmentPrepared timing + the async-pre-step pipeline to the run pipeline / environment, promotion to container-core's singleton seam, the closed-event dispatch to events' early-multicaster, and failure routing to the run pipeline's handle_run_failure. The three realizations deliberately span the design axes: R1 (literal minimal owned registry — highest intent fidelity, the safe default), R2 (fold into the environment customize window — maximal unification, but couples to environment's open keystone and has a real coverage gap for non-env shared objects + a promote-timing conflict), R3 (declarative build-time-resolved resource DAG — earliest fail-fast + AOT fit, but massively over-engineers a deliberately minimal concept). All three stay implementation-agnostic and hold the deferred §3 keystones (type-erasure/registry substrate, scope/ownership-handle shape, metadata/codegen boundary, compile-vs-runtime split, async-context-propagation, unified error model, cross-crate composition) as CANDIDATES — R1 leans minimal/runtime, R2 leans unify, R3 leans AOT/build-time, spanning the compile-vs-runtime axis so Phase 2's signal stays unbiased. Provider/registry abstractions kept ORIGIN-AGNOSTIC (a native, WASM-module, or test-double initializer/resource participates identically; a test can construct a bootstrap context directly and register fakes). Grounding cross-checked: spring-boot-4-di-design.md §244 (createBootstrapContext is run-step 3), §266 (the first two run-listener callbacks take a ConfigurableBootstrapContext), §293 (bootstrapContext.close(context) in prepareContext fires BootstrapContextClosedEvent and promotes singletons), §295-299 (the bootstrap context design rationale + the v4 package move to org.springframework.boot.bootstrap); the charter invariants (async-first + explicit execution context §2.3, no global locks §2.5, no async Drop / explicit awaited teardown, rich diagnostics §1.7/§2.9, thin macros §2.10, unification §2.11, intent-not-mechanism §2.2); the nightly envelope (AsyncDrop avoid; TypeId/'static keying limits on generics; AFIT/RPITIT not dyn-safe → boxed supplier futures at the dyn edge; linkme/inventory tradeoffs); the cross-crate doc (Layer 0/A/B DCE, force-link + anti-DCE self-check mandate, Architectures A-D, §170 ordering-as-data, the leaf-core/leaf-boot/leaf-codegen topology); and the upstream Phase-1 designs — ESPECIALLY environment R2 (the MutationToken/EnvCustomizer customize window + the explicitly-named "mirrors Spring's BootstrapContext for pre-container expensive clients" async pre-step at /home/jan/projects/testing/leaf/docs/design/phase1/02-configuration-environment.md), the value-injection + profiles designs naming the same BootstrapContext-discipline async-pre-materialization pipeline as a shared open question, and the events-lifecycle context-close design (no-async-Drop explicit-awaited-drain + CAS close-once + cancel-vs-close fork at /home/jan/projects/testing/leaf/docs/design/phase1/05-events-lifecycle.md). Notable tensions to flag for Phase 3: the THREE JVM-shaped mechanics most at risk of being ported blindly are Scope.PROTOTYPE (questionable need in a millisecond-lived share-one-object phase), the promote-into-not-yet-existing-container timing (a genuine sequencing conflict under R2's env-seal folding), and the BootstrapContextClosedEvent dispatch before the bean bus exists (must reconcile with the early-multicaster handoff). The single highest-leverage unification question is WHERE the async-pre-step (fetch-remote → snapshot → sync-use) lives framework-wide, since environment, value-injection, and profiles all independently point at the bootstrap context as its home — Phase 2 must give it ONE owner.

## Further bootstrap mechanics flagged by the critic (revisit in Phase 3/4)

- **Process keep-alive (spring.main.keep-alive / KeepAlive listener)** — Spring's KeepAlive listener (gated by spring.main.keep-alive, bound via bindToSpringApplication) spawns a non-daemon thread so a NON-WEB, bean-only application does not exit the moment run() returns — it keeps the JVM process alive until the context is closed. spring-boot-4-di-design.md line 293 ('add the KeepAlive listener if configured') and line 260 list it among the spring.main.* knobs.
