In async Rust the intent is: after a successful run() for an app with no long-running Lifecycle component holding the process, the bootstrap task must AWAIT a shutdown signal (the registerShutdownHook future) rather than returning and letting the runtime wind down — the 'how does a server-less leaf app stay running' question. _(The spring.main.keep-alive VALUE is stored in extra-11's BootstrapSettings (02-configuration-environment.md line 1762/1771), but NO design owns the BEHAVIOR. exit-code-shutdown owns arming/firing the shutdown hook and the termination/exit-code coordination, but explicitly models the steady-state as 'return-code-to-caller' — it never owns the keep-alive WINDOW (await-until-signal) that prevents an immediate exit for an app whose only 'work' is bean side-effects. spring-application-run's run() ends at 'if running: ready' and hands back; runners run before ready and return. So a leaf app with no auto-started runtime-lifecycle component (no server/scheduler holding a task) would complete run() and exit — silently dropping the keep-alive intent. This is sharper in async Rust than on the JVM (no ambient non-daemon-thread notion), and it is the natural seam between spring-application-run's tail, exit-code-shutdown's hook, and runtime-lifecycle's 'is anything actually running' — currently unowned.)_
- **ApplicationStartup recorder wiring at boot (context.setApplicationStartup) + the boot-level root step** — Spring's run() has an explicit step (run() step 11, line 244: 'context.setApplicationStartup()') that INSTALLS the bootstrap-selected ApplicationStartup recorder onto the context so that refresh-lifecycle's StartupSteps record into the same recorder the boot phase used, and the whole run nests as one tree. The intent: the run is the ROOT startup step (the spring-application-run JSON asserts 'leaf.application.run' as the root under which refresh-lifecycle's phases nest), and the boot pipeline owns choosing/installing the recorder and establishing the boot root as the parent of the container refresh root. _(startup-instrumentation (05-events-lifecycle.md line 541) defines its root as 'leaf.context.refresh' and frames itself purely as the OBSERVER of refresh-lifecycle — it never mentions a boot-level root span, nor the act of INSTALLING the recorder into the context (Spring's setApplicationStartup), nor how the boot root becomes the parent of the refresh root across the boot->refresh handoff. spring-application-run's interaction note claims 'the run carries parent linkage explicitly into the refresh fan-out (the §2.3 fix)' and that leaf.application.run is the root — but NO design owns the actual seam: who creates the boot recorder, when it is set on the context (the prepare_context/setApplicationStartup moment), and how the refresh root's parentId points at the boot root. This is a concrete ownership gap between spring-application-run and startup-instrumentation, not just a naming question, and it is the mechanism that makes boot-failure forensics (run-phase + nested refresh-phase in one tree) actually work.)_

## Area coherence notes

- AVAILABILITY-STATE OWNERSHIP IS SPLIT AND MUST BE RECONCILED. Three Bootstrap designs publish/consume availability (run-listeners-events fires AvailabilityChange(Liveness CORRECT) with Started and Readiness ACCEPTING_TRAFFIC with Ready; spring-application-run lists 'AvailabilityState publication as CORE'; exit-code-shutdown flips readiness REFUSING_TRAFFIC on shutdown), but the RETAINED, queryable, runtime-mutable availability STATE model is owned by lifecycle-events (05-events-lifecycle.md line 795, HALF 2 — a reactive last-write-wins state cell with an event projection, where ANY component can flip readiness mid-flight). The Bootstrap designs correctly defer the STATE model to lifecycle-events and keep only the milestone FIRING — this boundary is coherent AS STATED, but lifecycle-events' own area-coherence note (line 963) flags that the reactive-state/notification substrate is re-proposed three times (lifecycle-events availability cell, runtime-lifecycle R3 watch<RunState>, context-close R3 watch<RunDown>) and is unreconciled. exit-code-shutdown R2 adds a FOURTH (TerminationState watch). The Bootstrap availability publication sits on top of an unreconciled substrate; the boot designs must not assume a distinct availability mechanism from runtime-lifecycle/lifecycle-events' eventual state machine.
- RUN PIPELINE CORRECTLY DRIVES refresh-lifecycle / context-close / runtime-lifecycle WITHOUT DUPLICATING THEM — verified against 05-events-lifecycle.md. spring-application-run's refresh_context delegates WHOLLY to refresh-lifecycle's refresh() as an all-or-nothing unit (matches refresh-lifecycle's interaction note, line 69, that finish_refresh auto-starts runtime-lifecycle and returns once auto-start completes). The run does NOT auto-start Lifecycle beans (correctly leaves that to refresh-lifecycle's finish_refresh), fires Started AFTER auto-start, and only TRIGGERS context-close (never tears down beans itself). The cancel-vs-close fork the run chooses on failure (pre-Refreshed -> refresh-lifecycle cancelRefresh, no ContextClosedEvent; post-Refreshed -> context-close clean close) is EXACTLY the distinction refresh-lifecycle (line 70/85) and context-close (R1, line 463 cancel_bring_up sibling entry point) model. This layering is coherent and non-duplicative.
- SHUTDOWN-HOOK / startupShutdownLock OWNERSHIP IS CLEANLY SPLIT BUT THE SERIALIZATION MODEL IS DEFERRED IN BOTH PLACES. exit-code-shutdown owns ARMING the signal-listener hook (registerShutdownHook analogue) and spring-application-run owns the run()-step-2 arming point; context-close owns the idempotent CAS close-once that dissolves the hook-vs-explicit-close race (05-events-lifecycle.md line 458 point 3/5, line 463). This is coherent. BUT refresh-lifecycle's open question (line 86) and context-close both defer the per-container bring-up/teardown serialization (Spring's ReentrantLock startupShutdownLock + stuck-thread-interrupt) to 'execution context, not a global lock' WITHOUT resolving it — and exit-code-shutdown's hook fires concurrently with a possible explicit close on the SAME container. The three features agree the CAS dissolves the race, but the broader concurrent-refresh/close-on-one-container serialization is an unresolved shared keystone the boot hook directly depends on.
- application-arguments IS DESIGNED TWICE: as the Bootstrap-area 'application-arguments' feature AND as config-environment's [extra-6] (02-configuration-environment.md line 1291, 'Command-line argument property source + ApplicationArguments parsing'). Both cover the same five load-bearing parts (the option/non-option grammar, the value-object, the property-source adaptation, the precedence rung, the injectable singleton). The two are complementary in framing (Bootstrap frames it as the run-pipeline's parse-step + runner-arg handoff + singleton registration; extra-6 frames it as a property-source TYPE in the config stack) but they are the SAME feature with two owners and two realization sets — a clear ownership-overlap to collapse in Phase 2/3 so the grammar, multi-valued->indexed adaptation, and OsString-decode policy are decided ONCE, not divergently across two areas.
- EARLY-MULTICASTER / EARLY-EVENT-BUFFERING IS ONE UNRESOLVED QUESTION RE-RAISED IN FOUR PLACES. run-listeners-events (standalone early multicaster + contextLoaded handoff), spring-application-run (fires Starting/EnvironmentPrepared/ContextInitialized/Prepared on a standalone early multicaster before the context's bus exists), bootstrap-context (BootstrapContextClosedEvent fires before the live bus exists), and context-initializers (ContextInitialized/Prepared fired on the standalone early multicaster) ALL depend on the same early-vs-context multicaster handoff. 05-events-lifecycle.md's area-coherence note (line 970) already flags THREE early-emission mechanisms in the lifecycle area (events early-buffer, lifecycle-events pre-context facts, startup-instrumentation pre-recorder steps); the Bootstrap area adds the run-event early sequence and the bootstrap-context closed-event as further consumers. All correctly defer to the events meta-design, but this is now the single most cross-cut early-emission concern and must resolve to ONE early-buffering primitive, not parallel channels per feature.
- NON-UNIFORM ERROR-ISOLATION POLICY for milestone-listener failures is consistently flagged but unresolved across the boot/lifecycle boundary. run-listeners-events needs a per-milestone error policy where Started/Ready listener failures ABORT startup (route into handle_run_failure -> failed -> FailureAnalysis) while early-event listener failures isolate. This is the SAME 'observe-and-fail-startup' non-default that lifecycle-events (line 795 HALF 1: 'an ApplicationReady-listener failure can FAIL startup') and the area-coherence note (line 962) flag as conflicting with event-multicaster's Spring-faithful 'abort-and-propagate' default and smart-initializing's all-or-nothing need. The Bootstrap run-event sequence is a direct consumer of whatever single error model with per-dispatch override the lifecycle area must settle — the boot designs correctly defer it but cannot assume a uniform isolate-or-abort default.
- FailureAnalysis SHARES the anti-DCE self-check + cross-tier report-rendering machinery with condition-report — both the failure-analysis design and 03-conditions-auto-configuration.md's condition-report flag the duplicated mechanism. This is a coherent Phase-2 unification target as stated, but it means the Bootstrap area's FailureAnalyzer chain and the Conditions area's condition-report must agree on ONE error-matching mechanism (downcast over a typed BootError cause chain vs TypeId catalog vs Diagnose-on-the-error) and ONE report-rendering substrate; resolving them independently would yield two incompatible diagnostics tiers for one boot failure (condition-not-met vs wiring-broken).
- DISCOVERY-SUBSTRATE + ANTI-DCE SELF-CHECK is raised by EVERY Bootstrap participant-bearing feature (run-listeners, context-initializers, runners, failure-analyzers, app-type deducers, bootstrap-registry-initializers) and is identical to the substrate question 05-events-lifecycle.md line 965 already flags for refresh-lifecycle/runtime-lifecycle/events. The Bootstrap area is the NATURAL HOME for the force-link discipline + the mandated anti-DCE manifest (the entry point emits the app-root force-link prelude), so the self-check's location/shape decision is acute HERE — but each Bootstrap feature describes the manifest's home slightly differently (run-pipeline 'force-link discipline + anti-DCE self-check', deduction 'a missing deducer silently mis-deduces', runners 'a DCE'd migration = data corruption'). Consistent in deferring, but the manifest must be ONE area-wide contract so every feature's loud startup diagnostic computes against the same expected-vs-found source list.
